# Code Review Remediation Plan

_Every confirmed finding from the whole-project review, re-checked against the real code by a second pass and turned into a concrete, individually-actionable fix. Companion to [`CODE_REVIEW_FINDINGS.md`](./CODE_REVIEW_FINDINGS.md) (raw findings). Findings in `tools/quar-mcp` are excluded (that server is being replaced — see [`BACKEND_PLAN.md`](./BACKEND_PLAN.md))._

**How to use:** work sprint by sprint, top to bottom. Each fix is one addressable item (`F###`) with its own root cause, fix approach, files, test, risk, and effort. Check the box when landed. Respect `Depends on` ordering. Land the test named in each item so the defect can't regress — the suite is currently 3363 green and must stay green.

## Summary

- **Total fixes:** 202 (verdict after code re-check: 196 real, 6 partly — 0 refuted)
- **By severity:** 4 critical, 58 high, 95 medium, 45 low
- **By effort:** 121×S, 79×M, 2×L _(S <2h · M half-day · L multi-day)_
- **By regression risk:** 0 high, 73 medium, 129 low

| Sprint    | Focus                                         | Fixes |
| --------- | --------------------------------------------- | ----- |
| [R1](#r1) | Critical: data loss & corruption              | 4     |
| [R2](#r2) | High: Rendering & GL                          | 5     |
| [R3](#r3) | High: Geometry, tools & coordinate spaces     | 12    |
| [R4](#r4) | High: Fonts, SVG, animation, rigging & export | 17    |
| [R5](#r5) | High: Web app (store, canvas, UI, services)   | 24    |
| [R6](#r6) | Medium severity                               | 95    |
| [R7](#r7) | Low severity & cleanup                        | 45    |

> Note on the "partly" verdicts (6): the defect is real but the original description was refined during code re-check — see each item's **Notes**.

## <a id="r1"></a>R1 — Critical: data loss & corruption

_Stop silent destruction of user work. These four are the highest priority; nothing about them is cosmetic — each permanently loses or corrupts artwork/rig/animation data. Order within by dependency._

**4 fixes** — effort 2×S, 2×M, 0×L.

| ID     | Sev      | Location                                         | Fix                                                                                                                                          | Eff | Risk   | Deps |
| ------ | -------- | ------------------------------------------------ | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --- | ------ | ---- |
| `F003` | critical | `packages/core/src/boolean/booleanOps.ts:63`     | nodeToPolygon lumps all path contours (including disjoint subpaths) into one Polygon, so disjoint pieces are treated as holes and their area | M   | medium | F110 |
| `F004` | critical | `packages/core/src/tools/SelectionTool.ts:1450`  | autoReparentAfterMove reparents any moved node whose parent is not an artboard (group children, bone children) to root, silently destroying  | S   | low    | F051 |
| `F002` | critical | `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts:3079`        | switchPage/addPage/deletePage do not guard against symbol-edit mode, so the active page's stored scene is overwritten with the symbol's cont | M   | medium | F029 |
| `F001` | critical | `apps/web/src/services/projectSerializer.ts:174` | serializeProject/deserializeProject silently drop ikChains and smartBoneActions, so all IK chains and Smart Bone constraints are lost on eve | S   | low    |      |

#### `F003` · critical · data-loss

**Location:** `packages/core/src/boolean/booleanOps.ts:63`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** F110  
**Finding:** nodeToPolygon lumps all path contours (including disjoint subpaths) into one Polygon, so disjoint pieces are treated as holes and their area is silently destroyed by subsequent boolean/eraser operations.

- **Root cause:** nodeToPolygon (packages/core/src/boolean/booleanOps.ts:54-63) unconditionally wraps ALL contours into a single Polygon: `return [transformedContours as Ring[]]`. For a path node, nodeToContours->pathToContours (lines 117-137) returns [primaryContour, ...subpathContours], so every subpath becomes an interior ring (ring index >=1) of the first contour. polygon-clipping's PolyIn (verified in node_modules/.pnpm/polygon-clipping@0.15.7 dist line 1238/1250-1258) always treats geomPoly[0] as the exterior ring and geomPoly[1..] as interior/hole rings and normalizes their winding. A subpath that is a DISJOINT piece (not geometrically inside the primary contour) is therefore treated as a hole; the region it encloses has net negative winding and is excluded from the resulting polygon, silently destroying its area. Confirmed end-to-end: EraserTool.strokeErase (EraserTool.ts:418-424) does performBoolean(shapePoly, eraserPoly,'subtract'), which yields a multi-Polygon MultiPolygon when the eraser splits a shape; polygonToContours (booleanOps.ts:190-217) flattens all rings into a flat contour list and createBooleanResultNode (booleanOps.ts:255-278) stores contour[0]->points, rest->subpaths with fillRule 'evenodd' (renders correctly via even-odd). On the NEXT eraser pass, nodeToPolygon converts that node back and re-lumps piece 2 as a hole of piece 1; the recomputed node replaces the original (EraserTool.ts:522-523) and piece 2 vanishes. The existing test 'handles path with subpaths' (booleanOps.test.ts:243-261) only covers a properly-nested hole and thus passed while masking this.
- **Fix:** In nodeToPolygon, replace the single-Polygon wrap with even-odd nesting classification that matches how the node is rendered (evenodd fillRule). Keep the fast path: if transformedContours.length === 1, return [[contour]] unchanged. Otherwise: (1) add a ray-cast point-in-ring helper `pointInRing(pt,ring)` (even-odd crossing count) — first check packages/core/src/math and path/pathUtils for an existing helper to reuse, else add a small local one; (2) for each contour i, compute depth_i = number of OTHER contours that contain a representative vertex of contour i; (3) even-depth contours are exterior rings (each starts a new Polygon), odd-depth contours are holes; (4) assign each hole to its immediate parent = the exterior contour that contains it with the greatest depth; (5) build and return the MultiPolygon `Polygon[]` where each Polygon = [exteriorRing, ...its holes]. This preserves the existing nested-hole behavior (outer+inner where inner is contained -> depth 1 -> one Polygon with 2 rings, keeping booleanOps.test.ts:243-261 green) and keeps disjoint pieces as separate Polygons so their area survives all subsequent operations. Note: this makes nodeToPolygon able to return a multi-Polygon MultiPolygon, which is why the intersect footgun (F110) must be fixed first.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/boolean/booleanOps.ts`
- **Test:** In packages/core/src/boolean/booleanOps.test.ts add: (a) 'keeps disjoint subpath as separate polygon, not a hole' — makePath with primary square (0,0)-(40,40) and a disjoint subpath square (60,0)-(100,40), closed; expect nodeToPolygon(...).length === 2 (two Polygons) and total enclosed area ~= sum of both squares (not one square minus a hole); (b) regression 'nested subpath stays a hole' — the existing outer/inner case still returns length 1 with result[0].length === 2 rings; (c) round-trip data-loss guard — take that 2-piece node, run performBoolean(nodeToPolygon(node), eraserFarPoly,'subtract') with an eraser that misses both pieces, and assert polygonToContours(result) still yields 2 disjoint regions with unchanged total area (proves piece 2 is no longer destroyed on a second pass).
- **Notes:** Confirmed critical/data-loss. nodeToPolygon is shared by all boolean ops, the eraser, and the renderer, so the single-contour fast path must remain byte-identical and the nested-hole test must stay green. The manual even-odd classification is preferred over routing through polygonClipping.xor(...contours) because xor would re-tessellate/merge the exterior geometry before the real op.

#### `F004` · critical · data-corruption

**Location:** `packages/core/src/tools/SelectionTool.ts:1450`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** F051  
**Finding:** autoReparentAfterMove reparents any moved node whose parent is not an artboard (group children, bone children) to root, silently destroying hierarchy.

- **Root cause:** autoReparentAfterMove (SelectionTool.ts:1433-1488) only early-continues for node.type==='artboard' (line 1440). For every other moved node it computes targetParentId = findArtboardAtPoint(center)?.id ?? null and reparents whenever targetParentId !== currentParent (lines 1450-1453). A group child (parent=group) or a mid-chain bone (parent=bone, which resolveHitToScope resolves to itself via the bone break at line 580) that is NOT inside any artboard yields targetParentId=null !== its real parent, so sg.moveNode(id, null) rips it out to root, destroying the hierarchy. Position is re-expressed through the parent world transform (lines 1459-1481) preserving world _position_, but rotation/scale of the old parent are not compensated, so children of rotated/scaled parents also visibly change orientation/size. Because onPointerUp calls this whenever mode==='moving' && moveStartPositions.size>0 (line 347), even a click with zero movement triggers it (and no undo snapshot was pushed since onTransformStart is deferred to first move, line 318).
- **Fix:** In autoReparentAfterMove, after the existing `if (node.type==='artboard') continue;`, add a guard restricting the feature to artboard containment: only allow reparenting when the node is currently free or already inside an artboard. Concretely, after computing `const currentParent = node.parent;`, insert: `if (currentParent !== null) { const p = sg.getNode(currentParent); if (!p || p.type !== 'artboard') continue; }`. This preserves the four passing artboard reparent tests (rect at root -> artboard; rect child-of-artboard -> root) while never detaching group children, bone children, or symbol-instance children. Separately, rely on the F051 fix to gate the whole moving-completion branch (including the autoReparentAfterMove call) on actual movement (moveUndoPushed) so a mere click can no longer reparent.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/tools/SelectionTool.ts`
- **Test:** In SelectionTool.test.ts: (1) create a group with a child rect, enter the group (setEnteredGroupId), select the child, pointerDown+pointerMove(real displacement, staying outside any artboard)+pointerUp, assert child.parent still === group id. (2) Build a 2-bone chain (root->child), click the child (no drag) then pointerUp, assert child.parent still === 'rootBone'.
- **Notes:** Confirmed worse than the shape-only claim: bones and symbol-instance children are also detached, and a bare click (no drag) triggers it. The parent-type guard is the core fix; the no-movement half is covered by F051.

#### `F002` · critical · data-corruption

**Location:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts:3079`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** F029  
**Finding:** switchPage/addPage/deletePage do not guard against symbol-edit mode, so the active page's stored scene is overwritten with the symbol's contents.

- **Root cause:** switchPage (editorStore.ts:3079), addPage (2940) and deletePage all snapshot the LIVE scene via `sceneGraphJSON: structuredClone(sceneGraph.toJSON())` with no check of editingSymbolId. enterSymbolEdit (3446) loads the symbol definition into the live sceneGraph and leaves editingSymbolId + editingSymbolPrevState set. None of the page actions touch editingSymbolId in their set() blocks, so during symbol edit the page snapshot records the symbol's few nodes as the active page's artwork, editingSymbolId stays set on the new page, and editingSymbolPrevState still holds page A's scene — so a later exitSymbolEdit (3457-3480) writes the current (page B) content as the symbol definition and restores page A's old scene into page B. PageTabs.tsx (48/55/61) calls these with no guard.
- **Fix:** At the top of switchPage, addPage and deletePage (after the initial `const state = get()` and the same-page no-op guard), if `state.editingSymbolId` is set, call `get().exitSymbolEdit(sceneGraph)` first. exitSymbolEdit saves the edited symbol definition, restores editingSymbolPrevState.sceneData (the real page-A scene) into the live graph, and clears editingSymbolId/editingSymbolPrevState. Then re-read `get()` for a fresh state object and proceed with the existing snapshot/switch logic so it snapshots the restored page scene, not the symbol. (Do this after F029 lands so exitSymbolEdit also restores the page undo/redo stacks.) Alternative if exit-first is undesirable: early-return with a toast refusing page navigation while editingSymbolId is set.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts`
- **Test:** In the 'pages' describe block: enter symbol edit for a symbol whose definition differs from the active page, then call switchPage to another page. Assert (1) the original page's stored sceneGraphJSON equals its pre-edit content (not the symbol nodes), (2) editingSymbolId is null after the switch, (3) the symbol definition captured the edits made during symbol edit.
- **Notes:** Same root family as F029 (symbol-edit mode not isolated). Fixing via exit-first is cleanest once F029 makes exitSymbolEdit restore the page undo/redo stacks, hence the dependency.

#### `F001` · critical · data-loss

**Location:** `apps/web/src/services/projectSerializer.ts:174`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** serializeProject/deserializeProject silently drop ikChains and smartBoneActions, so all IK chains and Smart Bone constraints are lost on every save/reload.

- **Root cause:** projectSerializer.ts persists only three rigging collections. EditorStateSnapshot (lines 93-106) declares vitruvianControllers/dynamicChains/globalWind but not ikChains/smartBoneActions. serializeProject's rigging block (lines 174-180) writes only those three; deserializeProject's applyEditorState call (lines 430-432) restores only those three; and getEditorSnapshot in useProjectActions.ts (lines 72-88) never reads state.ikChains or state.smartBoneActions. Yet both collections are real store state (editorStore.ts:260 ikChains, 274 smartBoneActions) that is consumed at runtime by usePlayback.ts (evaluateIKChains, lines 29-30 and 49-50), Canvas.tsx (evaluateIKChains 577-578, evaluateSmartBones 633-635), PropertiesPanel.tsx:1953, MenuBar.tsx:253, and SmartBonePanel.tsx. So every save/reload silently drops all IK chains and Smart Bone actions. The test file (projectSerializer.test.ts, 939 lines) never references either field, so the gap is untested.
- **Fix:** 1) In projectSerializer.ts import IKChain and SmartBoneAction from '@quar/types' (both exported at packages/types/src/index.ts:378 and :462). 2) Add optional `ikChains?: IKChain[]` and `smartBoneActions?: SmartBoneAction[]` to EditorStateSnapshot (after line 102) and to the `rigging` sub-object type in both ProjectDataV1 (lines 44-48) and ProjectDataV2 (lines 77-81). 3) In serializeProject's rigging object (lines 174-180) add `ikChains: editorState.ikChains ? structuredClone(editorState.ikChains) : []` and `smartBoneActions: editorState.smartBoneActions ? structuredClone(editorState.smartBoneActions) : []`. 4) In deserializeProject's applyEditorState call (near lines 430-432) add `ikChains: v2.rigging?.ikChains ?? []` and `smartBoneActions: v2.rigging?.smartBoneActions ?? []`. 5) In useProjectActions.ts getEditorSnapshot (lines 72-88) add `ikChains: state.ikChains` and `smartBoneActions: state.smartBoneActions`. No change needed in @quar/core writeQuarFile/parseQuarFile — the nested rigging object is serialized wholesale, and core's migrateV1ToV2 already copies `rigging` verbatim.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/services/projectSerializer.ts`, `apps/web/src/hooks/useProjectActions.ts`, `apps/web/src/services/projectSerializer.test.ts`
- **Test:** In projectSerializer.test.ts add a JSON round-trip test: build EditorStateSnapshot with a non-empty ikChains (one IKChain with an id) and smartBoneActions (one SmartBoneAction with an id), call serializeProject, assert data.rigging.ikChains/smartBoneActions are present, then deserializeProject into a fresh scene graph and assert appliedState.ikChains and appliedState.smartBoneActions round-trip by id. Add a binary variant via serializeProjectToBinary/deserializeProjectFromBinary to cover the .quar path.
- **Notes:** Highest-value fix and lowest risk; do this first. Additive fields only — existing files that lack them default to [].

## <a id="r2"></a>R2 — High: Rendering & GL

_Fix GL state/program discipline, cache lifecycle, and skinned-render correctness in the WebGL pipeline. Several of these interact (cache eviction depends on the skinned-render cache-seeding fix), so respect the dependsOn ordering._

**5 fixes** — effort 2×S, 3×M, 0×L.

| ID     | Sev  | Location                                               | Fix                                                                                                                                          | Eff | Risk   | Deps |
| ------ | ---- | ------------------------------------------------------ | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | --- | ------ | ---- |
| `F036` | high | `packages/core/src/rendering/FramebufferManager.ts:67` | The framebuffer pool has a global size cap but no eviction of stale-size entries, so after canvas resizes the pool fills with unusable sizes | S   | low    |      |
| `F037` | high | `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts:1184`    | invalidateCache()/clearCache() have zero production callers, so geometryCache and booleanRingCache entries for deleted nodes and for previou | M   | medium | F040 |
| `F039` | high | `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts:3270`    | renderSkinnedFillsGPU restores the VAO but leaves the skinned shader program bound, so the next non-skinned shape's u_model upload is silent | S   | low    |      |
| `F040` | high | `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts:3377`    | Skinned nodes are permanently invisible after project reload because renderSkinnedNode requires a geometry-cache entry that only the non-ski | M   | medium |      |
| `F041` | high | `packages/core/src/rendering/WebGLRenderer.ts:144`     | After a WebGL context restore, the renderer resumes with dead GPU objects because handleContextRestored never invalidates cached programs/bu | M   | medium |      |

### Rendering & GL

#### `F036` · high · performance

**Location:** `packages/core/src/rendering/FramebufferManager.ts:67`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** The framebuffer pool has a global size cap but no eviction of stale-size entries, so after canvas resizes the pool fills with unusable sizes and every effect frame permanently creates and destroys canvas-sized FBOs/textures.

- **Root cause:** FramebufferManager.release() (packages/core/src/rendering/FramebufferManager.ts:56-73) enforces only a global cap via getTotalPoolSize() >= MAX_POOL_SIZE (8) and, when full, destroys the entry currently being released (destroyEntry(entry), line 68) rather than evicting a stale-size entry. acquire() (lines 33-51) reuses only an exact sizeKey match (`${w}x${h}`, line 26). EffectRenderer acquires every FBO at the single canvas size per frame (EffectRenderer.ts:76,158,333,352). After a canvas/panel resize, ResizeObserver (Canvas.tsx:509-519) calls setViewport with new sizes; the pool retains up to 8 entries of now-dead sizes, and because the cap is already reached, every new-size release() destroys its entry (line 68). Result: acquire() at the current size always falls through to createFramebuffer() (canvas-sized RGBA8 texture, line 92-121) and release() always destroys it — 3+ full-canvas GPU texture alloc/free per blended-effect node per frame, indefinitely, plus ~8 stale FBOs pinned until dispose().
- **Fix:** Purge stale-size pooled entries on size change. EffectRenderer always acquires at one (canvasWidth,canvasHeight) per frame, so a size transition is a clean signal. In FramebufferManager add a private field `lastKey: string | null = null`. At the top of acquire(width,height), compute key; if lastKey !== null && key !== lastKey, iterate this.pool: for every bucket whose map-key !== key, call destroyEntry on each pooled entry and delete that bucket from the map (leave the active Set untouched — those are in flight). Then set lastKey = key and proceed with the existing acquire logic. This guarantees the pool only ever holds entries of the current size, so releases at the current size are pooled and reused (no per-frame create/destroy) and stale-size GPU memory is freed promptly. Keep the existing MAX_POOL_SIZE cap in release() as a same-size safety limit. (Equivalent alternative: expose a public purge(width,height) method and have EffectRenderer call it when it detects a size change; the in-acquire approach keeps the manager self-contained and is preferred.)
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/rendering/FramebufferManager.ts`
- **Test:** New packages/core/src/rendering/FramebufferManager.test.ts: (1) acquire+release at 100x100 to populate the bucket; then acquire at 200x200 and assert the 100x100 entry's fbo+texture were destroyed (gl.deleteFramebuffer / gl.deleteTexture called with those handles) and getTotalPoolSize-equivalent shows no 100x100 bucket remains. (2) acquire+release twice at 200x200 and assert gl.createTexture is called only once (second acquire reuses the pooled entry). Requires extending createMockWebGL2Context in packages/core/src/test/setup.ts with createTexture/createFramebuffer/bindTexture/texImage2D/texParameteri/framebufferTexture2D/checkFramebufferStatus(returning FRAMEBUFFER_COMPLETE)/deleteTexture/deleteFramebuffer/bindFramebuffer, with createTexture/createFramebuffer returning fresh unique objects per call so handles are distinguishable.
- **Notes:** Confirmed exactly as described. Self-contained in FramebufferManager; no callers change. No existing FramebufferManager tests, so the mock GL context must be extended (that extension is also needed by F116's test).

#### `F037` · high · memory-leak

**Location:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts:1184`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** F040  
**Finding:** invalidateCache()/clearCache() have zero production callers, so geometryCache and booleanRingCache entries for deleted nodes and for previously opened projects accumulate for the lifetime of the editor.

- **Root cause:** invalidateCache(nodeId) (ShapeRenderer.ts:1184) and clearCache() (1191) are only defined and referenced from dist/\*.d.ts and tests — grep across apps/web/src and packages src shows zero production callers. Canvas.tsx handleNodeRemoved (Canvas.tsx:192-197) only bumps a version and calls disposeTexture for image nodes; it never calls invalidateCache, so geometryCache entries (populated by getCachedTessellation/getCachedMultiContourTessellation/renderText/renderImage) leak on every node deletion for all node types. On project/page switch, SceneGraph.fromJSON (SceneGraph.ts:419-459) does an atomic this.nodes swap and emits NO nodeRemoved events, and the ShapeRenderer instance persists (created once at Canvas.tsx:495), so both geometryCache and booleanRingCache retain entries for every node of every previously opened project/page for the renderer lifetime. dispose() clears geometryCache but not booleanRingCache (4421).
- **Fix:** 1) In Canvas.tsx handleNodeRemoved, add shapeRendererRef.current.invalidateCache(node.id) for all node types (not only images). 2) Add a bulk eviction path for project/page switches: either (a) emit a new 'graphReplaced' event from SceneGraph.fromJSON after the atomic swap and subscribe to it in Canvas.tsx to call shapeRenderer.clearCache() plus dispose all textures, or (b) call shapeRenderer.clearCache() from the editorStore fromJSON call sites (editorStore.ts:2839/2866/2952/2986/3088/3446/3468) via the Canvas ref. Preferred: emit 'graphReplaced' from fromJSON so all consumers stay in sync. 3) Also clear booleanRingCache in clearCache (already done at 1193) and add this.booleanRingCache.clear() to dispose() at 4421. NOTE: clearing the cache on switch makes skinned nodes invisible unless F040 is fixed first (renderSkinnedNode/Image return early when no cache entry exists).
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx`, `packages/core/src/SceneGraph.ts`, `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts`
- **Test:** Unit (ShapeRenderer): render a rectangle, assert getTessellatedVertices(id) non-null, call invalidateCache(id), assert getTessellatedVertices(id) === null. Integration (Canvas or editorStore): after fromJSON/page switch, assert the renderer's cache no longer contains a prior page's node id. Add a SceneGraph test that fromJSON emits a 'graphReplaced' event.
- **Notes:** Reviewer's refinement is correct: image textures ARE freed on per-node deletion via disposeTexture, so the GPU-texture leak is specific to the project/page-switch path; the geometryCache/booleanRingCache leak applies to all node types on both deletion and switch. Must land F040 before the clearCache-on-switch part to avoid regressing skinned-node visibility.

#### `F039` · high · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts:3270`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** renderSkinnedFillsGPU restores the VAO but leaves the skinned shader program bound, so the next non-skinned shape's u_model upload is silently dropped and it renders with a stale model matrix.

- **Root cause:** renderSkinnedFillsGPU ends by only restoring the VAO: `this.renderer.bindVAO(this.vao)` (ShapeRenderer.ts:3270). The GL program remains skinnedProgram/skinnedGradientProgram (bound via useProgram inside the fill loop at 3231/3253). When a skinned node has an empty strokes array, renderSkinnedNode returns after the fills block (3434 `if (strokes.length>0)` is false), so renderSkinnedStrokes — the only place that calls useProgram(this.program) at 3288 — never runs. The next flat node's render method (renderRectangle:1768, renderEllipse:1845, renderPolygon, renderPath:2040, renderText:2140, renderBone) calls gl.uniformMatrix3fv(this.program.uniforms.u_model,...) WITHOUT first calling useProgram(this.program) — they rely on the flat program already being bound. With skinnedProgram bound, that uniform call targets a location from a different program → GL_INVALID_OPERATION, silently ignored. renderFill then re-binds this.program via useProgram (cached by program object, WebGLRenderer.ts:266-271) and draws with this.program's stale u_model from the previous flat node.
- **Fix:** Add `if (this.program) this.renderer.useProgram(this.program);` at the end of renderSkinnedFillsGPU right after bindVAO(this.vao) (ShapeRenderer.ts:3270). This restores the flat program so subsequent nodes' direct u_model uploads land correctly. (Alternative, more invasive: make every render\* method call useProgram(this.program) before its first gl.uniformMatrix3fv — but the single restore in renderSkinnedFillsGPU is the minimal, targeted fix. renderArtboardBackground at 1810 already follows the useProgram-before-uniform pattern and would remain correct either way.)
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts`
- **Test:** Render sequence: a skinned rectangle with fills and empty strokes, followed by a plain rectangle at a distinct transform. Capture the model matrix passed to gl.uniformMatrix3fv for the flat program on the second node's draw and assert it equals the second rectangle's world matrix (not the previous flat node's). Simpler proxy: assert useProgram(this.program) is invoked after renderSkinnedFillsGPU when the skinned node has no strokes.
- **Notes:** Manifests specifically when a skinned node takes the GPU fill path and has zero strokes; the gradient-fill case leaves skinnedGradientProgram bound with the same consequence.

#### `F040` · high · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts:3377`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Skinned nodes are permanently invisible after project reload because renderSkinnedNode requires a geometry-cache entry that only the non-skinned render path populates.

- **Root cause:** renderSkinnedNode (ShapeRenderer.ts:3376-3377) does `const cached = this.geometryCache.get(node.id); if (!cached) return;` and renderSkinnedImage (3464-3465) does the same. The geometryCache is only populated by the non-skinned render paths (getCachedTessellation in renderRectangle/Ellipse/Polygon, getCachedMultiContourTessellation/getCachedTessellation in renderPath, renderText, and the image-quad block in renderImage at 1953-1963). But renderShape dispatches any node with skinData directly to renderSkinnedNode/renderSkinnedImage (1454-1467), never through the non-skinned path. So a skinned node whose bind-pose tessellation was never cached (fresh project load via fromJSON, or paste/duplicate producing a new node id via structuredClone of skinData) returns early and is permanently invisible. The existing test (ShapeRenderer.test.ts:1132) only passes because it renders the node non-skinned first, then adds skinData — masking the bug.
- **Fix:** In renderSkinnedNode, when cached is missing OR cached.geoKey !== buildGeometryKey(node), compute the bind-pose tessellation on the spot before proceeding: switch on node.type to build pathPoints (createRectanglePath/createEllipsePath/createPolygonPath/createStarPath as the render\* methods do) and call getCachedTessellation; for path nodes with subpaths call getCachedMultiContourTessellation else getCachedTessellation(applyCornerRadius(...)). Factor this into a private helper ensureBindPoseGeometry(node) that returns the entry. In renderSkinnedImage, when cache missing, populate the quad the same way renderImage does (blX/blY..trX/trY positions + fillIndices [0,1,2,2,1,3]) under node.id. Do NOT rebind/unbind (destructive — recomputes auto weights, discards painted weights).
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts`
- **Test:** Add skinData to a rectangle node BEFORE the first render (opposite order of the existing 1132 test), render, and assert gl.drawElements was called (node drew). Repeat for a skinned image asserting the texture quad drew. Regression test for paste: clone a bound skinned node under a new id and assert it renders without a prior non-skinned render.
- **Notes:** This is a prerequisite for F037's clearCache-on-project-switch: without on-demand tessellation, clearing the cache on switch would make every skinned node invisible. Reviewer's note that paste/duplicate also triggers it within a session is correct.

#### `F041` · high · context-loss-recovery

**Location:** `packages/core/src/rendering/WebGLRenderer.ts:144`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** After a WebGL context restore, the renderer resumes with dead GPU objects because handleContextRestored never invalidates cached programs/buffers and no recreation path exists, leaving the canvas permanently blank.

- **Root cause:** Two independent gaps. (1) WebGLRenderer.handleContextRestored (WebGLRenderer.ts:144-148) only sets contextLost=false, re-runs initializeState(), and calls onContextRestored — it never clears the this.programs (line 39) / this.buffers (line 40) maps nor resets currentProgram/currentVAO (lines 43-44), so those maps still reference GPU objects created on the dead context. (2) setContextRestoredHandler / setContextLostHandler (lines 130-136) are never called anywhere in app/library source — grep over packages+apps finds callers only in dist/ and the class itself. Canvas.tsx's render loop (Canvas.tsx:524-528) merely skips frames while isContextLost() is true and resumes the moment it flips false, calling grid.render / shapeRenderer.render which do useProgram on invalidated ShaderPrograms (WebGLRenderer.useProgram, line 266-271) plus Grid VAO/buffers, ShapeRenderer's 6 programs + VAOs + vertex/index buffers + textureCache, and EffectRenderer's FBO pool — all created on the lost context. Every draw then fails with INVALID_OPERATION and the canvas stays blank until a full page reload.
- **Fix:** Part A (WebGLRenderer.ts, handleContextRestored): before calling onContextRestored, drop references to the dead GPU objects — this.programs.clear(); this.buffers.clear(); this.currentProgram = null; this.currentVAO = null. Do NOT call gl.deleteProgram/deleteBuffer on the lost context (the browser has already destroyed those objects; the maps just hold stale JS wrappers). Part B (apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx init effect, ~line 469-500): extract the creation of Grid, ShapeRenderer (which internally news EffectRenderer at ShapeRenderer.ts:684), and OnionSkinRenderer into a local helper (e.g. buildRenderers()). Call it initially, then register renderer.setContextRestoredHandler(() => { rebuild renderers by calling buildRenderers(), reassign gridRef/shapeRendererRef/onionSkinRendererRef, and re-run renderer.setViewport(currentWidth,currentHeight) so buffers/textures are re-sized }). Since the context is already restored when the handler fires, either recreate fresh renderers and let the old JS wrappers be GC'd (simplest — the underlying GL objects are gone), or dispose the old ones first (dispose deletes are harmless no-ops on a restored context). Ensure the render loop reads renderers via the refs (it already does via gridRef/shapeRendererRef) so the swapped instances take effect.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/rendering/WebGLRenderer.ts`, `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx`
- **Test:** WebGLRenderer.test.ts: after createShaderProgram('x',...) and createBuffer('b',...), dispatch a 'webglcontextlost' event (with preventDefault stub) then 'webglcontextrestored'; assert getProgram('x') === undefined and getBuffer('b') === undefined (maps cleared) and that a registered setContextRestoredHandler is invoked. A Canvas-level integration/behavior check for renderer rebuild can be added but the unit-level map-clearing test is the load-bearing regression guard.
- **Notes:** Confirmed real via grep. Part A alone is trivial and low-risk; Part B touches the Canvas init lifecycle and is where the regression risk lives (ref reassignment + viewport re-init). No hard dependency on other findings, though it shares the rendering subsystem with F036/F116.

### Core geometry & paths

#### `F031` · high · data-loss

**Location:** `packages/core/src/boolean/booleanOps.ts:376`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** F003  
**Finding:** booleanOperation silently drops nested boolean-group children (nodeToPolygon returns null for groups), so flattening a boolean group that contains another boolean group loses that geometry while deleting the children.

- **Root cause:** booleanOperation (booleanOps.ts:362-401) converts children with nodeToPolygon directly (lines 371 and 376). nodeToContours (lines 70-83) has no 'group' case and hits `default: return null`, so nodeToPolygon returns null for any group node. When a boolean group being flattened contains a nested boolean group child: if it is the FIRST child, `let accum = nodeToPolygon(...); if (!accum) return null` aborts and booleanOperation returns null; if it is a LATER child, `if (!poly) continue` (line 377) silently skips it. Either way editorStore.flattenBooleanGroup (editorStore.ts:2540-2567) then does sceneGraph.removeNode(groupId) which removes the whole group INCLUDING the nested group's descendants -> that geometry is permanently lost. The intended recursive path exists but is dead/stubbed: childToPolygon (booleanOps.ts:324-330) is only called by computeBooleanGroupResult (which editorStore imports at line 42 but never calls), and computeNestedBooleanGroup (booleanOps.ts:337-351) is a stub that always `return null`. The working recursion lives only in ShapeRenderer.computeNestedBooleanPolygon (ShapeRenderer.ts:2506-2539), which flatten does not use. Additionally, flattenBooleanGroup calls get().pushUndo at line 2515 BEFORE any validation, so the abort cases (not a boolean group, <2 children, empty/null result) leave a spurious no-op undo entry.
- **Fix:** Two edits. (1) booleanOps.ts: give booleanOperation an optional resolver param `resolveGroupChildren?: (group: GroupNode) => { children: Node[]; worldTransforms: Matrix3[] } | null` and implement a real nested conversion mirroring ShapeRenderer.computeNestedBooleanPolygon. Introduce a local `toPolygon(node, transform, depth)` used for both the first and subsequent operands: if node.type==='group' && node.booleanOp && resolver provided, recursively fetch its children via the resolver, convert each with toPolygon(child, childTransform, depth+1) (recursing for deeper nesting, bounded by MAX_BOOLEAN_GROUP_DEPTH=10, line 288), and fold them with performBoolean using the nested group's own booleanOp; otherwise return nodeToPolygon(node, transform). Replace the two nodeToPolygon calls at lines 371 and 376 with toPolygon. Also remove/repurpose the dead computeNestedBooleanGroup stub so the real logic is the single source. (2) apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts flattenBooleanGroup: pass a resolver that reads children from sceneGraph (`group.children.map(id=>sceneGraph.getNode(id)).filter(Boolean)` and `worldTransforms` via sceneGraph.getWorldTransform). Move get().pushUndo(sceneGraph) from line 2515 down to immediately before the first mutation (before sceneGraph.addNode(resultNode...) at line 2563) so the not-a-group / <2-children / empty-result early returns no longer push a spurious undo entry.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/boolean/booleanOps.ts`, `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts`
- **Test:** In booleanOps.test.ts: add a test that builds two overlapping rects R1,R2 as a nested boolean 'union' group used as the SECOND child of an outer 'union' with a third rect, provide a resolveGroupChildren that returns R1/R2 and their transforms, and assert the result node's geometry/area includes the nested union region (not dropped); add a companion test with the nested group as the FIRST child asserting a non-null result. Plus an editorStore-level test (or extend the existing store test suite): flattenBooleanGroup on a group whose child is a nested boolean group preserves that geometry; and on an empty-result abort the undo stack length is unchanged (proves the pushUndo move).
- **Notes:** Real high/data-loss but confined to the flatten-of-nested-boolean-group flow. The new resolver param is optional so existing callers and all current tests are unaffected. Soft dependency on F003: the recursive leaf conversion still calls nodeToPolygon, so a nested group whose descendant is a multi-piece path only round-trips correctly once F003 lands. The reviewer's note that computeBooleanGroupResult is 'equally broken but has no runtime impact' is accurate — it is imported but never invoked; fixing booleanOperation is sufficient for the user-facing defect, though repairing childToPolygon/computeNestedBooleanGroup in the same edit removes the latent trap.

#### `F034` · high · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/gradient/gradientUtils.ts:244`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** getNodeLocalBounds for polygons multiplies by transform.scale and uses the circumscribed-circle box, mismatching the renderer's gradient space, so gradient handles are misplaced and drags write wrong gradient coordinates.

- **Root cause:** packages/core/src/gradient/gradientUtils.ts getNodeLocalBounds polygon branch (lines 240-245) returns [-r*sx, -r*sy, r*sx, r*sy]: it (a) multiplies node.radius by transform.scale and (b) uses the circumscribed-circle box. Neither matches the renderer's gradient space. The gradient fragment shader normalizes v_localPos (= a_position, the raw tessellated vertex, ShapeRenderer.ts:104,133-135) over u_bounds, which is set to computeBounds(vertices) / computeBounds(outline) (ShapeRenderer.ts:2871,2827). renderPolygon tessellates at the UNSCALED node.radius via createPolygonPath(0,0,node.radius,...) / createStarPath(...) (ShapeRenderer.ts:1867-1878) and applies scale only through u_model = worldMatrix (ShapeRenderer.ts:1888-1890). GradientHandleOverlay.tsx:74 gets localBounds from getNodeLocalBounds and at :197-208 passes them together with the full worldMatrix (which already contains scale, via sceneGraph.getWorldTransform) into gradientNormalizedToWorld/worldToGradientNormalized, so scale is applied twice. PropertiesPanel.tsx:135,533-538 resizes polygons by writing transform.scale, so scaled polygons are a normal case: at scale 2 the end handle (normalized x=1) maps to localX=r\*sx then is scaled again by worldMatrix → ~4r offset instead of 2r, floating outside the shape, and dragging writes normalized coords off by the scale factor. Separately, createPolygonPath starts at Math.PI/2 (pathUtils.ts:760) so the true vertex bbox differs from [-r,-r,r,r] even at scale 1 (e.g. a triangle's bbox is ~[-0.866r,-0.5r,0.866r,r]). The path branch (lines 246-258) is a smaller parallel mismatch: it uses only anchor pt.position and ignores bezier curve extrema and node.subpaths, while the renderer tessellates the actual curves (renderPath → applyCornerRadius → tessellatePathToVertices, ShapeRenderer.ts:2084-2091). Rectangle (233-237) and ellipse (238-239) branches already match the renderer and must stay unchanged.
- **Fix:** Rewrite getNodeLocalBounds so polygon and path branches return the SAME bounds the renderer normalizes over — the unscaled tessellated-vertex bbox — never applying transform.scale (scale lives in worldMatrix and would double-apply). Add imports to gradientUtils.ts: createPolygonPath, createStarPath, tessellatePathToVertices, applyCornerRadius from '../path/pathUtils' (no cycle: pathUtils does not import gradient). Define a local const GRADIENT_BOUNDS_TOLERANCE = 1.0 to mirror ShapeRenderer's DEFAULT_TESSELLATION_TOLERANCE (which is module-local at ShapeRenderer.ts:381 and not exported); the exact tolerance barely affects a bbox. Polygon branch: replicate renderPolygon exactly — const pathPoints = node.innerRadius !== undefined ? createStarPath(0,0,node.radius,node.innerRadius,node.sides,undefined,node.cornerRadius) : createPolygonPath(0,0,node.radius,node.sides,undefined,node.cornerRadius); then return computeBounds(tessellatePathToVertices(pathPoints, true, GRADIENT_BOUNDS_TOLERANCE)). Do NOT read transform.scale. Path branch: iterate contours [node.points, ...(node.subpaths ?? [])], for each run applyCornerRadius(contour, node.closed) then tessellatePathToVertices(processed, node.closed, GRADIENT_BOUNDS_TOLERANCE), computeBounds on each, and union the four min/max values (guard empty node.points → return [0,0,0,0]). Leave rectangle and ellipse branches untouched. No change is needed in GradientHandleOverlay.tsx — it only consumes getNodeLocalBounds. Optionally remove or implement the orphaned doc comment at pathUtils.ts:820-823.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/gradient/gradientUtils.ts`
- **Test:** Add a describe('getNodeLocalBounds') block to packages/core/src/gradient/gradientUtils.test.ts (import getNodeLocalBounds). (1) Scale invariance for polygons: build a polygon node (type:'polygon', radius:100, sides:5) with transform.scale {x:1,y:1} and an identical one with {x:2,y:2}; assert getNodeLocalBounds returns the same bounds for both (proves scale is no longer baked in), and assert both equal computeBounds(tessellatePathToVertices(createPolygonPath(0,0,100,5,undefined,undefined), true, 1.0)) (proves it matches the renderer's unscaled vertex bbox and is NOT [-100,-100,100,100]). (2) Non-circumscribed box: for a triangle (sides:3, radius:100) assert maxX < 100 and minY > -100 (real vertex bbox is tighter than the circle box). (3) Star: for a node with innerRadius set, assert bounds match computeBounds of createStarPath output. (4) Path bezier extrema: build a closed path node with two smooth points whose out/in bezier handles bow well outside the anchor-point bbox; assert getNodeLocalBounds is wider than the anchor-only bbox (i.e. includes the curve extrema). (5) End-to-end double-scale guard: with a scale-2 polygon, confirm gradientNormalizedToWorld({x:1,y:0.5}, getNodeLocalBounds(node), worldMatrix) lands near 2*r from center (not 4*r), using a worldMatrix built from mat3 scale(2,2).
- **Notes:** Confirmed real and high. Two distinct bugs in one branch (double scale + circumscribed box); the path branch is a smaller correctness mismatch fixed in the same edit. Only consumer of getNodeLocalBounds is GradientHandleOverlay (verified by grep), so regression surface is limited to gradient-handle rendering/drag math; rectangle and ellipse branches are already correct and left alone, keeping risk low. Watch two things during implementation: ensure no import cycle (pathUtils imports only bezier/math, so importing it into gradientUtils is safe), and keep the tessellation-closed flag consistent with the renderer (polygons/stars always closed; paths use node.closed). Stroke gradients normalize over computeBounds(outline) which is marginally larger than the fill bbox; matching the fill/tessellated bbox is a close, acceptable approximation and a large improvement over the current anchor-only/circumscribed values.

#### `F035` · high · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/path/pathUtils.ts:855`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Stroke align 'inside'/'outside' is inverted for every shape generated by the app's own shape tools (rectangle, ellipse, polygon, star).

- **Root cause:** generateStrokeOutlineVertices (packages/core/src/path/pathUtils.ts:852-864) assumes 'Left = outward (positive perpendicular)'. Perpendicular is computed as perp=(-dy,dx) of the edge tangent (lines 905-908, 944-945). For every app-generated closed shape the winding is positive, so perp actually points INTO the interior. Concretely, getShapeOutlinePoints (shapeToPath.ts:34-43) centers a rectangle at origin, giving top edge TL(-w/2,-h/2)->TR(w/2,-h/2) with tangent (w,0) and perp=(0,+1) which points toward +y = the interior. So for align='inside' (leftOffset=0, rightOffset=-width) the band is laid along -perp = OUTSIDE the shape; align='outside' lands inside. Rectangle signed area = +w*h (>0); ellipse = +2*rx\*ry; polygon/star use increasing-angle parametrization -> all positive winding. ShapeRenderer.ts:3309/3339/1160/4305 passes closed=true plus stroke.align, and PropertiesPanel.tsx:1004+3093 pass the UI 'inside'/'outside' straight through with no inversion, so the result is user-visible for all built-in closed shapes (rect/ellipse/polygon/star). Center align is symmetric and unaffected.
- **Fix:** In generateStrokeOutlineVertices, after computing leftOffset/rightOffset from align (pathUtils.ts:855-864), when `closed` is true compute the signed area of the tessellated loop via shoelace over the numVertices points read from `vertices` with wraparound: A += x*i\*y*{i+1} - x\_{i+1}_y_i for i in 0..numVertices-1 (i+1 mod numVertices), A _= 0.5. If A > 0 (perp points toward interior for these positively-wound loops), negate BOTH leftOffset and rightOffset so 'inside' offsets toward the interior and 'outside' away from it. Negation is a no-op for center (offsets are +-halfWidth, still symmetric) and only changes inside/outside. Do NOT apply when closed is false, so existing open-path inside/outside tests (pathUtils.test.ts:615-676) still pass. This also corrects outlineStroke.ts (which calls the same function with closed+align) with no change there. Keep the miter/widthProfile scaling after the offsets are chosen.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/path/pathUtils.ts`
- **Test:** In pathUtils.test.ts, add a closed-shape test: build vertices for a positively-wound rectangle centered at origin, e.g. [-50,-30, 50,-30, 50,30, -50,30], numVertices=4, width=10, closed=true. Call with align='inside' and assert all outline points lie within the original rectangle bounds (|x|<=50 and |y|<=30, i.e. the band sits between the path and the interior). Call with align='outside' and assert every outline point has |x|>=50 or |y|>=30 on the appropriate edges (band sits outside). Also assert center align remains symmetric about each edge. Optionally add a reverse-wound rectangle to confirm the signed-area branch flips correctly.
- **Notes:** Real, high-value correctness bug. Only affects inside/outside alignment on closed shapes; default 'center' users never hit it, which is why it survived. Shares the function with F115 but edits a different region (offset setup vs profile sampling) - coordinate the edit but no logical dependency.

### Scene graph, symbols & format

#### `F042` · high · crash

**Location:** `packages/core/src/SceneGraph.ts:446`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** fromJSON accepts cyclic children arrays and nodes with missing/non-array children, causing stack-overflow crashes or infinite-loop hangs when the graph is later traversed.

- **Root cause:** SceneGraph.fromJSON (packages/core/src/SceneGraph.ts:419-459) validates only node.id (line 436) and nulls parent pointers to missing nodes (lines 446-450). It never validates node.children: it does not check children is an array, does not filter dangling child ids, and does not detect cycles. Upstream validateProjectData -> validateNodes (apps/web/src/services/projectSerializer.ts:293-310) only checks id/type/transform, so a corrupt/hand-crafted .quar passes both gates. The traversal/removal/transform routines that consume the loaded graph have NO cycle or non-array guards: traverse (lines 363-381) and traverseVisible (lines 393-406) recurse over node.children with no visited set (children cycle A->B->A -> RangeError stack overflow; missing/non-array children -> 'children is not iterable' TypeError); removeNode (lines 95-125) recurses children before deleting from the map (line 122), so a children cycle infinite-recurses; getWorldTransform (line 311) recurses parent with no guard, and isAncestorOf (lines 285-294) / getEffectiveOpacity (lines 335-341) use while-loops that spin forever on a parent cycle (A.parent=B, B.parent=A). Note getDescendants (line 261) DOES have a visited set, confirming the omission elsewhere is inconsistent, not intentional.
- **Fix:** Add a hierarchy-sanitization step in fromJSON after the parent-orphan pass (line 450) and before the atomic swap (line 456). (1) Coerce children: for every node in newNodes, if !Array.isArray(node.children) set node.children = []; else filter node.children to ids that exist in newNodes. (2) Enforce single-parent + break cycles with an iterative DFS from validRootIds using a global `visited` Set and a per-path `onStack` Set: when about to descend into a childId that is already onStack (back-edge) OR already visited under a different parent (cross-edge/shared child), splice that id out of the current node's children array; otherwise mark visited, set the child's parent pointer to the current node id, and recurse. (3) Reconcile parent pointers so each visited node's parent equals the parent that owns it in children. Keep the change contained to fromJSON so load-time input is always acyclic and children arrays are always valid; downstream traverse/removeNode/getWorldTransform then cannot loop. (Optional defense-in-depth, not required for this finding: add a visited/MAX_DEPTH guard to traverse, traverseVisible, and removeNode mirroring getDescendants — recommend as a follow-up but the fromJSON sanitize is the primary fix.)
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/SceneGraph.ts`
- **Test:** In SceneGraph.test.ts fromJSON describe block: (a) 'sanitizes cyclic children arrays' — fromJSON with nodes A(children:['B']), B(children:['A']), rootNodeIds:['A']; assert that a subsequent sceneGraph.traverse(()=>{}) does NOT throw and terminates, and that the back-edge was removed (B.children no longer contains 'A'). (b) 'coerces missing/non-array children' — fromJSON with a node whose children is undefined and another whose children is 'oops'; assert getNode(id).children deep-equals [] and traverse() does not throw. (c) 'drops dangling child ids' — node with children:['ghost'] where 'ghost' is not in nodes; assert children === [].
- **Notes:** High-value hardening against untrusted .quar files. The DFS cycle-break also naturally produces the reachability info needed by F187, so implement both together.

### Tools, selection & coordinate spaces

#### `F048` · high · data-loss

**Location:** `packages/core/src/tools/EraserTool.ts:568`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Point-mode eraser deletes points from locked and hidden path nodes, and can remove those nodes entirely.

- **Root cause:** erasePoints() at EraserTool.ts:568 iterates the scene with this.context.sceneGraph.traverse(...). SceneGraph.traverse (SceneGraph.ts:363-381) visits every node unconditionally with no visible/locked filtering. The callback only guards `if (node.type !== 'path') return;` (line 569) and never checks node.locked or node.visible. So point-mode erasing strips points from locked paths and from hidden paths (invisibly), and when pointsToKeep.length < 2 the node is pushed to pathsToRemove (line 587) and deleted at line 604. Stroke mode does NOT have this bug because it uses traverseVisible (line 364) plus `if (node.locked) return;` (line 376).
- **Fix:** In erasePoints(), change `this.context.sceneGraph.traverse((node) => {` at line 568 to `this.context.sceneGraph.traverseVisible((node) => {` (traverseVisible skips invisible nodes AND their whole subtree, matching stroke-mode semantics and covering the hidden-parent case). Then add a locked guard mirroring stroke mode: immediately after the `if (node.type !== 'path') return;` check (line 569), add `if (node.locked) return;`. The callback signature (node) => void is compatible with traverseVisible. No other changes needed; pathsToUpdate/pathsToRemove logic is unaffected.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/tools/EraserTool.ts`, `packages/core/src/tools/EraserTool.test.ts`
- **Test:** In EraserTool.test.ts 'point eraser mode' describe: (1) 'should not erase points from a locked path' — build a 4-point path via createTestPath, set path.locked = true, addNode, run a click-erase near the first point, assert getNode(path.id) still defined and (getNode(path.id) as PathNode).points.length === 4. (2) 'should not erase points from a hidden path' — same but set path.visible = false, assert points.length unchanged and node still exists. The existing 'should delete individual points from path' test (visible+unlocked) is the regression guard that erasing still works.
- **Notes:** traverseVisible only descends visible subtrees, so it also handles the reviewer's hidden-parent concern (a visible path under a hidden group is skipped). Uses the same public method stroke mode already relies on, so no API risk.

#### `F049` · high · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/tools/RectangleTool.ts:80`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Alt (center-origin) drag toward the left or up silently fails to create a rectangle because BaseTool.getRectFromPoints returns negative width/height in the fromCenter branch.

- **Root cause:** BaseTool.getRectFromPoints (packages/core/src/tools/BaseTool.ts:185-191) returns the fromCenter rect without normalizing sign: {x: start.x - width, y: start.y - height, width: width*2, height: height*2}. width/height are raw (end - start) deltas and can be negative. For an Alt-drag from (100,100) to (50,60): width=-50, height=-40 -> the returned rect has width=-100, height=-80. RectangleTool.onPointerUp (RectangleTool.ts:80) gates creation on `rect.width >= this.getMinimumSize() && rect.height >= this.getMinimumSize()` (min=1), which is false for negative widths, so no node is created for up/left Alt-drags. During drag, RectangleTool.onPointerMove also sets previewNode.width/height to the negative values (degenerate preview). EllipseTool.getEllipseFromPoints (EllipseTool.ts:152-153) uses Math.abs in its fromCenter branch, confirming the omission is a bug. ArtboardTool (ArtboardTool.ts:67,74) uses the same helper and same gate, so it shares the failure.
- **Fix:** In BaseTool.getRectFromPoints, normalize the fromCenter branch to absolute magnitudes so the returned rect always has positive width/height and its top-left is start - |half-extent|. Replace the fromCenter return with: const aw = Math.abs(width); const ah = Math.abs(height); return { x: start.x - aw, y: start.y - ah, width: aw _ 2, height: ah _ 2 }. This keeps the geometric center at `start` (x + width/2 = start.x - aw + aw = start.x) and fixes all four drag directions for Rectangle and Artboard tools at once. No change needed in RectangleTool/ArtboardTool. Verify the existing down-right fromCenter test (BaseTool.test.ts:196-207) still yields x=0,y=20,width=100,height=60 (it does, since those deltas are already positive).
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/tools/BaseTool.ts`
- **Test:** In BaseTool.test.ts getRectFromPoints describe: add a case for up-left Alt-drag: testGetRectFromPoints({x:100,y:100},{x:50,y:60},false,true) should return {x:50,y:60,width:100,height:80} (center stays at 100,100). Also add a RectangleTool integration test: onPointerDown at (100,100) with a preceding-state, onPointerUp with worldPosition (50,60) and altKey:true (createMockPointerEvent), then assert a rectangle node was added to sceneGraph and its width/height are 100/80.

#### `F050` · high · coordinate-space

**Location:** `packages/core/src/tools/SelectionTool.ts:328`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Move drag adds the world-space delta directly to a node's local transform.position, so children of scaled/rotated groups move at the wrong speed/direction and snap against the wrong grid.

- **Root cause:** In onPointerMove moving branch, `const delta = vec2.subtract(worldPos, this.startPoint)` is a world-space delta, and it is added directly to `startPos` (=node.transform.position, which is LOCAL for a nested node) at line 328: `const rawPos = vec2.add(startPos, delta)`. For children of scaled/rotated groups the local frame differs from world, so the node moves at the wrong speed/direction. The arrow-nudge path (lines 511-523) has the identical defect: `vec2.add(node.transform.position, delta)` with a world-space arrow delta. Additionally snapNodePosition computes visual edges from centerPos as if it were world-space, so snapping is also wrong for nested nodes.
- **Fix:** Convert the world delta into each node's parent-local frame using the linear part (rotation+scale, no translation) of the parent world transform, mirroring DirectSelectionTool.getNodeLinearMatrix. In the moving loop: for each node, if node.parent, compute `const pw = this.context.sceneGraph.getWorldTransform(node.parent); const lin = { a: pw.a, b: pw.b, c: pw.c, d: pw.d, tx: 0, ty: 0 }; const inv = mat3.invert(lin); const localDelta = inv ? mat3.transformPoint(inv, worldDelta) : worldDelta;` else localDelta=worldDelta; then `rawPos = vec2.add(startPos, localDelta)`. Apply the same conversion in the ArrowKey nudge loop before adding delta. Root nodes (parent null) keep localDelta===worldDelta, so all existing move/nudge tests (which use root nodes) are unaffected. Note in a comment that snapNodePosition still assumes world-space for nested nodes (a deeper, separate limitation) — leave that out of scope.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/tools/SelectionTool.ts`
- **Test:** In SelectionTool.test.ts: create a group with transform.scale={x:2,y:2}, add a child rect at local (0,0), enter the group, select the child, pointerDown then pointerMove by world (dx,dy)=(40,20), assert child.transform.position moved by local (20,10) (i.e., worldDelta/scale). Add an analogous nudge test with a rotated parent asserting the local-axis mapping.
- **Notes:** Coordinate with F052 (both touch the move/nudge loops) and F054 (same rotate-into-local-frame technique).

#### `F051` · high · data-corruption

**Location:** `packages/core/src/tools/SelectionTool.ts:347`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** A mere click on a node (no drag) fires onTransformComplete('move'), inserting spurious position keyframes into the animation timeline.

- **Root cause:** onPointerDown always sets mode='moving' and populates moveStartPositions for any node click (lines 263-276). onPointerUp gates the completion branch only on `mode==='moving' && moveStartPositions.size>0` (line 347), which is true for a zero-movement click, so it calls autoReparentAfterMove + onTransformComplete(selectedIds,'move'). In useCanvasTools.ts onTransformComplete, shouldKf returns true when autoKeyframe is ON or the property already has a track (lines 231-236), so a click on an animated node at frame N inserts transform.position.x/y keyframes freezing the interpolated value. The tool already sets moveUndoPushed only on first real move (line 318-321) but never uses it to gate completion. The resizing/rotating branches (lines 352-359) have the same flaw: clicking a handle or rotation zone without dragging fires onTransformComplete('resize'/'rotate') (and, unlike move, even pushes an undo snapshot on pointerDown at lines 159/186).
- **Fix:** Gate each completion branch on actual movement. For moving: change the condition to `if (this.mode==='moving' && this.moveUndoPushed)` (moveUndoPushed is only set when a real pointerMove occurs) — this also stops the F004 reparent-on-click. Add a `private dragMoved = false;` field: set it false in onPointerDown's resize and rotation start branches (near lines 187 and 160), and set it true at the top of the resizing and rotating handling in onPointerMove (lines 306-314). In onPointerUp, still reset resizeState/rotationState unconditionally, but only call onTransformComplete('resize') / ('rotate') when this.dragMoved is true. Existing resize/rotate tests all include a pointerMove, so dragMoved is true and they still fire; the 'return to idle after resize/rotate completes' tests (down+up, no move) only assert mode, which still resets. The mock context omits onTransformComplete, so no existing test asserts it.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/tools/SelectionTool.ts`
- **Test:** In SelectionTool.test.ts, extend the mock context with an onTransformComplete spy (vi.fn). Test A: pointerDown+pointerUp on a selected node with no pointerMove -> expect spy NOT called. Test B: pointerDown+pointerMove(displacement)+pointerUp -> expect spy called once with 'move'. Test C: click a resize handle (down+up, no move) -> spy NOT called with 'resize'.
- **Notes:** This is the enabling fix for F004's no-movement half. Confirmed the mock ToolContext has no onTransformComplete, so gating is safe for the current suite.

#### `F052` · high · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/tools/SelectionTool.ts:488`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Ctrl+A selects every node including descendants of groups, so a subsequent drag or arrow-nudge moves nested children twice (parent delta plus own delta).

- **Root cause:** Ctrl+A handler (lines 483-493) does `this.context.sceneGraph.traverse((node)=>allIds.push(node.id))`, selecting every node including group descendants. The move loop (lines 325-337) and nudge loop (lines 511-523) then iterate all selected ids and add the delta to each node's transform.position. Because a child's world position is the sum of its ancestors' local positions, a node whose d ancestors are all selected is displaced (d+1)x per drag/nudge (linear, not exponential as one might assume). The store-level selectAll (editorStore.ts:1686) is likewise descendant-inclusive and feeds the same loops, so fixing only Ctrl+A would not cover the web path.
- **Fix:** Add a private helper `filterTopLevelSelected(ids: Set<string>): string[]` that drops any id whose ancestor chain (walk node.parent via sceneGraph.getNode) contains another id in the set. Apply it where the move/nudge sets are built so double-application is impossible regardless of how the selection was formed: (a) in onPointerDown when populating moveStartPositions, iterate the filtered set instead of currentSelectedIds; (b) in the ArrowKey nudge loop, iterate the filtered set. Also recommended for parity: apply the same filter when building resize/rotate node sets (captureNodeStates input and initialRotations) so a selected group+child doesn't double-scale/double-rotate. Optionally also make the core Ctrl+A select only root-level nodes, but the loop-level filter is the robust fix and keeps the existing 'select all on Ctrl+A' test (two root rects -> size 2) passing.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/tools/SelectionTool.ts`
- **Test:** In SelectionTool.test.ts: create a group with a child rect at local (10,0); select BOTH group and child (setSelectedIds([group,child])); nudge ArrowRight by 1; assert the child's WORLD position advanced by exactly 1 (group.position.x+=1, child.position.x unchanged) rather than 2. Add a drag variant asserting the same.
- **Notes:** Coordinate with F050 since both edit the move/nudge loops. The linear (d+1)x multiplier refinement from the reviewer is correct; not exponential.

#### `F053` · high · feature-bypass

**Location:** `packages/core/src/tools/SelectionTool.ts:555`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Locked nodes are fully selectable, movable, resizable, rotatable, and deletable via the canvas — node.locked is never checked by SelectionTool or DirectSelectionTool.

- **Root cause:** hitTest (551-562) and getNodesInRect (773-802) both traverse via traverseVisible and never consult node.locked; the move/resize/rotate loops and the Delete handler (lines 395-405, which loops selectedIds and calls removeNode) also ignore it. So a locked node is fully selectable, movable, resizable, rotatable, and deletable from the canvas. EraserTool.ts:376 explicitly does `if (node.locked) return;`, confirming locked is meant to protect nodes from canvas edits.
- **Fix:** In SelectionTool: (1) in hitTest's traverseVisible callback, `if (node.locked) return;` before isPointInNode so clicks pass through locked nodes; (2) in getNodesInRect's traverseVisible callback, skip locked nodes so marquee ignores them; (3) in onPointerDown when populating moveStartPositions, skip nodes whose getNode(id).locked is true so a mixed selection drag never moves a locked node; (4) in captureNodeStates and the nudge/rotate loops, skip locked nodes; (5) in the Delete/Backspace handler, only removeNode ids whose node is not locked, and adjust selection accordingly (keep locked ids selected or clear only removed ones). For full coverage the reviewer also flags DirectSelectionTool (hitTestNode/getPathNodes/getImageNodes editing locked paths) — add the same node.locked skips there in a follow-up. No existing test locks a node then expects it selectable, so the suite is unaffected.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/tools/SelectionTool.ts`, `packages/core/src/tools/DirectSelectionTool.ts`
- **Test:** In SelectionTool.test.ts: add a locked rectangle (locked:true); click its center -> assert it is NOT selected (selection empty / click-through). Then setSelectedIds([lockedId]) and press Delete -> assert the node still exists in the scene graph.
- **Notes:** Skipping locked nodes in hitTest makes clicks pass through them, matching EraserTool's behavior; acceptable and un-tested currently.

#### `F054` · high · coordinate-space

**Location:** `packages/core/src/tools/SelectionTool.ts:1102`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Resizing a rotated shape applies the raw world-space drag delta to the un-rotated bounds, so handles resize along the wrong axis (or not at all).

- **Root cause:** For a single rotated node, getSelectionBoundsForDisplay returns un-rotated bounds + rotation, and TransformHandles.hitTest inverse-rotates the click so the visually-rotated handle can be grabbed. But performResize (1094-1145) computes `delta = vec2.subtract(worldPos, this.startPoint)` in WORLD axes and feeds it to calculateNewBounds, which adds delta.x to width and delta.y to height of the un-rotated rect (lines 1298-1333). The rotation is never applied to the delta, so a 90deg-rotated rectangle's visual 'right' handle (pointing up in world) does width += delta.x = 0 for a vertical drag; at 180deg the resize direction inverts. resizeState never stores the rotation angle.
- **Fix:** Store rotation in the resize state and rotate the drag delta into the bounds' un-rotated frame, then rotate the resulting position back. (1) Add `rotation: number` to the ResizeState interface and set it from displayResult when creating resizeState in onPointerDown (line 189-193). (2) In performResize, compute `const rad = this.resizeState.rotation * Math.PI/180; const worldDelta = vec2.subtract(worldPos, this.startPoint); const delta = rad ? vec2.rotate(worldDelta, -rad) : worldDelta;` and pass `delta` to calculateNewBounds. (3) After computing the per-node `newWorldPosition` (which is now in the un-rotated bounds frame), rotate it back around the initial bounds center: `if (rad) { const c = initialBounds.center; newWorldPosition = { x: c.x + Math.cos(rad)*(newWorldPosition.x-c.x) - Math.sin(rad)*(newWorldPosition.y-c.y), y: c.y + Math.sin(rad)*(newWorldPosition.x-c.x) + Math.cos(rad)*(newWorldPosition.y-c.y) }; }` before converting through parentWorldTransform inverse. This preserves the fixed-anchor-corner property (calculateNewBounds keeps the opposite corner fixed in local frame; rotating around the original center maps it back to its original world position). rotation=0 (all existing single-node tests and every multi-selection) is identity, so the suite is unaffected.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/tools/SelectionTool.ts`
- **Test:** In SelectionTool.test.ts: create a 100x100 rect centered at (100,100) with transform.rotation=90; select it; grab the visually-repositioned corner handle (compute screen pos via the same inverse-rotation the existing 'preserve initial rotation offset' test uses) and drag outward along the visual axis; assert the rect's width/height grew along its own local axis (the expected dimension changes, the perpendicular one does not) and the opposite corner's world position is unchanged.
- **Notes:** vec2.rotate(v, radians) exists in math.ts. Multi-selection resize uses rotation 0 and is unaffected. The math is sound because the anchor corner is fixed in the local frame and rotated back around the original rotation center.

#### `F055` · high · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/tools/WeightPaintTool.ts:230`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Weight paint brush compares the world-space cursor against node-LOCAL tessellated vertices, so painting lands at the wrong location for any bound node not at the world origin.

- **Root cause:** WeightPaintTool.paintAtWorldPosition (WeightPaintTool.ts:227,230) fetches vertices via context.getTessellatedVertices(boundNodeId), which resolves to ShapeRenderer.getTessellatedVertices (ShapeRenderer.ts:3568-3572) returning cached.vertices — node-LOCAL tessellation coordinates (renderRectangle builds createRectanglePath(-node.width\*anchor.x, ...) at ShapeRenderer.ts:1750-1756 and the vertex shader applies u_model separately). It then passes those local coords straight to paintAtPositionWithVertices(worldX, worldY, vertexPositions) (line 230), whose distance test computes dx = vx - worldX (lines 271-272) as if vx/vy were world coordinates. For a 100x100 rect bound at position (100,100) (as in the test fixture, WeightPaintTool.test.ts:14), local verts span ~±50 around origin, so clicking the visible shape at world (100,100) finds nothing within brushRadius (~30) and paints nothing; clicking empty canvas near (0,0) paints. editorStore.bindMeshToBones (apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts:988-996) explicitly transforms these same local vertices to world before auto-weighting, confirming the vertices are local. There are no other (non-test) callers of paintAtPositionWithVertices, so the tool is self-contained and always mis-targets for non-origin nodes.
- **Fix:** In paintAtWorldPosition, before calling paintAtPositionWithVertices, transform the cached LOCAL vertices into world space using the node's world matrix, preserving paintAtPositionWithVertices' documented 'world positions' contract. Concretely: after obtaining vertexPositions, compute const m = this.context.sceneGraph.getWorldTransform(this.boundNodeId); build a new Float32Array worldVerts of the same length where for each i: lx=vertexPositions[i*2], ly=vertexPositions[i*2+1]; worldVerts[i*2]=m.a*lx+m.c*ly+m.tx; worldVerts[i*2+1]=m.b*lx+m.d*ly+m.ty; then call paintAtPositionWithVertices(worldX, worldY, worldVerts). (Matches the transform in editorStore.bindMeshToBones lines 992-995 and PointMagnetTool's inverse-transform approach.) Note: brushRadius stays in world units so no radius scaling is needed with this forward-transform approach. Leave paintAtPositionWithVertices unchanged so any future UI caller passing true world vertices still works.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/tools/WeightPaintTool.ts`
- **Test:** In WeightPaintTool.test.ts: create the bound rect at position (100,100); set context.getTessellatedVertices = () => new Float32Array([-50,-50, 50,-50, -50,50, 50,50]) (local corners). Activate, set brushRadius 30. onPointerDown at worldPosition (150,150) (world position of local corner (50,50)) and assert the corresponding vertex's weight for the active bone changed; then in a fresh tool/skin, paint at world (0,0) and assert NO vertex weight changed (proving world targeting, not local).
