### Animation engine

#### `F030` · high · data-loss

**Location:** `packages/animation/src/Timeline.ts:167`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** moveKeyframe silently deletes any pre-existing keyframe at the destination time, so dragging a keyframe across another one in the timeline permanently destroys it.

- **Root cause:** packages/animation/src/Timeline.ts moveKeyframe() lines 159-172: after removing the moved keyframe and setting keyframe.time = newTime, it re-inserts with `if (insertIndex < len && track.keyframes[insertIndex].time === newTime) { track.keyframes[insertIndex] = keyframe; }` — this OVERWRITES (destroys) a pre-existing different keyframe sitting at newTime. The dope-sheet drag path proves reachability: apps/web/src/components/layout/Timeline.tsx handleKeyframePointerMove (lines 300-305) computes an incremental deltaFrames and calls moveSelectedKeyframes -> KeyframeManager.moveKeyframes -> moveKf on each selected keyframe. KeyframeManager.moveKeyframes (lines 87-113) sorts to avoid collisions only AMONG the selected set; it gives no protection against colliding with a NON-selected keyframe already on the same track, so dragging one keyframe onto another silently deletes the stationary one.
- **Fix:** Make moveKeyframe non-destructive: before mutating, if a DIFFERENT keyframe already occupies newTime, refuse the move. Rewrite Timeline.ts moveKeyframe as: find keyframe by id (return false if missing); if keyframe.time === newTime return true (no-op); `const occupied = track.keyframes.find(kf => kf.time === newTime && kf.id !== keyframeId); if (occupied) return false;` then removeKeyframe, set keyframe.time = newTime, binarySearch insertIndex, and always splice-insert (the occupied case is now impossible so drop the overwrite branch entirely). This 'blocks/skips' onto an occupied slot rather than destroying it (a fast drag with delta>=2 still jumps over the obstacle). Do NOT change addKeyframe's same-time replace (that replace is intentional for setting a value at a frame).
- **Files:** `packages/animation/src/Timeline.ts`
- **Test:** In packages/animation/src/Timeline.test.ts moveKeyframe describe: build a track with keyframes at 0,10,20; capture the id+value of the time-10 keyframe; call moveKeyframe(track, idOfTime0Kf, 10); assert it returns false, track.keyframes.length is still 3, and the original time-10 keyframe (matched by id) is unchanged. Add a second assertion that moving to an unoccupied time (e.g. 15) still succeeds and returns true.
- **Notes:** Existing moveKeyframe tests only move onto unoccupied times (15, 25) so they keep passing. Alternative UX (swap/bounce or defer-collision-to-pointer-up) is nicer but a larger change; blocking is the minimal correct data-loss fix. No hard dependency on other findings.

### Export (Lottie/PNG/sprite)

#### `F056` · high · correctness

**Location:** `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieConverter.ts:73`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Layers get ip:0/op:duration while the animation uses ip:startFrame/op:endFrame, so any export with startFrame > 0 produces a completely blank Lottie.

- **Root cause:** lottieExporter.ts:49 computes duration = endFrame - startFrame and passes it to nodeToLottieLayer (line 64). nodeToLottieLayer (lottieConverter.ts:73-74) hardcodes ip:0, op:duration, st:0. The composition (lottieExporter.ts:74-75) uses ip:startFrame, op:endFrame. Keyframe times are absolute Quar frames and st=0, so keyframes still play at their absolute comp frames correctly, but the layer visibility window is [0, duration) = [0, endFrame-startFrame) while the composition plays [startFrame, endFrame). When startFrame>0 the layer's op (endFrame-startFrame) is less than endFrame, so the layer disappears for the final `startFrame` frames of the export. The headline 'completely blank' is an overstatement — it is a blank TAIL of length startFrame, not a fully blank export (only fully blank when startFrame >= endFrame-startFrame).
- **Fix:** Give nodeToLottieLayer the real composition window instead of a raw duration. Minimal-diff option: append an optional param startFrame (default 0) to nodeToLottieLayer(node, timeline, layerIndex, canvasH, duration, nodeResolver, startFrame=0) and set the layer to ip: startFrame, op: startFrame + duration, keep st: 0. In lottieExporter.ts:64 pass startFrame as the new 7th argument (resolver stays 6th). This yields layer ip=startFrame, op=endFrame with st=0, matching the composition window; absolute keyframe times remain correct. Do NOT set st=startFrame (would double-shift absolute keyframes). Existing test calls that pass only 5 args keep ip=0/op=duration behavior unchanged.
- **Files:** `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieConverter.ts`, `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieExporter.ts`, `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieExporter.test.ts`
- **Test:** In lottieExporter.test.ts, call exportToLottieJson with a static rectangle and options {startFrame:30, endFrame:90}; assert animation.ip===30, animation.op===90, and every layer has ip===30 and op===90 (currently layers would be ip:0/op:60, leaving comp frames 60..90 blank).
- **Notes:** Underlying defect is real; only the 'completely blank' impact wording is overstated (actual = blank tail of length startFrame). The reviewer's alternative (shift keyframes by -startFrame, use ip:0/op:duration everywhere) is more invasive and unnecessary given st=0 + absolute keyframes already work.

#### `F057` · high · correctness

**Location:** `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieConverter.ts:277`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Group children have their parent-local position flipped with canvasH, displacing every group child by the full canvas height.

- **Root cause:** groupToLottieShapes (lottieConverter.ts:277) emits each child's shape-group ('gr') transform position as k:[childNode.transform.position.x, canvasH - childNode.transform.position.y]. This 'tr' is in the group LAYER's local space, and the group layer is already placed at flipY(group position) by buildLottieTransform with positive scale (no axis reflection). createGroupNode (SceneGraph.ts:43-56) uses createDefaultTransform so a group made by groupSelection sits at (0,0) while children keep world coords. Net comp-Y of a child = layer_p.y + tr_p.y = (canvasH - groupY) + (canvasH - childY) = 2\*canvasH - childY for groupY=0 — a full canvas height too low (typically off-canvas). Correct local Y conversion for a child is y -> -y (verified: layer applies group offset + Y-flip, child tr must supply child-relative Lottie-local offset, which for a Y-up world child at origin group is [x, -y]).
- **Fix:** Change lottieConverter.ts:277 from k:[childNode.transform.position.x, canvasH - childNode.transform.position.y] to k:[childNode.transform.position.x, -childNode.transform.position.y]. Rotation on line 279 already correctly negates (-childNode.transform.rotation), so leave it. canvasH is then unused by that expression but is still needed for recursive nodeToLottieShapes calls, so keep the param.
- **Files:** `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieConverter.ts`, `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieConverter.test.ts`
- **Test:** Add a groupToLottieShapes test with a resolver returning one visible rectangle child at transform.position {x:100,y:200}; assert the child 'gr' item's trailing 'tr'.p.k === [100, -200] (buggy output with CANVAS_H=500 would be [100, 300]). Existing tests only cover empty groups.
- **Notes:** The line-277 position fix is independent. Grouped PATH children additionally need F058's geometry Y-negation to render fully correctly (they share pathPointsToLottieVertices), so full grouped-path fidelity depends on F058; grouped rect/ellipse children are unaffected by F059 because the child 'gr' transform carries no erroneous anchor.

#### `F058` · high · correctness

**Location:** `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieConverter.ts:318`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Local shape geometry is never Y-flipped, so exported paths, polygons, and stars render vertically mirrored about their anchor.

- **Root cause:** pathPointsToLottieVertices (lottieConverter.ts:318,322,329) pushes vertex and handle Y unchanged; the comment at 305-307 wrongly assumes the layer transform Y-flips geometry. The layer uses positive scale (scaleTo100) which does NOT reflect the Y axis — only the position translation is Y-flipped and rotation negated. I proved that to reproduce the Quar Y-up->Lottie Y-down reflection with positive scale + negated rotation + Y-flipped position, the LOCAL geometry must be Y-negated (L' = (x, -y)). PathNode geometry (used at lines 191 and 202 for subpaths) is therefore rendered mirrored about the node origin; both vertex Y and relative handle Y are wrong. Polygons/stars are NOT affected: generatePolygonPoints (line 523) starts at -π/2 while Quar-native createPolygonPath (pathUtils.ts:760) starts at +π/2, so it already emits the Y-negated (Lottie-down) geometry — verified identical outline. Because polygonToLottieShapes feeds generatePolygonPoints THROUGH the same pathPointsToLottieVertices, negating unconditionally inside that shared function (as the reviewer's suggested fix says to do 'and in generatePolygonPoints output') would double-negate polygons and break them.
- **Fix:** Apply the Y-negation ONLY to real paths, not polygons. Add an optional param negateY:boolean=false to pathPointsToLottieVertices; when true, push v as [x, -y], in-handle as [handleIn.x - x, -(handleIn.y - y)], out-handle as [handleOut.x - x, -(handleOut.y - y)] (zero handles stay [0,0]). Call it with negateY=true from pathToLottieShapes for both the primary path (line 191) and subpaths (line 202). Leave polygonToLottieShapes (line 232) calling it with the default false so generatePolygonPoints output is untouched. Do NOT modify generatePolygonPoints (it is already correct) despite the reviewer's contradictory phrasing.
- **Files:** `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieConverter.ts`, `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieConverter.test.ts`
- **Test:** Add a pathToLottieShapes test: path with point {position:{x:0,y:50}, handleOut:{x:10,y:70}} and a second point; assert the emitted sh vertex v[0]===[0,-50] and out-handle o[0]===[10,-20] (Y negated). Add a regression assertion that polygonToLottieShapes on a hexagon still yields first vertex ≈ [0,-radius] (unchanged, proving no double-negation). Keep existing pathPointsToLottieVertices direct-call tests green by relying on the negateY default of false.
- **Notes:** Reviewer's suggested fix is partly wrong: it says also negate in generatePolygonPoints/the shared function, which would break polygons. The surgical per-path flag avoids that. Handle offsets only need their Y component negated (relative-offset math), not the whole handle.

#### `F059` · high · correctness

**Location:** `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieConverter.ts:472`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Layer anchor is set to [w*ax, h*ay] while rect/ellipse shapes are emitted centered at local [0,0], displacing every rectangle by half its size and every ellipse by its radius in the exported Lottie.

- **Root cause:** buildLottieTransform (lottieConverter.ts:461-472) sets layer anchor a=[width*anchor.x, height*anchor.y] (or radiusX*2*ax, radiusY*2*ay for ellipse), but rectangleToLottieShapes (line 124) and ellipseToLottieShapes (line 159) emit the primitive at local p=[0,0]. Lottie renders comp = position + R*S*(local - anchor); with local center [0,0] and anchor [w/2,h/2] the rect center lands at position-(w/2,h/2) and rotation orbits the shape corner. Verified against Quar native: renderRectangle (ShapeRenderer.ts:1750-1756) builds the rect at (-w*ax,-h*ay,w,h) so transform.position is the pivot/local origin and (anchor 0.5) the center; renderEllipse (line 1833) uses createEllipsePath(0,0,rx,ry) so the ellipse is always centered on the pivot regardless of anchor. Thus rects are displaced by (w/2,h/2)\*... (i.e. (w(0.5), h(0.5)) for anchor 0.5) and ellipses by (rx,ry).
- **Fix:** The Quar pivot is the local origin, which maps to the Lottie position, so the layer anchor must be [0,0], and any anchor-dependent geometry offset belongs in the shape's local p. In buildLottieTransform, set a:{a:0,k:[0,0]} and remove the width/height/radius-based anchorX/anchorY computation. In rectangleToLottieShapes set rect.p.k = [width*(0.5-anchor.x), -height*(0.5-anchor.y)] (rect center relative to pivot, Y-negated; = [0,0] for anchor 0.5) using node.transform.anchor (default {x:0.5,y:0.5}). In ellipseToLottieShapes keep ellipse.p.k=[0,0] (ellipse geometry is always pivot-centered in Quar). Polygons/paths already have anchor [0,0] (no width/height/radiusX) so they are unaffected.
- **Files:** `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieConverter.ts`, `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieConverter.test.ts`
- **Test:** Update the existing 'anchor is computed from node dimensions' test (lottieConverter.test.ts:903-908) to expect t.a.k===[0,0]. Add: (a) rectangleToLottieShapes with anchor {x:0.5,y:0.5} → rc.p.k===[0,0]; with anchor {x:0,y:0} on a 100x50 rect → rc.p.k===[50,-25] and buildLottieTransform a.k===[0,0]; (b) ellipseToLottieShapes → el.p.k===[0,0] and buildLottieTransform a.k===[0,0] for a radiusX/radiusY node.
- **Notes:** Also fixes the rotation-orbits-corner symptom. Note the Quar anchor semantics differ between rect (geometry offset by -w\*ax) and ellipse (always centered) — the fix accounts for both. This touches buildLottieTransform, same function as F060 but different lines; can be implemented together.

#### `F060` · high · correctness

**Location:** `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieConverter.ts:481`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Animated rotation keyframe values are not negated, so keyframed rotation plays in the opposite direction (and static single-keyframe rotation is un-negated too).

- **Root cause:** buildLottieTransform (lottieConverter.ts:481) calls trackToLottieAnimated(rotTrack, -transform.rotation). trackToLottieAnimated (lottieKeyframes.ts:77-98) applies its third `transform` arg (defaulting to VALUE_TRANSFORMS.identity) to keyframe values, and only uses the second arg as the default when NO track/keyframes exist. So the negation is applied only to the static default: with a rotation track the keyframe values pass through identity un-negated (even a single-keyframe track at line 87 emits transform(kf.value)=value). Static rotation exports r=-θ (test line 506-510) but keyframed rotation exports +θ, so animations play mirrored and a static->animated switch flips sign. The negation convention is confirmed by position (flipY applied to every keyframe via positionTracksToLottie), the line-434 comment, and the group-child static case at line 279.
- **Fix:** Change line 481 to r: trackToLottieAnimated(rotTrack, transform.rotation, (v) => -v). Passing defaultValue=transform.rotation with transform=(v)=>-v yields -transform.rotation for the no-track case (unchanged) and negates every keyframe value (single and multi) for animated tracks. No tangent changes needed — cubic-bezier easing y-values are normalized progress and remain valid when both s and e are negated.
- **Files:** `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieConverter.ts`, `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieConverter.test.ts`
- **Test:** Add a buildLottieTransform test with a transform.rotation track of keyframes [{t:0,value:0},{t:30,value:90}]; assert t.r.a===1 and the first keyframe's s===[-0]/e===[-90] (values negated). Add a single-keyframe rotation track value 45 → t.r.k===-45. Existing static test (r=-45) and the animated-flag test (r.a===1) remain green.
- **Notes:** One-line fix. Shares buildLottieTransform with F059 but independent lines.

#### `F061` · high · correctness

**Location:** `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieKeyframes.ts:124`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** F195  
**Finding:** All named easing presets (every option in the Timeline easing menu) export as hold keyframes, turning smooth animation into stepped jumps.

- **Root cause:** quarKeyframeToLottie (lottieKeyframes.ts:118-125) derives the segment easing via quarEasingToLottieTangents -> easingToBezierPoints (Easing.ts:449-462), which returns null for EVERY named string easing except 'linear'. On a null result the single-value path sets result.h = 1 (a literal hold, line 124). The Timeline easing preset menu (apps/web/src/components/layout/Timeline.tsx:17-25) stores its 8 presets as named strings — 'linear','easeInCubic','easeOutCubic','easeInOutCubic','easeInBack','easeOutBack','easeOutBounce','easeOutElastic' — so all 7 non-linear presets export as HOLD on single-value tracks (rotation via lottieConverter.ts:481, opacity :490, cornerRadius :126, stroke width :408). The multi-value path positionTracksToLottie (lines 180-184) hits the same null trigger but has a different failure mode: it sets neither h nor i/o, so the renderer falls back to default/linear interpolation and the easing is silently dropped. bakeTrackToLinearKeyframes exists but is wired into neither path (grep: no non-test callers). Note: the intended CSS-style easings easeInCubic/easeOutCubic/easeInOutCubic and easeInBack/easeOutBack are all perfectly cubic-bezier representable, so exporting them as hold is a genuine correctness loss, not a necessary approximation.
- **Fix:** Two-part fix, both in lottieKeyframes.ts. (1) MAPPING (fixes the monotonic + back families, i.e. 5 of the 7 broken menu presets): add a module-level constant NAMED_EASING_BEZIER: Partial<Record<EasingType,[number,number,number,number]>> mapping the single-cubic-representable Penner easings to their standard easings.net control points — quad/cubic/quart/quint/sine/expo/circ in in/out/inOut variants, plus easeInBack [0.6,-0.28,0.735,0.045], easeOutBack [0.175,0.885,0.32,1.275], easeInOutBack [0.68,-0.55,0.265,1.55] (Lottie accepts tangent y outside 0..1 for overshoot). In quarEasingToLottieTangents, for string easings look up this map first and build tangents from it before delegating to easingToBezierPoints; leave easingToBezierPoints (and thus Easing.test.ts) untouched to avoid changing graph-editor/GraphEditorUtils behavior. This automatically fixes BOTH quarKeyframeToLottie and positionTracksToLottie because both call quarEasingToLottieTangents. (2) BAKING (fixes the remaining genuinely multi-oscillation easings — bounce, elastic, which stay null): wire bakeTrackToLinearKeyframes into the converter. In trackToLottieAnimated, if any keyframe.easing satisfies easingNeedsBaking, return { a:1, k: bakeTrackToLinearKeyframes(track, fps, transform) }. Add an analogous joint bake for positionTracksToLottie: when either X or Y track uses a baking easing, iterate integer frames over the union range and emit multi-dim linear keyframes (sampling each track per frame). bakeTrackToLinearKeyframes's fps parameter is currently unused (dead), so fps need NOT be threaded through lottieConverter for the loop to work — pass any value or drop the param. Also harden positionTracksToLottie lines 180-184 so the null-tangent branch never silently drops easing after mapping+baking are in place.
- **Files:** `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieKeyframes.ts`, `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieKeyframes.test.ts`
- **Test:** In lottieKeyframes.test.ts: (a) quarKeyframeToLottie with nextKf.easing 'easeInOutCubic' asserts result.i/result.o are the mapped bezier tangents and result.h is undefined (regression against the current h:1); (b) positionTracksToLottie with an X-and-Y track whose next keyframe uses 'easeOutCubic' asserts result.k[0].i/.o are set (non-linear) on both dimensions; (c) a track whose next keyframe uses 'easeOutBounce' produces a:1 with per-frame baked keyframes (k.length == lastTime-firstTime+1) instead of a single h:1 hold.
- **Notes:** Mapping alone is an S-effort, low-risk change that fixes the majority of the menu; the bake-wiring (esp. the joint X/Y position bake) is the part that makes this M. Baking depends on F195 — until bakeTrackToLinearKeyframes is made easing-aware, wiring it in would still emit linear for bounce/elastic. Baking increases keyframe count / .lottie file size, acceptable and standard for non-bezier easings. Do NOT modify easingToBezierPoints in Easing.ts: Easing.test.ts:466-468 asserts easeInQuad/easeInBounce/easeOutElastic return null and GraphEditorUtils relies on it.

### Fonts & text

#### `F032` · high · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/font/FontManager.ts:89`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** loadFontFromUrl and loadGoogleFont permanently cache a rejected promise on failure, so a single transient network error makes that font unloadable for the rest of the session.

- **Root cause:** In loadFontFromUrl (packages/core/src/font/FontManager.ts:78-91) and loadGoogleFont (lines 113-127) the async IIFE only calls this.loadingPromises.delete(key) on the success path (line 85 / line 121), AFTER opentype.parse succeeds. If fetch rejects or response.ok is false (line 80/116) the IIFE rejects and that delete is never reached, so the rejected promise stays registered in loadingPromises. The early-return guard (lines 75-76 / 110-111: `const loading = this.loadingPromises.get(key); if (loading) return loading;`) then hands that same rejected promise back on every subsequent call, making the font unloadable for the session. Reviewer's refinement is correct: removeFont (227-236) iterates [...this.fontCache.keys()] and only deletes loadingPromises entries whose key is ALSO in fontCache; a failed load never populates fontCache, so removeFont cannot clear the stale entry. Only dispose() (line 243, clears loadingPromises wholesale) or a page reload recovers, and dispose() has no callers. Confirmed reachable: App.tsx:19/24 call loadFontFromUrl and PropertiesPanel.tsx:2120/2215 call loadGoogleFont; re-selecting the same family in the dropdown re-enters loadGoogleFont and returns the cached rejected promise. loadFontFromBuffer is NOT affected because its parse is synchronous and throws before the loadingPromises.set at line 57 runs, so no rejected promise is ever stored there.
- **Fix:** In BOTH loadFontFromUrl and loadGoogleFont: remove the success-only `this.loadingPromises.delete(key)` line from inside the async IIFE (line 85 and line 121). Keep the fontCache.set / availableFonts.set writes (they must only run on success). After the existing `this.loadingPromises.set(key, promise)` (line 89 / 125), add a cleanup that runs on BOTH settle paths: `void promise.catch(() => {}).finally(() => this.loadingPromises.delete(key));`. The `.catch(() => {})` prevents an unhandled-rejection warning on the derived cleanup promise while the original `promise` returned to the caller still rejects normally. Net effect: after any failure the loadingPromises entry is cleared so the next loadFontFromUrl/loadGoogleFont call re-fetches. Do not remove the delete without adding the finally, or successful loads would leak a resolved entry (the F178 bug).
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/font/FontManager.ts`
- **Test:** Create packages/core/src/font/FontManager.test.ts. Mock opentype.js (`vi.mock('opentype.js', () => ({ default: { parse: vi.fn(() => ({ mock: 'font' })) } }))`) and stub global.fetch. Test: set fetch to reject once (or resolve {ok:false}), `await expect(fm.loadFontFromUrl('u','Roboto','google',400)).rejects.toThrow()`, then set fetch to resolve {ok:true, arrayBuffer: async()=>new ArrayBuffer(4)}, call loadFontFromUrl again with the same family/weight and assert it now RESOLVES to a font, that fetch was invoked a second time (stale promise cleared), and that fm.isLoading('Roboto') is false. Add the equivalent test for loadGoogleFont('Roboto', 400).

#### `F033` · high · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/font/textToShape.ts:57`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** F181  
**Finding:** convertTextToPath/convertTextToPathGroup misplace the converted paths: they ignore the anchor-based metric centering that renderText applies, and do not rotate/skew the center offset.

- **Root cause:** textToShape.ts computes the converted node's world placement as worldCenter = transform.position + geometryCenter*scale (convertTextToPath lines 56-58; convertTextToPathGroup lines 143-144), where geometryCenter = computeSubpathsBounds(result.subpaths) center. But ShapeRenderer.renderText (2119-2135) and renderTextWithOverride (4131-4147) place transform.position at the ANCHOR-based METRIC center: they translate the glyph geometry inside the world matrix by -(getTextBounds.x + width*anchor.x, getTextBounds.y + height\*anchor.y). The world matrix itself is mat3.compose(position, rotation, scale, anchor) (ShapeRenderer 1579-1584), whose linear part is R·S (math.ts compose: translate→rotate→scale→translate(-anchor); NOTE skew is not a compose parameter, so skew is never applied by the renderer). Net rendered position of a glyph vertex v = position + R·S·(v − anchoredMetricPoint − anchorFraction). The convert functions (a) never subtract the metric center anchoredMetricPoint, and (b) apply only component-wise scale, never the rotation R. So the converted path/group lands ≈ R·S·anchoredMetricPoint (~half the text width/height, e.g. ~28px x / ~8px y for 'Hello' 24px) away from the rendered text, and is additionally wrong whenever rotation is non-zero.
- **Fix:** In textToShape.ts import getTextBounds from './textMetrics'. In BOTH convertTextToPath and convertTextToPathGroup, after computing the geometry center (centerX/centerY, or overallCX/overallCY): (1) mb = getTextBounds(textNode.content, textNode.fontFamily, textNode.fontSize, textNode.lineHeight, textNode.letterSpacing, textNode.textAlign) — and also pass textNode.fontWeight as the new trailing arg once F181 lands, so the metric font matches the renderer's glyph font. (2) anchoredMetricX = mb.x + mb.width _ textNode.transform.anchor.x; anchoredMetricY = mb.y + mb.height _ textNode.transform.anchor.y. (3) offsetX = geometryCenterX − anchoredMetricX; offsetY = geometryCenterY − anchoredMetricY. (4) Apply the node's local linear transform matching mat3.compose (scale THEN rotate; do NOT apply skew): const sx = offsetX*textNode.transform.scale.x, sy = offsetY*textNode.transform.scale.y; const rad = textNode.transform.rotation*Math.PI/180; const wx = Math.cos(rad)*sx − Math.sin(rad)*sy; const wy = Math.sin(rad)*sx + Math.cos(rad)\*sy. (5) worldCenterX = textNode.transform.position.x + wx; worldCenterY = position.y + wy. Use this for both the single PathNode position (currently 57-58) and the group position (currently 143-144); the group's child positions (glyphCX−overallCX etc.) stay unchanged and remain exact because the group origin now sits at the rendered overall-geometry-center. The ~0.5px anchor-fraction residual (from compose's translate(-anchor)) cancels exactly for the single PathNode case (PathNode anchor is also 0.5,0.5) and is sub-pixel/negligible for the group case, so it can be ignored.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/font/textToShape.ts`, `packages/core/src/font/textToShape.test.ts`
- **Test:** In textToShape.test.ts add tests that let the functions run to completion: mock getFontOrFallback to return a truthy font, mock textToSubpaths (or supply a font whose glyphs yield a known single square subpath) so computeSubpathsBounds gives a known geometryCenter gc, and mock getTextBounds to return a known metric rect mb. With rotation 0, scale (1,1), anchor (0.5,0.5), assert the resulting node.transform.position === position + (gc − (mb.x+mb.width*0.5, mb.y+mb.height*0.5)). Add a rotation=90 case asserting the offset is rotated (proves R is applied). Add a group case asserting group.transform.position uses overallCenter with the same formula.
- **Notes:** Depends on F181 only for consistency: F033 must call getTextBounds exactly as renderText does. If F181 threads fontWeight into getTextBounds/renderText, F033 must pass textNode.fontWeight too; if F181 is not done first, F033 must call getTextBounds WITHOUT weight to still match renderText. Existing textToShape.test.ts cases mock getFontOrFallback→null and return early, so they are unaffected by this change.

### Rigging

#### `F062` · high · correctness

**Location:** `packages/rigging/src/ik.ts:351`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** positionsToRotations sets the chain-root bone's LOCAL rotation to its solved WORLD angle, ignoring the root bone's parent world rotation, so IK breaks for any rig nested under a rotated/scaled group or symbol instance.

- **Root cause:** In positionsToRotations (ik.ts:349-354), the root bone (i===0) gets localAngle = worldAngle, assuming the chain root's parent has zero world rotation. The world positions come from extractIKJoints via sceneGraph.getWorldTransform (ik.ts:397-406), which DOES include any parent group/symbol/bone transform, so positions[1]-positions[0] is a true world direction. When applyIKResult writes this as the bone's LOCAL rotation (ik.ts:428-433), the scene graph recomposes world = parentWorld \* local, adding the parent's rotation back in and pointing the chain off-target by the parent's world rotation. The single-bone early-return (ik.ts:120-136, line 132) has the identical defect: it returns the world angle as the local rotation. dynamicChain.ts applyChainToBones (lines 339-348) shows the correct pattern the IK code is missing: for the root bone read node.parent, get parent world transform, subtract atan2(parentWt.b, parentWt.a).
- **Fix:** Add optional field `rootParentWorldRotation?: number` to the IKJoint interface (ik.ts:23-29). In extractIKJoints, after building the joint array, compute it for joints[0]: read chain[0].parent; if set, wt=sceneGraph.getWorldTransform(parentId), rootParentWorldRotation = Math.atan2(wt.b, wt.a) \* (180/Math.PI); else 0; assign to joints[0].rootParentWorldRotation. In solveFABRIK, read const rootParentRot = joints[0]?.rootParentWorldRotation ?? 0. Pass rootParentRot into positionsToRotations (add a param) and use it for i===0: localAngle = normalizeAngle(worldAngle - rootParentRot). Also fix the single-bone branch (line 132) to return normalizeAngle(angle - rootParentRot) as the rotation (compute rootParentRot before that branch). Keep default 0 so all existing direct-solveFABRIK tests (which pass no rootParentWorldRotation) are unchanged. Use atan2(b,a) to match applyChainToBones (rotation only; non-uniform scale/skew remains an accepted edge case).
- **Files:** `packages/rigging/src/ik.ts`
- **Test:** In ik.test.ts, add a test: build a mock scene graph where a group/parent node is rotated 90deg and a 2-bone chain root is parented under it (parent supplied to the mock nodes map so getWorldTransform accumulates it). Run extractIKJoints -> solveFABRIK -> applyIKResult toward a world-space target; assert the solved root LOCAL rotation equals (desiredWorldAngle - 90) within tolerance, i.e. that the chain points at the target once the parent's 90deg is re-applied by the scene graph. Also add a single-bone variant asserting the same for the joints.length===1 path.
- **Notes:** Real and high-impact for any rig nested under a rotated group, symbol instance, or a chainDepth-limited chain whose root has a rotating parent bone. Child bones are already correct (their local = world[i]-world[i-1] cancels the shared parent offset); only the root is wrong, plus the single-bone branch.

#### `F063` · high · performance

**Location:** `packages/rigging/src/ik.ts:428`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** applyIKResult unconditionally calls updateNode on every bone every RAF frame, causing a permanent 60fps React re-render storm across the whole UI whenever any IK chain exists

- **Root cause:** applyIKResult (ik.ts:413-435) calls sceneGraph.updateNode(boneId, {transform:{...,rotation:clamped}}) for every bone with no check whether the value changed. SceneGraph.updateNode (packages/core/src/SceneGraph.ts:200-204) invalidates the world transform and emits {type:'nodeChanged'} unconditionally on every call. evaluateIKChains is invoked inside the Canvas requestAnimationFrame render loop (apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx:574-579) every frame whenever ikChains.length>0 && !isPlaying, and also from usePlayback.ts:29-31/49-51. So while any enabled IK chain exists in the normal stopped rigging-edit state, every bone re-emits nodeChanged ~60x/sec even when the target has not moved and the pose is stable, driving continuous React re-renders (Canvas, Timeline, LayerPanel) with full scene-graph traversals.
- **Fix:** In applyIKResult, after computing `clamped`, guard the write: `if (Math.abs(clamped - bone.transform.rotation) < 1e-4) continue;` before calling updateNode. This makes a stable IK pose emit zero nodeChanged events per frame while still updating (and emitting) when the target actually moves. Optionally (broader, separate change) add a dirty check in SceneGraph.updateNode to skip emit when no field changed, but the applyIKResult epsilon guard is the targeted fix and sufficient.
- **Files:** `packages/rigging/src/ik.ts`
- **Test:** In ik.test.ts applyIKResult describe: create a bone whose transform.rotation already equals the result's rotation; wrap sceneGraph.updateNode with a spy/counter; call applyIKResult and assert updateNode was NOT called (count 0). Then call with a different rotation and assert it WAS called (count 1). This proves the no-op guard.
- **Notes:** Real. Under React 18 automatic batching the per-bone emits coalesce to ~one re-render per subscriber per frame (not per bone), but it is still a permanent ~60fps re-render storm; the guard eliminates it entirely when the pose is unchanged.

#### `F064` · high · correctness

**Location:** `packages/rigging/src/smartBones.ts:162`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** When the driver value is below the first morph target, evaluateSmartBoneAction applies that target's offsets at FULL strength instead of scaling them, so a single-target Smart Bone action deforms the mesh permanently regardless of bone rotation.

- **Root cause:** packages/rigging/src/smartBones.ts lines 156-162: in evaluateSmartBoneAction the `else if (!lower)` branch (driver value below the smallest target's driverValue) sets `offsets = (upper!.offsets[nodeId] ?? []).map(...)` — the FULL first-target offset, not a scaled/ramped one. The inline comment 'Before first target — use first target scaled by position' documents an intended ramp-from-zero that was never implemented. currentDriverVal at line 138-139 is effectively clamp(driverValue, rangeMin, rangeMax); at rest (bone rotation 0, driver range [0,90]) it is 0, and with a single target at driverValue=90 the loop at 145-154 leaves lower=null, upper=target@90, so the full morph is applied over the entire [0,90) region including the rest pose. The past-last-target clamp (163-165, lower===upper) is correct and must stay. Confirmed reachable via apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx:634 evaluateSmartBones in the render loop.
- **Fix:** In the `else if (!lower)` branch, ramp from the driver's rangeMin (implicit zero rest) up to the first (upper) target: `const denom = upper.driverValue - action.driver.rangeMin; const t = denom !== 0 ? (currentDriverVal - action.driver.rangeMin) / denom : 1; offsets = interpolateMorphOffsets([], upper.offsets[nodeId] ?? [], t);`. interpolateMorphOffsets already clamps t via its `t<=0`/`t>=1` guards and treats the empty A array as zero displacement, so this yields zero at rangeMin and full at the target. The `denom !== 0` guard avoids NaN when the first target sits at rangeMin (also protects degenerate inverted-range cases). Leave the lower===upper / past-last-target branch (163-165) unchanged. Do NOT touch computeBlendWeight or the two-target interpolation branch — those are correct and covered by existing passing tests.
- **Files:** `packages/rigging/src/smartBones.ts`, `packages/rigging/src/smartBones.test.ts`
- **Test:** In smartBones.test.ts under `describe('evaluateSmartBoneAction')`, add cases for a single target at driverValue=90 with driver range [0,90] and nodeVertexCounts mesh-1=4: (a) bone rotation 0 -> assert result offsets[0] and offsets[1] are ~0 (mesh undeformed at rest — fails before fix, which returns 10/20); (b) bone rotation 45 -> assert offsets[0]~5, offsets[1]~10 (half strength ramp); (c) bone rotation 90 -> assert offsets[0]~10, offsets[1]~20 (existing full-strength behavior preserved).
- **Notes:** Behavior change to morph semantics below the first target, but existing tests are unaffected: 'evaluates single target at full blend' uses rotation=90 (full, unchanged) and 'interpolates between two targets' has an explicit target at driverValue=0 so lower is non-null and never hits the patched branch.

### SVG import/export

#### `F043` · high · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgConverter.ts:424`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Group transform Y-flip formula shifts all group children by viewBoxHeight: position.y is set to viewBoxHeight - ty instead of -ty.

- **Root cause:** convertGroup (svgConverter.ts:420-425) parses the group's SVG transform, then at line 424 sets `svgTransform.position.y = ctx.viewBoxHeight - svgTransform.position.y`. This applies an ABSOLUTE viewBox Y-flip to a value that must be a RELATIVE parent->child delta. Derivation: a child shape's local Quar position is computed by buildTransform as (cx, viewBoxHeight - cy) using the GLOBAL viewBoxHeight (leaves are flipped globally, not per-group). For the child's world position (P_group + child_local) to equal the correct Y-flipped SVG target (tx+cx, viewBoxHeight-ty-cy), the group's Y must satisfy P_group.y + viewBoxHeight - cy = viewBoxHeight - ty - cy, i.e. P_group.y = -ty. The code produces viewBoxHeight - ty, an error of exactly +viewBoxHeight. Also, unlike buildTransform (line 547) which negates rotation for the Y-flip convention, convertGroup leaves rotation un-negated, so a rotated group spins the wrong way. The error is masked only when a transformed group is the SOLE root (importSvg recenters it, and children ride along) or when all roots are transformed groups sharing the common +viewBoxHeight offset; it is visible when a transformed group coexists with untransformed roots, and always for nested (non-root) transformed groups which importSvg never offsets (importSvg.ts:96 only offsets roots).
- **Fix:** In convertGroup, replace line 424 `svgTransform.position.y = ctx.viewBoxHeight - svgTransform.position.y;` with `svgTransform.position.y = -svgTransform.position.y;` (relative delta, x stays as tx). Also negate rotation inside the same `if (el.transform)` block to match buildTransform's Y-flip convention: `svgTransform.rotation = -svgTransform.rotation;`. Keep scale and skew as decomposed (matching buildTransform lines 548-549). Leave the no-transform branch (createDefaultTransform) untouched. Scope note: this fully fixes the common translate-only group case (the vast majority: Illustrator/Inkscape layer groups). Fully-correct rotated/scaled GROUP import is a deeper architectural issue because leaf children are Y-flipped with the global viewBoxHeight rather than composed through the group's local frame; that rework is out of scope for this fix and should be tracked separately.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgConverter.ts`, `packages/core/src/svg/__tests__/svgConverter.test.ts`
- **Test:** In svgConverter.test.ts group describe block: (1) `<g transform="translate(30, 40)"><rect width="10" height="10"/></g>` in viewBox 0 0 200 200 -> assert group.transform.position.x toBeCloseTo(30) and position.y toBeCloseTo(-40) (NOT 160). (2) `<g transform="rotate(30)"><rect width="10" height="10"/></g>` -> assert group.transform.rotation toBeCloseTo(-30). Existing untransformed-group tests (lines 251-280) still pass since the `if (el.transform)` guard skips them.
- **Notes:** No existing test covers transformed groups, so no test locks in the bug; the fix won't break current tests. Independent of F044 (different function) though both touch Y-flip conventions in the same file.

#### `F044` · high · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgConverter.ts:543`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** buildTransform applies only the translation components of an element's SVG transform to its center, so any transform containing rotation/scale (rotate(a), scale(k), matrix with rotation) places the element at the wrong position.

- **Root cause:** buildTransform (svgConverter.ts:543-546) and buildCenteredPathTransform (svgConverter.ts:508-511) place the shape by adding only the DECOMPOSED TRANSLATION component of the SVG transform to the center: `x: centerX + svgTransform.position.x, y: viewBoxHeight - (centerY + svgTransform.position.y)`. The code comment (line 541) says 'We need to transform the center point through it' but it never does. The correct center is M*(cx,cy) — the full affine applied to the center — because rotate/scale/matrix have non-identity linear parts that move the center even when their translation component (tx,ty) is 0. Verified failure: `<circle cx="50" cy="0" r="10" transform="rotate(90)"/>` — SVG matrix [0,1,-1,0,0,0] maps (50,0)->(0,50) so it renders at Y-flipped (0, viewBoxHeight-50); current code decomposes tx=ty=0 and yields position (50, viewBoxHeight), leaving the circle at its untransformed spot. Same for `scale(2)` (center (50,50) should double to (100,100), code keeps (50,50)) and for Illustrator's baked `matrix(...)`. Only pure-translate transforms import correctly (their linear part is identity, so center+translation == M*center). buildCenteredPathTransform has the identical defect for path/polygon/polyline/line/compound nodes; note its viewBoxHeight param is currently unused (`_viewBoxHeight`).
- **Fix:** Import `parseSvgTransformToMatrix` and `decomposeMatrix` from './svgUtils' (both already exported in svgUtils.ts:239,311). In buildTransform's `if (svgTransformAttr)` branch: `const m = parseSvgTransformToMatrix(svgTransformAttr); const [a,b,c,d,tx,ty] = m; const tCx = a*centerX + c*centerY + tx; const tCy = b*centerX + d*centerY + ty; transform.position = { x: tCx, y: viewBoxHeight - tCy };` then `const dec = decomposeMatrix(m); transform.rotation = -dec.rotation; transform.scale = dec.scale; transform.skew = dec.skew;`. Leave the else branch unchanged. For buildCenteredPathTransform, rename `_viewBoxHeight` to `viewBoxHeight` and use it: the incoming `center` is in Y-UP space (points were already flipped before centerPathPoints), so reconstruct the SVG-space center Y before applying M: `const m = parseSvgTransformToMatrix(svgTransformAttr); const [a,b,c,d,tx,ty] = m; const cySvg = viewBoxHeight - center.y; const tX = a*center.x + c*cySvg + tx; const tYsvg = b*center.x + d*cySvg + ty; transform.position = { x: tX, y: viewBoxHeight - tYsvg };` then decompose for rotation(negated)/scale/skew. Both formulas reduce EXACTLY to the current output for pure-translate (verified), so translate transforms and no-transform paths are unchanged.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgConverter.ts`, `packages/core/src/svg/__tests__/svgConverter.test.ts`
- **Test:** In svgConverter.test.ts: (1) `<circle cx="50" cy="0" r="10" transform="rotate(90)"/>` viewBox 0 0 200 200 -> assert position.x toBeCloseTo(0), position.y toBeCloseTo(150). (2) `<circle cx="50" cy="50" r="10" transform="scale(2)"/>` viewBox 0 0 400 400 -> assert position.x toBeCloseTo(100), position.y toBeCloseTo(300). (3) centered-path coverage: `<path d="M 40 0 L 60 0" transform="rotate(90)" stroke="black" fill="none"/>` viewBox 0 0 200 200 -> segment center (50,0) rotates to (0,50), Y-flip -> assert position.x toBeCloseTo(0), position.y toBeCloseTo(150). (4) regression: a rect with `transform="translate(10,20)"` still matches the old center+translation result.
- **Notes:** No existing converter/importer test uses a rotate/scale/matrix transform on a shape (only translate, which is preserved), so existing tests stay green. importSvg bounds (computeNodesBounds) remain approximate for scaled shapes because width/radius aren't baked, but that's pre-existing and untested. Independent of F043.

#### `F045` · high · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgExporter.ts:396`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Text (and image) elements are exported inside the global scale(1,-1) Y-flip group without a counter-flip, so all exported text and images render vertically mirrored (upside-down).

- **Root cause:** exportNodesToSvg (packages/core/src/svg/svgExporter.ts:585-592) wraps every emitted element in <g transform="scale(1,-1) translate(...)"> to convert Quar Y-up geometry to SVG Y-down. This is correct for exporter-authored geometry (paths, rects, ellipses) whose coordinates are emitted in Y-up space, but <text> glyph runs (textToSvg, line 382-397) and <image> raster content (imageToSvg, line 405-413) are rendered by the SVG engine in its own Y-down space. Placing them inside the scale(1,-1) group mirrors the glyphs/pixels vertically. Neither textToSvg nor imageToSvg emits a compensating local scale(1,-1), so exported text and images render upside-down. Confirmed the only production caller (apps/web/src/services/exportService.ts:219) always wraps output in the flip group, so a fix inside textToSvg/imageToSvg is always applied in the right context; nodeToSvgElement is otherwise only invoked by tests.
- **Fix:** Append a local counter-flip to the transform of <text> and <image> so the double flip cancels for the raster/glyph content while position stays correct. TEXT: in textToSvg build the transform to end with scale(1,-1). Since tfAttr may be empty, construct the element transform explicitly, e.g. compose the node.transform parts (reuse transformToSvgAttr's inner parts) and append 'scale(1,-1)', producing transform="<nodeParts> scale(1,-1)" (always present now). This flips glyphs about the local baseline/origin so they render upright inside the root flip. Verify baseline vertical placement visually; if text sits one line off, add a 'translate(0,-fontSize)' before the scale as a refinement. IMAGE: in imageToSvg the box spans y in [Y, Y+H] with Y=-anchorY. Append a flip about the box's horizontal center: transform="<nodeParts> translate(0,<H-2*anchorY>) scale(1,-1)" (rightmost applied first: scale(1,-1) then translate(0, H-2*anchorY) keeps the box region invariant while un-mirroring pixels). Concretely translateY = fmt(node.height - 2\*anchorY). Extract a helper that returns the node.transform's translate/rotate/scale part-string (refactor transformToSvgAttr to expose the joined parts) so both callers can append the counter-flip cleanly.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgExporter.ts`, `packages/core/src/svg/__tests__/svgExporter.test.ts`
- **Test:** In svgExporter.test.ts add: (1) export a single TextNode via exportNodesToSvg and assert the <text> element itself carries scale(1,-1) in addition to the root group (e.g. total occurrences of 'scale(1,-1)' === 2 for one text node), proving the net glyph orientation is upright; (2) export a single ImageNode and assert the <image> transform contains both 'scale(1,-1)' and the compensating 'translate(0,<H-2*anchorY>)' (e.g. for height=150 anchor.y=0 assert translate(0,150)); (3) a matrix round-trip assertion multiplying root flip * element transform and checking the resulting y-axis sign is positive (upright) for both. Keep existing substring assertions passing.
- **Notes:** Real visual correctness bug: all exported text and images currently render upside-down. Fix is localized to textToSvg/imageToSvg. Minor risk: nodeToSvgElement called standalone in tests will now emit text/image with a counter-flip (would look flipped if used WITHOUT the root flip), but no production path does that. Baseline vertical placement for text is a refinement worth eyeballing in a real browser during /verify.

#### `F046` · high · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgParser.ts:217`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Gradient coordinates given as percentages (x1="0%" x2="100%", the most common authoring form) are parsed with parseFloat, yielding 100 instead of 1.0 — gradients render wrong and round-trip corrupts.

- **Root cause:** packages/core/src/svg/svgParser.ts:213-231 (collectGradients) reads gradient coordinate attributes with bare parseFloat: `if (x1 !== null) gradient.x1 = parseFloat(x1)` (and same for y1/x2/y2/cx/cy/r/fx/fy). parseFloat("100%") returns 100. The Quar Gradient convention for start/end is normalized 0-1: convertGradient (svgConverter.ts:643-644) copies g.x1/g.x2 straight into start/end, and svgExporter.ts:117-120 multiplies start/end by 100 and appends '%'. So percentage-authored gradients (the Illustrator/Inkscape default form `x1="0%" x2="100%"`) import with end.x=100 — 100x outside the shape — rendering as an essentially solid first-stop color, and re-export writes `x2="10000%"`. Because the exporter always emits percentages, this is also a direct same-codebase round-trip corruption. Note parseGradientStops (line 251) already divides '%' offsets by 100, so the correct pattern already exists in the file. Separately, gradientUnits="userSpaceOnUse" absolute pixel coordinates are passed un-normalized into the same 0-1 fields, but that is a distinct, larger problem.
- **Fix:** Add a small helper in svgParser.ts, e.g. `function parseGradientCoord(v: string): number { const t = v.trim(); return t.endsWith('%') ? parseFloat(t) / 100 : parseFloat(t); }`. Replace the nine parseFloat(...) calls on x1,y1,x2,y2 (lines 217-220) and cx,cy,r,fx,fy (lines 227-231) with parseGradientCoord(...). Keep this finding scoped to percentage handling (fixes the common objectBoundingBox case and round-trip). For gradientUnits='userSpaceOnUse' absolute coordinates, leave the existing behavior but add a one-line console.warn (or TODO comment) noting they are not yet normalized against the referencing shape's bbox — track as a separate follow-up rather than expanding this fix.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgParser.ts`
- **Test:** In svgParser.test.ts: parse `<linearGradient id="g" x1="0%" y1="0%" x2="100%" y2="0%">` with two stops and assert grad.x1===0 and grad.x2===1 (not 100). Add a radial case `cx="50%" r="50%"` asserting cx===0.5, r===0.5. Add a converter/round-trip test in svgConverter.test.ts: convert a rect with fill=url(#g) using percentage gradient coords and assert node.fills[0].gradient.end.x===1.
- **Notes:** userSpaceOnUse normalization (needs the referencing shape's bounding box) is intentionally out of scope here; if the implementer chooses to also normalize userSpaceOnUse this becomes effort M. Touches the same function region as F131's coord inheritance but no hard ordering — review F046 and F131 together.

#### `F047` · high · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgPathParser.ts:35`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Path tokenizer cannot parse SVG's compact arc-flag syntax (e.g. "a1 1 0 011 1"), producing short arg lists that the parser turns into NaN coordinates.

- **Root cause:** tokenizePath (svgPathParser.ts:29-101) tokenizes with a single number regex (line 35: `/([Mm...])|([+-]?(?:\d+\.?\d*|\.\d+)...)/g`) that has no notion of SVG arc flag syntax. For arc commands the largeArcFlag/sweepFlag (arg indices 3,4) may be written without separators (compact form emitted by SVGO/Figma), e.g. `100` meaning flag=1,flag=0,x=0. The regex greedily reads `100` as the number 100 and `011` as 11, so the 7-arg group is mis-tokenized. Two failure routes, both confirmed by tracing: (a) trailing incomplete arc `M0 0a1 1 0 011 1` → args=[1,1,0,11,1] (5 args, never reaches expected 7 so never flushed mid-loop, flushed at line 99). Parser case 'A' (467-508) reads args[5]/args[6]=undefined → x=currentX+undefined=NaN. `if(currentX===x...)` is false (NaN!==NaN), arcToCubicBeziers runs with x2=NaN, dTheta=NaN, segments=Math.max(1,Math.ceil(NaN))=NaN, loop `0<NaN` never runs → empty array (arc silently vanishes), but currentX/currentY are set to NaN at 505-506, poisoning every subsequent relative command's points. (b) SVGO circle `M8 0a8 8 0 100 16 8 8 0 100-16z` → second arc group mis-shifts to [0,100,-16], so rx=args[0]=0 → arcToCubicBeziers degenerate branch (123-124) emits point {x:x2,y:y2}={NaN,NaN} directly into a PathPoint. Downstream convertPath (svgConverter.ts:306) drops <2-point subpaths so shapes silently disappear, and NaN points corrupt bounds.
- **Fix:** Rewrite tokenizePath as a hand-written scanner instead of the global-regex loop. Keep the argCounts table. Use a sticky number regex `/[+-]?(?:\d+\.?\d*|\.\d+)(?:[eE][+-]?\d+)?/y` with lastIndex=i for readNumber(), and a separate readFlag() that skips whitespace/commas then consumes exactly ONE character '0' or '1' (returns 0/1, advances i by 1). Main loop: skip ws/commas; if current char is a command letter, set cmd and advance (Z/z → push {cmd,[]}, reset cmd, continue); then read one argument group of argCounts[cmd] values — for cmd A/a at group-index 3 and 4 call readFlag(), otherwise readNumber(); if any value is null/NaN, stop parsing (do not emit a partial/NaN token); push {command:cmd,args}; then apply implicit-repeat mapping (M→L, m→l, others unchanged) and loop so a following number reuses cmd. This makes `100`→flag 1, flag 0, number 0, and `011`→flag 0, flag 1, and guarantees no NaN/short-arg tokens ever reach the parser. Spaced flags (e.g. `... 0 0 1 100 50`) still read correctly since readFlag consumes one char after skipping separators.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgPathParser.ts`
- **Test:** In packages/core/src/svg/**tests**/svgPathParser.test.ts add an 'arc compact flags' describe: (1) `parseSvgPath('M0 0a1 1 0 011 1')` — assert every returned point.position.x/y (and non-null handles) is Number.isFinite, and the final point ≈ (1,1); (2) SVGO circle `parseSvgPath('M8 0a8 8 0 100 16 8 8 0 100-16z')` — assert result length 1, closed true, and no NaN in any point coordinate/handle; (3) regression: existing spaced-arc `parseSvgPath('M 0 50 A 50 50 0 0 1 100 50')` still ends at ~(100,50). All prior parser tests must stay green.
- **Notes:** parseSvgPath is used by convertPath for every imported SVG path, so the tokenizer rewrite must preserve all existing behaviors (implicit L after M, compact comma notation, negative-as-separator, decimals w/o leading zero, multi-subpath, Z merge). The scanner design above reproduces each.

### Web — UI, panels & timeline

#### `F007` · high · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/common/ConsentBanner.tsx:44`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** The GDPR banner reappears on every page load for any user who accepted it without opting into Google Fonts.

- **Root cause:** ConsentBanner.tsx has two distinct defects at the flagged spot. (1) The visibility initializer on line 43-45 is `localStorage.getItem(STORAGE_KEY) !== 'true' || !hasGoogleFontsConsent()`. `setGoogleFontsConsent(false)` (line 29-38) does `removeItem`, so declining Google Fonts stores NO persistent flag; `hasGoogleFontsConsent()` therefore returns false forever for anyone who accepts without ticking the box, making `!hasGoogleFontsConsent()` permanently true and the banner reappear on every load. This exactly matches the misleading comment on line 42 ("Show banner if either: never accepted OR Google Fonts consent not yet granted"), so it is intended-but-wrong. (2) The direct `localStorage.getItem(STORAGE_KEY)` on line 44 is inside a `useState` initializer and is NOT wrapped in try/catch (unlike the guarded `hasGoogleFontsConsent`/`setGoogleFontsConsent` helpers). `localStorage.setItem` on line 50 in handleAccept is likewise unguarded. In storage-blocked contexts (Safari private mode, sandboxed iframe, cookies disabled) these throw. Confirmed via App.tsx (renders <ConsentBanner/> directly under BrowserRouter) and main.tsx (renders only StrictMode>App) that there is NO error boundary above ConsentBanner — the only ErrorBoundary lives inside Editor.tsx — so a throw in the initializer render crashes the entire app to a blank page.
- **Fix:** In ConsentBanner.tsx: (a) Change the visibility initializer (lines 43-45) to depend ONLY on STORAGE_KEY and guard it: `const [visible, setVisible] = useState(() => { try { return localStorage.getItem(STORAGE_KEY) !== 'true'; } catch { return false; } });`. Remove the `|| !hasGoogleFontsConsent()` term entirely — Google Fonts consent stays a separate checkbox whose default still comes from the already-guarded `hasGoogleFontsConsent` on line 47. (b) Guard the accept write on line 50: wrap `localStorage.setItem(STORAGE_KEY, 'true')` in try/catch (or add a `setConsentAccepted()` helper mirroring the existing `setGoogleFontsConsent` try/catch shape). (c) Update the now-inaccurate comment on line 42.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/common/ConsentBanner.tsx`, `apps/web/src/components/common/ConsentBanner.test.tsx`
- **Test:** New ConsentBanner.test.tsx with three cases: (1) reappear bug — `localStorage.setItem('quar-consent-accepted','true')` with the Google-Fonts key unset, render <ConsentBanner/>, assert `screen.queryByTestId('consent-banner')` is null (fails before fix). (2) crash bug — `vi.spyOn(Storage.prototype,'getItem').mockImplementation(() => { throw new Error('blocked'); })`, assert rendering <ConsentBanner/> does not throw. (3) accept crash — spy `setItem` to throw, render fresh (no accepted flag), click `consent-accept`, assert no throw.

#### `F012` · high · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/LayerPanel.tsx:804`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Drag-reorder drops layers at the wrong position: root rows are displayed reversed but insertion uses raw array indices, and same-parent moves have no removal-shift adjustment.

- **Root cause:** Two independent, compounding defects in the drag-reorder path.
  (1) Reversal mismatch: roots are DISPLAYED reversed (LayerPanel.tsx:412 `const rootNodes = [...sceneGraph.getRootNodes()].reverse()`) but the drop insert index is computed in UN-reversed array coordinates. In handlePointerUp (lines 799-804) `siblings = sceneGraph.getRootNodes().map(n=>n.id)` is in raw rootNodeIds order, `targetIndex = siblings.indexOf(dropTarget.nodeId)`, and `insertIndex = position==='before' ? targetIndex : targetIndex+1`. Because the visual list is reversed, 'before' (drawn ABOVE the row via `.dropBefore` box-shadow `0 -2px`, confirmed LayerPanel.module.css:251-256) actually corresponds to a HIGHER array index for roots, so the node lands on the opposite side of the indicator (e.g. rootNodeIds [A,B,C] shown C,B,A; drag C 'before' A -> insertIndex=indexOf(A)=0 -> moveNode(C,null,0) -> [C,A,B] -> shown B,A,C: C at the bottom instead of just above A).
  (2) Same-parent removal shift: SceneGraph.moveNode (SceneGraph.ts:127-175) removes the node from its parent array BEFORE splicing at the given index. For a move within the same parent from a lower index to a position after it, the target index is now stale by one. Group children are rendered NON-reversed (LayerPanel.tsx:283 `node.children.map`), so children [X,Y,Z] drag X 'before' Z -> insertIndex=indexOf(Z)=2 -> after X removed array is [Y,Z] -> splice(2) -> [Y,Z,X], i.e. below Z instead of above it. There is also a genuine display inconsistency: roots reversed, children not.
- **Fix:** In handlePointerUp (LayerPanel.tsx:790-819), fix the index math in two steps. Step A - orientation-aware before/after: after computing array-order `siblings` and `targetIndex`, branch on whether the drop parent is root. For root drops (parentId === null) the display is reversed, so map: position 'before' -> insertIndex = targetIndex + 1; position 'after' -> insertIndex = targetIndex. For group-child drops (parentId !== null, currently array-order display) keep: 'before' -> targetIndex, 'after' -> targetIndex + 1. Leave 'inside' -> 0. Step B - removal shift: inside the move loop (lines 811-819), for each id compute an effective index: read the node's current sibling index (its index in its current parent's children, or in rootNodeIds if root); if that node currently has the SAME parent as the drop parentId AND its current index < insertIndex, use insertIndex-1 for that node's moveNode call, else insertIndex. Increment the running insertIndex only after a successful move. Verify against: roots [A,B,C] drag C 'before' A -> [A,C,B] (shown B,C,A); roots [A,B,C] drag A 'before' B -> [B,A,C] (shown C,A,B); children [X,Y,Z] drag X 'before' Z -> [Y,X,Z]. Optionally (cleaner, higher-churn) also render children reversed (`[...node.children].reverse()` at line 283) so display orientation is uniform and only one before/after formula is needed; if doing that, apply the same reversed formula to both roots and children — but this changes existing child ordering expectations so gate it behind test review.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/LayerPanel.tsx`
- **Test:** In LayerPanel.test.tsx drag-and-drop describe block, add DOM-driven reorder tests using the SceneGraphCapture pattern already in the file. (1) Root reorder: add rects A,B,C (rootNodeIds [A,B,C]); simulate pointerDown on the A row (bottom-displayed), pointerMove past threshold, pointerMove over the top quarter of the C row so hitTest yields {C,'before'}, pointerUp on content; assert sceneGraph.getRootNodes ids are [B,A,C] and the displayed top row is A. (2) Group-child reorder: group with children [X,Y,Z]; drag X 'before' Z; assert group.children === ['Y','X','Z']. Because jsdom getBoundingClientRect returns zeros, either mock getBoundingClientRect on the rows to return distinct rects, or unit-test an extracted pure `computeInsertIndex(dropTarget, siblings, isRoot, draggedCurrentIndex)` helper covering the four before/after x root/child combinations plus the same-parent shift case.

#### `F013` · high · data-loss

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/MenuBar.tsx:310`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** File > New Project (and Ctrl+N) wipes the current project and clears undo history without any unsaved-changes confirmation.

- **Root cause:** MenuBar.handleNew (MenuBar.tsx:307-311) calls projectActions.newProject() unconditionally with no isDirty check. useProjectActions.newProject (useProjectActions.ts:96-138) removes every scene node, resets pages/timeline/selection to a fresh default page and calls clearHistory() (line 137) — destroying undo history and all in-memory work. For a never-saved project (projectId===null) the 30s auto-save (useProjectActions.ts:442-454, gated on `isDirty && projectId`) has never run, so everything since app start is unrecoverable. The keyboard path is equally unguarded: Editor.tsx:74 wires onNew:()=>projectActions.newProject() into useProjectShortcuts (Ctrl+N). 'Open' has the same exposure: the actual replacement is openProject (useProjectActions.ts:205-225, clearHistory at 220), reached from MenuBar.handleOpenProject (MenuBar.tsx:364-371) after the ProjectListDialog pick, and from Editor.tsx:75 onOpen. Note the reviewer's 'handleOpen' cite is imprecise — handleOpen (MenuBar.tsx:313-319) only lists projects; the destructive call is handleOpenProject/openProject, which is where the guard must go.
- **Fix:** Add an unsaved-changes confirmation before any destructive project swap. In MenuBar.tsx add state `pendingDestructive: 'new' | {type:'open', id:string} | null`. In handleNew: read useEditorStore.getState().isDirty; if false call projectActions.newProject() as today, if true setPendingDestructive('new') instead. In handleOpenProject: if isDirty, stash the id in pendingDestructive={type:'open',id} rather than calling openProject immediately. Render a 3-button dialog (reuse the existing saveAsOverlay/saveAsDialog markup pattern already in MenuBar.tsx:1094-1132) with Save / Discard / Cancel: Save => `await projectActions.saveProject()` then run the pending action; Discard => run pending action directly; Cancel => setPendingDestructive(null). Give the dialog data-testid="discard-confirm-dialog" and buttons data-testids. For the keyboard path, route Editor.tsx onNew/onOpen through the same guard: simplest is to move the isDirty check + confirm into the shared handlers — expose guarded onNew/onOpen from MenuBar via a custom window event, OR (lower-effort, covers both UI and keyboard in one chokepoint) gate inside useProjectActions.newProject and openProject with a blocking window.confirm('Discard unsaved changes?') when useEditorStore.getState().isDirty is true, returning early on cancel. Recommend the MenuBar 3-way dialog for the menu buttons plus a window.confirm guard inside useProjectActions.openProject/newProject so Ctrl+N/Ctrl+O are also protected. Keep the not-dirty fast path unchanged so existing tests that set isDirty:false still call newProject directly.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/MenuBar.tsx`, `apps/web/src/hooks/useProjectActions.ts`, `apps/web/src/pages/Editor.tsx`
- **Test:** MenuBar.test.tsx: with isDirty:true, open File menu, click 'New Project', assert projectActions.newProject NOT called yet and discard-confirm-dialog is shown; click Discard => newProject called once; in a second case click Cancel => newProject not called; and with isDirty:false, click 'New Project' => newProject called immediately (preserves existing behavior). If guarding useProjectActions: add a useProjectActions.test.ts case mocking window.confirm to return false with isDirty:true and assert sceneGraph.removeNode/clearHistory were not invoked.
- **Notes:** Reviewer's line cite conflates handleOpen (list only) with handleOpenProject/openProject (the destructive call). The guard belongs at openProject/handleOpenProject, not handleOpen. Coordinate with F162 since both edit MenuBar.tsx (different regions: handleNew ~307 vs currentFrame subscription ~121 and traversal ~208).

#### `F014` · high · data-loss

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/PageTabs.tsx:140`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Single click on a page tab's X icon permanently deletes the entire page with no confirmation and no undo.

- **Root cause:** PageTabs.tsx close button (lines 134-151) and context-menu Delete (lines 184-193) call handleDeletePage => useEditorStore.getState().deletePage on a single click with no confirmation. deletePage (editorStore.ts:2972-3010) filters the page out of state.pages immediately and, when deleting the active page, calls sceneGraph.fromJSON on the adjacent page and replaces undoStack/redoStack with the adjacent page's stacks (lines ~2985-3006). Confirmed via grep: no undo snapshot is pushed for page add/delete — pushUndo only snapshots per-page scene-graph node state, and deletePage overwrites the undoStack — so page deletion is permanently non-undoable. The only guard is `if (state.pages.length <= 1) return` (editorStore.ts:2973) which merely prevents deleting the final page. isDirty is set true so an already-saved project (projectId set) auto-saves the loss to disk within 30s.
- **Fix:** Require an explicit confirmation before deletePage. Mirror the existing two-click pattern from Projects.tsx (pendingDeleteId state + 3s reset timeout, Projects.tsx:45,71-75,95-108): add `const [pendingDeleteId,setPendingDeleteId]=useState<string|null>(null)` and a useEffect that clears it after 3s. In the X close-button onClick: if pendingDeleteId===page.id call handleDeletePage(page.id); else setPendingDeleteId(page.id) and add a visual 'confirm' class/title ('Click again to confirm'). For the context-menu Delete (lines 184-193), either route through the same two-click state or (clearer for a menu) show a nested confirm — simplest is to add a window.confirm(`Delete page "${name}"? This cannot be undone.`) guard before handleDeletePage in that handler. Stop propagation must remain (line 139). Optionally, for a stronger fix, make deletion undoable by snapshotting the removed PageData and adding a restorePage store action, but the confirmation is the required data-loss mitigation.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/PageTabs.tsx`
- **Test:** PageTabs.test.tsx: with two pages, click page-tab-close-page-1 once => assert pages.length still 2 and the close button shows the pending/confirm state; click it a second time => assert deletePage ran (pages.length===1). Separate test: context-menu Delete with window.confirm mocked to return false => pages unchanged; mocked true => page removed. Note the existing suite has no delete test, so this is net-new coverage.
- **Notes:** Two-click confirm keeps the interaction consistent with Projects.tsx. If the team prefers a modal, a shared confirm dialog is fine but higher effort. Undoable-snapshot is a nice-to-have follow-up, not required to close the data-loss risk.

#### `F015` · high · stale-event-listener

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/PropertiesPanel.tsx:247`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** numericInputProps attaches a wheel listener once per DOM element (guarded by the \_\_numWheel marker) and never rebinds or removes it, so the listener permanently uses first-render getValue/onChange closures.

- **Root cause:** numericInputProps (apps/web/src/components/layout/PropertiesPanel.tsx:235-261) attaches the non-passive wheel listener inside a ref callback that self-guards with an element marker: line 247 `if ((el as ...).__numWheel) return;` then line 248 sets it true and line 249 addEventListener('wheel', ...). Because numericInputProps returns a NEW ref closure on every render, React detaches (ref(null) -> early return at line 245) and reattaches (ref(el)) each render, but the \_\_numWheel marker on the reused DOM node makes every reattach early-return, so the listener created on FIRST mount is never replaced. Its closure captures the first-render getValue/onChange. The Size W input (lines 1508-1511) passes `() => Math.round(size.width)` and `(v) => handleSizeChange('width', v)` directly (NOT through the render-synced numericRef used only by position/rotation at 1457-1458 and 2391-2392). `size` is computed fresh each render at line 1293 and handleSizeChange (607-636) closes over `selectedId`, so both are frozen at first mount. Confirmed: (1) same-node stale value — external resize to 300 then wheel still reads first-render width; (2) selection-switch — wheel on node B's W input runs handleSizeChange bound to node A's selectedId, mutating the unselected node.
- **Fix:** In numericInputProps, stop capturing getValue/onChange in the one-time listener. Before the **numWheel guard, always refresh a per-element handler record: `const rec = el as unknown as Record<string, unknown>; rec.**numWheelHandlers = { getValue, onChange };`. Then keep the guard, and inside the single wheel listener read through the record instead of the closure: `const h = rec.**numWheelHandlers as { getValue: () => number; onChange: (v: string) => void }; h.onChange(String(h.getValue() + delta));`. Because React invokes the fresh ref closure (with current getValue/onChange) on every render's attach call, rec.**numWheelHandlers stays current while the listener is bound once. This mirrors the numericRef indirection already used for position/rotation and fixes all numericInputProps callers at once.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/PropertiesPanel.tsx`
- **Test:** In PropertiesPanel.test.tsx: render panel with a rectangle (width 100) selected, capture sceneGraph. (a) Same-node: act -> sceneGraph.updateNode(id,{width:300}); focus the W input (getByTestId/id 'prop-size-w'); fireEvent.wheel(input,{deltaY:-1}); expect sceneGraph.getNode(id).width === 301 (proves live read, not 101). (b) Selection-switch: add rect A(width100) and rect B(width200); select A, then select B; focus B's W input; fireEvent.wheel(deltaY:-1); expect B.width changed and A.width still 100 (proves listener targets the currently-selected node).

#### `F016` · high · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/PropertiesPanel.tsx:249`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** F015  
**Finding:** numericInputProps attaches a wheel listener once per DOM element and never refreshes it, so the captured getValue/onChange closures are permanently stale for every input except position/rotation

- **Root cause:** Exact duplicate of F015's root cause, described at the addEventListener line (249) and enumerating the full set of affected inputs. Confirmed by reading the code: only the position inputs (1456-1459) and rotation input (2390-2393) route through the render-synced numericRef (numericRef.current is reassigned every render at 1305-1312). Every other numericInputProps caller — Size W/H (1508-1511, 1537-1540), corner radius (1718-1721), polygon sides (1758-1761), inner radius (1806-1813), bone length (1865-1878), font size, line height, fill/stroke opacity/width, effect fields, opacity, and vertex X/Y/R (2583-2586, 2622-2625, 2667-2670) — passes render-scope closures directly, so all share the single stale-listener defect.
- **Fix:** No separate change: the single numericInputProps fix described in F015 (refresh a per-element \_\_numWheelHandlers record each render and have the one listener read through it) resolves every affected input including all those listed here. After applying F015, verify a second affected input (e.g. inner radius or bone length) also reads live values via a wheel test. Do not implement twice.
