- **Notes:** Duplicate of F015 (same helper, same lines). Recorded separately for traceability; a single fix closes both. Kept high severity to match F015.

#### `F017` · high · data-corruption

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/PropertiesPanel.tsx:2521`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Vertex keyframes use the combined getAllPoints index in a 'points.N' property path, which corrupts the path node when the selected vertex belongs to a subpath

- **Root cause:** Vertex editing addresses combined-array indices with points.N paths. dsPoints[].pointIndex indexes the flattened array from getAllPoints (pathUtils.ts:444-449 = node.points concatenated with each subpath). handleVertexPosChange writes edits back correctly via setAllPoints (2507-2511), but the keyframe track it creates uses `points.${sp.pointIndex}.position.${axis}` (2516/2521); handleVertexCornerRadiusChange uses `points.${sp.pointIndex}.cornerRadius` (2550/2554); and the indicators/toggles use `points.${dsPoints[0].pointIndex}...` (2595/2603, 2634/2642, 2679/2687). For a compound path (subpaths present) a subpath vertex has pointIndex >= node.points.length, so the track addresses node.points out of bounds. On evaluation applyAnimatedValues -> setProperty (PropertyBinding.ts:40-67) clones the points array, indexes the missing element, creates a bare {position:{x}} object, and leaves undefined holes at the skipped indices, corrupting the path node (undefined points, a typeless point). Note detectInterpolationType already supports the correct subpaths form: `.x`/`.y` -> number (500-503) and `subpaths.N.M.cornerRadius` -> number (555-556), and getProperty/setProperty traverse arrays generically, so `subpaths.si.pi.position.x` is a valid, non-corrupting address.
- **Fix:** Add a local helper in PropertiesPanel that maps a combined pointIndex to the correct property-path prefix: `function vertexPropPath(node, combinedIdx, suffix){ const pl = node.points.length; if (combinedIdx < pl) return `points.${combinedIdx}.${suffix}`; let off = pl; const subs = node.subpaths ?? []; for (let si=0; si<subs.length; si++){ if (combinedIdx < off + subs[si].length) return `subpaths.${si}.${combinedIdx-off}.${suffix}`; off += subs[si].length; } return `points.${combinedIdx}.${suffix}`; }` (avoids needing to export getSubpathBoundaries; boundaries are trivially the points/subpath lengths). Replace the four keyframe path builders (2516, 2521, 2550, 2554) using `n`/the loop's node, and the three indicator/toggle sites (2595/2603, 2634/2642, 2679/2687) using the selected path node and dsPoints[0].pointIndex, with vertexPropPath(node, idx, 'position.x'|'position.y'|'cornerRadius'). Keep suffix 'position.x' etc.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/PropertiesPanel.tsx`
- **Test:** In PropertiesPanel.test.tsx: build a path node with points.length=3 and subpaths=[[3 points]]; set store directSelectionPoints to a subpath vertex (combined pointIndex=3, i.e. first vertex of subpath 0); enable autoKeyframe; move currentFrame to 5; call the vertex X edit (fireEvent.change on data-testid 'vertex-pos-x'); assert a timeline track exists with property 'subpaths.0.0.position.x' and NO track 'points.3.position.x'; then evaluate/apply at frame 5 and assert node.points.length still 3 with no undefined holes.

#### `F018` · high · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/SymbolLibraryPanel.tsx:121`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Double-click-to-edit a symbol first fires click twice, placing two unwanted symbol instances into the scene before entering edit mode.

- **Root cause:** SymbolLibraryPanel.tsx renders each symbol row (lines 117-147) with BOTH onClick={()=>handleClick(symbol.id)} (line 121) and onDoubleClick={()=>handleDoubleClick(symbol.id)} (line 122) on the same div. The DOM fires click, click, dblclick for a double-click, so handleClick => placeSymbolInstance runs twice before handleDoubleClick => enterSymbolEdit. placeSymbolInstance (editorStore.ts ~3396-3432) unconditionally pushUndo and addNode a new instance at (0,0) each call, so two stray symbol-instance nodes are added. enterSymbolEdit (editorStore.ts, ~after 3432) then structuredClone(sceneGraph.toJSON()) into editingSymbolPrevState — capturing the two stray instances — and exitSymbolEdit restores that snapshot, so the two unwanted instances persist into the scene (and get saved). The existing 'double-click enters edit mode' test (SymbolLibraryPanel.test.tsx:132-146) uses fireEvent.doubleClick, which in jsdom dispatches only the dblclick event (no preceding click events), so it never reproduced the bug.
- **Fix:** Debounce single-click placement so a double-click cancels it. Add `const clickTimerRef = useRef<ReturnType<typeof setTimeout> | null>(null)`. In handleClick: if a timer is already pending, clear it; then set clickTimerRef.current = setTimeout(() => { placeSymbolInstance(sceneGraph, symbolId); clickTimerRef.current = null; }, 250). In handleDoubleClick: if clickTimerRef.current clear it and null it (cancelling the pending placement), then call enterSymbolEdit(symbolId, sceneGraph). Add a useEffect cleanup on unmount that clears any pending timer. This ensures a double-click places zero instances and single-click places exactly one after 250ms. Import useRef and useEffect (currently only useState/useCallback are imported at line 7).
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/SymbolLibraryPanel.tsx`
- **Test:** SymbolLibraryPanel.test.tsx with vi.useFakeTimers(): (a) reproduce the double-click sequence — fireEvent.click(item); fireEvent.click(item); fireEvent.doubleClick(item); vi.advanceTimersByTime(300); spy on the placeSymbolInstance store action (or count symbol-instance nodes added to the sceneGraph) and assert it was called 0 times while editingSymbolId==='sym-1'. (b) single click: fireEvent.click(item); vi.advanceTimersByTime(300); assert placeSymbolInstance called exactly once. Because jsdom fireEvent.doubleClick alone won't emit the preceding clicks, explicitly fire the click events (or use @testing-library/user-event's dblClick which emits the full sequence).
- **Notes:** Debounce introduces a ~250ms delay on single-click placement — acceptable and standard for click/dblclick disambiguation. An e.detail>1 guard alone is insufficient (it only suppresses the second click, leaving one stray instance from the first). The context-menu 'Edit Symbol' path (lines 79-84) is unaffected and remains the instant edit entry point.

#### `F019` · high · data-loss

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Timeline.tsx:303`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Dragging a keyframe across another keyframe on the same track in the dope sheet silently and permanently deletes the keyframe it passes over.

- **Root cause:** moveKeyframe (packages/animation/src/Timeline.ts:151-173) re-inserts the moved keyframe and at lines 166-167 overwrites whatever keyframe already sits on the destination frame: `if (insertIndex < len && keyframes[insertIndex].time === newTime) { keyframes[insertIndex] = keyframe }`. The dope-sheet drag in Timeline.tsx handleKeyframePointerMove (297-308) commits `moveSelectedKeyframes(keyframeMap, deltaFrames)` on EVERY pointermove and re-bases `dragRef.current.startX = e.clientX`, so a dragged keyframe steps through intermediate frames one integer at a time; the moment it lands on a stationary keyframe's frame that keyframe is silently replaced. There is no timeline-level undo: HistorySnapshot (editorStore.ts:2809-2812, 2830-2833) clones only sceneGraph.toJSON()+selectedNodeIds, never `timeline`, and moveSelectedKeyframes (editorStore.ts:2074-2090) never pushes undo, so the deletion is permanent. Reviewer's caveat is correct — a very fast single pointermove that jumps >1 frame can skip B's exact integer frame — but any normal/slow drag samples it and destroys B.
- **Fix:** Defer the timeline mutation to pointer-up so nothing passed-over is written. In Timeline.tsx: (1) handleKeyframePointerDown records the original startX/startFrame and a pendingDelta=0; (2) handleKeyframePointerMove computes deltaFrames from the ORIGINAL startX each time (do NOT re-base startX, do NOT call moveSelectedKeyframes) and stores it as dragRef.current.pendingDelta, driving a visual preview by offsetting the rendered `left` of selected keyframe diamonds by pendingDelta (add pendingDelta to kf.time when computing style.left for selected kfs); (3) handleKeyframePointerUp, if pendingDelta!==0, calls moveSelectedKeyframes(keyframeMap, pendingDelta) exactly once then clears dragRef. Because only the final destination is written, keyframes crossed mid-drag are never touched. Additionally harden the single final commit against dropping directly onto an occupied stationary frame: in KeyframeManager.moveKeyframes (packages/animation/src/KeyframeManager.ts:87-113) build a Set of the moving keyframe ids, and before applying, clamp deltaFrames toward zero to the largest magnitude for which no moving keyframe's target frame equals a stationary (non-moving) keyframe's frame on the same track (slide up to the wall instead of overwriting). Keep the existing highest/lowest-first sort so within-selection order still cascades cleanly.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Timeline.tsx`, `packages/animation/src/KeyframeManager.ts`
- **Test:** KeyframeManager unit test in packages/animation: a single track with A@10 (in moving set) and B@11 (not moving); moveKeyframes([A], +5) must leave B@11 present and place A at the clamped non-colliding frame (blocked at 10), asserting keyframes.length stays 2 and B's id survives. Plus a Timeline component test: 2 keyframes on one track at 10 and 11, pointerdown on the one at 10, pointermove crossing frame 11 to ~15, pointerup; assert both keyframe ids still exist in the store timeline. Also assert a normal move onto free space still relocates the keyframe.
- **Notes:** Deferred-commit is the cleaner of the reviewer's two options and eliminates the pass-over deletion entirely; the KeyframeManager clamp is a reinforcing guard for the intentional-drop-onto-occupied case. Touches the shared animation package (also used by GraphEditor), so exercise both dope-sheet and graph paths.

#### `F020` · high · data-corruption

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/timeline/GraphEditor.tsx:345`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Graph-editor keyframe drag creates two keyframes at the same time on one track (violating the sorted-unique invariant) and can silently switch which keyframe is being dragged.

- **Root cause:** editorStore.ts:1920 updateKeyframeTimeAndValue locates the dragged keyframe by TIME (line 1930: findIndex(kf => kf.time === oldTime)), then reassigns time+value (1934) and .sort() (1936) with NO de-duplication — unlike Timeline.moveKeyframe (Timeline.ts:151-173) which replaces any keyframe already sitting at newTime to keep the sorted-unique invariant. GraphEditor.tsx:345 calls it with dragMode.startTime as the key even though dragMode.kfId is available in drag state (defined at line 31/252). Landing on an occupied frame therefore produces two keyframes with identical time on one track. Worse, line 353 (setDragMode({...dragMode, startTime: newTime, ...})) advances startTime to the now-occupied frame, so on the NEXT mousemove findIndex(kf.time === startTime) resolves to the FIRST duplicate — the pre-existing neighbor, not the dragged kf — silently switching the drag target. interpolateValue (Timeline.ts:223) guards before.time === after.time and returns before.value, so this is a persistent bad-data/curve-discontinuity state, not a crash.
- **Fix:** Make the drag update id-based and dedup-safe. Add a store action updateKeyframeTimeAndValueById(nodeId, property, keyframeId, newTime, newValue): find track by nodeId+property, find the kf by id (not time), set roundedTime = Math.max(0, Math.round(newTime)) and value; before inserting, if a DIFFERENT keyframe already occupies roundedTime, remove that occupant (replace/merge, matching Timeline.moveKeyframe semantics) so the sorted-unique invariant holds; then re-sort and set immutably. In GraphEditor.tsx handleMouseMove keyframe branch (line 345) call the new action with dragMode.kfId instead of dragMode.startTime. Since lookup is now by stable id, stop mutating dragMode.startTime/startValue on line 353 for lookup purposes — keep startTime/startValue as fixed constraint anchors (this also removes the silent-switch mechanism). Coordinate this edit with F166 which rewrites the same setDragMode call.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts`, `apps/web/src/components/timeline/GraphEditor.tsx`
- **Test:** editorStore.test.ts: create a track with kf A@time5 value0 (id captured) and kf B@time10 value100; call updateKeyframeTimeAndValueById(node, prop, A.id, 10, 0); assert track.keyframes.length === 1 (or that no two keyframes share a time), that the surviving kf sits at time 10, and that a re-read finds A by id at its new time (proving the drag target did not switch to B). Add a second assertion iterating keyframes to confirm strictly increasing unique times.

#### `F021` · high · data-corruption

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/timeline/GraphEditor.tsx:557`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** F020  
**Finding:** Arrow-key nudge of multiple selected keyframes on one track corrupts values when keyframes are adjacent: one keyframe's value overwrites another's and one keyframe moves twice.

- **Root cause:** GraphEditor.tsx:503-589 keydown handler captures state via getState() at line 537, then loops over the STALE state.timeline.tracks snapshot (line 545) and identifies each selected kf by its stale kf.time, passing it as oldTime to state.updateKeyframeTimeAndValue (lines 549/557/565/573). Because that store action is time-keyed and non-dedup (see F020 rootCause), with A@5 v0 and B@6 v100 both selected, ArrowRight moves A to 6 → store now holds A@6 and B@6 duplicates; the loop's second iteration (still holding the stale B object) passes oldTime=6, whose findIndex(kf.time===6) returns the FIRST duplicate (A) and retimes it to 7 with B's snapshot value 100. Final [B@6 v100, A@7 v100]: A's value 0 destroyed, B never moved. ArrowLeft near frame 0 similarly piles clamped keyframes at time 0.
- **Fix:** Nudge by id, not by stale time, and route time moves through cascade-safe logic. Build keyframeMap { kfId -> {nodeId, property} } for the currently selected ids from FRESH state. For ArrowLeft/ArrowRight call the existing state.moveSelectedKeyframes(keyframeMap, e.key==='ArrowLeft' ? -delta : delta) — it delegates to KeyframeManager.moveKeyframes (KeyframeManager.ts:87-113) which sorts by direction (highest-time first for +delta) and uses id-based moveKf with sorted-unique replacement, eliminating the cascade and duplicates. For ArrowUp/ArrowDown (value nudge) reuse F020's new id-based action: iterate selectedKeyframeIds, look up each kf by id in fresh state, and set value±delta via updateKeyframeTimeAndValueById(nodeId, property, kfId, kf.time, kf.value±delta) so a track already containing a duplicate cannot be mis-targeted. Remove the stale-snapshot for-loop over state.timeline.tracks (lines 545-583).
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/timeline/GraphEditor.tsx`, `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts`
- **Test:** editorStore/GraphEditor test: track with A@5 v0 and B@6 v100, both ids selected; dispatch ArrowRight (delta 1) through the nudge path; assert exactly two keyframes remain with A at time 6 value 0 and B at time 7 value 100 (the reviewer's expected result), proving no value overwrite and no double-move. Add an ArrowLeft-near-zero case asserting the sorted-unique invariant (no two keyframes share time 0).

#### `F022` · high · data-loss

**Location:** `apps/web/src/hooks/useProjectActions.ts:159`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** F167  
**Finding:** saveProject clears isDirty before the IndexedDB write completes, and MenuBar discards the promise, so a failed save is silent and never retried.

- **Root cause:** In apps/web/src/hooks/useProjectActions.ts, saveProject clears the dirty flag BEFORE the async write: useEditorStore.setState({ isDirty:false, projectCreatedAt: data.createdAt }) at lines 159-162 runs before await dbSave(...) at line 170. saveProject has a try/finally (lines 143-175) but NO catch, so a dbSave rejection propagates. The manual caller MenuBar.tsx:324 does `void projectActions.saveProject()` with no .catch and toast is never imported there (grep shows zero toast usage in MenuBar.tsx). Net effect on a failed manual save: the dirty indicator disappears (isDirty was already false), the 'Project saved' toast at line 172 never fires (correct), AND no error toast fires — a silent failure. Autosave (line 447) does toast.error('Auto-save failed') but isDirty is still wrongly cleared at 159, so even there the UI stops showing unsaved state.
- **Fix:** In useProjectActions.ts saveProject: remove the isDirty:false / projectCreatedAt setState at lines 159-162 and instead set it AFTER `await dbSave(...)` resolves (immediately before setLastProjectId/toast.success). On the failure path isDirty is thus never cleared, so the dirty indicator remains. Apply the same reordering to saveProjectAs (move the setState at lines 191-194 to after dbSave at line 197). For the missing error toast on manual save: import toast into MenuBar.tsx and change handleSave (line 324) to `projectActions.saveProject().catch(() => toast.error('Failed to save project'))` and handleSaveAsConfirm (line 336) to `projectActions.saveProjectAs(saveAsName.trim()).catch(() => toast.error('Failed to save project'))`. Do NOT add a catch inside saveProject itself, because the autosave path (line 447) already toasts 'Auto-save failed' and an internal toast would double-fire. Note this reorder should be folded together with the F167 single-serialize refactor since both edit the same lines 152-172 block.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/hooks/useProjectActions.ts`, `apps/web/src/components/layout/MenuBar.tsx`
- **Test:** In useProjectActions.test.ts, add a saveProject test: set mockEditorState.projectId='existing-id' and mockEditorState.isDirty=true, make mockSave.mockRejectedValueOnce(new Error('write failed')), call saveProject inside act and expect it to reject; assert mockEditorState.isDirty is still true (i.e. useEditorStore.setState was never called with an object containing isDirty:false) and that toast.success was NOT called. Optionally add a MenuBar test asserting toast.error is shown when saveProject rejects.
- **Notes:** Real and the most user-impactful of the four. The existing test 'marks project as not dirty after save' uses a resolving dbSave mock, so moving isDirty:false to after the successful await keeps that test green.

#### `F023` · high · shortcut-conflict

**Location:** `apps/web/src/hooks/useTimelineShortcuts.ts:102`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Space toggles playback even while the focused canvas uses Space for pan mode, so every space-pan also starts/stops the animation.

- **Root cause:** Canvas.tsx handleKeyDown Space branch (apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx:1393-1400) calls e.preventDefault() and arms pan mode (isSpaceHeldRef=true, cursor='grab') but never calls e.stopPropagation(). The <canvas tabIndex={0}> (line 2261) is the focused element after any canvas click, so on Space the native keydown bubbles past React's root listener up to window. useTimelineShortcuts registers a native window keydown listener (useTimelineShortcuts.ts:169) whose early guard (lines 44-51) only skips input/textarea/select tagNames — 'canvas' is not excluded — so control reaches `case ' ':` (lines 102-108). Because the first Space press has event.repeat=false, it passes the `!event.repeat` guard and calls callbacks.togglePlay(). Result: each time the user begins a Space-pan, playback toggles (starts animating mid-pan; next Space-pan stops it). Confirmed the two listeners are independent (no dedup) and useTimelineShortcuts is wired with the real togglePlay via Editor.tsx:23 -> usePlayback.
- **Fix:** Recommended minimal fix (in one of the target files): in useTimelineShortcuts.ts inside `case ' ':`, before the `!event.repeat` toggle, add a guard using the already-declared `target` (line 45): `if (target && target.tagName?.toLowerCase() === 'canvas') break;`. This stops the window handler from toggling play when the drawing canvas is focused (where Space is the pan modifier), while preserving Space=play when focus is on body/panels (the existing 'Space should call togglePlay' test dispatches on window with no target, so target.tagName is undefined and still toggles). For precision against unrelated <canvas> elements, gate on a data attribute (e.g. add `data-quar-canvas` to the drawing canvas at Canvas.tsx:2258 and check `target.dataset?.quarCanvas`). Alternative single-line fix: in Canvas.tsx handleKeyDown Space branch (line 1394) add `e.stopPropagation();` — same UX effect, implemented in Canvas instead.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/hooks/useTimelineShortcuts.ts`
- **Test:** In useTimelineShortcuts.test.ts: dispatch a Space keydown whose target is a <canvas> element (Object.defineProperty(event,'target',{value: document.createElement('canvas')})) and assert callbacks.togglePlay was NOT called; keep the existing test proving Space DOES call togglePlay when target is not a canvas (default window/body target).
- **Notes:** Real and correctly described. Tradeoff: the recommended fix (and both reviewer options) disable Space=play whenever the drawing canvas is focused, which is the common case — this is a deliberate resolution of an inherent Space=pan vs Space=play conflict, not a pure win. If preserving Space-tap=play on the canvas is required, the fuller fix is tap-vs-hold: Canvas stopPropagation on Space keydown, and on Space keyup call togglePlay only if no pan-drag occurred during the hold (requires threading togglePlay into Canvas) — that is effort M and higher risk. Chose S for the guard since it is contained and leaves existing tests green.

#### `F024` · high · state-leak

**Location:** `apps/web/src/pages/Projects.tsx:79`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** New Project from the landing page resets only 4 store fields, so the previous project's pages, timeline, symbols and rigging state leak into (and get saved with) the new project.

- **Root cause:** handleNewProject (apps/web/src/pages/Projects.tsx:79-84) mutates only projectId/projectName/isDirty/projectCreatedAt via useEditorStore.setState, then navigate('/editor'). The Zustand store is a global singleton and is never reset when the user returns to the landing route, so it still holds the previously opened project's pages[], activePageId, symbols[], timeline, timelineDuration, frameRate, guides[], vitruvianControllers[], dynamicChains[], globalWind, plus currentFrame/selection/clipboard. New Project navigates without a ?project= param, so useProjectActions runs with loadProjectId=null and the loadOnMount effect (useProjectActions.ts:405-412) skips loading — nothing overwrites the stale state. On mount SceneGraphProvider creates a fresh EMPTY SceneGraph, but PageTabs/Timeline/SymbolLibrary read from the stale store. switchPage (editorStore.ts:3056-3105) then snapshots the empty live scene into the stale active page entry and loads another stale page, and saveProject serializes all of project A's pages/symbols/rigging under the new Untitled project. Separately confirmed useProjectActions.newProject (useProjectActions.ts:117-137) also omits guides/vitruvianControllers/dynamicChains/globalWind/timelineDuration/frameRate/onionSkin from its reset, so those leak even through the in-editor File>New path.
- **Fix:** Add a shared reset action to editorStore, e.g. resetProject(): void that set()s the full project-scoped default state in one call: projectId:null, projectName:'Untitled Project', isDirty:false, projectCreatedAt:null, currentFrame:0, isPlaying:false, timeline:createTimeline({duration:300,frameRate:30}), timelineDuration:300, frameRate:30, autoKeyframe:false, selectedNodeIds:new Set(), selectedKeyframeIds:new Set(), keyframeClipboard:null, clipboard:null, enteredGroupId:null, editingSymbolId:null, editingSymbolPrevState:null, symbols:[], guides:[], vitruvianControllers:[], dynamicChains:[], globalWind:{...default from editorStore.ts:1457}, onionSkin:{...DEFAULT_ONION_SKIN_SETTINGS}, and pages:[createDefaultPage()] with activePageId set to that page's id (reuse the existing createDefaultPage() helper at editorStore.ts:126 and capture its id). Then (1) in Projects.tsx handleNewProject, replace the 4-field setState with useEditorStore.getState().resetProject() before navigate('/editor'); the fresh SceneGraphProvider already yields an empty SceneGraph that matches the empty default page. (2) In useProjectActions.newProject, clear the live SceneGraph (existing loop at lines 98-101), call resetProject(), then clearHistory() — dropping the now-redundant inline setState so both entry points share one source of truth. Do NOT clear the SceneGraph from the store action itself (store has no direct SceneGraph handle on the landing page).
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts`, `apps/web/src/pages/Projects.tsx`, `apps/web/src/hooks/useProjectActions.ts`
- **Test:** In Projects.test.tsx: before render, useEditorStore.setState with a stale project A (pages: [pageA1, pageA2], activePageId: pageA1.id, symbols:[{...}], guides:[{...}], vitruvianControllers:[{...}], dynamicChains:[{...}]); render <Projects/>, fireEvent.click new-project-card, then assert useEditorStore.getState() has pages.length===1, symbols/guides/vitruvianControllers/dynamicChains all empty arrays, projectId===null, activePageId===pages[0].id, and isDirty===false. Add a parallel editorStore unit test asserting resetProject() zeroes the same fields.

### Web — canvas & render loop

#### `F006` · high · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/canvas/GuideOverlay.tsx:122`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** F067  
**Finding:** The window-level Delete/Backspace handler for a selected guide never checks whether focus is in an input or whether the user is deleting something else, so once a guide is selected any later Delete/Backspace press deletes the guide and preventDefault breaks Backspace in text fields.

- **Root cause:** GuideOverlay.tsx lines 118-130: the useEffect (gated only on `selectedGuideId`) registers a `window` keydown listener that, on Delete/Backspace, unconditionally calls `e.preventDefault()` and `onRemoveGuideRef.current(selectedGuideId)`. It never inspects `document.activeElement`, unlike Canvas.tsx which computes `isInput` (lines 1389-1390) and guards its Delete branch (line 1502). Two aggravating facts confirmed by reading the code: (1) the listener is on `window`, not the `<canvas>` element, so it fires on every keydown regardless of focus and regardless of the canvas-element handler; neither handler calls stopPropagation, so a canvas-focused Delete runs BOTH the Canvas `deleteSelection` and this guide removal. (2) `selectedGuideId` can never be cleared by clicking away (see F067), so once any guide is selected the listener stays armed indefinitely. Scenario B: focus a PropertiesPanel numeric input and press Backspace -> this window listener fires, `preventDefault()` blocks the character deletion, and the guide is silently removed. Scenario A: guide selected + shape selected, press Delete -> shape and guide both deleted.
- **Fix:** In the keydown handler at lines 121-127, before doing anything, read the active element and bail when it is a text-editing context, mirroring Canvas.tsx:1389-1390. Concretely: `const ae = document.activeElement as HTMLElement | null; const tag = ae?.tagName; if (tag === 'INPUT' || tag === 'TEXTAREA' || tag === 'SELECT' || ae?.isContentEditable) return;` placed at the top of `handleKeyDown`, before the `e.key === 'Delete' || e.key === 'Backspace'` check. This resolves Scenario B (Backspace in inputs no longer removes the guide and no longer preventDefaults). Scenario A (a canvas-focused Delete removing both a shape and a selected guide) is resolved by the F067 fix, which makes clicking a shape deselect the guide so they are never both 'selected' at once; do not add stopPropagation here (if only a guide is selected, Canvas's deleteSelection is a harmless no-op). Keep the existing `preventDefault()` inside the removal branch since it now only runs when not in an input and a guide is genuinely selected.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/canvas/GuideOverlay.tsx`, `apps/web/src/components/canvas/GuideOverlay.test.tsx`
- **Test:** In GuideOverlay.test.tsx add an interaction test: render GuideOverlay with one guide and a real focused `<input>` in the DOM; select the guide by `fireEvent.pointerDown` on its transparent hit `<line>`; focus the input (`input.focus()`), then dispatch `fireEvent.keyDown(window, { key: 'Backspace' })`; assert `onRemoveGuide` was NOT called. Add a second case: with no input focused (activeElement = body) and the guide selected, `fireEvent.keyDown(window, { key: 'Delete' })` DOES call `onRemoveGuide` with the guide id.
- **Notes:** The isInput guard (Scenario B) is independently applicable and low-risk. Full resolution of Scenario A depends on F067 restoring deselection so a guide is not left selected while the user operates on shapes.

#### `F008` · high · memory-leak

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx:194`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** GPU textures of deleted image nodes are never disposed because the nodeRemoved listener treats the SceneGraphEvent payload as a Node, making the only disposeTexture call site dead code.

- **Root cause:** SceneGraph.emit (packages/core/src/SceneGraph.ts:527-534) invokes every listener with the event object `{ type: 'nodeRemoved', nodeId: id }` (built at line 124), NOT the removed Node. Canvas.tsx:192-197 declares `handleNodeRemoved = (node: Node) => { ... if (node.type === 'image' ...) disposeTexture(node.src) }`. At runtime the argument is the event, so `node.type === 'nodeRemoved'` (never 'image') and `node.src` is undefined — the guard is always false, making the disposeTexture call dead code. Confirmed this is the ONLY real-source caller of ShapeRenderer.disposeTexture (grep: all other hits are dist/ build artifacts). ShapeRenderer.textureCache (ShapeRenderer.ts:648) is only fully cleared in dispose() at line 4377, so deleted image textures leak until Editor unmount. Extra wrinkle: removeNode has already deleted the node from this.nodes before emitting (line 122), and the event carries only nodeId, so even a corrected src lookup cannot re-fetch the node from the graph.
- **Fix:** Two-part fix. (1) In SceneGraph.ts: extend SceneGraphEvent interface (line 20-25) with an optional `node?: Node`, and in removeNode (line 124) emit `{ type:'nodeRemoved', nodeId: id, node }` using the `node` already fetched at line 96. (2) In Canvas.tsx: change handleNodeRemoved to `(event: SceneGraphEvent) => { incrementVersion(); const removed = event.node; if (removed?.type === 'image' && shapeRendererRef.current) {...} }`. Before disposing, guard against shared textures: scan the live scene graph for any remaining image node whose `src` equals `removed.src` (sceneGraphRef.current.traverse) and only call disposeTexture(removed.src) when none remain (duplicated image nodes share the same data-URL src via structuredClone, so a naive dispose would break the surviving copy).
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/SceneGraph.ts`, `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx`
- **Test:** SceneGraph.test.ts: after addNode(imageNode) then removeNode(id), the 'nodeRemoved' listener receives an event whose `node` is the removed node. Canvas.test.tsx (or a focused unit): add two image nodes sharing src A plus one with unique src B; spy on ShapeRenderer.disposeTexture; remove the src-B node -> disposeTexture called with B; remove one src-A node -> disposeTexture NOT called (still referenced); remove the last src-A node -> disposeTexture called with A.

#### `F009` · high · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx:234`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Ctrl+Shift+G is handled twice when the canvas is focused (canvas onKeyDown + window keydown listener), cascading ungroup into nested groups and pushing a spurious undo snapshot.

- **Root cause:** Two handlers process Ctrl+G/Ctrl+Shift+G when the canvas is focused. The canvas element (tabIndex 0, Canvas.tsx:2261) has onKeyDown={handleKeyDown}; that handler (lines 1471-1478) calls ungroupSelection/groupSelection then e.preventDefault() and return, but never e.stopPropagation(). The native keydown then bubbles to the window listener installed at line 240 (handleGlobalKeyDown, defined 224-238) which only re-checks ctrlKey/metaKey and key g/G and never inspects e.defaultPrevented — so it runs group/ungroup a second time. For ungroup this is destructive: after the first call G1 is dissolved and selectedNodeIds becomes its moved children (editorStore.ts:1778-1783); the second ungroupSelection passes the `size === 0` guard (1746), calls pushUndo again (1747, spurious identical snapshot), and dissolves any nested group among the new selection. Ctrl+G (group) is masked because groupSelection guards `size < 2` (1700) and post-group selection is a single group id, so the second call early-returns harmlessly.
- **Fix:** Remove the Ctrl+G / Ctrl+Shift+G block from the canvas-level handleKeyDown (Canvas.tsx:1471-1479) entirely and rely solely on the window-level handleGlobalKeyDown, which already fires regardless of focus — this eliminates the duplication in both focused and unfocused states. If keeping the canvas block is desired, instead add `if (e.defaultPrevented) return;` as the first line of handleGlobalKeyDown (after the existing early returns is fine, but before the group/ungroup calls) since the canvas handler already calls preventDefault on the same native event that reaches window. Prefer the removal approach for clarity.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx`
- **Test:** editorStore test: select an outer group G1 that contains a nested group G2; call ungroupSelection(sg) once, then with the resulting child selection call ungroupSelection(sg) again -> assert the second call dissolves G2 and pushes a second undo snapshot (demonstrates the current bug). Then, after the fix, an integration test dispatching a Ctrl+Shift+G keydown on the focused canvas should invoke ungroupSelection exactly once (spy) and leave G2 intact.

#### `F010` · high · performance

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx:578`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** With any enabled IK chain, the RAF loop forces a full React re-render of the Canvas subtree at 60fps even when completely idle.

- **Root cause:** The RAF loop calls evaluateIKChains(ikChains, sceneGraph) every frame while not playing (Canvas.tsx:575-580). evaluateIKChains -> applyIKResult (packages/rigging/src/ik.ts:413-435) unconditionally calls sceneGraph.updateNode(boneId, { transform: {...rotation: clamped} }) for every bone in the solve result, with no comparison to the bone's current rotation. SceneGraph.updateNode (SceneGraph.ts:186-205) always emits 'nodeChanged' (line 204). Canvas subscribes that event to incrementVersion -> setSceneGraphVersion (Canvas.tsx:189, 200), forcing a React re-render of the Canvas subtree. For a static IK target FABRIK converges to the same rotations each frame, yet updateNode+emit still fire, so an enabled IK chain drives a 60fps re-render even when fully idle (React 18 batches the per-bone emits into one render/frame, but that render still happens every frame). Note: the defect's root cause is in ik.ts, not Canvas.tsx, though it is triggered from the Canvas render loop.
- **Fix:** In applyIKResult (packages/rigging/src/ik.ts:413-434), after computing `clamped`, compare against the bone's current rotation and skip the updateNode call when unchanged within an epsilon: `if (Math.abs(clamped - bone.transform.rotation) < 1e-6) continue;` before the sceneGraph.updateNode call. This prevents the spurious 'nodeChanged' emit (and thus the re-render) when the pose is static, while still updating when the target actually moves. Optionally also short-circuit evaluateIKChains when target/pole/root world transforms are unchanged since last frame, but the per-bone epsilon skip is sufficient and lowest-risk.
- **Files:** `packages/rigging/src/ik.ts`
- **Test:** ik.test.ts: spy on sceneGraph.updateNode; build a chain already at its solved pose, call applyIKResult with rotations equal (within epsilon) to the bones' current rotations -> assert updateNode is NOT called. Complementary case: rotations differing beyond epsilon -> updateNode IS called.

#### `F011` · high · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx:1057`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Releasing the mouse outside the canvas mid-drag leaves the active tool stuck in dragging mode; the shape keeps following the cursor when the pointer re-enters.

- **Root cause:** Canvas tool drags are wired only through the canvas element's React onMouseDown/onMouseMove/onMouseUp/onMouseLeave (Canvas.tsx:2263-2266). handleMouseDown (964-995) forwards button-0 presses to toolPointerDown with no setPointerCapture and no document-level listeners — setupGlobalDragListeners (1998-2039) is invoked only from overlay/pen handlers (2069/2087/2105), never from canvas tool drags. handleMouseLeave (1057-1063) resets only isPanningRef and the cursor; it never calls toolPointerUp. SelectionTool.onPointerMove (packages/core/src/tools/SelectionTool.ts:295-341) keeps moving/resizing/rotating while state.isDragging is true and never checks event.buttons; only onPointerUp clears it. So if the button is released off-canvas (over a side panel) mid-drag, no mouseup reaches the tool; re-entering the canvas resumes glue-dragging on every handleMouseMove, and editorStore stays mid-transform.
- **Fix:** Guarantee pointer-up delivery. Preferred: convert the canvas tool interaction to Pointer Events — rename the canvas handlers to onPointerDown/Move/Up and, in the button-0/non-pan/non-text-edit branch of handleMouseDown, call `canvasRef.current.setPointerCapture(e.pointerId)` so all subsequent move/up route to the canvas even outside its bounds (release always delivers pointerup). Lower-churn alternative that reuses existing infra: in handleMouseDown's tool branch call setupGlobalDragListeners() (registers document pointermove/pointerup that forward to toolPointerMove/Up and self-clean on up), and add an `isToolDraggingRef` flag set on that mousedown and cleared in the global cleanup; in handleMouseMove/handleMouseUp early-return the toolPointerMove/toolPointerUp forwarding while isToolDraggingRef is set, to avoid double-forwarding (mouse + pointer events both fire for mouse input). Also have handleMouseLeave leave drag teardown to the global/captured pointerup rather than resetting nothing.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx`
- **Test:** Canvas interaction test: mousedown/pointerdown on canvas over a shape, move to start a drag, dispatch a mouseleave WITHOUT a canvas mouseup, then dispatch a document-level pointerup/mouseup (simulating release over a panel); move the pointer again over the canvas and assert the shape's transform.position no longer changes (drag ended) and editorStore is no longer mid-transform.

### Web — editor store

#### `F026` · high · data-loss

**Location:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts:86`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** HistorySnapshot omits the timeline, so undoing a node deletion restores the node but its keyframes are permanently lost.

- **Root cause:** HistorySnapshot (editorStore.ts:85-88) contains only sceneData + selectedNodeIds; pushUndo (2807-2823) captures only those. deleteSelection (1649-1685) and cutSelection (2894-2916) call `mgr.removeAllKeyframesForNode(id)`, which reassigns `this.timeline.tracks = this.timeline.tracks.filter(...)` on the live store timeline (KeyframeManager.ts:174-177), and also filter ikChains/smartBoneActions/dynamicChains store arrays. undo (2825-2850)/redo (2852-2877) only call sceneGraph.fromJSON and restore selection — they never restore timeline or the rigging arrays, so keyframes and chains removed on delete are permanently lost after undo.
- **Fix:** Extend HistorySnapshot to also hold `timeline`, `ikChains`, `smartBoneActions`, `dynamicChains` (and vitruvianControllers for symmetry). In pushUndo, capture structuredClone(get().timeline) and the rigging arrays. In undo() and redo(), when building currentSnapshot capture the same fields, and in the restoring set() include `timeline: structuredClone(snapshot.timeline)`, `ikChains`, `smartBoneActions`, `dynamicChains` from the popped snapshot. Also update timelineDuration/frameRate scalars from the restored timeline (ties into F104). The per-page undoStack/redoStack storage keeps working unchanged since they store HistorySnapshot[].
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts`
- **Test:** Add a position keyframe track for a rect (via addKeyframe), select+deleteSelection the rect, then undo; assert timeline.tracks again contains a track with that nodeId. Second case: createIKChain on a bone, deleteSelection the IK target, undo; assert ikChains restored to length 1.
- **Notes:** Because undo/redo would restore the whole timeline and rigging arrays wholesale, this also makes F101 and F171 removals undo-safe regardless of order. structuredClone of timeline on every pushUndo adds cost but is bounded by MAX_UNDO_STACK_SIZE=50.

#### `F027` · high · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts:2341`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** bringForward moves the node two z-positions instead of one due to an off-by-one insert index.

- **Root cause:** bringForward calls `sceneGraph.moveNode(id, parentId, index + 2)` (editorStore.ts:2341). SceneGraph.moveNode removes the node from its parent/root list BEFORE splicing at the given index (SceneGraph.ts:140-175), so every index past the node's old position shifts left by one. For siblings [A,B,C,D], bringForward on A (index 0): remove A -> [B,C,D], splice(2,0,A) -> [B,C,A,D], skipping two positions. sendBackward correctly uses index-1 (2364), confirming the asymmetry. Wired to Ctrl+], the Edit menu and LayerPanel context menu.
- **Fix:** Change line 2341 to `sceneGraph.moveNode(id, parentId, index + 1)`. The existing `if (index >= siblings.length - 1) continue` guard already prevents moving the topmost node, and index+1 after removal lands exactly one slot forward.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts`
- **Test:** Using the REAL SceneGraph from @quar/core (the test mock's moveNode is a no-op vi.fn), add root siblings A,B,C,D; select A; call bringForward(sg); assert getRootNodes order is [B,A,C,D]. Also select C and bringForward -> [B,A,D,C] to cover the second-to-last case.
- **Notes:** Test must import the real SceneGraph; the existing createMockSceneGraph\* helpers stub moveNode as a no-op and cannot exercise the ordering.

#### `F028` · high · data-loss

**Location:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts:3387`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** detachInstance (and deleteSymbol's detach paths) only re-add the definition's root nodes, dropping all descendants and leaving dangling children ids in the scene graph.

- **Root cause:** resolveSymbolInstance (symbolResolver.ts:74-95) returns ALL definition nodes (roots + descendants). detachInstance (editorStore.ts:3363-3389) filters to rootNodes (rootIds set) and adds only `structuredClone(child)` per root via addNode(clone, groupId). The clone keeps its original `children` array referencing definition-node ids that are never added, and the descendant nodes are discarded — producing a group whose child holds dangling child ids and losing all nested artwork. The same defect exists in deleteSymbol's single-root path (3300-3307) and multi-root path (3308-3331).
- **Fix:** Add a shared helper (mirroring pasteClipboard's remap at 1573-1639) e.g. `cloneResolvedSubtree(resolved, rootIds, newParentId)` that: builds an old->new id map for every resolved node, deep-clones each, rewrites `id`, `parent` (roots -> newParentId), and `children` (map through the id table, dropping ids not in the resolved set), then adds nodes parent-first into the scene graph. Use it in detachInstance (replace the rootNodes-only loop) and in both deleteSymbol detach paths. For deleteSymbol's single-root case, still allow the replacement-with-transform behavior but clone the full subtree under it.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts`
- **Test:** Build a symbol definition with a group root that has a child rect (both in sceneGraphJSON.nodes, group.children=[rectId]). Place an instance, select it, call detachInstance(sg). Assert the resulting group has exactly one child whose id resolves to a real node of type 'rectangle', and that toJSON produces no child id that fails getNode (no dangling references).
- **Notes:** resolveSymbolInstance is cached and returns shared node references — clone before mutating (structuredClone per node, as the helper does).

#### `F029` · high · data-corruption

**Location:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts:3434`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** enterSymbolEdit leaves the page-level undo/redo stacks live, so Ctrl+Z inside symbol edit restores the page scene into the symbol session and exitSymbolEdit then saves the whole page as the symbol definition.

- **Root cause:** enterSymbolEdit (editorStore.ts:3434-3455) saves editingSymbolPrevState (scene + selection) and loads the symbol into the live graph, but does NOT clear or stash undoStack/redoStack (unlike switchPage which swaps per-page stacks). The Canvas.tsx Ctrl+Z handler (1451-1461) calls `undo(sceneGraph)` with no editingSymbolId check, and undo() does `sceneGraph.fromJSON(pageSnapshot)` (2839). So one Ctrl+Z inside symbol edit replaces the symbol canvas with the full page scene; a subsequent exitSymbolEdit (3462) then serializes that page content as the symbol's sceneGraphJSON, corrupting the symbol and all its instances.
- **Fix:** On enterSymbolEdit, stash the current undoStack/redoStack (e.g. add fields to editingSymbolPrevState: `undoStack`, `redoStack`) and set undoStack:[], redoStack:[], canUndo:false, canRedo:false in the set(). On exitSymbolEdit, restore those stacks (and canUndo/canRedo from their lengths) in its set(). Optionally also add an `if (get().editingSymbolId) return;` early guard in undo()/redo() (or in the Canvas.tsx handler) as belt-and-suspenders so keyboard undo inside symbol edit only affects the symbol's own (cleared) stack.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts`
- **Test:** Draw/add a rect then pushUndo (page stack has 1). enterSymbolEdit; assert canUndo===false and undoStack length 0. Call undo(sg); assert the symbol scene (getNode of a symbol-def node) is unchanged and the page rect did not reappear. exitSymbolEdit; assert undoStack restored to the pre-edit page stack (length 1, canUndo true).
- **Notes:** F002 depends on this so page-switch-via-exitSymbolEdit also restores the page's undo/redo stacks.

### Web — services & persistence

#### `F025` · high · error-handling

**Location:** `apps/web/src/services/projectStorage.ts:95`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** saveProject only listens to tx.onerror, but quota-exceeded failures at IndexedDB commit time fire only the transaction's abort event, so the returned promise never settles.

- **Root cause:** In apps/web/src/services/projectStorage.ts the three write transactions register only tx.oncomplete and tx.onerror: saveProject (lines 91-104), deleteProject (lines 141-146), setSetting (lines 170-175). IndexedDB surfaces a QuotaExceededError two ways: (a) as a request error that bubbles request.onerror -> tx.onerror -> abort (the current code handles this at line 95-103), and (b) detected only when buffered writes flush at commit time, in which case NO request error fires and the transaction goes straight to abort, firing only tx.onabort with tx.error = QuotaExceededError. Case (b) is unhandled, so the returned Promise never resolves or rejects — it hangs forever. Confirmed downstream impact in apps/web/src/hooks/useProjectActions.ts: saveProject sets manualSavingRef.current = true (line 142) and clears it in a finally (lines 173-175); if `await dbSave(...)` (line 170) never settles, the finally never runs, manualSavingRef stays true, and the auto-save guard at line 444 (`!manualSavingRef.current`) is permanently false, silently killing all future autosaves. The StorageQuotaError class (lines 71-76) is unreachable via the abort path.
- **Fix:** Add a tx.onabort handler to each of the three write Promises. For saveProject mirror the onerror quota mapping: `tx.onabort = () => { const e = tx.error; reject(e?.name === 'QuotaExceededError' ? new StorageQuotaError() : (e ?? new DOMException('Transaction aborted', 'AbortError'))); };`. For deleteProject and setSetting: `tx.onabort = () => reject(tx.error ?? new DOMException('Transaction aborted', 'AbortError'));`. Guard against double-settle is unnecessary because oncomplete/onerror/onabort are mutually exclusive per transaction. Optionally (defense-in-depth) add the same onabort to the readonly transactions (loadProject 111-115, listProjects 122-135, getSetting 157-164) so an unexpected abort rejects instead of hanging, but the quota failure only affects the three write paths.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/services/projectStorage.ts`
- **Test:** In apps/web/src/services/projectStorage.test.ts add a suite that stubs the DB layer to force an abort: mock initDB (or spy on the resolved IDBDatabase.transaction) to return a fake transaction object exposing objectStore().put and settable oncomplete/onerror/onabort, then invoke saveProject and synchronously fire tx.onabort with tx.error = a DOMException('quota','QuotaExceededError'); assert `await expect(saveProject(...)).rejects.toBeInstanceOf(StorageQuotaError)`. Add a second case firing onabort with a generic error and assert the promise rejects (settles) rather than hanging. Repeat one abort test each for deleteProject and setSetting asserting they reject rather than hang.

### Animation engine

#### `F105` · medium · memory-leak

**Location:** `packages/animation/src/Easing.ts:137`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** cubicBezierCache is an unbounded module-level Map that grows by one entry per unique cubic-bezier control-point tuple and is never evicted.

- **Root cause:** packages/animation/src/Easing.ts line 125 declares `const cubicBezierCache = new Map<string,(t:number)=>number>()` and getCachedCubicBezier (lines 127-140) does `cache.set(key, fn)` with key `${x1},${y1},${x2},${y2}` and no eviction/size cap. During a Sprint-23 tangent-handle drag, apps/web/src/components/timeline/GraphEditor.tsx (lines 394 and 419) calls tangentsToEasing -> createCubicBezier producing a new float-valued cubic-bezier per pointermove, stored on the keyframe; each re-render's buildTrackCurvePath -> sampleCurveSegment (GraphEditorUtils.ts line 516 applyEasing) then calls getCachedCubicBezier with a brand-new unique float key, inserting a permanently retained closure. Keys are essentially never reused, so the Map grows unbounded across an editing session.
- **Fix:** Bound the cache in Easing.ts. Add `const MAX_CUBIC_BEZIER_CACHE = 256;` and in getCachedCubicBezier, after `cubicBezierCache.set(key, fn)`, evict the oldest entry when over capacity: `if (cubicBezierCache.size > MAX_CUBIC_BEZIER_CACHE) { const oldest = cubicBezierCache.keys().next().value; if (oldest !== undefined) cubicBezierCache.delete(oldest); }` (Map preserves insertion order, giving FIFO eviction; drag-created keys are transient so eviction order is unimportant). To make it testable, also export a tiny accessor `export function _cubicBezierCacheSize(): number { return cubicBezierCache.size; }`.
- **Files:** `packages/animation/src/Easing.ts`
- **Test:** In packages/animation/src/Easing.test.ts: import applyEasing, createCubicBezier and the new \_cubicBezierCacheSize; loop ~1000 iterations calling applyEasing(0.5, createCubicBezier(i/1000, 0.1, 0.9, i/1000)) with unique control points; assert \_cubicBezierCacheSize() <= 256. Add a correctness assertion that applyEasing still returns 0/1 at the endpoints after eviction.
- **Notes:** FIFO cap is sufficient; a full LRU (re-insert on hit) is optional. Rounding the key to fixed precision is an alternative but risks returning a slightly-wrong cached fn, so the size-cap approach is preferred.

#### `F106` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/animation/src/GraphEditorUtils.ts:362`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** fitKeyframesToView clamps scaleX/scaleY to a minimum of 1 px-per-unit, so 'fit to view' fails whenever the frame or value range exceeds the usable pixel size — common for position tracks.

- **Root cause:** packages/animation/src/GraphEditorUtils.ts fitKeyframesToView lines 362-363: `const scaleX = Math.max(1, usableWidth / timeRange); const scaleY = Math.max(1, usableHeight / valueRange);`. The lower clamp of 1 px-per-unit means when the true fit scale is <1 (e.g. a Position Y track 100->800, valueRange 700, usableHeight ~170 -> true scale 0.24) the scale is forced to 1 and the ~700px-tall curve overflows the ~250px view (centered on midVal, roughly half clipped top and bottom). Same for timelines wider than the panel in pixels. Additionally usableWidth/usableHeight (lines 359-360) are computed as viewWidth/Height - padding*2 with no guard, so when the view is smaller than 2*padding (80px default) they go negative. GraphEditor.tsx calls this with the real panel rect (lines 133 and 602). Existing tests (GraphEditorUtils.test.ts lines 326-363) only assert scale > 0, so the clamp is unexercised.
- **Fix:** In fitKeyframesToView replace the clamp floor 1 with a small positive epsilon and guard the usable dimensions: add `const EPS = 0.0001;`, set `const usableWidth = Math.max(1, viewWidth - padding * 2);` and `const usableHeight = Math.max(1, viewHeight - padding * 2);`, then `const scaleX = Math.max(EPS, usableWidth / timeRange);` and `const scaleY = Math.max(EPS, usableHeight / valueRange);`. Centering math (offsetX/offsetY, lines 366-370) is unchanged and, with the correct scale, maps maxVal to y=padding and minVal to y=viewHeight-padding (verified: y = viewHeight/2 - (value-midVal)\*scaleY).
- **Files:** `packages/animation/src/GraphEditorUtils.ts`
- **Test:** In GraphEditorUtils.test.ts fitKeyframesToView describe: (1) large-range fit — keyframes [{time:0,value:100},{time:60,value:800}], view 800x250, padding 40; assert result.scaleY < 1 and that graphToScreen(0,100,result).y and graphToScreen(60,800,result).y both fall within [0,250] (i.e. not clipped). (2) long-timeline — timeRange 2000 in width 800 -> assert scaleX < 1. (3) tiny view — fitKeyframesToView(kfs, 50, 50, 40) returns finite positive scaleX/scaleY (no negative usable dimension).
- **Notes:** Existing scale>0 assertions still pass since epsilon>0. Independent of other findings.

#### `F107` · medium · data-corruption

**Location:** `packages/animation/src/PropertyBinding.ts:60`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** setProperty creates a plain object `{}` for missing intermediate segments of numeric-index paths, corrupting array-typed node fields (fills, strokes, effects, vertexOffsets) into non-iterable objects.

- **Root cause:** In setProperty (packages/animation/src/PropertyBinding.ts:52-64), the per-level clone (lines 55-60) uses the ternary `typeof existing === 'object' && existing !== null ? (Array.isArray ? [...] : {...}) : {}`. When an intermediate path segment is missing/undefined it ALWAYS falls through to a plain `{}`, ignoring whether the segment being created should be an array. For a numeric-index path onto an absent array field this corrupts it into a plain object: e.g. `setProperty(image, 'vertexOffsets.0.x', v)` -> `vertexOffsets = {'0':{x:v}}` (not an array), and `setProperty(regularGroup, 'fills.0.color', v)` -> `fills = {'0':{color:v}}`. Separately, when the array DOES exist but the numeric index is out of range (e.g. pasting `fills.3.color` onto a 1-fill shape), cloning the array and assigning index 3 produces a SPARSE array `[{..},<hole>,<hole>,{color}]`. Confirmed downstream breakage: ShapeRenderer.ts:447-450 indexes `vo[0].x..vo[3].x` (a partial/plain-object vertexOffsets yields undefined -> `undefined.x` throws or wrong distortion), and ShapeRenderer.ts:4082 `for (const fill of node.fills)` iterates holes as undefined -> `undefined.visible` throws. vertexOffsets is typed `[Vector2,Vector2,Vector2,Vector2]` and consumed by index across DirectSelectionTool/SelectionManager too.
- **Fix:** Two-part fix in setProperty's loop (lines 52-63). (1) When `existing` is not a non-null object, choose the new container based on the NEXT segment: `const cloned = /^\d+$/.test(parts[i + 1]!) ? [] : {};` instead of always `{}`. This makes `vertexOffsets.0.x` and group `fills.0.color` produce proper arrays. (2) Add a sparse-array guard: when the container `current` is an Array and the key being written (either an intermediate `parts[i]` or the leaf `parts[parts.length-1]`) is a numeric index whose value is >= the array's current length, skip the mutation and return the node effectively unchanged for that path (do not extend arrays with holes). Simplest implementation: compute the numeric leaf/intermediate index and if `Array.isArray(current) && idx > current.length` (or the existing array lacks that slot) return `root as N` without writing. Keep behavior identical for all in-range writes so existing tests (fills.0._, cornerRadius.0-3, strokes.0._) are unaffected. Document that setProperty never grows arrays (animation should only mutate existing indices).
- **Files:** `packages/animation/src/PropertyBinding.ts`
- **Test:** In packages/animation/src/PropertyBinding.test.ts (or PropertyBinding.image.test.ts): (a) `setProperty(imageNodeWithoutVertexOffsets, 'vertexOffsets.0.x', 5)` -> `Array.isArray(result.vertexOffsets)` is true and `result.vertexOffsets[0].x === 5`; (b) `setProperty(groupNodeWithoutFills, 'fills.0.color', {r:1,g:2,b:3,a:1})` -> `Array.isArray(result.fills)` is true; (c) out-of-range guard: `setProperty(rectWithOneFill, 'fills.3.color', color)` -> resulting `fills` contains no holes (assert `result.fills.every(f => f !== undefined)` and iterating `for (const f of result.fills)` never yields undefined), and the original single fill is preserved.
- **Notes:** setProperty is the core of applyAnimatedValues, so it runs every frame during playback/scrub/export. Part (1) is unambiguously correct and low-risk. Part (2) changes semantics (out-of-range indexed writes become no-ops) — this is the intended hardening but must be covered by the sparse-array test to avoid silently dropping a legitimate write elsewhere.

#### `F108` · medium · performance

**Location:** `packages/animation/src/PropertyBinding.ts:588`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** evaluateNodeAtFrame scans ALL timeline tracks for each node, making per-frame playback evaluation O(animatedNodes x totalTracks) — quadratic in scene size

- **Root cause:** evaluateNodeAtFrame (PropertyBinding.ts:581-599) linearly scans `timeline.tracks` filtering by nodeId. Callers loop over animated nodes and call it once per node: usePlayback.ts:36-46, Canvas.tsx (onion skin) :554-561, and packages/export/src/frameRenderer.ts:93-102. Net cost per frame is O(animatedNodes x totalTracks) = quadratic in scene size. Additionally evaluateTrack (lines 572-573) recomputes detectInterpolationType + getInterpolator per track per frame, uncached. No correctness bug today; purely a scalability gap versus the documented '60fps with 200+ characters' target. NOTE the reviewer's suggested invalidation ('rebuilt only when timeline.tracks changes') is unsafe: getOrCreateTrack (Timeline.ts:69) does `timeline.tracks.push(track)` IN PLACE, and the store's addKeyframeAtFrame (editorStore.ts:2011-2022) uses KeyframeManager then `set({ timeline: { ...timeline } })`, which copies `tracks` by reference — so the tracks ARRAY identity does NOT change when a new node is keyframed. A cache keyed by tracks-array identity would go stale and a newly-keyframed node would silently stop animating.
- **Fix:** Build a nodeId->tracks index once and have evaluateNodeAtFrame consume it. Preferred self-contained approach (only touches PropertyBinding.ts): add `const trackIndexCache = new WeakMap<Timeline, Map<string, PropertyTrack[]>>();` keyed by the TIMELINE OBJECT (not tracks array) — the store replaces the timeline object via `{ ...timeline }` on every edit (editorStore.ts:2022/2036/2047/2069, 1805/1826), so this key is invalidated on edits yet stable across playback frames. Add a helper `getTrackIndex(timeline)` that lazily builds `Map<nodeId, PropertyTrack[]>` (O(tracks)) and caches it; evaluateNodeAtFrame then does `const tracks = getTrackIndex(timeline).get(nodeId) ?? []` and iterates only those. Also cache per-track interpolation via `const trackInterpCache = new WeakMap<PropertyTrack, { type: InterpolationType; interp: Fn }>();` (track.property is immutable per track object, so this is always safe regardless of array mutation) and use it inside evaluateTrack. Net: O(tracks + nodes) per frame. Lower-staleness-risk alternative (more blast radius): export `buildTrackIndex(timeline)` + `evaluateNodeTracks(tracks, frame)` from PropertyBinding.ts and refactor the 3 callers to build the index once per frame and pass per-node lists — this removes all cross-frame caching. Recommend the WeakMap-by-timeline-object approach; document the store invariant it depends on.
- **Files:** `packages/animation/src/PropertyBinding.ts`
- **Test:** In PropertyBinding.test.ts: (a) cache-correctness / no-stale regression — create a timeline, addKeyframe for node A, assert evaluateNodeAtFrame(timeline, 'A', f) is correct; then simulate the store adding a new node B by pushing a track into the SAME tracks array AND creating a fresh timeline object (`const t2 = { ...timeline }`), and assert evaluateNodeAtFrame(t2, 'B', f) returns B's value (proves invalidation keys on the timeline object, not the tracks array); (b) repeated calls on the same timeline object return identical results (cache hit is correct); (c) evaluateNodeAtFrame for a nodeId absent from a many-track timeline returns an empty Map.
- **Notes:** Real but low urgency at current scene scale. The risk is entirely in cache invalidation: a wrong key turns a perf fix into a stale-animation correctness bug, hence the explicit correction to the reviewer's array-identity suggestion and the dedicated no-stale test.

#### `F109` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/animation/src/Timeline.ts:275`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** The rotation interpolator forces shortest-path wrapping to [-180, 180], making it impossible to animate rotations of more than 180 degrees between two keyframes; a 0-to-360 keyframe pair produces no motion at all.

- **Root cause:** packages/animation/src/Timeline.ts interpolators.rotation (lines 272-277) wraps the delta to [-180,180] via `const diff = ((((b - a + 180) % 360) + 360) % 360) - 180; return a + diff * t;`. This interpolator is bound to transform.rotation in packages/animation/src/PropertyBinding.ts getInterpolator (lines 462-463, case 'rotation') and detectInterpolationType (line 498). For a 0->360 keyframe pair diff evaluates to 0, so the editor shows zero motion; any span >180 deg takes the shortest arc instead of the authored one. Meanwhile the Lottie exporter (packages/export/src/lottie/lottieConverter.ts line 481, trackToLottieAnimated with -transform.rotation) emits the raw keyframed degrees which Lottie interpolates numerically -> a full spin, producing an editor-vs-export WYSIWYG divergence.
- **Fix:** Change interpolators.rotation in Timeline.ts to a plain numeric lerp identical to interpolators.number: `rotation: (a, b, t) => a + (b - a) * t`. This makes the editor honor the authored keyframe values (>180 and 360 spins work) and matches the numeric interpolation Lottie uses on export. Keep the named 'rotation' interpolator (PropertyBinding references it) rather than remapping to number, to minimize churn.
- **Files:** `packages/animation/src/Timeline.ts`
- **Test:** In Timeline.test.ts add a rotation-interpolation describe: create a number track, addKeyframe(track,0,0) and addKeyframe(track,10,360); interpolateValue(track,5,interpolators.rotation) should be close to 180 (was 0). Add 0->270 case: at t=5 expect ~135. Optionally add a PropertyBinding.test.ts case asserting evaluateTrack/getInterpolator('rotation') at the midpoint of a 0->360 rotation track yields 180.
- **Notes:** Grep confirms no existing test asserts shortest-path rotation values, so the change breaks nothing. This is a design-vs-domain decision documented by a comment (line 273) but undefended by tests and contradicted by export behavior; plain lerp is the WYSIWYG-correct default. A future opt-in shortest-path mode would need a new per-track/keyframe data field, out of scope here.

### Core geometry & paths

#### `F110` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/boolean/booleanOps.ts:176`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** performBoolean spreads polyB's polygons as separate clipping geometries, which breaks 'intersect' when polyB is a multi-part MultiPolygon: intersection(A, B1, B2) computes A∩B1∩B2 instead of A∩(B1∪B2).

- **Root cause:** performBoolean (booleanOps.ts:165-180) spreads polyB into separate clip geometries for every op: e.g. intersect does `polygonClipping.intersection(polyA as Polygon[], ...(polyB as Polygon[]))`. polygon-clipping's operation() (dist line 1685-1687, verified) constructs one MultiPolyIn per argument, so spreading a multi-part MultiPolygon polyB=[B1,B2] yields separate operands and intersection returns A ∩ B1 ∩ B2 instead of the intended A ∩ (B1 ∪ B2). Confirmed via the .d.ts signature `intersection(geom: Geom, ...geoms: Geom[])` with `Geom = Polygon | MultiPolygon`: passing polyB unspread is treated as a single unified operand. union and subtract are genuinely correct with the spread (A ∪ B1 ∪ B2 == A ∪ (B1∪B2); difference's signature is designed to subtract multiple clips, A − B1 − B2 == A − (B1∪B2)); xor is also correct because the polygons within a MultiPolygon are disjoint, so B1 ⊕ B2 == B1 ∪ B2. Only intersect is wrong, and only when the multi-part MultiPolygon is polyB (the 2nd+ operand). Today this is reachable only via ShapeRenderer.renderBooleanGroup (line 2335) fed by computeNestedBooleanPolygon (ShapeRenderer.ts:2506-2539), which can return a multi-part polyB for a nested boolean group used as a 2nd+ child under an intersect op.
- **Fix:** In performBoolean change the intersect case to pass polyB as a single geometry: `return polygonClipping.intersection(polyA, polyB);` (drop the `...(polyB as Polygon[])` spread; the `as Polygon[]` casts are unnecessary since Geom accepts MultiPolygon, but keeping/removing them is cosmetic). Recommended: for defensiveness and to kill the footgun entirely, also pass polyB unspread for union, subtract, and xor (all provably equivalent for these ops), so no op can ever mis-split a multi-part second operand. This is important because after F003 lands, nodeToPolygon can itself return a multi-part MultiPolygon (disjoint path pieces), making intersect over such a node as the 2nd operand reachable through booleanOperation and the eraser paths too.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/boolean/booleanOps.ts`
- **Test:** In booleanOps.test.ts (performBoolean describe): build polyA = single square (0,0)-(100,100) and polyB = a two-Polygon MultiPolygon of two DISJOINT squares, one overlapping A (e.g. (50,0)-(150,100)) and one far away (e.g. (500,500)-(600,600)); assert performBoolean(polyA, polyB, 'intersect') is NON-empty and equals A ∩ firstSquare (min x ~50, max x ~100). With the current spread bug this returns [] (empty) because A does not overlap the far square; the fix makes it non-empty. Optionally add a symmetric union/xor case to confirm no regression when unspreading the other ops.
- **Notes:** Real medium/correctness; rendering-only impact today (nested boolean group intersect) but broadened by F003. Order this first — it is a tiny, low-risk change and it makes F003's newly multi-part MultiPolygons safe under intersect. The existing intersect tests use single-Polygon operands and stay green.

#### `F112` · medium · crash

**Location:** `packages/core/src/path/bezier.ts:134`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** bezier.cubicLength recurses without a depth cap, so any non-finite control point causes infinite recursion and a RangeError stack-overflow crash.

- **Root cause:** bezier.cubicLength (bezier.ts:130-143) recurses via subdivide with no depth cap and no finite guard. Termination depends on `controlLength - chordLength < tolerance`; if any control point is non-finite, chordLength/controlLength are NaN, `NaN < tolerance` is false, and subdivide propagates NaN, so recursion never terminates -> RangeError stack overflow. Reachable on the render/tween path (shapeTween.ts:62/144, pathUtils.ts:344) if a malformed/NaN .quar import or an upstream non-finite coordinate reaches it. The reviewer's zero-vector-normalize example is NOT a valid trigger because vec2.normalize (math.ts) is guarded and returns {0,0}; the function-level defect stands regardless.
- **Fix:** Add a `depth: number = 0` parameter to cubicLength (after tolerance). At the top, if any of p0.x,p0.y,p1.x,p1.y,p2.x,p2.y,p3.x,p3.y is not Number.isFinite, return a finite fallback: Number.isFinite(chord) ? chord : 0 (chord = vec2.distance(p0,p3)). Add a hard cap: if depth >= 24 return (controlLength + chordLength) / 2. Pass depth+1 in both recursive calls (bezier.ts:140-141). 24 levels is far more than any finite curve needs (control-chord difference converges ~4x per level) so accuracy for legitimate curves is unchanged, while guaranteeing termination.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/path/bezier.ts`
- **Test:** In bezier.test.ts under describe('cubicLength'): assert bezier.cubicLength({x:0,y:0},{x:NaN,y:0},{x:1,y:1},{x:2,y:2}) returns a finite number without throwing (expect(Number.isFinite(result)).toBe(true)); repeat with Infinity in a control point. A regression of the current code would stack-overflow. Also keep an existing normal-curve assertion to confirm the depth param/cap did not change finite-input results.
- **Notes:** Real defect, but a robustness/defense-in-depth crash (needs non-finite input, which does not arise from normal finite user-drawn/keyframed data). Medium is fair. Consider also guarding the malformed-import path upstream, but that is out of scope for these files.

#### `F113` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/path/brushOutline.ts:236`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** generateRoundCap sweeps the semicircular cap backward into the stroke body instead of extending beyond the endpoint, producing a self-intersecting outline and no visible round cap.

- **Root cause:** generateRoundCap (brushOutline.ts:219-244) sweeps angle = startAngle + t\*PI (line 236). For an end cap (isStart=false) with tangent (1,0) at endpoint: perp=(0,1), leftPt=(xe,+hw), rightPt=(xe,-hw), fromPt=leftPt so startAngle=+PI/2; sweeping +PI puts the apex at t=0.5 -> angle=PI -> (center.x - radius, center.y) = (xe-hw,0), i.e. INTO the stroke body instead of beyond the endpoint. Start cap (isStart=true, fromPt=rightPt, startAngle=-PI/2) apex lands at (x0+hw,0), forward into the body. Because caps are spliced between the left side and reversed right side (brushOutline.ts:152-186), the closed polygon self-intersects and tapered ends (added only when startWidth/endWidth < 30% of max, lines 148-180) render as a notch/overlap instead of a round cap. Reachable via tapered pressure brush strokes (BrushTool.ts:326 and editorStore applyBrushStrokeProfile -> generateBrushOutline).
- **Fix:** In generateRoundCap change line 236 from `const angle = startAngle + t * Math.PI;` to `const angle = startAngle - t * Math.PI;`. Verified for both ends: end cap starts at leftPt(+PI/2), sweeps -PI so apex at angle 0 -> (center.x+radius, center.y) beyond the endpoint, ending at rightPt(-PI/2) at t=1 -> endpoints preserved. Start cap starts at rightPt(-PI/2), sweeps -PI so apex at angle -PI -> (center.x-radius, center.y) behind the start, ending at leftPt at t=1. Endpoints still land exactly on leftPt/rightPt so the splice into the outline stays continuous. Single-character sign flip; no other changes.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/path/brushOutline.ts`
- **Test:** In brushOutline.test.ts under describe('generateRoundCap'): end cap - generateRoundCap({x:100,y:0},{x:100,y:5},{x:100,y:-5},4,false); the apex is index 2 (t=0.5 of 4 segments); assert cap[2].x is close to 105 (beyond the endpoint), i.e. > 100 (currently ~95). Start cap - generateRoundCap({x:0,y:0},{x:0,y:5},{x:0,y:-5},4,true); assert cap[2].x is close to -5 (behind the start), i.e. < 0 (currently ~5). Also assert first/last cap points still equal the from/to offset points so continuity is preserved.
- **Notes:** Real. Existing generateRoundCap test only checks point count (line 190-196) and the taper test (line 78-110) only checks Y-spread, so neither locks in the wrong direction - low regression risk.

#### `F114` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/path/outlineStroke.ts:185`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** outlineStroke places the result at the wrong world position for rotated nodes because the local centering offset is not rotated (or skewed).

- **Root cause:** outlineStroke (outlineStroke.ts:183-186) computes the result's world position as position + S*center: worldX = node.transform.position.x + centerX*sx, worldY = position.y + centerY*sy, with no rotation. But mat3.compose (math.ts:249-273) builds T(position)*R(rotation)*S(scale)*T(-anchor), so a local point maps to world = position + R*S*(local-anchor). The result PathNode is re-centered to origin (points offset by -center) with the same rotation/scale, so to keep the stroke geometry at the same world location the centering offset must be R(rotation)*S*center, not S\*center. This is wrong for any rotated node whose local geometry center is off-origin - chiefly free-form/edited PathNodes (node.points not centered). Built-in shapes are unaffected because getShapeOutlinePoints centers rect/ellipse/polygon at origin (shapeToPath.ts:36-72) so center~=0. The skew part of the finding is a non-issue: compose takes no skew, so copying transform.skew on line 208 is inert.
- **Fix:** In outlineStroke.ts replace lines 183-186 with a rotation of the scaled center offset: const rad = (node.transform.rotation _ Math.PI) / 180; const cos = Math.cos(rad), sin = Math.sin(rad); const offX = centerX _ sx; const offY = centerY _ sy; const worldX = node.transform.position.x + (offX _ cos - offY _ sin); const worldY = node.transform.position.y + (offX _ sin + offY * cos). This matches mat3.rotate's convention (math.ts:156-160: a=cos,b=sin,c=-sin,d=cos -> transformPoint gives x'=cos*x - sin*y, y'=sin*x + cos\*y). Leave the skew copy on line 208 as-is (harmless) or drop it; no functional effect. No change needed to the point re-centering (lines 167-177).
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/path/outlineStroke.ts`
- **Test:** In outlineStroke.test.ts add a rotated off-origin path test: makeOpenPath([makeCorner(5,0), makeCorner(15,0)], 4) so the stroke-outline AABB center is ~ (10,0); set node.transform = { position:{x:0,y:0}, rotation:90, scale:{x:1,y:1}, anchor:{x:0.5,y:0.5}, skew:{x:0,y:0} }. Assert result.transform.position.x is close to 0 and result.transform.position.y is close to 10 (R(90)\*(10,0) = (0,10)). The current code yields (10,0), so this fails before the fix. Add a rotation:0 control asserting position stays ~ (10,0) to confirm non-rotated behavior is unchanged.
- **Notes:** Real but narrow: only rotated PathNodes with off-origin geometry are misplaced; origin-centered built-in shapes are unaffected. Skew claim is not real (compose ignores skew) - do not attempt a skew correction.

#### `F115` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/path/pathUtils.ts:972`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Stroke widthProfile is interpolated by tessellation vertex index instead of arc length, distorting the taper on paths with mixed straight and curved segments.

- **Root cause:** In generateStrokeOutlineVertices the widthProfile is sampled with t = i/(numVertices-1) (pathUtils.ts:972), where i is the tessellated vertex INDEX. bezier.tessellate (bezier.ts:149-184) is adaptive: a straight segment emits ~2 vertices while a tight curve emits many, so vertex index is not proportional to arc length. A stroke.widthProfile (set in editorStore.ts:705 and passed through ShapeRenderer.ts:3315/3345) applied to a path that is a long straight run followed by a curl therefore squeezes the whole taper into the densely-tessellated curled part and leaves the straight part near full width. generateBrushOutline (brushOutline.ts:33-93) already does this correctly by resampling on cumulative arc length.
- **Fix:** In generateStrokeOutlineVertices, before the main per-vertex loop, precompute cumulative arc length over `vertices`: cumDist[0]=0; for i=1..numVertices-1 cumDist[i]=cumDist[i-1]+hypot(x*i-x*{i-1}, y*i-y*{i-1}); totalLength=cumDist[numVertices-1]. Then in the widthProfile branch (line 972) replace `const t = numVertices > 1 ? i / (numVertices - 1) : 0;` with `const t = totalLength > GEOMETRY_EPSILON ? cumDist[i] / totalLength : (numVertices > 1 ? i/(numVertices-1) : 0);`. Only the widthProfile branch changes; when no profile is supplied behavior is unchanged. This mirrors generateBrushOutline's arc-length resampling. GEOMETRY_EPSILON is already defined at module scope (pathUtils.ts:11).
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/path/pathUtils.ts`
- **Test:** In pathUtils.test.ts, add a mixed-spacing test: vertices = [0,0, 100,0, 101,0, 102,0, 103,0] (numVertices=5) so index and arc length diverge (index 1 is at 100/103 ~= 0.97 of the length but 0.25 of the index). Call with width=10, closed=false, align='center', widthProfile=[1,0] (linear taper). The left side is at outline indices 0..; leftSide[1] is outline[2],outline[3].
