With arc-length sampling the multiplier at vertex 1 is ~1-100/103 ~= 0.03, so outline[3] (leftSide[1].y = 5\*multiplier) should be ~0.15 (assert < 0.5). With the current index-based code it would be ~3.75. Add a symmetric assertion on the right side.
- **Notes:** Real. No existing tests cover widthProfile in this function, so regression risk is low. Independent of F035 though both edit generateStrokeOutlineVertices.

#### `F142` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/tweening/shapeTween.ts:278`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** addPointsToPath drops the corrected handleIn produced by segment subdivision, so the point following any subdivided curved segment keeps its original full-length handleIn and the normalized path is geometrically wrong.

- **Root cause:** In packages/core/src/tweening/shapeTween.ts, subdivideSegmentPoints (lines 111-121) correctly shortens the endpoint's handleIn using the last de Casteljau sub-curve's incoming control point (curve.p2, i.e. bezier.subdivide's right.p2 — confirmed bezier.ts:122, splitAtMultiple pushes the trailing right-curve at bezier.ts:400). But addPointsToPath discards that corrected endpoint: line 278's loop `for (j = 0; j < subPoints.length - 1; j++)` pushes only 'all but the last' sub-point, dropping the endpoint that carries the shortened handleIn. The endpoint is instead re-created with its ORIGINAL (full-length) handleIn in every path: (a) the next segment's un-subdivided start via clonePathPoint(p0) at line 273; (b) the next subdivided segment's start subPoints[0], which is clonePathPoint(p0) whose handleIn subdivideSegmentPoints never touches; (c) the open-path tail push clonePathPoint(points[len-1]) at line 286; (d) the closed-path wraparound endpoint points[0] == result[0], which is pushed at seg=0 (line 273/276) and never re-assigned. Because the endpoint's handleIn spans the whole pre-split segment instead of just the last sub-segment, the last sub-segment's cubic bulges; interpolatePathPoints returns source exactly at t=0 (and target at t=1), so the tween's first/last frame no longer matches the real shape — a visible pop. No existing test asserts endpoint handle magnitudes (the closest, 'preserves handles during normalization' at test line 153, only checks result.source[1].type==='smooth'), so it is uncaught.
- **Fix:** Carry the subdivided endpoint's corrected handleIn forward onto whichever point represents that endpoint in the result. In addPointsToPath, declare `let pendingHandleIn: Vector2 | null = null;` before the `for (seg...)` loop (Vector2 is already imported at line 8). (1) In the `extraForSeg === 0` branch: replace `result.push(clonePathPoint(p0))` with `const startClone = clonePathPoint(p0); if (pendingHandleIn !== null) { startClone.handleIn = pendingHandleIn; startClone.type = 'smooth'; } pendingHandleIn = null; result.push(startClone);`. (2) In the `else` (subdivided) branch: after computing `subPoints`, do `if (pendingHandleIn !== null) { subPoints[0]!.handleIn = pendingHandleIn; subPoints[0]!.type = 'smooth'; } pendingHandleIn = null;` BEFORE the push loop, then after pushing subPoints[0..length-2] set `pendingHandleIn = subPoints[subPoints.length - 1]!.handleIn;` (this is the corrected endpoint handleIn; safe to reference directly since that sub-point is otherwise discarded, or clone as {x,y} to be defensive). (3) After the loop, for the open-path tail: `const lastClone = clonePathPoint(points[points.length - 1]!); if (pendingHandleIn !== null) lastClone.handleIn = pendingHandleIn; result.push(lastClone);`. (4) For the closed path, add an else: `if (pendingHandleIn !== null && result.length > 0) result[0]!.handleIn = pendingHandleIn;` so the wraparound endpoint (result[0]) receives its shortened handleIn. Do NOT alter handleOut anywhere — the endpoint's handleOut belongs to the following (untouched) segment and must stay original; the finding concerns handleIn only. Setting type='smooth' on the receiving point mirrors subdivideSegmentPoints' own endpoint handling and is optional for rendered geometry (curves are defined by handles regardless of type) but keeps output self-consistent.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/tweening/shapeTween.ts`, `packages/core/src/tweening/shapeTween.test.ts`
- **Test:** In shapeTween.test.ts under the normalizePointCount describe, add a test that subdivides a symmetric open arc and asserts the endpoint handleIn is shortened. E.g.: `const src = [smooth(0,0, 0,0, 40,0), smooth(100,0, -40,0, 0,0)]; const tgt = [corner(0,0), corner(50,0), corner(100,0)]; const { source } = normalizePointCount(src, tgt, false, false);` then `expect(source).toHaveLength(3);` and `expect(source[2].handleIn!.x).toBeCloseTo(-20, 0);` (splitting the symmetric cubic near t=0.5 gives right-curve p2 = lerp((60,0),(100,0),0.5) = (80,0), so handleIn = (80-100, 0) = (-20,0); before the fix it stays -40). Also assert `Math.abs(source[2].handleIn!.x)` is < 30 to make intent explicit. Add a second test for the closed-path wraparound: build a closed path whose LAST (wraparound) segment is the longest so extras land on it (e.g. `[corner(0,0), corner(10,0), corner(10,10), corner(-90,0)]` closed, subdivided +1), and assert `result.source[0].handleIn` is non-null and shorter than the original wraparound-segment handle, proving result[0] received the carried handleIn.
- **Notes:** Reviewer's description and suggested fix are accurate. Existing tests assert only lengths, types, and positions (not endpoint handle magnitudes), so this change should not break them. The degenerate-segment branch (subdivideSegmentPoints lines 63-71) returns an endpoint clone with original handleIn, but for a zero-length segment the handle correction is moot, so carrying it is harmless. Referencing subPoints[last].handleIn directly is safe because that sub-point is never pushed; clone to {x,y} only if defensively avoiding shared references.

### Export (Lottie/PNG/sprite)

#### `F143` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieKeyframes.ts:178`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** F061  
**Finding:** positionTracksToLottie takes easing only from the X track, so easing on Y-only (or Y-differing) position/scale animation is silently dropped to linear.

- **Root cause:** positionTracksToLottie:178-179 selects the segment easing exclusively from the X track: `const nextKfX = trackX?.keyframes.find(kf => kf.time === nextT); const easing = nextKfX?.easing ?? 'linear'`. When trackX is undefined (Y-only animation), or when X has no keyframe exactly at nextT (misaligned tracks — see the 'handles misaligned track times' test at lottieKeyframes.test.ts:475-489), nextKfX is undefined and easing falls back to 'linear', discarding whatever easing the Y keyframe carried. Additionally, lines 182-183 duplicate the single X tangent into both output dimensions (`x: [tangents.i.x[0], tangents.i.x[0]]`), so even when both tracks animate, Y's own easing is never applied to the Y dimension.
- **Fix:** In positionTracksToLottie change the easing lookup to prefer X's keyframe at nextT but fall back to Y's keyframe at nextT before defaulting to linear: `const nextKf = trackX?.keyframes.find(kf => kf.time === nextT) ?? trackY?.keyframes.find(kf => kf.time === nextT); const easing = nextKf?.easing ?? 'linear';`. Preferred (addresses the duplication too): compute tangentsX from the X keyframe's easing and tangentsY from the Y keyframe's easing independently, and assign result.i = { x: [tangentsX.i.x[0], tangentsY.i.x[0]], y: [tangentsX.i.y[0], tangentsY.i.y[0]] } (and o analogously), so each dimension carries its own easing. Handle the null-tangent case consistently with F061 (map/bake) rather than silently dropping. Coordinate with F061 since both edit lines 178-184.
- **Files:** `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieKeyframes.ts`, `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieKeyframes.test.ts`
- **Test:** positionTracksToLottie with trackX undefined and trackY = [{0,0},{30,200, easing: cubicBezier [0,0,0.58,1]}] asserts the exported first keyframe has i/o tangents equal to that easing's tangents (currently they are absent because easing resolves to 'linear'). Add a second test with misaligned X/Y tracks where the Y keyframe at nextT carries a cubic easing and X has none at that time, asserting the easing survives.
- **Notes:** Real and correctly described. It overlaps F061's multi-value observation (both touch the null-tangent branch and the same 178-184 block); implement together, doing F061's mapping first so the fallback easing actually converts to tangents instead of hitting the same null path. The per-dimension-easing improvement is optional but is the fully-correct form and removes the tangent-duplication defect noted in the finding.

#### `F144` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/export/src/spriteSheet.ts:131`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** exportSpriteSheet with multiplier > 1 draws oversized frame canvases into cells laid out at unscaled size, making frames overlap and corrupting the atlas.

- **Root cause:** In packages/export/src/spriteSheet.ts the atlas layout is computed from the UNSCALED frameWidth/frameHeight (packGrid/packMaxRects at lines 66-73) and the atlas canvas is sized to packResult.atlasWidth/Height (76-86), but createFrameRenderer produces a canvas of ceil(width*multiplier) x ceil(height*multiplier) pixels (frameRenderer.ts:55-60). The blit at spriteSheet.ts:131 uses the 3-argument atlasCtx.drawImage(frameCanvas, rect.x, rect.y), which draws the frame at its native (scaled) pixel size. With multiplier>1 each frame is drawn multiplier-times larger than its cell, so frames overlap and overflow the atlas. The rotated branch (124-129) has the identical 3-arg defect but is unreachable here because packMaxRects is called with allowRotation defaulting to false, so rect.rotated is never true in this path.
- **Fix:** Recommended (preserves multiplier as a true resolution scale, matching PngSequence semantics): in exportSpriteSheet compute scaledFrameWidth = Math.ceil(frameWidth _ multiplier) and scaledFrameHeight = Math.ceil(frameHeight _ multiplier) (mirroring frameRenderer.ts:55-56 so cell size exactly matches the frame canvas), and use those scaled values in the packGrid/packMaxRects calls (lines 66-73) and, if desired, scale padding by multiplier. The atlas then sizes to the scaled packResult dims and the existing 3-arg drawImage(frameCanvas, rect.x, rect.y) becomes correct because frameCanvas dims now equal rect.width/height. Pass scaledFrameWidth/scaledFrameHeight (not the raw options values) into generateSpriteSheetMetadata's frameWidth/frameHeight so metadata frame regions stay consistent with the scaled atlas. Simpler low-effort alternative (multiplier acts only as supersampling AA, atlas stays logical size, zero metadata changes): keep the unscaled layout and change the blit to the 5-arg form atlasCtx.drawImage(frameCanvas, rect.x, rect.y, rect.width, rect.height), and in the rotated branch use atlasCtx.drawImage(frameCanvas, 0, 0, rect.height, rect.width). Pick one; do not mix. Either eliminates the overlap/corruption.
- **Files:** `packages/export/src/spriteSheet.ts`
- **Test:** Add a test in packages/export/src/spriteSheet.test.ts that exercises exportSpriteSheet with multiplier=2. vi.mock('./frameRenderer') so createFrameRenderer returns a handle whose preloadTextures resolves and whose renderFrame returns a stub canvas sized frameWidth*2 x frameHeight*2; stub document.createElement('canvas').getContext('2d') with a spy that records every drawImage call and provides no-op save/restore/translate/rotate/fillRect plus a toBlob that yields a Blob. Assert that (a) the atlas canvas width/height are large enough to contain every drawn frame at its actual drawn size, and (b) the drawn destination rectangles for the frames are pairwise non-overlapping (for the recommended fix the atlas is 2x and rects match; for the alternative fix assert each drawImage was called with dWidth=frameWidth and dHeight=frameHeight). This fails on the current 3-arg unscaled-layout code because drawn frames overlap.
- **Notes:** Only external @quar/export API consumers passing multiplier>1 are affected; the shipped ExportDialog reimplements compositing inline and hardcodes multiplier:1 (ExportDialog.tsx:247), so the app UI is not impacted. Independent of F145 (does not require changing generateSpriteSheetMetadata's logic even under the recommended fix, only the args passed to it).

#### `F145` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/export/src/spriteSheetMetadata.ts:58`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Metadata includes frames that failed to pack (x/y = -1 sentinel), so consumers read garbage regions for frames that are not in the atlas.

- **Root cause:** packMaxRects (packages/export/src/binPacking.ts:144-155) pushes a sentinel rect {x:-1, y:-1, width, height} for any frame that does not fit the 4096x4096 bin, and atlasWidth/atlasHeight are computed from usedW/usedH covering only placed frames (lines 171-182). exportSpriteSheet skips blitting these (spriteSheet.ts:112: `if (!rect || rect.x < 0) continue`), so the atlas contains no pixels for them. But generateSpriteSheetMetadata (spriteSheetMetadata.ts:58) iterates packResult.rects with no filter and emits `frame: { x: -1, y: -1, w, h }` entries pointing outside the atlas. TexturePacker-JSON consumers (PixiJS, Phaser) will sample out-of-bounds/wrapped UVs for those frames rather than failing. Only reachable via the packed layout (packMaxRects) on bin overflow; packGrid never emits sentinels.
- **Fix:** In generateSpriteSheetMetadata, skip sentinel rects inside the loop at spriteSheetMetadata.ts:58 by adding `if (rect.x < 0 || rect.y < 0) continue;` as the first statement of the for-body. This keeps the metadata consistent with the exportSpriteSheet blit-skip (spriteSheet.ts:112) and the binPacking sentinel convention. Do NOT throw here — the blit path already silently drops overflow frames, so throwing would be inconsistent; surfacing a loud warning/error when frames overflow the bin is a larger, separate improvement out of scope for this finding.
- **Files:** `packages/export/src/spriteSheetMetadata.ts`
- **Test:** Add a test in packages/export/src/spriteSheet.test.ts (generateSpriteSheetMetadata describe block) that passes a hand-built PackResult mixing a valid rect (frameIndex:0, x:0,y:0,w:64,h:64) with a sentinel rect (frameIndex:1, x:-1,y:-1,w:64,h:64) and asserts Object.keys(meta.frames).length === 1 and that no emitted frame has frame.x < 0 or frame.y < 0. This fails on current code which emits the -1 entry.
- **Notes:** No existing test constructs sentinel (x:-1) rects, so filtering them will not break the current suite (the existing 'uses fallback filename for out-of-range rects' test uses valid x:0,y:0). Independent of F144.

#### `F192` · medium · data-loss

**Location:** `packages/export/src/exportUtils.ts:33`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** A filename pattern without the {N} placeholder generates identical filenames for every frame, so JSZip silently overwrites and the exported ZIP contains only the last frame.

- **Root cause:** generateFrameFilenames (packages/export/src/exportUtils.ts:33) builds each name as `pattern.replace('{N}', paddedFrame) + '.' + extension`. String.replace with no match returns the pattern unchanged, so if the pattern lacks the {N} placeholder every frame in the loop gets an identical filename. Consumers key on that name: JSZip's zip.file(name, blob) stores entries in a name-keyed map, so identical names overwrite and only the last frame survives (pngSequence.ts:80 and ExportDialog.tsx:184); the same collision also collapses generateSpriteSheetMetadata's `frames` Record to a single key. The ExportDialog Pattern field (ExportDialog.tsx:471-478) is unvalidated free text with only a placeholder, so a user typing e.g. 'frame' silently loses all but one frame from the ZIP.
- **Fix:** Fix at the source in generateFrameFilenames so all callers are protected: detect whether the pattern contains the placeholder once (`const hasPlaceholder = pattern.includes('{N}')`) and inside the loop build the filename as `(hasPlaceholder ? pattern.replace('{N}', paddedFrame) : pattern + '_' + paddedFrame) + '.' + extension`. This guarantees unique, order-preserving filenames even when {N} is missing. Optionally (defense in depth, not required) add validation/warning in ExportDialog.tsx near the Pattern input to nudge users to include {N}, but the util change alone resolves the data loss for both the package API and the app.
- **Files:** `packages/export/src/exportUtils.ts`
- **Test:** Add a test in packages/export/src/frameRenderer.test.ts (generateFrameFilenames describe block) asserting generateFrameFilenames('frame', 0, 2, 'png') returns three DISTINCT names (e.g. ['frame_0.png','frame_1.png','frame_2.png']) and that new Set(names).size === names.length. This fails on current code which returns ['frame.png','frame.png','frame.png'].
- **Notes:** All existing generateFrameFilenames tests use patterns that already contain {N} ('frame*{N}','shot*{N}','f\_{N}'), so appending-when-missing does not regress them. Independent of F144/F145.

### Fonts & text

#### `F111` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/font/glyphConverter.ts:62`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Every anchor adjacent to a curve segment is unconditionally marked type 'smooth', so sharp glyph corners become symmetry-enforced points that distort when edited.

- **Root cause:** glyphConverter.glyphPathToSubpaths marks curve-adjacent anchors 'smooth' without any collinearity test: newly pushed curve endpoints are hardcoded type:'smooth' (line 76-77 for C, 124 for Q); the previous point is upgraded corner→smooth whenever it merely has a handleOut (62-64 for C, 112-114 for Q); and Z-close upgrades the first point to smooth on transferring a handleIn (138-139). None checks whether handleIn and handleOut are actually collinear. DirectSelectionTool handle-drag (line 449-455) routes non-ctrl drags through updateHandleWithSymmetry (pointUtils.ts:105-141), which for type 'smooth' forces the opposite handle to −normalize(draggedHandle)\*len (making it anti-collinear) AND fabricates an opposite handle when it is null. Therefore a genuine glyph cusp (two non-collinear handles) or a single-handle endpoint that is mislabeled 'smooth' gets distorted the moment its handle is dragged. The mislabel does NOT affect the rendered curve/tessellation (tessellatePathToVertices reads handleIn/handleOut, not type) — only interactive editing.
- **Fix:** Add a helper isSmoothTangent(handleIn, handleOut) that returns true only when both are non-null and vec2.dot(vec2.normalize(handleIn), vec2.normalize(handleOut)) < −0.999 (anti-collinear = true smooth tangent). Change curve endpoints to default to type:'corner' at push time (lines 76-77 and 124). Replace the three unconditional upgrades with the geometric test evaluated when BOTH of a point's handles are known: (a) in C and Q, after setting prevPt.handleOut, set prevPt.type = isSmoothTangent(prevPt.handleIn, prevPt.handleOut) ? 'smooth' : 'corner' (this also correctly upgrades the previously-pushed point once its outgoing curve arrives); (b) in the Z-close branch, after transferring last.handleIn to first, set first.type = isSmoothTangent(first.handleIn, first.handleOut) ? 'smooth' : 'corner'. Net effect: only genuinely collinear-handle anchors become 'smooth'; single-handle points and cusps stay 'corner'.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/font/glyphConverter.ts`, `packages/core/src/font/glyphConverter.test.ts`
- **Test:** Add (1) a cusp test: M(0,0) → C into point P → C out of P with the two handles NON-collinear, assert P.type==='corner' and both handles preserved; (2) a smooth test: handles collinear/opposite through P, assert P.type==='smooth'; (3) a single-handle test (M→single C→Z open) asserting the lone-handle endpoints are 'corner'. Update existing assertions that currently expect single-handle points to be 'smooth' (glyphConverter.test.ts lines 78, 85, 106) to expect 'corner'.
- **Notes:** Type label is edit-only metadata; no rendering/tessellation consumer reads it, so runtime regression risk is low. Main cost is updating the 3 existing test expectations that assert single-handle glyph endpoints are 'smooth'. Shares the file with F180 (soft coordination, not a hard dependency).

### Rendering & GL

#### `F038` · medium · performance

**Location:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts:2062`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Compound-path rendering re-runs applyCornerRadius + tessellatePathToVertices on every contour every frame, even when the node has no visible strokes.

- **Root cause:** In renderPath's compound-path branch (ShapeRenderer.ts:2043-2081), after rendering fills from the cached multi-contour tessellation, the code unconditionally loops over allContours (2059-2079) and runs applyCornerRadius(contour,true) + tessellatePathToVertices(...) for EVERY contour EVERY frame, then only inside that loop checks `for (const stroke of node.strokes) if (stroke.visible && stroke.width>0)`. When node.strokes is empty or all strokes invisible, the per-contour re-tessellation is pure waste. Additionally the stroke cache never engages: renderStroke is called with id `node.id+'_s'` (2070), but getCachedStrokeOutline (1153) looks up geometryCache.get('node.id_s') which is never populated (multi-contour tessellation is cached under node.id, not the '\_s' id), so generateStrokeOutlineVertices + earcut (1160-1171) also recompute every frame even when strokes exist.
- **Fix:** 1) Compute `const hasVisibleStroke = node.strokes.some(s => s.visible && s.width>0)` and wrap the entire contour re-tessellation loop (2059-2079) in `if (hasVisibleStroke)`, so no work happens when there are no strokes. 2) Avoid re-tessellating per frame: extend getCachedMultiContourTessellation to also store the per-contour Float32Array[] (it already computes contourArrays at 2578-2582 and stores contourVertexCounts at 2649-2656; add `contours: contourArrays` to the cache entry). Then in renderPath's stroke branch, read cached.contours instead of recomputing applyCornerRadius+tessellatePathToVertices. 3) Fix stroke id collision: give each contour a distinct id (e.g. `node.id + '_c' + index`) so per-contour stroke outlines cache independently, matching the text path pattern (renderText uses node.id+`_tc${ci}` at 2164).
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts`
- **Test:** Spy on tessellatePathToVertices (or a wrapper): render a compound PathNode with subpaths and empty strokes twice; assert tessellatePathToVertices is called only during the first (cache-miss) render, not the second. Second test: compound path WITH a visible stroke rendered twice — assert the stroke outline isn't regenerated on the second frame once per-contour caching is in place.
- **Notes:** Reviewer refinements verified: the shared '\_s' id cannot be fixed by just creating a cache entry because strokeKey (1152) is `${width}:${align}[:wp]` and does not encode contour identity — all contours would collide on one entry. Distinct per-contour ids are required.

#### `F116` · medium · performance

**Location:** `packages/core/src/rendering/EffectRenderer.ts:164`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** compositeWithBlendMode performs a synchronous full-canvas gl.readPixels plus texSubImage2D upload per blended node per frame, stalling the GPU pipeline and breaking the 60fps target.

- **Root cause:** compositeWithBlendMode (EffectRenderer.ts:144-217) captures the current default-framebuffer content with a synchronous gl.readPixels(0,0,canvasWidth,canvasHeight,RGBA,UNSIGNED_BYTE, resolvePixelBuffer) (lines 163-172) and then re-uploads the identical pixels into dstFBO.texture via gl.texSubImage2D (lines 173-184). readPixels forces a GPU->CPU pipeline flush/stall. This runs once per non-normal-blend-mode node per frame: renderNodeWithEffects calls it at line 123, and ShapeRenderer invokes renderNodeWithEffects per node (ShapeRenderer.ts:1317, 1407, 1496). On a 1920x1080 canvas at devicePixelRatio 2 that is ~33MB readback + ~33MB upload per blended node per frame; with a few blended layers during playback this dominates frame time and drops well below the 60fps target. The readback exists to avoid blitFramebuffer from the multisampled default FB (antialias defaults to true, WebGLRenderer.ts:64), which fails on Chrome/ANGLE.
- **Fix:** Primary (small, targeted): replace the readPixels + bindTexture + texSubImage2D block (EffectRenderer.ts:159-184) and the resolvePixelBuffer field (line 33) / dispose reset (line 405) with a single GPU-side copy: `gl.bindFramebuffer(gl.FRAMEBUFFER, null); gl.bindTexture(gl.TEXTURE_2D, dstFBO.texture); gl.copyTexSubImage2D(gl.TEXTURE_2D, 0, 0, 0, 0, 0, canvasWidth, canvasHeight);`. copyTexSubImage2D reads from the (default) read framebuffer with an implicit MSAA resolve and writes directly into the texture — no CPU transfer, no buffer allocation — while sidestepping the blitFramebuffer multisample restriction that motivated the original readback. IMPORTANT caveat for the implementer: verify copyTexSubImage2D succeeds from the antialiased default framebuffer on target browsers/ANGLE (same MSAA concern that blocked blitFramebuffer); if it errors with INVALID_OPERATION, fall back to the robust alternative. Robust alternative (larger, the reviewer's suggestion): render the whole scene into an intermediate non-multisampled offscreen FBO in the Canvas render loop, then blend-mode compositing samples/blits that FBO texture directly (no default-FB readback) and a single final pass blits the scene FBO to the default framebuffer; this requires threading the scene texture through renderNodeWithEffects/compositeWithBlendMode and restructuring Canvas.tsx + ShapeRenderer.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/rendering/EffectRenderer.ts`
- **Test:** New EffectRenderer.test.ts (or extend once created): drive compositeWithBlendMode with a non-normal blend mode and assert gl.readPixels is NOT called and gl.copyTexSubImage2D IS called with (TEXTURE_2D,0,0,0,0,0,canvasWidth,canvasHeight); also assert resolvePixelBuffer is no longer allocated. Requires the same mock-GL extensions as F036 plus copyTexSubImage2D/activeTexture/blendFuncSeparate/isEnabled stubs. If the robust scene-FBO route is taken instead, the test asserts compositeWithBlendMode consumes the passed scene texture and performs no readPixels.
- **Notes:** Real medium perf bug. The copyTexSubImage2D fix keeps filesToChange to EffectRenderer.ts only and is low-to-medium risk, but carries the MSAA-from-default-FB caveat noted above — the implementer must confirm it on Chrome/ANGLE before committing. If instead the scene-FBO restructure is chosen, that variant allocates a persistent canvas-sized FBO and should land after F036 (dependsOn F036) so the pool-eviction fix doesn't churn the scene target; the copyTexSubImage2D variant has no such dependency.

#### `F117` · medium · cpu-gpu-skinning-parity

**Location:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts:335`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** GPU skinning shader's zero-weight fallback uses the raw bind-pose LOCAL position (`skinned = pos`) while CPU deformVertices transforms zero-weight vertices through skinData.meshBindMatrix, so unweighted vertices render in the wrong place on the GPU path whenever the mesh's bind transform is non-iden…

- **Root cause:** The GPU skinned vertex shaders use `if (totalWeight <= 0.0) skinned = pos;` (SKINNED_VERTEX_SHADER:335 and SKINNED_GRADIENT_VERTEX_SHADER:368), i.e. the raw bind-pose LOCAL position. CPU deformVertices (cpuSkinning.ts:108-113 and 130-134) transforms zero-weight / no-influence vertices through skinData.meshBindMatrix (`result = meshBindMatrix * v`). For weighted vertices the GPU path already folds meshBindMatrix into each bone matrix (gpuSkinning.ts:140 finalMatrix = boneTimesIBM × meshBindMatrix), so weighted verts match; only the zero-weight fallback diverges. Whenever meshBindMatrix is non-identity, unweighted GPU vertices render at the wrong location.
- **Fix:** 1) Add `uniform mat3 u_meshBind;` to both SKINNED_VERTEX_SHADER and SKINNED_GRADIENT_VERTEX_SHADER and change the fallback to `if (totalWeight <= 0.0) skinned = u_meshBind * pos;`. 2) Add 'u_meshBind' to the uniform name lists for skinnedProgram (line 768) and skinnedGradientProgram. 3) In renderSkinnedFillsGPU, before drawing, upload the mesh-bind matrix on the active skinned program: convert skinData.meshBindMatrix (6-el affine [a,b,c,d,tx,ty]) to a column-major mat3 Float32Array [a,b,0, c,d,0, tx,ty,1] and call gl.uniformMatrix3fv(program.uniforms['u_meshBind'], false, m) for both skinnedProgram and skinnedGradientProgram (mirroring uploadBoneMatrices).
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts`
- **Test:** Rigging-level parity test: for a mesh with a non-identity meshBindMatrix and at least one vertex with empty influences, compute CPU deformVertices output and the GPU shader's fallback formula (u_meshBind \* pos) for that vertex and assert they match. At ShapeRenderer level, assert gl.uniformMatrix3fv is called with the converted meshBind matrix for the skinned program during a skinned render.
- **Notes:** Reviewer correctly excludes the >32-bone case: renderSkinnedNode only takes the GPU path when boneCount <= MAX_BONES_GPU=32 (3391-3396), else full CPU fallback. Genuinely reachable GPU divergence: overflow verts beyond skinData.vertices.length, and verts normalized/painted to empty influences (incl. the transient state right after createSkinBinding before auto-weights).

#### `F118` · medium · performance

**Location:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts:2084`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** renderPath clones every path point (applyCornerRadius) and builds an O(points) geometry-key string on every frame for every path node, even on tessellation-cache hits

- **Root cause:** renderPath (ShapeRenderer.ts:2084) calls `applyCornerRadius(node.points, node.closed)` unconditionally every frame before getCachedTessellation. applyCornerRadius (pathUtils.ts:514) always allocates a new result array and clonePathPoint()s every point (519,528,534,540...), so on cache hits the clone is pure garbage. Then getCachedTessellation → buildGeometryKey(node) (416,424-443) iterates every point/handle to build an O(points) string key every frame purely to validate the cache entry. Both allocate immediately-discarded garbage each frame for every path node.
- **Fix:** 1) Skip applyCornerRadius when unnecessary: before line 2084 compute `const hasCorner = node.points.some(p => p.cornerRadius && p.cornerRadius > 0)` (also account for defaultRadius if used) and pass `hasCorner ? applyCornerRadius(node.points, node.closed) : node.points` into getCachedTessellation. Apply the same guard in the compound-path branch (2061) and getCachedMultiContourTessellation (2580). 2) (Optional, larger) Replace the per-frame buildGeometryKey string with a monotonically bumped version/dirty counter on the node invalidated from nodeChanged, or a cheap numeric hash, to avoid the O(points) string on cache hits.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts`
- **Test:** Spy on applyCornerRadius (or wrap it): render a PathNode with no cornerRadius on any point twice and assert applyCornerRadius is not invoked (or invoked 0 times) on the render frames. Render a path WITH a cornerRadius point and assert corners are still rounded (unchanged output).
- **Notes:** Reviewer nuance verified: the applyCornerRadius clone is trivially removable on cache hits; eliminating buildGeometryKey's O(points) string needs a dirty-flag/version refactor and is optional. The cheap win (corner-radius pre-scan) should ship first.

#### `F119` · medium · cache-invalidation

**Location:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts:2146`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Text tessellated with a fallback font is cached under a geoKey that omits the actually-used font, so the text keeps rendering in the wrong font after the requested font finishes loading.

- **Root cause:** renderText calls fm.getFontOrFallback(node.fontFamily, node.fontWeight) (ShapeRenderer.ts:2114) which, when the requested family/weight is not yet loaded, returns the first cached font (FontManager.ts:152-160). The resulting glyph tessellation is cached under geoKey = buildGeometryKey(node) (2143) whose text case (445) encodes the REQUESTED family/weight, not the font actually used. When the real font finishes downloading, the cached entry still satisfies `cached.geoKey === geoKey` at 2146, so the stale fallback-font glyphs render forever — and nothing calls invalidateCache/clearCache to evict it. User sees the wrong typeface until they edit content/size (which changes geoKey).
- **Fix:** Make the text cache key reflect the font actually resolved and invalidate on font loads. Simplest: add a monotonic `loadGeneration` counter to FontManager, incremented in loadFont on each successful load, exposed via a getter. In renderText compute `const geoKey = buildGeometryKey(node) + ':fg' + fm.loadGeneration` (use the same variable for both the read at 2146 and the cache write at 2248-2249). Optionally also append whether the exact font resolved (`fm.getFont(family,weight) != null`) so keys differ for fallback vs real. When loadGeneration bumps, the stale entry no longer matches and text re-tessellates with the now-loaded font. Do the same for renderTextWithOverride if it ever caches (currently it does not, so no change needed there).
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts`, `packages/core/src/font/FontManager.ts`
- **Test:** With FontManager holding only a fallback font, render a text node (requesting an unloaded family) and capture the tessellated glyph vertices. Load the requested font (bumping loadGeneration), render again, and assert the tessellation was recomputed (different vertices / cache miss) rather than reused.
- **Notes:** buildGeometryKey is a free function taking only Node, so it cannot see FontManager state — the generation suffix must be appended in renderText where fm is in scope. Only renderText caches text geometry, so the change is localized.

#### `F120` · medium · memory-leak

**Location:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts:2439`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** F037  
**Finding:** Boolean-group tessellation cache grows without bound while children move: the cache key embeds child world transforms, and old entries are never evicted.

- **Root cause:** renderBooleanGroup keys its tessellation cache by buildBooleanGroupCacheKey (ShapeRenderer.ts:2306,2544-2559), which embeds every child's world transform (a,b,c,d to 4dp, tx,ty to 2dp). Entries are stored in geometryCache (2436) and booleanRingCache (2439) and never evicted (invalidateCache/clearCache have no production callers — see F037). Interactively dragging/resizing a child mints a fresh key on nearly every pointermove (translation quantized to 0.01px), so both maps grow unbounded for the renderer lifetime. Separately, deleted boolean groups (and their old transform-keyed entries) leak because Canvas nodeRemoved never invalidates.
- **Fix:** Key boolean-group cache entries by the group node id instead of the transform-embedding string, and store the transform-key inside the entry for staleness comparison: use geometryCache.get(groupNode.id); if entry.boolKey !== currentTransformKey, recompute and overwrite (evicting the previous vertices) and set entry.boolKey = currentTransformKey; likewise store booleanRingCache under groupNode.id. This bounds each group to a single entry. Combine with F037's nodeRemoved→invalidateCache(groupNode.id) so deleted groups free their entry. Extend the TessellationCacheEntry (or a parallel field) with an optional boolKey string.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts`
- **Test:** Render a 2-child boolean group, move a child by 1px, render again; assert geometryCache size for boolean groups stays at 1 (keyed by group id) rather than growing to 2, and that the re-rendered geometry reflects the moved child (staleness check triggered).
- **Notes:** Reviewer correction verified: looping playback does NOT grow the cache (frames are integer-quantized/deterministic, ~one entry per unique frame). Unbounded growth is from interactive child drag/resize and from un-evicted deleted-node entries. All leaked memory is CPU-side JS heap. The delete-leak portion overlaps F037's nodeRemoved wiring, hence dependsOn F037.

#### `F121` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts:2690`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** All draw paths upload into fixed 10,000-vertex GPU buffers with no size check, so complex geometry silently renders as garbage or disappears.

- **Root cause:** vertexBuffer is allocated once at MAX_VERTICES*2 floats (10000*2 = 80KB) and indexBuffer at MAX_VERTICES\*3 uint32 (ShapeRenderer.ts:380,676-677,804,809). All draw paths upload with gl.bufferSubData(...,0,vertices/indices) with no capacity check: renderFill (2690,2704), renderFillGradient (2875,2882), renderStrokeStrip (2799), renderSkinnedFillsGPU (3224,3248,3263), etc. When tessellated geometry exceeds the fixed capacity, bufferSubData writes past the buffer → GL_INVALID_VALUE (upload rejected) and the subsequent drawElements/drawArrays references vertices/indices beyond the buffer → the draw is dropped (INVALID_OPERATION) and the shape silently vanishes.
- **Fix:** Add a capacity check + grow-on-demand helper. Before each bufferSubData upload, compare data.byteLength against the current buffer capacity (track capacity in fields, e.g. this.vertexBufferBytes / this.indexBufferBytes, set at init). If the incoming array is larger, call gl.bufferData(target, newByteLength, gl.DYNAMIC_DRAW) to reallocate (rounding up, e.g. next power of two) and update the tracked capacity, then bufferSubData. Centralize into private uploadVertices(data)/uploadIndices(data) methods and route renderFill/renderFillGradient/renderStrokeStrip/renderSkinnedFillsGPU through them. Guard against exceeding GL limits if desired. Alternatively chunk very large draws, but growth is simpler and correct.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts`
- **Test:** Construct a path/polygon that tessellates to > MAX_VERTICES vertices, render it, and assert gl.bufferData is called to grow the buffer and gl.drawElements is called with the full index count (not dropped). Verify no GL error is recorded in the mock.
- **Notes:** Reviewer's symptom refinement verified: WebGL bounds-checks draws, so the dominant outcome is the shape silently disappearing (draw dropped), not garbage triangles. Coordinate with F184 (which converts fillIndices to a cached Uint32Array) since both touch the index upload path.

#### `F122` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts:4178`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Ghost (onion-skin) rendering of text earcuts the concatenated multi-contour glyph array without hole indices, filling letter counters and bridging glyphs.

- **Root cause:** renderTextWithOverride (ghost/onion-skin path) tessellates each glyph contour then concatenates all of them into one flat `combined` array (ShapeRenderer.ts:4159-4176) and passes it to renderNodeGhost → renderFillsAndStrokesGhost, which runs `earcut(tessellated.subarray(0,numVerts*2))` with NO hole indices (1717). So glyph counters (holes of o/e/a/etc.) get filled and separate glyphs get bridged by spurious triangles. Ghost strokes are equally wrong: renderStrokeWithColor generates a single outline around the concatenated array, drawing bridge segments between glyph contours. Contrast renderText (2214-2245) which groups contours by containment and passes per-group hole offsets to earcut, and renderPathWithOverride (4014-4106) which already does containment-grouped ghost fills + per-contour ghost strokes.
- **Fix:** Rewrite renderTextWithOverride's fill/stroke emission to mirror renderPathWithOverride's multi-contour branch (4024-4105): after building contourArrays and `combined`, compute globalVertStarts, call groupContoursByContainment(contourArrays), build per-group vertex arrays + groupHoles, run earcut per group with holes, remap local→global indices into ghostFillIndices, set the model matrix, then renderFillWithColor(combined, ghostFillIndices, tintedColor) for each visible fill. Render ghost strokes per contour: loop contourArrays and call renderStrokeWithColor(contourVerts, stroke, true, tintedColor) for each visible stroke. This can be factored into a shared helper used by both renderPathWithOverride and renderTextWithOverride.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts`
- **Test:** Ghost-render a text node containing a glyph with a hole (e.g. 'o') with onion-skin colorOverride; assert the ghost fill indices were produced via grouped earcut with hole offsets (counter left unfilled) rather than a single flat earcut, and that ghost strokes are emitted per contour (renderStrokeWithColor called once per glyph contour, not once over the concatenated array).
- **Notes:** Only affects onion-skin ghost frames of text nodes (a niche feature path), hence medium not high. renderPathWithOverride is the ready-made template.

#### `F183` · medium · performance

**Location:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts:984`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** A failing image src is retried on every render frame forever, spamming network requests and image decodes.

- **Root cause:** getTexture's error handler (ShapeRenderer.ts:983-985) only does `this.pendingImages.delete(src)` and records nothing about the failure. On the next frame renderImage calls getTexture(src) again (1909); it finds no cached texture and no pending entry, so it starts a brand-new Image() load (955-963). For an unreachable URL or corrupt data URI this issues a fresh network request + decode every animation frame (~60/s) indefinitely, flooding the network tab and console with errors.
- **Fix:** Add a private `failedImages = new Set<string>()`. In the .catch handler, add `this.failedImages.add(src)` alongside the pendingImages.delete. At the top of getTexture, return null immediately if `this.failedImages.has(src)`. Clear a src from failedImages when its node's src changes or on an explicit retry (e.g. expose a retryTexture(src) or clear failedImages in dispose and when disposeTexture(src) is called so a genuinely new/edited src can reload). Optionally add backoff instead of permanent suppression, but a simple failed-set removes the per-frame flood.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts`
- **Test:** Call getTexture(badSrc) and reject the load; call getTexture(badSrc) again on subsequent frames and assert no new Image()/load is initiated (spy on Image construction or on the network attempt) and getTexture returns null. Verify that after disposeTexture(badSrc) (or src change) a reload IS attempted again.
- **Notes:** Reviewer labeled low, but a continuous 60/s network+decode flood for any broken image src is closer to medium user impact; still a small, contained fix. Ensure the failed-set is invalidated on src change/dispose so legitimately re-added images can load.

#### `F184` · medium · performance

**Location:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts:2702`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** renderFill converts the cached number[] fillIndices to a new Uint32Array on every draw call, allocating per fill per node per frame in the hottest render path

- **Root cause:** Despite tessellation and earcut indices being cached, the index data is re-converted to a fresh typed array on every draw: renderFill does `const indicesArray = new Uint32Array(fillIndices)` (ShapeRenderer.ts:2702), renderFillGradient `new Uint32Array(cachedIndices)` (2880), and renderSkinnedFillsGPU twice (3246,3261) — once per visible fill per node per RAF frame. A 300-shape scene allocates/copies 300+ typed arrays (each potentially thousands of ints) 60x/sec. Additionally setGradientUniforms allocates ~6 small Float32Arrays per gradient draw (2923,2932,2938,2948-2961). All of this is pure GC churn since the data is immutable once cached.
- **Fix:** 1) Store fill indices as a Uint32Array in TessellationCacheEntry: change the fillIndices field (or add fillIndicesU32) and convert once at cache-creation time in getCachedTessellation (1120,1126), getCachedMultiContourTessellation (2654), renderText (2251), renderImage (1956), and the boolean-group cache (2433). Update renderFill/renderFillGradient/renderSkinnedFillsGPU to upload the cached Uint32Array directly and pass its .length to drawElements, removing the per-draw allocation. (Callers that read fillIndices as number[] — e.g. length checks — still work on a typed array.) 2) In setGradientUniforms, reuse preallocated scratch Float32Arrays (e.g. this.\_scratchVec4/\_scratchVec2 filled in place) instead of `new Float32Array([...])` per uniform.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts`
- **Test:** Render the same filled shape across two frames and assert no new Uint32Array is allocated for indices on the second (cache-hit) frame — e.g. spy on the upload path to confirm it receives the same cached typed-array reference both frames. For gradients, assert setGradientUniforms does not allocate a new Float32Array per uniform on repeat draws.
- **Notes:** Touches the same renderFill/renderFillGradient/renderSkinnedFillsGPU index-upload lines as F121; sequence with F121 (capacity check operates on the now-cached Uint32Array) to avoid conflicting edits. TessellationCacheEntry.fillIndices is currently typed number[] (interface line 398) and consumed in several places — updating the type must be done consistently.

### Rigging

#### `F146` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/rigging/src/dynamicChain.ts:171`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** stepDynamicChain silently returns for dt > 0.1s, so bakeDynamicChainToKeyframes (dt = 1/frameRate) produces a completely frozen chain — constant keyframes — for any project frame rate of 9 fps or lower, with no error.

- **Root cause:** packages/rigging/src/dynamicChain.ts:171 `if (dt <= 0 || dt > 0.1) return;` silently no-ops for dt>0.1s. packages/rigging/src/bakeDynamicChain.ts:46 sets `dt = 1/frameRate` and line 71 calls stepDynamicChain once with that dt and no substepping/clamp. For frameRate <= 9, 1/9 ≈ 0.1111 > 0.1 so every per-frame step returns immediately; applyChainToBones (line 72) still runs but reads unchanged rest-pose particles, so all baked rotation keyframes record the (near-)constant rest rotation and no gravity/wind/inertia is ever integrated. Verified: 1/9>0.1 true, 1/10=0.1 not >0.1 (10fps works). Latent: grep confirms no app/UI caller of bakeDynamicChainToKeyframes (only the rigging barrel export and its test), so it is not presently user-reachable, but it is a real correctness bug in an exported, tested function.
- **Fix:** Substep the physics in bakeDynamicChainToKeyframes so each solver call receives a dt inside the solver limit. Replace the single stepDynamicChain call (line 71) with: `const substeps = dt > 0.1 ? Math.ceil(dt / 0.05) : 1; const subDt = dt / substeps; for (let s = 0; s < substeps; s++) stepDynamicChain(chain, state, sceneGraph, subDt, windForce);` then keep the single applyChainToBones(chain, state, sceneGraph) after the loop. Gating on `dt > 0.1` means only currently-broken frame rates change; every frame rate that already works (dt <= 0.1, e.g. 24fps -> substeps=1) is byte-for-byte unchanged, so all existing bake tests pass. 0.05 matches the real-time clamp in Canvas.tsx:595. Preferred over the alternatives (clamping dt inside stepDynamicChain, or returning null from bake): substepping preserves Verlet accuracy and does not alter the shared solver guard that also protects evaluateDynamicChains. Optionally export a shared MAX_STEP_DT=0.1 constant from dynamicChain.ts and reference it in both the guard and the bake gate to prevent drift.
- **Files:** `packages/rigging/src/bakeDynamicChain.ts`, `packages/rigging/src/bakeDynamicChain.test.ts`
- **Test:** In bakeDynamicChain.test.ts add a test mirroring 'records varying rotations when gravity is applied' but at frameRate=8 (dt≈0.125>0.1): makeChain({gravity:200,gravityAngle:-90}), bake endFrame=20; assert kfs = result.boneKeyframes.get('bone-2') has kfs[0].value !== kfs[20].value (frozen/equal before fix, varies after). Optionally assert the sign/direction of change matches the 24fps baseline.
- **Notes:** Latent bug (no app caller today); fix is contained and only activates below 10fps. Keep stepDynamicChain's existing guard as a safety net for other callers; do not remove it.

#### `F147` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/rigging/src/ik.ts:193`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Pole targets are silently ignored for 2-bone chains (the primary elbow/knee use case) because applyPoleTarget is gated on joints.length >= 3, making applyPoleTarget's dedicated 'one middle joint' branch unreachable dead code.

- **Root cause:** solveFABRIK gates the pole-target pass on `if (poleTarget && joints.length >= 3)` (ik.ts:193). A 2-bone chain has joints.length===2 and positions.length===3, so the pole pass never runs for the primary elbow/knee case. applyPoleTarget's dedicated `positions.length <= 3` branch (ik.ts:219-254), which projects the single middle joint toward the pole and re-enforces BOTH bone lengths (lines 250-253), is therefore unreachable dead code. The existing test 'applies pole target to influence bend direction' (ik.test.ts:345-373) only asserts rotations.size===2, so it passes despite the pole doing nothing.
- **Fix:** Change the gate at ik.ts:193 from `joints.length >= 3` to `joints.length >= 2`. This routes 2-bone chains (positions.length===3) into the already-correct positions.length<=3 branch of applyPoleTarget, which re-enforces both bone lengths so it does not introduce the F148 defect. No change to applyPoleTarget needed.
- **Files:** `packages/rigging/src/ik.ts`
- **Test:** Strengthen/replace the existing 2-bone pole test: with target {x:100,y:0} and each bone length 100, solve once with poleTarget {x:50,y:100} (up) and once with {x:50,y:-100} (down). Assert the resulting root rotation is positive for the up pole and negative for the down pole (or that the reconstructed middle joint y-sign matches the pole y-sign), proving the pole actually disambiguates bend direction rather than only asserting rotations.size.
- **Notes:** Real. Independent of F148 (different applyPoleTarget branch). Changes solver output for any 2-bone chain that has a pole target, but the only existing test asserts size, so no test breakage.

#### `F148` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/rigging/src/ik.ts:283`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** applyPoleTarget's long-chain branch re-enforces bone lengths for all segments EXCEPT the last one, so with a pole target the solver can report converged=true while the reconstructed chain's end effector misses the target.

- **Root cause:** applyPoleTarget's long-chain branch (positions.length>3, i.e. 3+ bones) re-enforces bone lengths with `for (let i = 0; i < positions.length - 2; i++)` (ik.ts:283-286). This rebuilds positions[1]..positions[length-2] from the root but never re-normalizes the final segment positions[length-2]->positions[length-1]. After the pole projection moves the middle joints, positions[length-2] shifts while the tip positions[length-1] is left at its post-forward-pass location (~target), so the last bone's length is violated. The next iteration's convergence check (ik.ts:174-176) measures only dist(positions[endIdx], target), which stays within tolerance, so the loop breaks with a length-violating chain. positionsToRotations then derives angles only, and applyIKResult reconstructs with true bone lengths, placing the real tip off-target while endEffectorError (ik.ts:205, = dist(positions[last],target)) still reports converged.
- **Fix:** Change the loop bound at ik.ts:283 from `i < positions.length - 2` to `i < positions.length - 1`, so the last segment is also length-corrected (positions[length-1] = positions[length-2] + dir\*boneLengths[length-1]). This moves the tip off the target within that iteration, but the next FABRIK backward/forward pass re-pulls the tip to the target, and now endEffectorError honestly reflects a length-valid chain.
- **Files:** `packages/rigging/src/ik.ts`
- **Test:** In ik.test.ts, add a 3-bone-chain integration test (root at origin, no parent group, no angle constraints) with a pole target node, target reachable, generous maxIterations (e.g. 50). After solveFABRIK->applyIKResult, reconstruct the actual end-effector world tip (via getBoneWorldTip / mock FK from the applied local rotations) and assert dist(actualTip, target) <= tolerance. Before the fix this fails (result.converged true but reconstructed tip off); after the fix the reported convergence matches the reconstructed tip.
- **Notes:** Real, isolated to the long-chain (3+ bone) pole branch. Alters convergence dynamics for pole chains, so verify the existing 'pole target on 3-bone chain' test still returns rotations.size===3. Independent of F147 (different branch).

#### `F149` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/rigging/src/ik.ts:307`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** F062  
**Finding:** applyConstraints clamps each bone's WORLD-space segment angle against angleMin/angleMax, but everywhere else (fk.ts clampBoneRotation, applyIKResult) those limits are defined on LOCAL rotation, so constrained IK chains are clamped in the wrong frame for every non-root bone.

- **Root cause:** applyConstraints (ik.ts:301-328) computes `angle = atan2(positions[i+1]-positions[i])` which is the WORLD-space direction of segment i, then clamps it directly against joint.angleMin/angleMax and rebuilds positions[i+1] from that clamped WORLD angle (lines 305-320). But angleMin/angleMax are LOCAL-rotation limits everywhere else: fk.ts clampBoneRotation (lines 33-39) clamps bone.transform.rotation (local), and applyIKResult (ik.ts:421-426) clamps the LOCAL rotation. For any non-root bone, world angle = parent's accumulated world rotation + local rotation, so clamping world against local limits distorts the pose whenever the parent segment is not at 0deg, and can prevent convergence to an otherwise-valid constrained pose.
- **Fix:** Rewrite applyConstraints to clamp in LOCAL frame. Track the running parent world angle: initialize prevWorldAngle = rootParentWorldRotation (the same joints[0].rootParentWorldRotation value introduced by F062; 0 for un-nested rigs). For each bone i: worldAngle = atan2(dir); localAngle = normalizeAngle(worldAngle - prevWorldAngle); clampedLocal = clamp(localAngle, min, max); clampedWorld = prevWorldAngle + clampedLocal; if |clampedLocal - localAngle| > 0.001 rebuild positions[i+1] at clampedWorld (cos/sin \* boneLengths[i]) and re-enforce downstream lengths (as now, lines 322-326); set prevWorldAngle = clampedWorld (the actual post-clamp world angle of bone i, which is the parent world angle for bone i+1).
- **Files:** `packages/rigging/src/ik.ts`
- **Test:** In ik.test.ts, add a 2-bone chain where the child has local limits [-90,90] and the target requires the child's WORLD angle to exceed 90 while its LOCAL angle stays within [-90,90] (e.g. root forced to a large rotation). Assert the solved child LOCAL rotation is within [-90,90] AND the chain still reaches the target (endEffectorError small) — before the fix the world-frame clamp forcibly bends the child to world-90 and the chain misses; after, the valid local pose is preserved.
- **Notes:** Real for non-root bones. Depends on F062 to reuse the rootParentWorldRotation plumbing for the root bone's local-frame reference; with that defaulting to 0, un-nested behavior is preserved. Single-bone constraint tests (ik.test.ts:278-339) go through the joints.length===1 branch, not applyConstraints, so they are unaffected; the loose multi-bone constraint tests (lines 302, 781) still hold since for un-nested rigs root local==world.

### SVG import/export

#### `F126` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgConverter.ts:345`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Fill is silently discarded for open subpaths, but SVG fills open paths (implicitly closing them for the fill operation) — imported artwork loses visible filled areas.

- **Root cause:** convertPath (svgConverter.ts:345) sets `fills: sp.closed ? convertFills(el.style, ctx.defs) : []`, and convertPolyline (svgConverter.ts:293) hardcodes `fills: []`. This contradicts SVG's fill rule: an open path/polyline IS filled, the fill operation implicitly closing the subpath. So `<path d="M 0 0 L 100 0 L 100 100" fill="red"/>` renders a filled red triangle in browsers, but import drops the fill; with the SVG default black fill it becomes fully invisible (no fill, default stroke none). The Quar renderer already fills open paths correctly: ShapeRenderer.getCachedTessellation (ShapeRenderer.ts:1118-1120) computes earcut fillIndices from ALL vertices regardless of the `closed` flag, and renderFillsAndStrokes (line 1692) renders every fill in node.fills while `closed` is only forwarded to renderStroke. So keeping the fill on an open PathNode renders the implicitly-closed fill AND the open stroke — exactly matching SVG. The reviewer's inclusion of convertLine (line 225) is NOT a defect: a line has 2 points, numVerts<3 -> earcut returns [] -> zero-area fill renders nothing, matching browsers.
- **Fix:** convertPath line 345: change to `fills: convertFills(el.style, ctx.defs),` (drop the sp.closed ternary). convertFills already returns [] when style.fill is null (fill="none"/stroke-only), so stroke-only open paths are unaffected while filled open paths keep their fill. convertPolyline line 293: change `fills: []` to `fills: convertFills(el.style, ctx.defs),`. Do NOT touch convertLine (line 225) — leave `fills: []` per the reviewer's correct carve-out. Keep `closed: false` in both (renderer fills as-if-closed via earcut, stroke stays open). MUST update the existing test 'open paths have no fills' (svgConverter.test.ts:179-188), which asserts the buggy behavior with fill="red": rename to 'open paths keep fill (SVG implicit closure)' and change `expect(node.fills).toHaveLength(0)` to `toHaveLength(1)`. A convertSvgToNodes-level import warning is optional and skipped here — convertSvgToNodes has no warnings channel (only importSvg does), and the renderer already fills correctly so no content is lost.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgConverter.ts`, `packages/core/src/svg/__tests__/svgConverter.test.ts`
- **Test:** In svgConverter.test.ts: (1) update/rename the line-179 'open paths have no fills' test to assert `node.closed === false` and `node.fills` toHaveLength(1) with color {r:255,g:0,b:0,a:1} for `<path d="M 0 0 L 100 0 L 100 100" fill="red"/>`. (2) new polyline test: `<polyline points="0,0 100,0 100,100" fill="green"/>` -> assert closed===false and fills toHaveLength(1). (3) regression: `<path ... fill="none" stroke="black"/>` still yields fills length 0, and `<polyline ... fill="none"/>` still fills length 0.
- **Notes:** Verified via renderer that keeping fills on an open path renders the implicitly-closed region. The only existing test that breaks is the one asserting the bug (line 179); it must be inverted as part of the fix. Behavioral change: open paths with a (possibly default-black) fill now render filled, matching SVG. Independent of F043/F044.

#### `F127` · medium · xss-injection

**Location:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgExporter.ts:390`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** SVG exporter interpolates untrusted node string properties into attribute values without XML-escaping (only node.content and fontFamily are escaped), enabling markup/script injection into the exported .svg.

- **Root cause:** In svgExporter.ts three string values are interpolated into attribute values without XML-escaping: stroke.cap at line 186 (stroke-linecap="${stroke.cap}"), stroke.join at line 190 (stroke-linejoin="${stroke.join}"), and node.fontStyle at line 390 (font-style="${node.fontStyle}"). node.content (line 395) and node.fontFamily (line 388) and node.src (image, line 412) are already routed through escapeXml (defined line 766). These three are typed as string-literal enums (Stroke.cap/join at packages/types/src/index.ts:79-80, TextNode.fontStyle at :287) so under normal in-app authoring they are safe, but the exporter's threat model includes re-exporting an attacker-supplied .quar whose deserialized values bypass TypeScript types; a crafted value like 'butt"><script>...' would break out of the attribute. The reviewer is correct that fontWeight (line 389) and fontSize (line 388) are number-typed (index.ts:286) and cannot inject markup, and letterSpacing (line 393) passes through fmt() so it is not a raw-string vector.
- **Fix:** Harden the three enum interpolations. Preferred: whitelist against the known enum members before emitting (drop/omit the attribute when the value is not a legal enum member) — for cap allow butt|round|square, for join allow miter|round|bevel, for fontStyle allow normal|italic — because escaping alone would still emit an invalid SVG attribute value. Minimal acceptable alternative: wrap each in escapeXml(): escapeXml(stroke.cap), escapeXml(stroke.join), escapeXml(node.fontStyle). If whitelisting, the existing guards (cap !== 'butt', join !== 'miter', fontStyle !== 'normal') already filter defaults, so just add an inclusion check. Optionally coerce fontWeight/fontSize with Number() as defense-in-depth for untrusted imports, but this is not required for the injection fix.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgExporter.ts`, `packages/core/src/svg/__tests__/svgExporter.test.ts`
- **Test:** Add tests that build a Stroke with cap and join cast to a malicious payload (e.g. 'round"/><script>alert(1)</script>') and a TextNode with fontStyle similarly poisoned (via `as unknown as ...` casts to bypass types), run strokeToSvgAttrs / textToSvg, and assert the output does NOT contain the raw '<script>' or a closing-attribute breakout ('"/>' / '"><'), and that legal values (cap='round', join='bevel', fontStyle='italic') still round-trip unchanged. Mirror the existing 'escapes XML special characters in text' test style.
- **Notes:** Real but low/medium severity: exported .svg is a blob download, not rendered inline in-app, so exploitation requires the victim to open the export as active content. Fix is trivial and pure hardening; no behavior change for valid inputs. Reviewer's dismissal of fontWeight as a non-vector is accurate.

#### `F128` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgImporter.ts:97`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** F129  
**Finding:** importSvg's scale option breaks layout: group children's relative positions are never scaled, and an explicit target position is multiplied by scale.

- **Root cause:** Two defects in the transform pass (svgImporter.ts:91-105). (1) Layout not scaled for group children: the position update is gated by `if (rootIds.includes(node.id) || !node.parent)` (line 96) so only roots get repositioned; group children (node.parent set) skip it, and scaleNodeDimensions (233-274) scales width/radiusX/radiusY/path-point positions but NEVER transform.position. Since convertGroup (svgConverter.ts:420-452) gives the group position {0,0} and stores children at absolute viewbox coords, scaling only dimensions leaves the gap between sibling children unchanged — importing `<g><rect x=0 w=50/><rect x=100 w=50/></g>` at scale=2 doubles each rect's size but keeps their centers 100 apart, collapsing the layout. (2) Target coordinate is scaled: line 97-98 computes `(pos + offset) * scale` with offset=target-center (line 91-92), so the final position = pos*scale + (target-center)*scale, i.e. the caller's target is multiplied by scale. importSvg(...,{position:{x:500,y:300},scale:0.5}) lands content at (250,150) instead of (500,300).
- **Fix:** Replace the per-node loop (94-105) with center-anchored scaling. Compute `const doReposition = centerAtOrigin || !!position; const targetX = position?.x ?? 0; const targetY = position?.y ?? 0;` For each node: `const isRoot = rootIds.includes(node.id) || !node.parent;` If isRoot && doReposition: `node.transform.position.x = (node.transform.position.x - centerX) * scale + targetX;` (same for y with centerY/targetY). If isRoot && !doReposition: `node.transform.position.x *= scale; node.transform.position.y *= scale;` (preserves current scale-about-origin behavior for the scale-only case). If non-root child: always `node.transform.position.x *= scale; node.transform.position.y *= scale;` (scales child offsets about the group origin so the parent's repositioned origin re-centers the whole group correctly via scene-graph compositing). Keep `if (scale !== 1) scaleNodeDimensions(node, scale)` for all nodes. Verified against all 4 existing importer transform tests: centers-at-origin, centerAtOrigin:false, imports-to-specific-position (scale 1), and applies-scale-factor all still produce their asserted values.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgImporter.ts`
- **Test:** In svgImporter.test.ts add: (1) position+scale — `importSvg(simpleSvg, sg, gen, {position:{x:500,y:300}, scale:0.5})`; assert node.transform.position.x≈500 and y≈300 (currently 250/150). (2) group layout scale — import `<g><rect x=0 y=0 width=50 height=50/><rect x=100 y=0 width=50 height=50/></g>` with {centerAtOrigin:false, scale:2}; fetch the two rect children and assert Math.abs(rectA.transform.position.x - rectB.transform.position.x)≈200 (gap doubled) and each width≈100.
- **Notes:** For grouped SVGs the centerX/centerY consumed here are wrong until F129 fixes computeNodesBounds, so the group-scale test only passes once F129 lands; implement F129 first (or together). Groups carrying their own transform have a pre-existing compositing limitation (child positions ignore parent translate) that is out of scope for this fix.

#### `F129` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgImporter.ts:205`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** computeNodesBounds treats group nodes as zero-size points, so centerAtOrigin fails to center any SVG whose content is wrapped in a <g> (the common case).

- **Root cause:** computeNodesBounds (svgImporter.ts:164-185) only considers root nodes (`if (!rootIds.includes(node.id) && node.parent) continue;` line 171) and getNodeHalfWidth/getNodeHalfHeight (187-231) fall through to `default: return 0` for type 'group'. So when the whole SVG is wrapped in one <g>, the only root is the group, contributing just its position {0,0} as a zero-size point → bounds {0,0,0,0}, center (0,0). The centering/positioning at 81-99 then offsets by target-0, ignoring where the content actually is. Confirmed both callers are affected: useProjectActions.ts:285 (centerAtOrigin:true) fails to center grouped content, and Canvas.tsx:1118 (centerAtOrigin:false, position:worldCenter) drops grouped content offset from the intended point by the content's true center, because line 81 (`centerAtOrigin || position || scale !== 1`) and line 91 (`centerAtOrigin || position`) both route through the same degenerate bounds.
- **Fix:** Make computeNodesBounds derive bounds from geometry-bearing leaf nodes, accumulating ancestor translations. Build `const byId = new Map(nodes.map(n => [n.id, n]));` add a helper worldPos(node) that starts from node.transform.position and walks node.parent via byId, adding each ancestor's transform.position (translate-only approximation, matching how the importer already composites). Iterate ALL nodes, `if (node.type === 'group') continue;` (groups have no geometry — skipping avoids polluting bounds with their {0,0} origin), then use worldPos(node).x ± getNodeHalfWidth(node) and worldPos(node).y ± getNodeHalfHeight(node) for min/max. The rootIds parameter/filter is no longer needed (remove it or leave unused). This yields the true content center that F128's offset logic then consumes.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgImporter.ts`
- **Test:** In svgImporter.test.ts: import `<g><rect x=50 y=50 width=100 height=100/></g>` with default options (centerAtOrigin:true). Fetch the group and the rect child; assert the child's world position centers on origin: `groupNode.transform.position.x + rectChild.transform.position.x` ≈ 0 and same for y (previously the group stays at {0,0} and content is left uncentered). Also assert the existing non-grouped 'centers at origin' rect test still passes.
- **Notes:** Independently testable at scale=1 (correct bounds alone re-centers groups via the existing root-offset path). F128 builds on the corrected center for the scale case.

#### `F130` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgParser.ts:143`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Percentage width/height on the root <svg> ('width="100%"') parses to 1 instead of falling back to viewBox, and without a viewBox it corrupts all Y-flipped geometry.

- **Root cause:** packages/core/src/svg/svgParser.ts:143-144: `const width = parseSvgLength(svgEl.getAttribute('width') || '') || viewBox?.width || 300`. parseSvgLength (svgUtils.ts:347-350) resolves '100%' with no reference argument to `parseFloat('100%')/100 = 1`, which is truthy, so width=1 and the `|| viewBox?.width` fallback is bypassed; same for height. Verified via grep that the only geometry consumer of parsed.width/height is svgConverter.ts:48 `const viewBoxHeight = parsed.viewBox?.height ?? parsed.height`. When a viewBox is present the `??` keeps viewBox.height, so parsed.height=1 is inert. When there is NO viewBox, viewBoxHeight = parsed.height = 1, and every convertX/convertLine/convertPolygon does `ctx.viewBoxHeight - y = 1 - y`, corrupting all Y-flipped geometry. So the bug is real but only bites for SVGs with percentage root dimensions AND no viewBox.
- **Fix:** Treat percentage (viewport-relative, hence unresolvable at parse time) root dimensions as absent so the existing `|| viewBox?.width || 300` fallback runs. Do NOT change parseSvgLength globally (it is used for stroke-width, rx, etc.). In parseSvg, capture the raw attrs and skip percentages: e.g. `const widthAttr = (svgEl.getAttribute('width') || '').trim(); const heightAttr = (svgEl.getAttribute('height') || '').trim(); const width = (widthAttr.endsWith('%') ? 0 : parseSvgLength(widthAttr)) || viewBox?.width || 300; const height = (heightAttr.endsWith('%') ? 0 : parseSvgLength(heightAttr)) || viewBox?.height || 150;` (or factor into a tiny local `absoluteLengthOrZero(attr)`).
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgParser.ts`
- **Test:** In svgParser.test.ts: parseSvg(`<svg width="100%" height="100%" viewBox="0 0 200 100"></svg>`) and assert result.width===200, result.height===100. Add a no-viewBox regression: parseSvg(`<svg width="100%" height="100%"><rect x="0" y="0" width="10" height="10"/></svg>`) then convertSvgToNodes and assert the rect's transform.position.y is derived from the 150 default (not 1) — i.e. not corrupted by viewBoxHeight=1.
- **Notes:** Impact is genuinely conditional (percentage dims + no viewBox). Still worth fixing since it is a silent full-geometry corruption; keep severity medium as the reviewer scoped it.

#### `F131` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgParser.ts:295`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Gradient href inheritance resolves only one level in document order, so chained gradient references (a→b→c) can end with zero stops depending on element order.

- **Root cause:** packages/core/src/svg/svgParser.ts:278-314 (resolveGradientInheritance) performs a single forward pass over the gradients Map in document/insertion order. For each gradient with a \_href it copies parent.stops only `if (gradient.stops.length === 0 && parent.stops.length > 0)` at that instant (line 295) and inherits coords the same way (lines 300-309). In a 3+ level chain a→b→c where an intermediate inherits its stops via href AND appears before its parent in document order, the parent has not been resolved yet when the child is processed. Traced with order [a(href=b), b(href=c), c(stops)]: processing a sees b.stops still empty → a ends with zero stops. Base-first order resolves fine, so failure is order-dependent, exactly as claimed. Additionally the `visited.has(id)` check on line 285 is dead code — each id is iterated exactly once and only added to `visited` after the check, so it never fires and provides no real cycle protection (only the `href === id` self-ref check works).
- **Fix:** Rewrite resolveGradientInheritance to resolve recursively with memoization and a real per-path cycle guard. Sketch: `const resolved = new Set<string>(); function resolve(id, ancestry){ const g = gradients.get(id); if(!g||resolved.has(id)) return; const href=g._href; if(href && href!==id && gradients.has(href) && !ancestry.has(href)){ resolve(href, new Set(ancestry).add(id)); const parent=gradients.get(href)!; if(g.stops.length===0 && parent.stops.length>0) g.stops=[...parent.stops]; if(g.type==='linear'){ if(g.x1===undefined) g.x1=parent.x1; if(g.y1===undefined) g.y1=parent.y1; if(g.x2===undefined) g.x2=parent.x2; if(g.y2===undefined) g.y2=parent.y2; } else { if(g.cx===undefined) g.cx=parent.cx; if(g.cy===undefined) g.cy=parent.cy; if(g.r===undefined) g.r=parent.r; if(g.fx===undefined) g.fx=parent.fx; if(g.fy===undefined) g.fy=parent.fy; } } delete g._href; resolved.add(id);} for(const id of gradients.keys()) resolve(id, new Set());`. The `ancestry` set is the genuine cycle guard (replaces the dead `visited` logic); `resolved` memoizes so each gradient is processed once. Preserve the internal `_href` cleanup.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgParser.ts`
- **Test:** In svgParser.test.ts: define three linearGradients where 'a' xlink:href='#b', 'b' xlink:href='#c', and only 'c' declares stops, emitted in FORWARD order (a, then b, then c) inside <defs>; parse and assert gradients.get('a').stops.length===2 and equals c's stops (proves order-independent chain resolution). Add a cycle test: a href='#b', b href='#a', neither with stops — assert parse completes without infinite loop/stack overflow and both end with 0 stops. Also add a 2-level base-first case to confirm no regression.
- **Notes:** No existing test covers chained/cyclic href inheritance, so regression risk is limited to the coord/stops inheritance already exercised by the flat-inheritance path — keep those assertions passing. Independent of F046 (different function) but both touch gradient handling; if F046 lands first, the normalized coords simply flow through this recursion unchanged.

### Scene graph, symbols & format

#### `F123` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/SceneGraph.ts:77`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** addNode registers the node in the map before validating parentId, so a failed add leaves an orphaned zombie node that blocks re-adding under the same id.

- **Root cause:** addNode (packages/core/src/SceneGraph.ts:72-93) calls this.nodes.set(node.id, node) at line 77 BEFORE resolving the parent (lines 79-83). When parentId is supplied but this.nodes.get(parentId) is undefined, the throw at line 82 leaves node registered in this.nodes but absent from rootNodeIds and from any parent.children — an unreachable zombie. Because the duplicate guard at line 74 keys off this.nodes.has(node.id), any retry of addNode(node) then throws 'already exists', so the id is permanently unusable this session, and toJSON (line 414 iterates this.nodes.values()) serializes the zombie into saved files as invisible junk. Existing test at SceneGraph.test.ts:85-88 only asserts the throw, not that the node was left unregistered, so it does not catch this.
- **Fix:** Reorder addNode to validate before mutating: after the duplicate check, if parentId is truthy do `const parent = this.nodes.get(parentId); if (!parent) throw new Error(...)` FIRST; only then this.nodes.set(node.id, node); then in the parentId branch set node.parent = parentId and parent.children.push(node.id); in the else branch set node.parent = null and this.rootNodeIds.push(node.id). This keeps this.nodes.set out of the failure path so a failed add leaves the graph untouched.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/SceneGraph.ts`
- **Test:** SceneGraph.test.ts addNode block: 'does not register node when parent not found' — const child = createGroupNode('child','Child'); expect(()=>sceneGraph.addNode(child,'nonexistent')).toThrow('not found'); then assert sceneGraph.getNode('child') is undefined, sceneGraph.getNodeCount() === 0, and that retrying sceneGraph.addNode(child) (no parent) now succeeds without throwing 'already exists'.
- **Notes:** Localized reorder; the success path and the existing 'throws not found' test both remain valid.

#### `F124` · medium · data-loss

**Location:** `packages/core/src/SceneGraph.ts:160`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** moveNode detaches the node from its old parent before validating the new parent, so a failed move leaves the node (and its whole subtree) unreachable.

- **Root cause:** moveNode (packages/core/src/SceneGraph.ts:127-184) detaches the node from its old container BEFORE validating the new parent. Lines 140-154 remove id from oldParent.children (parented case) or from rootNodeIds (root case); only afterwards, at lines 157-161, does it look up newParent and throw at line 160 if missing. On that throw the node is already detached — removed from its old parent/root list but node.parent still points at the old parent (or null) — so it (and its whole subtree) is unreachable via getRootNodes/traverse. The isAncestorOf circular-reference guard at line 132 already runs first, so it is unaffected. Existing test SceneGraph.test.ts:247-252 asserts only the throw, not post-throw reachability, so it misses the corruption. Reviewer's clarifications are accurate: both the root-node and parented cases corrupt, and current internal callers derive parentId from live nodes so real-world triggering is narrow (stale id, drag-drop racing a delete, or a future/MCP caller) — still a genuine invariant break.
- **Fix:** Hoist new-parent validation above the detach.
