After the isAncestorOf guard (line 136) and capturing previousParentId, add: `let newParent: Node | undefined; if (newParentId) { newParent = this.nodes.get(newParentId); if (!newParent) throw new Error(\`Parent node "${newParentId}" not found\`); }`. Then run the existing 'remove from old parent' block, then the 'add to new parent' block reusing the already-resolved `newParent` (drop the second lookup at line 158). A failed move now throws before any mutation, leaving the graph untouched.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/SceneGraph.ts`
- **Test:** SceneGraph.test.ts moveNode block: 'leaves node reachable when new parent not found' — build parent + child (child added under parent); expect(()=>sceneGraph.moveNode('child','nonexistent')).toThrow('not found'); then assert parent.children still contains 'child' and child.parent === 'parent'. Add a root-case variant: a root node whose failed move still leaves it in getRootNodes().
- **Notes:** Independent of F123 though the same validate-before-mutate pattern; existing 'throws not found' test still passes.

#### `F132` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/symbols/symbolResolver.ts:86`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** resolveSymbolInstance does not expand nested symbol-instance nodes, and no downstream consumer does either, so symbols nested inside symbols silently render nothing on canvas and are dropped from SVG export.

- **Root cause:** Nested symbol-instance nodes are never expanded. resolveSymbolInstance (packages/core/src/symbols/symbolResolver.ts:86-89) only does a flat structuredClone + shallow applyOverrides, so an instance node embedded in a definition's sceneGraphJSON.nodes stays an unexpanded instance with an empty children array. Both consumers then drop it: ShapeRenderer.renderResolvedNode (packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts:1640-1665) has no 'symbol-instance' case in its type switch and only recurses via node.children (empty for an instance in the flat list), and svgExporter.renderResolvedNodeToSvg (packages/core/src/svg/svgExporter.ts:509-539) hits `default: return ''`. Nesting is reachable because editorStore.createSymbol (apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts:3158-3187) collects nodesForDef with no type filter, so selecting an existing instance plus another shape embeds the instance in the new definition. Net effect: every instance of the outer symbol renders/exports only the non-nested siblings; the nested symbol's artwork is invisible on canvas and absent from SVG.
- **Fix:** Add explicit nested-instance handling to both resolved-node consumers (localized, low-risk, DRY relative to reworking the flat-node model). (1) ShapeRenderer.renderResolvedNode (ShapeRenderer.ts:1620-1678): add `case 'symbol-instance':` after the existing cases. Cast node to SymbolInstanceNode, look up `const def = this.symbolDefinitions.get(inst.symbolId)`; if missing, break. Cycle-guard: thread a new `visited: Set<string>` param through renderResolvedNode (default to a fresh Set at the top-level call site around ShapeRenderer.ts:1310-1313); if `visited.has(inst.symbolId)` break, else recurse with `new Set(visited).add(inst.symbolId)`. Resolve via resolveSymbolInstance(inst, def) + getResolvedRootNodes, build a local nodeMap, and for each root call renderResolvedNode(child, worldTransform, childNodeMap, visited') — worldTransform is already composed from the instance transform at lines 1629-1635, so the nested definition renders under the correct parent transform. (2) svgExporter.renderResolvedNodeToSvg (svgExporter.ts:502-540): add `case 'symbol-instance':` — look up `symbolDefs.get(node.symbolId)`; guard missing def and cycles via a threaded `visited` Set param (seed a fresh Set in symbolInstanceToSvg at svgExporter.ts:488-493). Resolve nested roots, build a nodeMap, wrap the recursively-rendered root elements in `<g${transformToSvgAttr(node.transform)}${opacityAttr}>...</g>` (mirroring symbolInstanceToSvg's own wrapper at line 495) so the nested instance's transform is applied.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts`, `packages/core/src/svg/svgExporter.ts`
- **Test:** In packages/core/src/svg/**tests**/svgExporter.test.ts add a nested-symbol export test: definition A = { rect with a distinctive fill (e.g. rgb 0,255,0) }, definition B = { a symbol-instance node referencing A + a plain rectangle }; add a symbol-instance-of-B node to the scene graph and call exportNodesToSvg([instB], sceneGraph, [defA, defB]). Assert the resulting SVG string contains A's distinctive rect (e.g. its fill/rect element) in addition to B's own rectangle. Before the fix the inner rect is absent.
- **Notes:** Finding is anchored at symbolResolver.ts:86 but the actual missing handling is in the two consumers, so filesToChange are ShapeRenderer.ts and svgExporter.ts, not symbolResolver.ts. Alternative single-source fix (change resolveSymbolInstance to take a Map<string,SymbolDefinition> and recursively expand nested instances into the flat list) is more invasive: requires re-IDing cloned sub-nodes to avoid collisions when a symbol is nested multiple times, composing the nested instance transform into sub-root transforms, and reworking the cache key — higher regression risk, so not recommended. Cycle guard is mandatory to avoid infinite recursion on self-referential symbols. A ShapeRenderer-level test is also possible but harder due to WebGL mocking; the svgExporter test is sufficient and deterministic.

#### `F133` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/symbols/symbolResolver.ts:150`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** getSymbolBounds returns 0x0 extent for path/text/group nodes and mixes parent-local child positions with root coordinates, producing missing or misplaced selection bounds for symbol instances.

- **Root cause:** getSymbolBounds (packages/core/src/symbols/symbolResolver.ts:101-179) has two defects. (a) The type switch default case (lines 150-154) assigns w=h=0 for path, text, and group nodes, so a definition composed only of brush/pen paths (or text) produces a degenerate 0x0 rect; SelectionManager.computeBounds guards `symBounds.width > 0 && symBounds.height > 0` (packages/core/src/selection/SelectionManager.ts:219) and therefore emits no selection box, and PropertiesPanel (apps/web/src/components/layout/PropertiesPanel.tsx:202) and SelectionTool (packages/core/src/tools/SelectionTool.ts:726) report wrong W/H. (b) The loop (111-167) iterates the flat node list and treats every node.transform.position as definition-root coordinates, ignoring hierarchy — it never composes a group's transform onto its children. A group child stored at parent-relative position is unioned in the wrong coordinate space while the group node itself contributes nothing (default w=h=0), so a definition containing a translated group yields bounds offset/inflated relative to the rendered artwork. Callers pass def.sceneGraphJSON.nodes (the full flat list incl. group children), confirming the mixed-space union.
- **Fix:** Rewrite getSymbolBounds to walk the hierarchy and use real per-type extents, mirroring SelectionManager.getLocalBounds + transformBoundsToWorld. Steps: (1) build a nodeMap by id from resolvedNodes; (2) determine roots = nodes with parent===null OR whose parent id is not present in the map; (3) recurse from each root: compute worldMatrix = parentMatrix multiplied by mat3.compose(node.transform.position, node.transform.rotation, node.transform.scale) — compose WITHOUT anchor to match SelectionManager's symbol-instance path (SelectionManager.ts:222) and avoid double-counting anchor; compute the node's anchor-baked LOCAL AABB per type reusing existing helpers: rectangle/artboard -> {x:-w*anchor.x, y:-h*anchor.y, w, h}; image -> same with width/height; ellipse -> {x:-radiusX, y:-radiusY, w:2rx, h:2ry}; polygon -> getPolygonBounds(0,0,radius,sides,1,1,innerRadius) from ../path/pathUtils; path -> getPathBounds(node.points, node.closed) (+ union subpaths) from ../path/pathUtils; text -> getTextBounds(...) from ../font/textMetrics; group/other -> null (no own geometry); transform the local AABB's 4 corners by worldMatrix (mirror transformBoundsToWorld from SelectionManager.ts:22-43) and union into min/max; then recurse into node.children via the map. Keep the empty-input and non-finite (!isFinite(minX)) guards returning {x:0,y:0,w:0,h:0}. This preserves the existing passing rect test (rect at 50,50 anchor 0.5 w100 h60 -> x0 y20 w100 h60) because rotation is 0. Add imports to symbolResolver.ts: getPathBounds, getPolygonBounds from '../path/pathUtils'; getTextBounds from '../font/textMetrics'; mat3 from '../math'.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/symbols/symbolResolver.ts`
- **Test:** In packages/core/src/symbols/symbolResolver.test.ts add: (1) 'computes non-zero bounds for a path-only definition' — build a PathNode with known point positions (e.g. points spanning x 0..40, y 0..20) at transform position (0,0); assert getSymbolBounds([path]).width and .height are > 0 and match the point extents (40 x 20). (2) 'composes group transform onto children' — a group node at transform.position (100,0) with one child rect (parent = group id, group.children = [rect id]) at group-local position (0,0); assert the returned bounds x is offset by the group translation (~100), proving child coords are composed through the parent rather than taken as root-space.
- **Notes:** Single-source fix in symbolResolver.ts benefits all three consumers (SelectionManager, SelectionTool, PropertiesPanel) at once. To avoid duplicating SelectionManager.getLocalBounds, an optional refactor is to extract a shared exported getNodeLocalBounds(node): Rect|null helper (e.g. into pathUtils or a new geometry module) used by both SelectionManager and symbolResolver — if done, add SelectionManager.ts to filesToChange; otherwise duplicate the minimal per-type logic. Independent of F132 (different function, no ordering constraint).

### Tools, selection & coordinate spaces

#### `F125` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/selection/SelectionManager.ts:233`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Selection bounds for a group ignore symbol-instance descendants, producing undersized bounds or no selection overlay at all.

- **Root cause:** In SelectionManager.collectNodeBounds, the 'group' branch (packages/core/src/selection/SelectionManager.ts:228-237) iterates sceneGraph.getDescendants(node.id) and, for each descendant, pushes transformBoundsToWorld(getLocalBounds(desc), worldTransform). getLocalBounds returns null for 'symbol-instance' (lines 373-374: 'No own geometry — bounds computed from resolved children'), so `if (localBounds)` on line 234 is false and the instance contributes zero rects. Symbol instances resolve their real geometry only in the dedicated top-level branch (lines 213-226) via getSymbolBounds(def.sceneGraphJSON.nodes), but that branch is guarded by `node.type === 'symbol-instance'` and ends with `return`, so it never runs for an instance that is a _descendant_ of a selected group. Confirmed by SceneGraph.getDescendants (SceneGraph.ts:256-279): it recursively collects scene-graph children (excluding the node itself), and a symbol instance's virtual children are not in the scene graph, so the grouped instance appears as a childless leaf that getLocalBounds cannot measure. Consequence: getGroupBounds (256-262) collects zero rects for a group whose only members are instances → returns null → getSelectionBoundsForDisplay (145-147) returns null → no selection box/handles; for mixed shape+instance groups the union excludes every instance, so the box is undersized and transform handles sit at wrong positions.
- **Fix:** Extract the top-level symbol-instance bounds logic (current lines 214-225) into a private helper, e.g. `private collectSymbolInstanceBounds(inst: SymbolInstanceNode, sceneGraph: SceneGraph, out: Rect[]): void` that: finds def via this.symbolDefinitions.find(d => d.id === inst.symbolId); if def && def.sceneGraphJSON.nodes.length > 0, computes symBounds = getSymbolBounds(def.sceneGraphJSON.nodes); if symBounds.width>0 && height>0, computes worldMatrix = inst.parent ? sceneGraph.getWorldTransform(inst.id) : mat3.compose(inst.transform.position, inst.transform.rotation, inst.transform.scale); pushes transformBoundsToWorld(symBounds, worldMatrix). Replace the body of the existing `if (node.type === 'symbol-instance')` branch (213-226) with a call to this helper (keeping the `return`). Then, inside the group descendants loop (230-237), before the getLocalBounds call, add: `if (desc.type === 'symbol-instance') { this.collectSymbolInstanceBounds(desc, sceneGraph, out); continue; }`. For descendant instances desc.parent is always truthy (they live inside the group), so getWorldTransform(desc.id) is used and correctly composes the group's transform. SymbolInstanceNode is already imported at line 6; narrow `desc` via the type check. No new plumbing needed — symbolDefinitions is already populated (SelectionTool sets it from context.getSymbolDefinitions).
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/selection/SelectionManager.ts`, `packages/core/src/selection/SelectionManager.test.ts`
- **Test:** In packages/core/src/selection/SelectionManager.test.ts (which currently has zero symbol-instance coverage): (1) Build a SceneGraph with a group node containing a single symbol-instance child (instance transform e.g. position offset, scale 1). Call manager.setSymbolDefinitions([def]) where def.id matches the instance.symbolId and def.sceneGraphJSON.nodes contains geometry producing non-zero getSymbolBounds (e.g. a rectangle). Call getSelectionBounds(new Set([groupId]), sceneGraph) (and/or getSelectionBoundsForDisplay) and assert the result is non-null and its rect width/height match the instance's world-space extent (currently it returns null / zero-size). (2) Mixed group: add both a plain rectangle and a symbol-instance placed apart; assert the union rect encloses both — specifically that it extends to cover the instance region, which the pre-fix code omits. Both tests fail before the fix and pass after.
- **Notes:** Additive only: it supplies bounds for nodes previously ignored, so no existing (non-instance) selection bounds change. Reviewer's suggested fix matches this plan. Verified: getSymbolBounds signature is getSymbolBounds(resolvedNodes: Node[]) (symbolResolver.ts:101); getDescendants is recursive so instances nested inside sub-groups are also reached with correct parent chains for getWorldTransform.

#### `F134` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/tools/BoneTool.ts:108`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Minimum bone length is documented as screen pixels but compared in world units, so bone creation silently fails when zoomed in and accidental click-bones appear when zoomed out.

- **Root cause:** BoneTool.MIN_BONE_LENGTH = 5 is documented 'Minimum drag distance (pixels)' (BoneTool.ts:9-10) but compared against `length`, which is computed from worldPosition deltas in onPointerUp (BoneTool.ts:104-108: dx/dy = event.worldPosition - startPoint) with no zoom compensation. At camera.zoom=8, a 32-screen-pixel drag is only 4 world units < 5, so the bone silently fails to create (preview vanishes, no feedback). At zoom=0.1, 5 world units is 0.5 screen px, so jitter creates stray bones. The sibling SNAP_DISTANCE check converts to screen space via camera.worldToScreen (BoneTool.ts:247-252), establishing that pixel-thresholds are the intended convention (also matching PenTool closeThreshold = 10 / camera.zoom, PenTool.ts:79).
- **Fix:** Convert the world-space drag length to the screen-pixel threshold before comparison. In onPointerUp, change the gate at line 108 from `if (length >= MIN_BONE_LENGTH)` to compare against a zoom-adjusted world threshold: const minWorldLength = MIN_BONE_LENGTH / this.context.camera.zoom; if (length >= minWorldLength) { ... }. At zoom=1 this is unchanged (5 world units), so existing tests (BoneTool.test.ts:86 'does not create bone for tiny drags < 5px') still pass.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/tools/BoneTool.ts`
- **Test:** In BoneTool.test.ts single-bone-creation describe: set context.camera.zoom = 8, onPointerDown at world (0,0), onPointerMove/onPointerUp at world (4,0) (4 world units = 32 screen px), and assert a bone node was added (getRootNodes length 1) with length ~4. Optionally add the inverse: at zoom=0.1, a drag of 4 world units (0.4 screen px) creates no bone.

#### `F135` · medium · performance

**Location:** `packages/core/src/tools/BrushTool.ts:247`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Brush preview re-runs a full Schneider curve fit over ALL captured points on every pointer move (O(n^2) per stroke), while the incremental commit pipeline that should prevent this is dead code.

- **Root cause:** BrushTool.updatePreviewNode (BrushTool.ts:238-256) re-runs schneiderFitCurve over this.allPoints (all captured points) on every onPointerMove (line 247), and createPathNode re-runs generateBrushOutline over the whole fitted spine. schneiderFitCurve is recursive with reparameterization, so each move is O(n) and the stroke is O(n^2). The incremental pipeline that would prevent this — committedCurves/committedWidths (lines 73-74) populated by commitFloatingPoints (lines 219-236, called every COMMIT_THRESHOLD=12 points from onPointerMove line 135) — is write-only dead code: neither updatePreviewNode nor finalizeStroke ever reads committedCurves/committedWidths (finalizeStroke, lines 258-268, refits all points from scratch). So commitFloatingPoints only adds extra wasted Schneider fits.
- **Fix:** Make the preview build from the already-committed curves plus a fit of only the small floating window. In updatePreviewNode: if committedCurves is non-empty, compute floatingCurves = schneiderFitCurve(this.floatingPoints.map(p=>p.position), SCHNEIDER_ERROR\*2) and set spine = curvesToPathPoints([...this.committedCurves, ...floatingCurves]); otherwise fall back to fitting allPoints (short strokes before first commit). Keep widths = this.allPoints.map(p=>p.width) unchanged — generateBrushOutline interpolates width parametrically by arc-length (brushOutline.ts:72-78), so it does not need a 1:1 point/width count. This bounds per-move work to the floating window (<= COMMIT_THRESHOLD + overlap points) instead of O(n). finalizeStroke may stay as a single full refit (runs once, cost acceptable) or, for consistency, commit remaining floatingPoints first and build from committedCurves; keep it as-is to minimize risk. Guard: if committedCurves is empty, behavior is identical to today.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/tools/BrushTool.ts`
- **Test:** In BrushTool.test.ts: vi.spyOn the schneider module's schneiderFitCurve (import \* as schneider), simulate a long stroke (>= 40 onPointerMove events with points spaced beyond the min-distance filter), and assert that no single schneiderFitCurve call made during onPointerMove receives an input array longer than COMMIT_THRESHOLD + overlap (e.g. <= 16). Also assert the final path node is still produced (getPreviewNode non-null mid-stroke, node added on pointerUp). Before the fix, the last move passes ~all points; after, it is bounded.

#### `F136` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/tools/DirectSelectionTool.ts:494`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Escape during a vertex/handle drag does not cancel the drag: points stay displaced, and clearing the selection mid-drag makes onPointerUp report an empty node set, skipping vertex keyframing.

- **Root cause:** DirectSelectionTool.onKeyDown Escape (DirectSelectionTool.ts:492-505) unconditionally calls clearPointSelection() when selectedPoints.length > 0, without checking dragMode. During a vertex drag (dragMode==='dragging-point'), each onPointerMove has already committed displaced positions to the scene graph via updateNode (lines 409-413), and initialPointPositions holds the originals. Pressing Escape mid-drag: (1) does NOT revert positions from initialPointPositions, so the vertices stay displaced; (2) empties selectedPoints, so remaining onPointerMove iterations no-op; (3) on onPointerUp (lines 464-472), nodeIds = new Set(this.selectedPoints.map(...)) is empty while hasDragged && dragMode is still 'dragging-point', so onTransformComplete('vertex-move') fires with an empty node set — with auto-keyframe on, the moved vertices get no keyframes and a subsequent timeline evaluation can snap them back, losing the edit. SelectionTool (SelectionTool.ts:409-424) reverts move-on-Escape, confirming the intended cancel-restores-original behavior. Handle drags have the same gap and additionally never capture the original handle at drag start (onPointerDown lines 213-224 store only dragHandle, comment 'stored implicitly' is inaccurate).
- **Fix:** Add explicit drag cancellation. (1) In onPointerDown handle-drag branch (after line 219), capture the original point deep-clone into a new field this.dragHandleInitialPoint = { ...point, handleIn: point.handleIn?{...point.handleIn}:null, handleOut: point.handleOut?{...point.handleOut}:null } where point = getAllPoints(node)[handleHit.pointIndex]. (2) Add private cancelActiveDrag(): if dragMode==='dragging-point', for each selectedPoint restore initialPointPositions via the same setAllPoints/updateNode path used in onPointerMove (or imagePointsToOffsets for image nodes); if dragMode==='dragging-handle' && dragHandle && dragHandleInitialPoint, rebuild the node's points with the initial point via setAllPoints and updateNode. Then reset: dragMode='idle', dragStartPoint=null, dragHandle=null, dragHandleInitialPoint=null, initialPointPositions.clear(), state.isDragging=false, hasDragged=false (keep selectedPoints intact, matching SelectionTool). (3) In onKeyDown Escape, at the top of the case add: if (this.state.isDragging && this.dragMode !== 'idle') { this.cancelActiveDrag(); return; } before the existing selectedPoints/group/tool-switch logic. Also reset dragHandleInitialPoint in onDeactivate/onPointerUp.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/tools/DirectSelectionTool.ts`
- **Test:** In DirectSelectionTool.test.ts: add a path node, select a point, onPointerDown on that point, onPointerMove to a new world position (verify the node point moved), then onKeyDown Escape and assert getAllPoints(node)[i].position equals the original position (reverted). Spy on context.onTransformComplete and assert it is NOT called on the following onPointerUp, and that getSelectedPoints() still contains the point. Add an analogous handle-drag revert test (select point, start handle drag via a handle hit, move, Escape, assert handleOut/handleIn restored).

#### `F137` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/tools/EraserTool.ts:514`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Stroke-erase of a shape inside a rotated or scaled group produces a wrongly-transformed result: only the position is converted to parent-local, not the world-baked geometry orientation.

- **Root cause:** In finalizeStrokeErase, contours come from polygonToContours(result) where result = performBoolean(nodeToPolygon(node, worldMatrix), ...) — i.e. WORLD-space geometry. createBooleanResultNode (booleanOps.ts:223-282) builds the node with identity rotation/scale and points centered on the world bbox center, and sets position = that world center. Then lines 509-517 convert ONLY resultNode.transform.position into parent-local via invParent, leaving the geometry world-baked. The scene graph computes the node's world transform as parentWorld \* localMatrix (SceneGraph getWorldTransform), so parentWorld's rotation/scale is applied to the already-world geometry offset a SECOND time. Translation-only parents (linear part = identity) render correctly; rotated/scaled parents produce geometry that is rotated/scaled twice about the center.
- **Fix:** Transform the contour geometry (not just the position) into parent-local space BEFORE calling createBooleanResultNode, and drop the position-only conversion. Concretely: after the 'no change' comparison block (which must keep using the world-space `contours`), compute `let localContours = contours;` then `if (parentId) { const parentWorld = this.context.sceneGraph.getWorldTransform(parentId); const invParent = mat3.invert(parentWorld); if (invParent) { localContours = contours.map(c => c.map(pt => ({ ...pt, position: mat3.transformPoint(invParent, pt.position) }))); } }`. Pass localContours to createBooleanResultNode (boolean-result points have handleIn/handleOut = null per booleanOps.ts:198-200, so only position needs transforming). Then DELETE the existing lines 509-517 position-only conversion block. Do NOT use the 'add as root' alternative the reviewer mentioned — it would break the existing 'should place replacement node in the same parent group' test (EraserTool.test.ts:555).
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/tools/EraserTool.ts`, `packages/core/src/tools/EraserTool.test.ts`
- **Test:** In EraserTool.test.ts 'grouped nodes' describe: 'should keep correct world geometry when parent is scaled/rotated' — create a GroupNode with transform.scale = {x:2,y:2}, addNode(group); add a 100x100 rectangle child via addNode(rect, group.id); run a thin horizontal performStrokeErase through it; get the replacement path node (group.children[0]); compute its world AABB by transforming each point with sceneGraph.getWorldTransform(resultId); assert the world width and height are ~200 (original 100 \* scale 2), e.g. both < 260. With the current bug the parent scale is applied twice so the world AABB would be ~400, failing the assertion. Optionally also test a rotated parent (transform.rotation = 90) and assert the world bbox size is unchanged rather than sheared.
- **Notes:** Separate pre-existing minor artifact (reviewer noted, out of scope): createBooleanResultNode sets anchor {0.5,0.5} in ABSOLUTE units (booleanOps.ts:268; mat3.compose subtracts anchor directly, math.ts:270), adding a fixed ~0.5px offset even at root. Fixing it means anchor {0,0} in createBooleanResultNode, which is shared by booleanOperation/computeBooleanGroupResult — do not bundle into this fix without checking those callers/tests. This finding and F190 both edit the same replacement block (lines ~509-528); sequence them to avoid churn.

#### `F138` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/tools/SelectionTool.ts:252`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Shift/Ctrl-clicking an already-selected node to deselect it still enters move mode, so any slight pre-release mouse motion drags the remaining selection.

- **Root cause:** In onPointerDown's additive branch (lines 248-257), when isAlreadySelected the node is removed via setSelectedIds(newIds) but execution falls through to 'Start move mode' (lines 263-276), capturing moveStartPositions for the remaining selected nodes. A slight pre-release mouse move then drags the remaining selection (and with auto-keyframe on, keyframes them). DirectSelectionTool handles the same case correctly by returning early after deselection (line 234-236: 'Don't start dragging if we just deselected').
- **Fix:** Add `return;` immediately after `this.context.setSelectedIds(newIds);` inside the `if (isAlreadySelected)` block in the additive branch, so a toggle-off click leaves mode='idle' and never captures moveStartPositions. This mirrors DirectSelectionTool. The 'remove from selection with Ctrl+click on selected' test only asserts the resulting selection, so it still passes.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/tools/SelectionTool.ts`
- **Test:** In SelectionTool.test.ts: select rects A,B,C; shift-click B (pointerDown with shiftKey) -> assert tool.getMode()==='idle' (not 'moving'); then pointerMove a few units and pointerUp -> assert A and C positions are unchanged.

#### `F139` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/tools/SelectionTool.ts:1147`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Resizing a selected symbol instance silently does nothing: handles are shown and 'resizing' mode engages, but performResize has no symbol-instance branch.

- **Root cause:** getSelectionBoundsForDisplay computes bounds for symbol-instance nodes (SelectionManager.ts:144-148), so resize handles render and hitTest returns a handle, and onPointerDown enters mode='resizing'. But captureNodeStates (1004-1053) has no symbol-instance branch (it only handles rectangle/ellipse/polygon/path/text/image/group/artboard), and performResize's type chain (1147-1243) likewise has no symbol-instance case, so no updateNode is ever called — the resize is a silent no-op, yet onTransformComplete('resize') still fires on release. In a multi-selection resize the instance stays frozen while siblings scale, corrupting relative layout.
- **Fix:** Treat symbol-instance like group (scale via transform.scale). (1) In captureNodeStates add `else if (node.type === 'symbol-instance') { state.scale = { ...node.transform.scale }; }`. (2) In performResize add a branch mirroring the group case: `else if (node.type === 'symbol-instance' && initialState.scale !== undefined) { const newScaleX = Math.max(0.01, initialState.scale.x * scaleX); const newScaleY = Math.max(0.01, initialState.scale.y * scaleY); this.context.sceneGraph.updateNode(id, { transform: { ...node.transform, position: newPosition, scale: { x: newScaleX, y: newScaleY } } }); }`. (3) Optional parity (outside this file): add 'symbol-instance' to the scale keyframe branch in useCanvasTools.ts onTransformComplete (currently lines 260-269 handle polygon/path/text/group) so resize keyframes the instance's transform.scale.x/y.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/tools/SelectionTool.ts`, `apps/web/src/hooks/useCanvasTools.ts`
- **Test:** In SelectionTool.test.ts: add a symbol-instance node plus a matching symbol definition (via context.getSymbolDefinitions) so bounds compute; select it, pointerDown on a corner handle, pointerMove to enlarge, pointerUp; assert transform.scale.x/y increased (non-1) proportionally to the drag.
- **Notes:** Requires the test to supply getSymbolDefinitions returning a def with non-empty sceneGraphJSON.nodes so getSelectionBoundsForDisplay yields handles; the current mock context does not set getSymbolDefinitions, so the test must override it.

#### `F140` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/tools/ToolManager.ts:277`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** The global 'f' tool shortcut (artboard) intercepts PointMagnetTool's documented F-key falloff cycling and yanks the user out of Smart Bone sculpting.

- **Root cause:** Plain lowercase 'f' is claimed by two independent tool-shortcut interceptors that both switch to the artboard tool before PointMagnetTool ever sees the key: (1) ToolManager.getToolForShortcut maps f->'artboard' (ToolManager.ts:277) and handleKeyDown (ToolManager.ts:191-203) consumes it and returns early when no modifiers are held; (2) the window-level useToolShortcuts hook maps f->'artboard' (apps/web/src/hooks/useToolShortcuts.ts:21) with no active-tool awareness. PointMagnetTool.onKeyDown cycles falloff on 'f'/'F' (PointMagnetTool.ts:156-162) and is unit-tested (PointMagnetTool.test.ts:180-186) by calling onKeyDown directly, but in production plain 'f' never reaches it — it yanks the user into the artboard tool mid Smart-Bone sculpt. Both interceptors bail on Shift (ToolManager.ts:193 and useToolShortcuts.ts:47), so Shift+F ('F') does reach the tool and cycles falloff; only the documented plain-'f' branch is unreachable. onDeactivate does not clear workingOffsets, so sculpted offsets are not lost — the harm is the tool switch + lost falloff cycling.
- **Fix:** Let the active tool opt out of the shortcut table for keys it consumes. (1) Add an optional method to BaseTool: `consumesKey?(event: KeyboardEvent): boolean` (default undefined). (2) Override it in PointMagnetTool to return true for keys it handles: ['f','F','[',']','Escape'].includes(event.key). (3) In ToolManager.handleKeyDown, before the shortcut lookup, add: if (this.activeTool?.consumesKey?.(event)) { this.activeTool.onKeyDown?.(event); return; }. (4) In useToolShortcuts (apps/web/src/hooks/useToolShortcuts.ts), read the active tool from the store and skip the table when the active tool consumes the key — minimally: subscribe to activeTool and `if (key === 'f' && activeTool === 'point-magnet') return;` before the TOOL_SHORTCUTS lookup (or generalize with a KEY_CONSUMING_TOOLS map). Both interceptors must be guarded because both fire on the same event (ToolManager via useCanvasTools.handleKeyDown canvas listener; useToolShortcuts via a window listener).
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/tools/BaseTool.ts`, `packages/core/src/tools/PointMagnetTool.ts`, `packages/core/src/tools/ToolManager.ts`, `apps/web/src/hooks/useToolShortcuts.ts`
- **Test:** In ToolManager.test.ts: set active tool to 'point-magnet', dispatch handleKeyDown with a plain 'f' KeyboardEvent, and assert the active tool type is still 'point-magnet' (not 'artboard') and that PointMagnetTool.getFalloff() changed (smooth->linear). Add a useToolShortcuts.test.ts case: with store activeTool='point-magnet', dispatching a window 'f' keydown does not call setActiveTool('artboard'); with any other tool, 'f' still switches to artboard.
- **Notes:** Full fix spans packages/core and apps/web because there are two interceptors; guarding only ToolManager leaves the window-level useToolShortcuts still stealing 'f'.

#### `F141` · medium · data-loss

**Location:** `packages/core/src/tools/WeightPaintTool.ts:235`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** F055  
**Finding:** When the tessellation cache misses, a single click paints EVERY vertex of the mesh at full brush strength, ignoring radius and falloff, silently flattening the weight map.

- **Root cause:** WeightPaintTool.paintAtWorldPosition fallback branch (WeightPaintTool.ts:231-244) runs whenever getTessellatedVertices returns null/empty (undefined provider, or a bound node whose geometry cache was never populated — realistically a hidden/visible=false bound node that is never rendered, or a fresh renderer post context-loss). It loops over every vertex and calls paintWeight(skinData, i, activeBoneId, this.brushStrength, this.paintMode) at FULL brushStrength with no spatial radius or falloff, then renormalizes the whole mesh — flattening the weight map on a single click. The stroke does push an undo checkpoint (onTransformStart at line 167), so it is recoverable, but the brush silently ignores its radius/falloff and destructively edits the entire mesh with no visual cue.
- **Fix:** Remove the destructive flood-fill fallback. Replace the else branch (lines 231-244) with a guarded no-op: if vertex positions are unavailable, do not modify weights; emit a single console.warn (e.g. 'WeightPaint: no tessellated geometry for node <id>; skipping stroke (render the node first)') gated so it only logs once per stroke. Do not call paintWeight or updateNode in this case. This coordinates with F055 (same method, main branch) and should be implemented together.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/tools/WeightPaintTool.ts`
- **Test:** In WeightPaintTool.test.ts: bind rect, do NOT provide context.getTessellatedVertices (or make it return null). Capture original vertex weights, onPointerDown at any position, and assert every vertex's influences are unchanged (deep equal to the captured snapshot) and that sceneGraph.updateNode was not invoked with a new skinData (spy on updateNode).
- **Notes:** Same method as F055 (paintAtWorldPosition); do the two fixes in one pass to avoid churn. Severity is data-loss-ish but recoverable via the stroke's undo checkpoint, so medium is appropriate.

### UI component library

#### `F150` · medium · controlled-uncontrolled

**Location:** `packages/ui/src/components/Checkbox.tsx:106`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Uncontrolled Checkbox never renders the check mark: visuals are driven solely by the `checked` prop, not the input's actual DOM state.

- **Root cause:** In Checkbox.tsx the visible box is driven entirely by the `checked` prop, not the input's DOM state. Line 106 `const isChecked = checked || indeterminate;` feeds the box background (line 111), and the check icon is gated on `checked ? <Check/> : null` (line 155). The input at line 141-146 renders `checked={checked}` with `onChange={onChange}` and no `defaultChecked` handling of its own (it flows through `...props` at line 150). When used uncontrolled (`<Checkbox label="Loop" />` or `<Checkbox defaultChecked />`), `checked` is undefined so React leaves the hidden input uncontrolled; clicking toggles the real DOM checked state and fires onChange, but `checked` stays undefined forever, so the visible box (the hidden input is opacity:0, line 42) never shows the checkmark. `defaultChecked` renders an unchecked-looking box over a checked input. Confirmed real; Checkbox.test.tsx only asserts onChange call counts (lines 27-37), never the visual.
- **Fix:** Add internal state mirroring native checked. Destructure `defaultChecked` out of props so it does not also hit the input. Compute `const isControlled = checked !== undefined;` and `const [internalChecked, setInternalChecked] = React.useState(defaultChecked ?? false);` then `const effectiveChecked = isControlled ? checked : internalChecked;`. Wrap onChange: `const handleChange = (e) => { if (!isControlled) setInternalChecked(e.target.checked); onChange?.(e); };`. Set the input to `checked={effectiveChecked}` and `onChange={handleChange}` (always controlled internally, so do NOT also pass defaultChecked to the input). Replace `isChecked = checked || indeterminate` with `effectiveChecked || indeterminate`, and change the icon gate at line 155 from `checked ?` to `effectiveChecked ?`.
- **Files:** `packages/ui/src/components/Checkbox.tsx`
- **Test:** In Checkbox.test.tsx: render uncontrolled `<Checkbox label="Loop" />`, `await user.click(screen.getByRole('checkbox'))`, then assert both `expect(screen.getByRole('checkbox')).toBeChecked()` and that the check icon is now visible via `expect(container.querySelector('.lucide-check')).toBeInTheDocument()`. Add a second case: `render(<Checkbox defaultChecked />)` shows `.lucide-check` on initial render.
- **Notes:** Blast radius is library-only: @quar/ui Checkbox is not imported anywhere in apps/web/src. Still a broken basic usage mode in a published component. Must destructure defaultChecked out of ...props to avoid React's controlled+defaultChecked conflict.

#### `F151` · medium · accessibility

**Location:** `packages/ui/src/components/Checkbox.tsx:141`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** F150  
**Finding:** The `indeterminate` prop is visual-only: the native input's `indeterminate` DOM property is never set, so ARIA/AT state contradicts what sighted users see.

- **Root cause:** In Checkbox.tsx the `indeterminate` prop (line 94) is purely cosmetic: it only switches the rendered icon to Minus (lines 153-154) and colors the box (via isChecked at line 106/111). The native input's `indeterminate` DOM property — which is NOT an HTML attribute and can only be set imperatively — is never assigned. The forwarded ref goes straight to the input (line 142 `ref={ref}`) and there is no useEffect setting `el.indeterminate`. Result: AT announces the box as plain 'not checked', `aria-checked="mixed"` / `:indeterminate` semantics never apply. Confirmed real; the test at lines 44-48 only checks the checkbox exists.
- **Fix:** Create an internal ref `const inputRef = React.useRef<HTMLInputElement>(null);`, point the input's `ref` at it, and forward to the external ref with `React.useImperativeHandle(ref, () => inputRef.current as HTMLInputElement, []);`. Add `React.useEffect(() => { if (inputRef.current) inputRef.current.indeterminate = indeterminate; }, [indeterminate]);` so the DOM property tracks the prop.
- **Files:** `packages/ui/src/components/Checkbox.tsx`
- **Test:** In Checkbox.test.tsx: `render(<Checkbox indeterminate />)` then `expect(screen.getByRole('checkbox')).toBePartiallyChecked()` (jest-dom matcher checks the .indeterminate DOM property). Add a toggle case: rerender with `indeterminate={false}` and assert `.not.toBePartiallyChecked()`.
- **Notes:** Same file as F150; implement together. F150 already restructures onChange/state, so layer this ref-merge + effect on top. Verify the existing `forwards ref` expectations still hold after switching to useImperativeHandle (Checkbox.test.tsx has no ref test currently, but other components do).

#### `F152` · medium · accessibility

**Location:** `packages/ui/src/components/Input.tsx:149`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Input's `<label>` is not associated with the input — no htmlFor/id and it does not wrap the input — so clicking the label does nothing and AT does not announce the field name.

- **Root cause:** In Input.tsx line 149 the label is a bare sibling `{label && <label style={labelStyles}>{label}</label>}` with no `htmlFor`, and the input (lines 156-163) gets no generated `id`, so they are never associated. `getByLabelText('Email')` fails, the field has no accessible name, and clicking the label text does not focus the input. Helper/error text (lines 170-171) is not linked via `aria-describedby`, and `error` sets no `aria-invalid`. Confirmed real; Input.test.tsx only checks label text via getByText (line 13-15).
- **Fix:** Destructure `id` and `'aria-describedby'` from props (or just `id`). Generate `const generatedId = React.useId();` and `const inputId = id ?? generatedId;`. Put `htmlFor={inputId}` on the label and `id={inputId}` on the input. Generate ids for helper/error: `const helperId = `${inputId}-helper``; render helper/error spans with that id; on the input set `aria-describedby={ (helperText && !error) || (error && errorMessage) ? helperId : undefined }`(merge with any caller-provided describedby) and`aria-invalid={error || undefined}`. Ensure `id`/`aria-\*`are set explicitly and not clobbered by`{...props}` (place after the spread or destructure them out).
- **Files:** `packages/ui/src/components/Input.tsx`
- **Test:** In Input.test.tsx: `render(<Input label="Email" />)` then `expect(screen.getByLabelText('Email')).toBeInTheDocument()`. Add: `render(<Input label="Email" error errorMessage="Invalid" />)` and assert `screen.getByLabelText('Email')` has `aria-invalid="true"` and an `aria-describedby` that resolves to the 'Invalid' text node.
- **Notes:** Blast radius library-only (not imported in app). Honor a caller-supplied id/aria-describedby rather than overwriting.

#### `F153` · medium · accessibility

**Location:** `packages/ui/src/components/Panel.tsx:114`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Collapsible panel header is a plain div with onClick — no keyboard access, no role, no aria-expanded — so keyboard and screen-reader users cannot expand/collapse panels at all.

- **Root cause:** In Panel.tsx the collapsible header is a plain `<div>` with `onClick={handleToggle}` (lines 108-115) — no `role`, no `tabIndex`, no keydown handler, no `aria-expanded`, no `aria-controls`. Keyboard and screen-reader users cannot expand/collapse. Confirmed accurate at the code level. Severity framing is somewhat overstated in the original finding: this @quar/ui Panel is not imported anywhere in apps/web/src (the editor's PropertiesPanel/LayerPanel/TimelinePanel are separate custom components), so there is no live app impact — it is a defect in a reusable published DS component only. Panel.test.tsx (lines 27-38) only exercises click toggling.
- **Fix:** Keep the header as a div (headerActions may contain <button>s, so a real nested <button> would be invalid HTML). When `collapsible`, add to the header div: `role="button"`, `tabIndex={0}`, `aria-expanded={isExpanded}`, `aria-controls={contentId}`, and an `onKeyDown` that calls `handleToggle()` and `e.preventDefault()` on 'Enter' or ' ' (Space). Generate `const contentId = React.useId();` and put `id={contentId}` on the content div (line 129). When not collapsible, omit role/tabIndex/aria-expanded so it is not announced as an interactive control. The existing headerActions stopPropagation (line 123) already prevents action clicks from toggling; ensure keyboard activation on nested action buttons is unaffected.
- **Files:** `packages/ui/src/components/Panel.tsx`
- **Test:** In Panel.test.tsx: render `<Panel title="Details">Body</Panel>`, `const header = screen.getByRole('button', { name: /Details/ })`, assert `header` has `aria-expanded="true"`, then `header.focus(); await user.keyboard('{Enter}')` and assert `screen.queryByText('Body')` is gone and `aria-expanded="false"`. Repeat with Space (' ').
- **Notes:** aria-controls will reference an id that is unmounted while collapsed (content is conditionally rendered at line 129); acceptable, or optionally keep content mounted with `hidden` for a fully valid reference. Use role=button (not <button>) to avoid button-in-button with headerActions.

#### `F154` · medium · accessibility

**Location:** `packages/ui/src/components/Select.tsx:153`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** F152  
**Finding:** Select has the same unassociated `<label>` defect as Input: no htmlFor/id association, so the combobox has no accessible name and label clicks are dead.

- **Root cause:** In Select.tsx line 153 the label is a bare sibling `{label && <label style={labelStyles}>{label}</label>}` with no `htmlFor`; the `<select>` (lines 155-173) gets no generated `id`. Identical defect to Input (F152): the combobox has no accessible name (`getByLabelText` fails), screen readers announce an unnamed combobox, label clicks are dead, and helperText/errorMessage (lines 176-177) are not wired via `aria-describedby`, with no `aria-invalid` on error. Confirmed real; Select.test.tsx only checks label text via getByText (lines 29-32).
- **Fix:** Mirror the F152 fix: destructure `id` from props, `const generatedId = React.useId(); const selectId = id ?? generatedId;`, set `htmlFor={selectId}` on the label and `id={selectId}` on the select. Add a `${selectId}-helper` id on the helper/error span and set `aria-describedby` to it when present, plus `aria-invalid={error || undefined}` on the select. Guard against `{...props}` clobbering the explicit id/aria attributes.
- **Files:** `packages/ui/src/components/Select.tsx`
- **Test:** In Select.test.tsx: `render(<Select options={options} label="Frame Rate" />)` then `expect(screen.getByLabelText('Frame Rate')).toBeInTheDocument()`. Add an error case asserting `aria-invalid="true"` and `aria-describedby` resolving to the error text.
- **Notes:** Same pattern as F152 in a sibling file; dependsOn is soft — do F152 first so this reuses the exact id/aria-describedby approach for consistency. Not a hard blocker; could be parallelized. Blast radius library-only.

### Web — UI, panels & timeline

#### `F070` · medium · duplication

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/common/ColorPicker.tsx:71`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** L · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Color<->hex conversion is independently implemented in at least 7 places and has already drifted: the UI copies break on the fractional/overshoot channel values the animation engine deliberately produces.

- **Root cause:** Color<->hex conversion is independently reimplemented across the codebase with no shared module in @quar/core (grep for colorToHex/hexToColor in packages/core/src/index.ts and packages/types returns nothing). Confirmed copies: ColorPicker.tsx rgbToHex (line 71) and hexToRgb (line 80); PropertiesPanel.tsx colorToHex (line 81) and hexToColor (line 88); GradientEditor.tsx colorToHex (line 42); svgExporter.ts colorToHex (line 39); svgUtils.ts parseHexColor (line 100); OnionSkinRenderer.ts hexToRgbNormalized (line 44); plus Python \_hex_to_color in tools/quar-mcp/app/tools/node_tools.py (line 334) — at least 7 places, so the count claim holds. The copies have DRIFTED on out-of-range channels: svgExporter.colorToHex clamps to [0,255] AND rounds (line 40-48), but PropertiesPanel.colorToHex and GradientEditor.colorToHex round WITHOUT clamping, and ColorPicker.rgbToHex neither rounds NOR clamps. Overshoot values (300) produce 3-hex-digit segments that padStart(2) does not truncate → malformed 7+ char '#12c...' strings; fractional values (127.5) produce '7f.8'; negatives produce '-14'. These malformed strings are fed to `type="text"` inputs and to CSS `backgroundColor` on swatches (browsers silently ignore invalid CSS color), so the symptom is a wrong/absent swatch plus garbled text, not a crash — matching the reviewer's self-corrections.
- **Fix:** Add a single shared module packages/core/src/color/colorHex.ts exporting: `colorToHex(color: Color): string` that rounds AND clamps each channel to [0,255] before `.toString(16).padStart(2,'0')` (port svgExporter's clamp+round version, uppercase '#RRGGBB'); a plain-channel `rgbToHex(r,g,b)` overload with the same clamp+round (ColorPicker calls with bare ints); `hexToColor(hex): Color | null` supporting 3/4/6/8-digit forms (reuse svgUtils.parseHexColor logic); and a normalized `hexToRgbNormalized` for OnionSkinRenderer. Export all from packages/core/src/index.ts. Replace every copy: ColorPicker (lines 71-88 — note line 154 initial hexInput and line 365 currentHex now clamp), PropertiesPanel (81-98), GradientEditor (42-49), svgExporter (39-50), svgUtils (100), OnionSkinRenderer (44). Port the same clamp+round into the Python \_hex_to_color / \_color_to_hex in node_tools.py so exports match.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/color/colorHex.ts`, `packages/core/src/index.ts`, `apps/web/src/components/common/ColorPicker.tsx`, `apps/web/src/components/layout/PropertiesPanel.tsx`, `apps/web/src/components/common/GradientEditor.tsx`, `packages/core/src/svg/svgExporter.ts`, `packages/core/src/svg/svgUtils.ts`, `packages/core/src/rendering/OnionSkinRenderer.ts`, `tools/quar-mcp/app/tools/node_tools.py`
- **Test:** packages/core unit test for colorHex.ts asserting colorToHex({r:300,g:-5,b:127.5,a:1}) === '#FF0080' (overshoot clamped, negative clamped, fractional rounded → well-formed 7-char hex), and round-trip hexToColor(colorToHex(c)) parity for in-range colors. Add a ColorPicker.test.tsx case rendering with an out-of-range color prop (e.g. r:300) and asserting the hex-input value is a valid 7-char '#RRGGBB'. Add a pytest parity test for node_tools \_hex_to_color/\_color_to_hex on the same out-of-range inputs producing identical output.
- **Notes:** Two reviewer description errors are already self-corrected and do not invalidate the finding: (1) none of the three components use `<input type="color">` — the malformed hex hits `type="text"` inputs and CSS backgroundColor; (2) in ColorPicker the bad hex surfaces in the initial hexInput state (line 154), not currentHex (line 365, which derives from hsvToRgb and is always rounded/well-formed) and self-corrects on blur. Substance (duplication + clamp drift) is confirmed.

#### `F071` · medium · data-loss

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/common/ExportDialog.tsx:151`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** A filename pattern without the {N} placeholder makes every frame get the same zip entry name, so the exported PNG-sequence zip silently contains only the last frame.

- **Root cause:** generateFrameFilenames (packages/export/src/exportUtils.ts:32) builds each name with `pattern.replace('{N}', paddedFrame)`. String.replace on a pattern lacking '{N}' returns the pattern unchanged, so every iteration produces the identical filename (e.g. 'static*name.png'). ExportDialog.tsx:184 then calls `zip.file(filenames[i], blob)` with the same name each time; JSZip keys files by name in its `files` object, so each call overwrites the previous entry and the final zip contains only the last frame. The pattern text input (ExportDialog.tsx:471-478) lets the user type any string with no validation, and the default 'frame*{N}' is only a placeholder. The exact same defect exists in the reusable exportPngSequence (packages/export/src/pngSequence.ts:54,80) since it uses the same helper. The current unit test at pngSequence.test.ts:50-54 explicitly asserts the buggy duplicate-name output.
- **Fix:** Fix centrally in generateFrameFilenames: detect placeholder once (`const hasPlaceholder = pattern.includes('{N}')`) and when absent, append the padded frame to guarantee uniqueness, e.g. `const base = hasPlaceholder ? pattern.replace('{N}', paddedFrame) : `${pattern}_${paddedFrame}`; const filename = base + '.' + extension;`. This repairs both the ExportDialog path and exportPngSequence at once. Additionally, in ExportDialog.tsx add a lightweight UI guard for good UX: since generateFrameFilenames now self-heals, no hard block is strictly required, but optionally show a subtle hint under the Pattern input when it lacks '{N}' (e.g. 'Frame number will be appended'). Update the existing test pngSequence.test.ts:50-54 to expect the new distinct names ('static_name_0.png', 'static_name_1.png').
- **Files:** `packages/export/src/exportUtils.ts`, `packages/export/src/pngSequence.test.ts`, `apps/web/src/components/common/ExportDialog.tsx`
- **Test:** In pngSequence.test.ts, replace the current 'handles pattern without {N} placeholder' test to assert distinct names: `generateFrameFilenames('static_name', 0, 1, 'png')` returns `['static_name_0.png','static_name_1.png']`; add a case asserting a 3-frame no-placeholder pattern yields 3 unique names.
- **Notes:** Central helper fix is preferred over per-call-site validation because the same bug lives in exportPngSequence. Must update the existing test that encodes the old behavior, otherwise the fix will break that test.

#### `F072` · medium · ui-state

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/common/ExportDialog.tsx:190`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Cancelling an export leaves the dialog permanently stuck in the progress view because `exporting` is never reset to false on the cancellation path.

- **Root cause:** The Cancel button handler (ExportDialog.tsx:382-385) and the Escape-during-export branch (lines 101-103) set `cancelledRef.current = true` and `cancelled: true` but never set `exporting: false`. In handleExport, the png-sequence loop breaks at line 171 and sprite-sheet at line 255; the finalize/download/close blocks are then skipped by the `if (!cancelledRef.current)` guards (lines 190, 277). There is no `else` and no outer reset, so after the try/catch completes normally `state.exporting` remains true and `state.progress` remains the last progress value. The body keeps rendering the progress view (`state.exporting && state.progress`, line 367) and the footer with Export/Cancel is hidden (`!state.exporting`, line 569), leaving the dialog frozen in the progress state. Only the header X (line 346) can dismiss it.
- **Fix:** In handleExport, after the main `try { ... } catch { ... }` block (i.e. wrapping around lines 126-324), add a reset for the cancellation case that covers both branches: `if (cancelledRef.current) { setState((s) => ({ ...s, exporting: false, progress: null, cancelled: false })); }`. Place it so it runs whether the png-sequence or sprite-sheet loop broke. Do NOT reset on the success path (close() already unmounts) nor duplicate the catch-block reset. This returns the dialog to the form view after Cancel so the user can adjust settings and retry.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/common/ExportDialog.tsx`
- **Test:** Add a test that starts a PNG export, clicks 'export-cancel', and asserts the dialog returns to the form view: `export-dialog-export` (footer) is visible again and `export-progress` is gone. This requires extending the '@quar/export' mock in ExportDialog.test.tsx to provide createFrameRenderer/getFrameCount/generateFrameFilenames (a fake renderer whose renderFrameAsBlob resolves a Blob and whose loop yields via setTimeout) so the export actually enters the rendering loop before cancel.
- **Notes:** Testability caveat: the current test file mocks '@quar/export' with only exportLottieBlob/analyzeLottieExport, so a real PNG export currently throws (createFrameRenderer undefined) and hits the catch which already resets exporting — the mock must be enriched to exercise the true cancel path.

#### `F073` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/common/ExportDialog.tsx:346`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** F072  
**Finding:** The header X button is not disabled during export; clicking it hides the dialog while the export keeps running invisibly and later triggers an unexpected download.

- **Root cause:** The header close button (ExportDialog.tsx:346) is `<button onClick={close}>` with no disabled state and no cancellation. It is not gated on `state.exporting`, unlike the backdrop mousedown (line 331 checks `!state.exporting`) and the tab buttons (line 358 `disabled={state.exporting}`). Clicking X during a long PNG/sprite export calls close() -> after EXIT_MS onClose() unmounts the dialog, but cancelledRef stays false so the async loop in handleExport keeps rendering frames, then hits `if (!cancelledRef.current)` (true) and calls downloadBlob + close() (lines 200-202 / 296-315) on the now-unmounted component — a surprise file download plus setState-on-unmounted-component warnings.
- **Fix:** Introduce a `requestClose` callback used by the header X: `const requestClose = useCallback(() => { if (state.exporting) { cancelledRef.current = true; } close(); }, [state.exporting, close]);` and set `onClick={requestClose}` on the header button (line 346). Setting cancelledRef before closing makes the loop break and makes the `if (!cancelledRef.current)` guards false, preventing the surprise downloadBlob. (Alternative, simpler but less friendly: `disabled={state.exporting}` on the X button, consistent with the tabs — but keeping it as a cancel-and-close is better UX and also covers the F072 stuck state.)
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/common/ExportDialog.tsx`
- **Test:** Add a test that starts a PNG export (with the enriched '@quar/export' mock from F072), clicks 'export-dialog-close' mid-render, waits for the loop to drain, and asserts downloadBlob (mocked exportService) was NOT called with a zip — i.e. no surprise download after dismissal.
- **Notes:** Coordinate with F072: both touch the cancellation flow. Not a hard code dependency, but implementing F072 first means the shared cancel-reset logic and the enriched test mock are already in place; sequencing avoids two conflicting edits to handleExport/cancel handling.

#### `F074` · medium · validation

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/common/ExportDialog.tsx:400`  
**Verdict:** partly · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Typed width/height and frame-range values are not clamped or cross-validated, producing silently broken exports (oversized canvases, empty zips).

- **Root cause:** Two distinct sub-issues. (1) Fully deterministic: width/height/frame onChange handlers (lines 400,410,423,432) store `parseInt(...) || fallback` with no clamping; the HTML `min`/`max` attributes only constrain spinner arrows, not typed values, so negatives or values > 8192 pass through. With startFrame > endFrame, getFrameCount returns Math.max(0, end-start+1)=0, the png loop never runs (line 170), and the guarded finalize (line 190) still generates and downloads an empty 'png-sequence.zip' via downloadBlob (line 201) then close() — an empty archive presented as success. (2) Browser-dependent: oversized width/height makes createFrameRenderer allocate a huge canvas/WebGL surface that may throw (caught at 321-324, silent console.error + reset) or silently produce a broken/huge output. The claim's empty-zip and unclamped-input parts are real; the oversized-canvas failure mode is real but non-deterministic.
- **Fix:** (a) Clamp in the onChange handlers: width/height -> `Math.min(8192, Math.max(1, parseInt(e.target.value) || <default>))`; startFrame/endFrame -> `Math.max(0, parseInt(e.target.value) || 0)`. (b) Cross-validate range: derive `const rangeValid = state.endFrame >= state.startFrame;` and disable the Export button (line 574-580) when `!rangeValid` (add `disabled` + a visible hint near the Frame Range row). (c) Defensive guard in handleExport: at the start of the png-sequence and sprite-sheet branches compute frameCount and `if (frameCount <= 0) { setState((s)=>({...s, exporting:false, progress:null})); return; }` so an empty archive is never produced even if the button guard is bypassed. Optionally add an `error: string | null` field to ExportDialogState and render it in the body to surface the reason instead of silently doing nothing.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/common/ExportDialog.tsx`
- **Test:** Tests: (1) typing '99999' into export-width leaves value clamped to '8192'; typing '-5' clamps to '1'. (2) setting start-frame > end-frame disables 'export-dialog-export' (assert disabled attribute) and, if clicked/forced, downloadBlob is never called with 'png-sequence.zip'.
- **Notes:** Larger than the others because it adds validation state/UI (disabled Export + optional error surface). Disabling the Export button changes existing UX; the existing test 'has Export button' only checks presence/text, so it stays green, but new range-validation tests should assert the disabled path explicitly. The oversized-canvas branch is inherently browser-dependent and only partly fixable via clamping; note that in verdict.

#### `F079` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/LayerPanel.tsx:293`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Layer rename never works for nested layers: the recursive child renderer hardcodes isRenaming={false}.

- **Root cause:** Nested (child) layer rows can never enter rename mode. Child rows are rendered through LayerRowById, and inside LayerRow's children map the prop is hardcoded `isRenaming={false}` (LayerPanel.tsx:293). LayerRowById (lines 305-356) subscribes to `selectedNodeIds` and `enteredGroupId` from the store but does NOT know about `renamingNodeId`, and it cannot: `renamingNodeId` is LOCAL component state in LayerPanel (`const [renamingNodeId, setRenamingNodeId] = useState<string|null>(null)` at line 384) — confirmed absent from editorStore.ts. handleDoubleClick (lines 436-439) and the single-select context-menu Rename item (line 602) both call setRenamingNodeId for ANY node id, but for anything below the root the InlineRenameInput (rendered only when isRenaming is true, line 226) never mounts, so the action silently does nothing. Only the root-level render (line 863 `isRenaming={renamingNodeId === node.id}`) works.
- **Fix:** Thread the renamingNodeId value down instead of the hardcoded boolean. Replace the `isRenaming: boolean` prop on both LayerRowProps and the LayerRowById prop object with `renamingNodeId: string | null`. Inside LayerRow, compute `const isRenaming = renamingNodeId === node.id;` and keep using it at line 226; when rendering children (lines 284-298) pass `renamingNodeId={renamingNodeId}` and delete the `isRenaming={false}` line (293). Inside LayerRowById, accept `renamingNodeId`, compute `isRenaming = renamingNodeId === nodeId` and pass it to its LayerRow, and forward `renamingNodeId` unchanged so it recurses. Update the root render at line 863 to pass `renamingNodeId={renamingNodeId}` instead of `isRenaming={...}`. (Alternative, matches reviewer's 'read from store' wording but broader: move renamingNodeId+setRenamingNodeId into editorStore and have LayerRowById read it via useEditorStore like selectedNodeIds — cleaner recursion but changes store surface; prop-threading is the contained, single-file fix and is preferred.)
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/LayerPanel.tsx`
- **Test:** In LayerPanel.test.tsx add a test: render a group with a child rect, then fireEvent.doubleClick on the child's `layer-row-<childId>` element (or open its context menu and click `context-menu-item-rename`); assert the `layer-rename-input` (data-testid) is now in the document. Then type a new name, press Enter, and assert sceneGraph.getNode(childId).name equals the new value. A companion negative assertion could snapshot that before the fix no input appears, but the positive path is sufficient to lock in the fix.

#### `F080` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/LayerPanel.tsx:771`  
**Verdict:** partly · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Drag state is never cleared when the pointer is released outside the panel (no pointer capture, no global pointerup), leaving a stale active drag.

- **Root cause:** handlePointerDown (LayerPanel.tsx:688-713) sets dragState but never captures the pointer (no setPointerCapture) and there is no window/document-level pointerup or pointercancel listener. handlePointerUp/handlePointerMove/handlePointerLeave are all bound to the content div (lines 848-850). If the user drags out of the panel and releases the button there, no pointerup reaches the content div, so dragState is never cleared; handlePointerLeave (lines 827-831) only nulls dropTarget, not dragState. dragState.active therefore stays true: on the next pointer re-entry handlePointerMove recomputes dropTarget (phantom indicator via the dropBefore/dropAfter box-shadow), and a subsequent pointerUp inside executes handlePointerUp's reorder branch (lines 771-819) unexpectedly.
- **Fix:** Guarantee terminal cleanup regardless of where the button is released. Preferred: add a useEffect that, while dragState is non-null, registers window listeners for 'pointerup' and 'pointercancel' that reset dragState(null), dropTarget(null) and didDragRef.current=false, cleaning them up when dragState becomes null. To avoid double-handling when the release happens INSIDE the panel (content onPointerUp already runs the drop and nulls dragState), the window handler should be a plain cancel-and-reset: if content's handlePointerUp already fired, dragState is already null and the effect has been torn down, so nothing happens; if released outside, the window handler cancels the drag with no reorder. Acceptable alternative: call `e.currentTarget.setPointerCapture(e.pointerId)` in handlePointerDown (guarded, e.g. `try { e.currentTarget.setPointerCapture(e.pointerId) } catch {}` because jsdom may not implement it) so pointerup always fires on the captured row and bubbles to handlePointerUp; note this suppresses hover pointerleave semantics. Do NOT touch didDragRef reset logic in handlePointerDown — it is correct.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/LayerPanel.tsx`
- **Test:** In LayerPanel.test.tsx: add two rows, pointerDown on a row, pointerMove past the 5px threshold (drag becomes active — assert the row has the dragging class), then simulate release outside the panel by firing pointerUp on window (fireEvent.pointerUp(window)) WITHOUT a content pointerUp. Assert: (a) no row carries the dragging class afterward, (b) no drop-indicator class (dropBefore/dropAfter/dropInside) is present, and (c) a subsequent pointerMove over another row does NOT set a drop indicator (dragState was cleared). Optionally spy on sceneGraph.moveNode and assert it was not called.
- **Notes:** The core defect is real; one of the originally-claimed consequences is not. Real: stale dragState when the pointer is released outside the panel -> phantom drop indicators on re-hover and a possible unintended (undoable) reorder. Not-real (already flagged by the reviewer, keep excluded from the fix rationale): the 'next click on a layer gets swallowed because didDragRef stays true' claim — handlePointerDown (line 693) sets didDragRef.current=false on every left-button pointerdown, which always precedes the row onClick, so handleSelect (lines 421-424) sees false and selection works normally.

#### `F081` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/PropertiesPanel.tsx:763`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Removing a fill/stroke/effect leaves behind index-based keyframe tracks, which then animate the wrong element or resurrect a malformed entry at the deleted index during playback

- **Root cause:** handleRemoveFill (760-768) and handleRemoveStroke (940-948) do `getNodeFills/Strokes(currentNode).filter((_,i)=>i!==index)` and updateNode, and store removeEffect (editorStore.ts:2238-2247) does `node.effects.filter((_,i)=>i!==effectIndex)` — none touch the timeline. Keyframe tracks are keyed by array position (`fills.N.color`, `strokes.N.width`, `effects.N.opacity`, created e.g. at 716-717, 892-893, and effect handlers 3325-3480). After removing element at index i, elements above i shift down by one but their tracks keep the old index, so a track `fills.i.color` now animates the wrong (shifted) fill, and a track `fills.<last>.color` addresses an out-of-bounds index -> setProperty (PropertyBinding.ts:40-67) fabricates a malformed entry. Corruption triggers on any timeline re-evaluation (usePlayback applies animations on every currentFrame change, not just playback), so a single scrub after removal manifests it.
- **Fix:** Add a store helper e.g. `removeAndReindexTracks(nodeId, prefix, removedIndex)` that: filters out tracks whose property matches `^${prefix}\.${removedIndex}(\.|$)`, and for every remaining track whose property matches `^${prefix}\.(\d+)(.*)` with captured index > removedIndex, rewrites the property to `${prefix}.${index-1}${rest}` (return a new tracks array so subscribers update). Call it from handleRemoveFill('fills'), handleRemoveStroke('strokes'), and inside removeEffect ('effects') with the removed index. Prefer implementing the reindex as a pure function in @quar/animation (Timeline.ts) and wiring a thin store action, so it is unit-testable. (Longer term: key tracks by stable element ids instead of array position, but reindex is the minimal correct fix.)
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts`, `apps/web/src/components/layout/PropertiesPanel.tsx`, `packages/animation/src/Timeline.ts`
- **Test:** Unit test the reindex helper directly: timeline with tracks 'fills.0.color','fills.1.color','fills.2.color'; remove index 1; assert result has 'fills.0.color' unchanged, the old 'fills.2.color' now 'fills.1.color', and no track referencing index 2. Plus an integration test: node with 3 fills and a 'fills.2.color' keyframe, call handleRemoveFill(1), scrub a frame, assert node.fills stays length 2 with no fabricated/undefined entry.

#### `F082` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/PropertiesPanel.tsx:1115`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Uniform corner-radius edits gate keyframing on the property string 'cornerRadius.undefined', so existing corner-radius keyframes are not updated and the edit is silently reverted

- **Root cause:** In handleCornerRadiusChange, the uniform (corner===undefined) path gates keyframing on a template string that interpolates undefined: line 1115 `shouldKeyframe(autoKeyframe, selectedId, `cornerRadius.${corner}`)` becomes 'cornerRadius.undefined' (also image path, 1142). shouldKeyframe (109-115) returns true when autoKeyframe is on (so auto-key works), but when autoKeyframe is OFF it calls findTrack(timeline,nodeId,'cornerRadius.undefined') which never matches an existing track, returns false, and the per-corner addKeyframeAtFrame calls at 1119-1122/1146-1149 are skipped. The node is still updated immediately (updateNode at 1114/1141), so the loss surfaces on the next timeline re-evaluation: the stale existing 'cornerRadius.0' keyframe re-applies to corner 0 and diverges from the just-typed uniform value. Polygon path (1154) correctly uses literal 'cornerRadius' and is unaffected.
- **Fix:** For the corner===undefined branch of the rectangle and image cases, change the gate from `cornerRadius.${corner}` to a real property. Simplest per reviewer: gate on 'cornerRadius.0' (`shouldKeyframe(autoKeyframe, selectedId, 'cornerRadius.0')`). More robust: OR across the four per-corner tracks (return true if any of cornerRadius.0..3 has keyframes). Keep the existing behavior of writing all four keyframes when a track exists / autoKeyframe on. Apply to both the rectangle branch (1115) and the image branch (1142).
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/PropertiesPanel.tsx`
- **Test:** Rectangle with an existing keyframe track 'cornerRadius.0' (keyframe at frame 0), autoKeyframe OFF; set currentFrame to 10 (no keyframe there); call handleCornerRadiusChange('20') with corner undefined (uniform CR input change); assert keyframes were added at frame 10 for cornerRadius.0..3 (currently none are added because the gate is 'cornerRadius.undefined').

#### `F083` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/PropertiesPanel.tsx:1771`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Inner Radius keyframe indicator defaults an unset innerRadius to 1 instead of poly.radius, turning a regular polygon into a degenerate 1px-inner star when keyframed

- **Root cause:** Inner Radius KeyframeIndicator onToggle (1771) creates a keyframe with `poly.innerRadius ?? 1`, while the field's display value (1780) uses `poly.innerRadius ?? poly.radius`. For a regular polygon innerRadius is undefined, so the IR field shows poly.radius (e.g. 50) but toggling the diamond writes value 1. On the next frame evaluation applyAnimatedValues sets innerRadius=1, and ShapeRenderer switches to createStarPath whenever node.innerRadius !== undefined (ShapeRenderer.ts:1868 and 3991), so the hexagon is redrawn as a degenerate 1px-inner spiky star, contradicting the displayed value and the shape the user keyframed.
- **Fix:** Change line 1771 to keyframe the same default the display uses: `onToggle={() => toggleKeyframe('innerRadius', poly.innerRadius ?? poly.radius)}`. One-token change; no other behavior affected.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/PropertiesPanel.tsx`
- **Test:** Render panel with a regular polygon selected (radius 50, innerRadius undefined); click the Inner Radius KeyframeIndicator (the diamond in the Inner Radius property header); assert the created keyframe's value === 50 (poly.radius), not 1.

#### `F084` · medium · data-loss

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/PropertiesPanel.tsx:1845`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Bone Length ScrubLabel calls pushUndo on every pointermove, flooding the 50-entry undo stack and destroying all prior undo history in a single scrub gesture

- **Root cause:** ScrubLabel fires onScrubStart exactly once on pointerdown (ScrubLabel.tsx:37) and onChange on every pointermove (ScrubLabel.tsx:52). The bone Length ScrubLabel wires BOTH onScrubStart={handleScrubStart} (PropertiesPanel.tsx:1840, which calls pushUndo once per gesture) AND an extra pushUndo(sceneGraph) inside onChange (1845). So a single drag pushes one snapshot at pointer-down plus one per pointermove event. pushUndo (editorStore.ts:2807-2819) caps the stack at MAX_UNDO_STACK_SIZE=50 and shifts out the oldest, so one sustained scrub floods and evicts all prior undo history. Scene document is not corrupted (hence medium), only recoverability is lost.
- **Fix:** Remove the redundant `pushUndo(sceneGraph);` at line 1845 inside the bone Length ScrubLabel onChange; onScrubStart={handleScrubStart} already snapshots once per gesture, matching every other ScrubLabel in the file. Leave the keyboard/text-input path (1859) as-is (one snapshot per committed keystroke is standard). Optionally also drop the per-notch pushUndo in the same input's numericInputProps wheel handler (1870) or replace it with a single snapshot to avoid a lesser wheel-scroll flood — but the primary fix is deleting line 1845.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/PropertiesPanel.tsx`
- **Test:** Render panel with a bone node selected; record useEditorStore.getState().undoStack.length; simulate a scrub on the L ScrubLabel: pointerdown on data-testid 'scrub-label-L', then dispatch several document pointermove events, then pointerup; assert undoStack length increased by exactly 1 (not once per move).

#### `F085` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Timeline.tsx:134`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Dope sheet only renders keyframes for root nodes, so keyframes on nodes inside groups are invisible and uneditable in the timeline.

- **Root cause:** The dope sheet's node list is populated solely from getRootNodes(): Timeline.tsx:134 `setNodes([...sceneGraph.getRootNodes()].reverse())`. Layer labels (886-895), track rows (977-1001) and the nodeKeyframes useMemo (160-178, calling getTracksByNode per listed node) all iterate only that root-only list, so keyframes on nodes nested inside groups are never rendered or made interactive. Yet usePlayback.applyAnimations (usePlayback.ts:24-46) drives animation from getAnimatedNodes(timeline) (Timeline.ts:331-339) which returns EVERY animated nodeId regardless of hierarchy and applies each via sg.getNode(nodeId).updateNode — so nested-node keyframes animate at runtime but are invisible/uneditable in the timeline. Secondary performance defect: the same effect subscribes to 'nodeChanged' (Timeline.tsx:139) and unconditionally allocates a fresh array via setNodes on every event; SceneGraph.updateNode emits 'nodeChanged' (SceneGraph.ts:204), and usePlayback calls sg.updateNode per animated node per frame (usePlayback.ts:43) plus tools/PropertiesPanel call it per pointer-move, so the whole dope sheet re-renders and the O(nodes×tracks) nodeKeyframes useMemo rebuilds on every transform tick.
- **Fix:** Correctness: build the dope-sheet node list from a full hierarchy traversal instead of getRootNodes only. Replace the update callback body with a traversal that collects all nodes, e.g. `const list: Node[] = []; sceneGraph.traverse((n) => { list.push(n); }); setNodes(list);` (traverse yields root-first, depth-first — optionally indent rows by depth for readability; keep a stable order). getTracksByNode/nodeKeyframes then surface nested-node keyframes and the diamonds become clickable/draggable. Performance: guard setNodes so it only replaces state when the visible node-identity list actually changed — keep a ref holding the last id+name signature (e.g. list.map(n=>n.id+':'+(n.name??'')).join('|')) and early-return inside `update` when the new signature equals the ref, otherwise update the ref and call setNodes. This keeps rename/add/remove/move responsive while eliminating churn on transform-only nodeChanged events during playback and drags.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Timeline.tsx`
