- **Test:** Timeline component test: create a group node with a child, add a keyframe on the child's track via the store, render Timeline in dopeSheet mode, assert the child's keyframe diamond (data-testid `keyframe-<id>`) is present and clicking it selects it. Performance test: render Timeline, fire a transform-only updateNode (nodeChanged) that does not change any node's id/name, and assert the nodes list reference is stable / setNodes not re-applied (e.g. spy render count unchanged).
- **Notes:** Two independent real defects bundled at one line. The traversal changes dope-sheet layout (adds nested rows); verify labels, track rows and nodeKeyframes stay index-aligned and that the empty-state (nodes.length===0) branch still works.

#### `F086` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Timeline.tsx:250`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** F019  
**Finding:** After dragging a multi-selected group of keyframes in the dope sheet, the selection collapses to just the dragged keyframe.

- **Root cause:** After a pointer-captured keyframe drag (onPointerDown/Move/Up on the keyframe div, Timeline.tsx:992-994), the browser still synthesizes a click on that element, firing onClick={handleKeyframeClick} (988). handleKeyframeClick (244-254) with shiftKey===false calls selectKeyframe(kfId), and editorStore.selectKeyframe (editorStore.ts:1997) sets selectedKeyframeIds to `new Set([id])`, collapsing any multi-selection down to the single dragged keyframe. There is no didDrag guard, and handleKeyframePointerUp (310-312) nulls dragRef before the click fires, so the click cannot detect that a drag just happened.
- **Fix:** Add a persistent `didDragRef = useRef(false)`. Reset it to false in handleKeyframePointerDown. Set it true in handleKeyframePointerMove whenever a real move is applied (with F019's deferred approach, set it true once pendingDelta becomes nonzero; standalone, set it when deltaFrames!==0). At the very top of handleKeyframeClick add: `if (didDragRef.current) { didDragRef.current = false; e.stopPropagation(); return; }` so the trailing click after a genuine drag is ignored and the multi-selection is preserved. Do NOT clear didDragRef in pointerup — let the click consume it; pointerdown resets it for the next interaction.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Timeline.tsx`
- **Test:** Timeline test: 3 keyframes on a track, shift-select all 3 (selectedKeyframeIds size 3), simulate a drag on one (pointerdown + pointermove with nonzero frame delta + pointerup) then dispatch the trailing click on that keyframe div; assert selectedKeyframeIds.size still === 3. Contrast test: a plain click (pointerdown + pointerup, no move) on a keyframe still selects exactly that one keyframe.
- **Notes:** Soft dependency: F019's deferred-commit rework already introduces the pendingDelta/drag-happened state, so doing F019 first lets F086 reuse the same flag rather than duplicating it. F086 can be implemented independently if F019 is deferred, but both edit the same keyframe drag handlers so they should land together.

#### `F087` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Timeline.tsx:357`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Dragging the work-area body past either timeline edge permanently shrinks the work area instead of preserving its width.

- **Root cause:** For a 'body' work-area drag, handleWorkAreaPointerMove (Timeline.tsx:353-357) computes newStart=initialStart+deltaFrames and newEnd=initialEnd+deltaFrames and calls setWorkAreaRange(newStart, newEnd). setWorkAreaRange (editorStore.ts:1851-1857) clamps start via `Math.max(0, round(start))` and end via `Math.min(duration-1, round(end))` INDEPENDENTLY, so when the body is dragged past an edge one bound saturates while the other keeps moving, compressing the region. With work area [50,100] and duration 300, dragging body -70: start=max(0,-20)=0, end=min(299,30)=30 — the 51-frame region shrinks to 31, made permanent on release; symmetric compression happens against the right edge. setWorkAreaRange is only called from this body-drag path so no other caller relies on the independent clamping.
- **Fix:** Clamp the drag delta before applying so both bounds shift by the same amount and width is preserved. In the body branch of handleWorkAreaPointerMove: `const maxDelta = (duration - 1) - drag.initialEnd; const minDelta = -drag.initialStart; const clamped = Math.max(minDelta, Math.min(maxDelta, deltaFrames)); setWorkAreaRange(drag.initialStart + clamped, drag.initialEnd + clamped);`. This holds (end - start) constant so the region stops at each edge instead of shrinking. (Optionally also make setWorkAreaRange itself width-preserving, but the component-level clamp is sufficient and the store fn has a single caller.)
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Timeline.tsx`
- **Test:** Interaction/unit test: set workAreaStart=50, workAreaEnd=100, timelineDuration=300, simulate a body pointerdown then pointermove with a large negative dx; assert resulting workAreaEnd-workAreaStart still === 50 (region [0,50], not [0,30]). Symmetric test dragging right: assert width preserved and end clamps at duration-1 while start stays width away.
- **Notes:** Lives in the same work-area handlers as F165; natural to fix in the same pass but no ordering dependency.

#### `F088` · medium · shortcut-conflict

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/timeline/GraphEditor.tsx:504`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** GraphEditor's window-level Delete/arrow-key handler fires regardless of focus, so keypresses aimed at the canvas also delete or nudge keyframes.

- **Root cause:** GraphEditor.tsx:503-589 attaches handleKeyDown to window and only gates on state.timelineViewMode==='graph' (lines 511/539), selectedKeyframeIds.size>0 (510/538), and an INPUT/TEXTAREA target check (507/535) — never on whether the graph editor itself is focused. The graphArea div (lines 622-631) has no tabIndex so it is not focusable; keyframe selection persists after the user clicks away. Canvas.tsx binds its own Delete/Backspace handler via element onKeyDown (line 2267) on a focusable <canvas tabIndex=0> (line 2261), deleting the selected node at line 1508. Because keydown bubbles from the canvas to window, both handlers fire on one Delete press — deleting the shape AND the selected keyframes. Likewise ArrowLeft/Right aimed at nudging a canvas shape also retimes selected keyframes.
- **Fix:** Scope the handler to the graph editor. Add tabIndex={0} to the graphArea div (containerRef) and focus it on interaction: call containerRef.current?.focus() in handleMouseDown (and on keyframe selection) so clicking to select keyframes moves focus into the graph area. Then gate the window keydown handler with an early return unless the graph editor owns focus: `if (!containerRef.current || !containerRef.current.contains(document.activeElement)) return;` placed before the Delete and Arrow branches (after the getState() read). This keeps the effect-based fresh-state reads but ensures keypresses routed to the canvas (activeElement === <canvas>, not contained) no longer reach the keyframe delete/nudge logic. Alternatively convert to a React onKeyDown on the focusable graphArea div; the containment gate is the smaller change.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/timeline/GraphEditor.tsx`
- **Test:** GraphEditor.test.tsx: in graph mode with two keyframes selected, set document focus outside the graph area (e.g. focus document.body or a stub focusable element) and dispatch a window keydown {key:'Delete'}; assert the selected keyframes are NOT removed. Then focus the graph area container (data-testid graph-editor-area) and dispatch Delete; assert the keyframes ARE removed. A parallel ArrowRight case asserts times are unchanged when focus is outside.

#### `F089` · medium · ui-consistency

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/timeline/GraphEditorPropertyList.tsx:43`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Curve colors and property-list legend colors diverge whenever node selection filters tracks, because the two components count globalIndex differently.

- **Root cause:** `globalIndex` (which is used purely to pick a distinct curve color via `getTrackColor(index)`) is computed by two independent, divergent counters. In `GraphEditorPropertyList.tsx:40-54` the counter only advances for tracks that survive the filters: the selection filter at line 43 does `continue` WITHOUT `globalIndex++`. In `GraphEditor.tsx:93-120` (`visibleTrackData` useMemo) the same selection filter (lines 100-103) does `globalIndex++` before `continue`, and it additionally advances the counter for visibility-filtered tracks (106-109) and for non-numeric tracks (116) that the property list does not skip/count the same way. Because the two counters increment on different track sets, the color index for a given `nodeId:property` differs between the curve (`GraphEditorCurves.tsx:22` and keyframe dots `GraphEditorKeyframes.tsx:44`) and the legend dot (`GraphEditorPropertyList.tsx:75/82`) whenever any node selection (or visibility toggle) filters tracks. Concretely, with nodes N1(x,y) and N2(rotation) and selectedNodeIds={N2}, the N2 curve renders getTrackColor(2)=#4488ff while its legend dot renders getTrackColor(0)=#ff4444. `getTrackColor` (GraphEditorUtils.ts:55) is a pure `index % TRACK_COLORS.length` lookup, so identical inputs are required for identical colors.
- **Fix:** Make both call sites derive the color index from one shared, selection/visibility-independent source keyed by trackId. 1) Add an exported helper in packages/animation/src/GraphEditorUtils.ts (auto-re-exported by index.ts via `export * from './GraphEditorUtils'`): `export function buildTrackColorIndexMap(tracks: Array<{ nodeId: string; property: string; keyframes: ReadonlyArray<unknown> }>): Map<string, number>` that iterates tracks in timeline order, skips tracks with `keyframes.length === 0`, and assigns a sequential index to `"${nodeId}:${property}"` for every remaining track (independent of selection, visibility, and numeric/non-numeric — the point is a single stable ordering both components agree on). 2) In GraphEditor.tsx `visibleTrackData` useMemo, build the map once from `timeline.tracks`, and replace the manual `globalIndex` counter: remove the `globalIndex++` statements at lines 101-102, 107-108, and 116, and push `{ track, globalIndex: colorIndexMap.get(trackId) ?? 0 }` using the trackId already computed at line 105 (compute trackId before the selection check so it is available on every branch). Keep the numeric-only push and the two filters otherwise unchanged. 3) In GraphEditorPropertyList.tsx, build the same map from `timeline.tracks`, drop the local `let globalIndex`/`globalIndex++` bookkeeping (lines 38, 51-53), and set each entry's `globalIndex` to `colorIndexMap.get("${track.nodeId}:${track.property}") ?? 0`. The dot color at line 75 then uses the same index as the curve. This also makes a property's color stable across selection/visibility changes, which is the desired UX. Do not change `getTrackColor` itself (keeps GraphEditorUtils.test.ts green).
- **Files:** `packages/animation/src/GraphEditorUtils.ts`, `apps/web/src/components/timeline/GraphEditor.tsx`, `apps/web/src/components/timeline/GraphEditorPropertyList.tsx`
- **Test:** Add an integration test in apps/web/src/components/timeline/GraphEditor.test.tsx that reproduces the mismatch: build a timeline with two nodes each having a numeric keyframed track (e.g. node1 'transform.position.x', node2 'transform.position.y' — ordered so an unselected node precedes the selected one), set `selectedNodeIds` to only the second node, render GraphEditor, then read the rendered curve's `stroke` attribute (querySelector inside graph-editor-curves) and the legend dot's inline `background-color` (the propertyDot div inside graph-property-list) and assert they resolve to the same color. Compute the expected hex with the exported `buildTrackColorIndexMap(timeline.tracks)` + `getTrackColor(index)` for the selected track's id; assert the path stroke equals that hex and that the dot's normalized color matches (convert the hex to rgb or compare via a small hex->rgb helper, since inline style backgroundColor normalizes to rgb() in jsdom while the path stroke stays hex). Pre-fix this fails (dot #ff4444 vs curve #4488ff); post-fix both equal getTrackColor of the stable index. Also add a focused unit test in packages/animation/src/GraphEditorUtils.test.ts for buildTrackColorIndexMap: it skips zero-keyframe tracks, assigns sequential 0..n indices in track order, and returns identical maps for identical input.
- **Notes:** Machine-confirmed and independently re-verified against the code — this is a genuine bug, not a mislabel. It is purely cosmetic (no data corruption) but actively misleads which curve maps to which property while editing, so medium is right. Low regression risk: `globalIndex` is used only for color selection (verified in GraphEditorCurves.tsx:22, GraphEditorKeyframes.tsx:44, GraphEditorPropertyList.tsx:75), and grep of GraphEditor.test.tsx shows no existing color/snapshot assertions, only presence checks. The chosen fix (shared trackId->index map) also fixes the secondary visibility-toggle divergence the reviewer noted, since indices become filter-independent. No dependsOn.

#### `F091` · medium · state-desync

**Location:** `apps/web/src/hooks/usePlayback.ts:91`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Store isPlaying is never reset when non-looping playback reaches the end, leaving the UI stuck in 'playing' state and blocking frame-step shortcuts.

- **Root cause:** In PlaybackController.\_tick, when non-looping playback advances past the end (packages/animation/src/PlaybackController.ts:234-241), it does `this._setFrame(effectiveEnd); this.pause(); return;`. pause() sets the controller's internal `_playing=false` but there is NO callback informing the outside world of the self-pause. usePlayback's onFrameChange (apps/web/src/hooks/usePlayback.ts:61-65) only calls setCurrentFrame(frame) — it never touches isPlaying. The store subscription in usePlayback syncs store->controller (pauses the controller when store.isPlaying goes false, lines 91-93) but there is no controller->store sync for the internal end-of-playback pause. Therefore store.isPlaying stays `true` after a non-looping play-to-end. This blocks the four frame-step shortcuts guarded by `!state.isPlaying` in useTimelineShortcuts.ts (`,` line 129, `.` line 137, Shift+`,` line 59, Shift+`.` line 67) and leaves the play button mislabeled. Note the ordering means polling ctrl.isPlaying inside onFrameChange would NOT catch it: onFrameChange fires from \_setFrame BEFORE this.pause() runs, so \_playing is still true at that moment — a dedicated post-pause callback is required.
- **Fix:** Add `onComplete?: () => void;` to PlaybackOptions (PlaybackController.ts:5-12), store it as a private `_onComplete` in the constructor, and invoke `this._onComplete?.();` immediately after the self-pause in the non-looping end branch of \_tick (after `this.pause();`, before `return;` at line ~240). In usePlayback.ts, pass `onComplete: () => useEditorStore.getState().setIsPlaying(false)` in the PlaybackController options object (lines 57-66). Re-entrancy is safe: setIsPlaying(false) triggers the store subscription, but its pause branch (usePlayback.ts:91) only fires when `ctrl.isPlaying` is still true — after the self-pause it is already false, so no double-pause loop.
- **Files:** `packages/animation/src/PlaybackController.ts`, `apps/web/src/hooks/usePlayback.ts`
- **Test:** PlaybackController.test.ts: construct with looping:false and an injected `requestFrame` you can drive manually, call play(), pump the tick callback with increasing timestamps until currentFrame reaches duration-1, then assert isPlaying===false AND the provided onComplete spy was called exactly once. Also add a usePlayback-level test asserting store.isPlaying becomes false when onComplete fires (this requires extending the usePlayback.test.ts mock PlaybackController, whose current play/nextFrame mocks never self-pause, to invoke opts.onComplete when driven to the end).
- **Notes:** Real; reviewer's severity refinement is accurate — the stuck state is recoverable via the transport stop() (usePlayback.ts:133-136 sets isPlaying=false) and Home/End (which don't guard on isPlaying), so it self-heals on the next transport action rather than locking permanently. Alternative implementation: a broader `onPlayStateChange(playing)` fired from play()/pause(); onComplete is preferred here as the minimal, targeted fix since the end-of-playback pause is the only silent self-pause in the controller (dispose only runs on unmount; all other pause()/stop() paths already set store.isPlaying via usePlayback).

#### `F092` · medium · state-leak

**Location:** `apps/web/src/hooks/useProjectActions.ts:117`  
**Verdict:** partly · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** newProject does not reset guides, vitruvianControllers, dynamicChains, globalWind, ikChains, or smartBoneActions, so the old project's rigging state and guides bleed into (and get saved with) the new project.

- **Root cause:** newProject in useProjectActions.ts (setState at lines 117-136) omits guides, globalWind, ikChains, and smartBoneActions, so they carry over from the previous project. The claim is partly wrong on two points I confirmed: (1) vitruvianControllers and dynamicChains ARE reset — clearHistory() at line 137 sets both to [] (editorStore.ts:2889-2890), so they do NOT leak; (2) ikChains and smartBoneActions are NOT in getEditorSnapshot (lines 72-88), so they are never serialized (serializeProject only writes guides, vitruvianControllers, dynamicChains, globalWind, symbols) — they leak at runtime only. guides and globalWind ARE in getEditorSnapshot, so they leak AND get persisted into the saved 'new' project. Stale ikChains are evaluated each frame but no-op safely because evaluateIKChains guards missing nodes (packages/rigging/src/ikEvaluator.ts:23 `if (!targetNode) continue;` and :40 `if (joints.length === 0) continue;`), so there is no crash — this is state hygiene / wrong-persisted-data, not corruption. openProject also leaks ikChains/smartBoneActions because deserializeProject's applyEditorState (projectSerializer.ts:422-436) sets vitruvianControllers/dynamicChains/globalWind/guides but never ikChains/smartBoneActions.
- **Fix:** In useProjectActions.ts newProject setState (lines 117-136) add: guides: [], ikChains: [], smartBoneActions: [], and globalWind reset to the store default { strength:0, direction:0, turbulence:0, frequency:1, enabled:false } (matches editorStore.ts:1457-1463; export a DEFAULT_WIND_SETTINGS const from editorStore to avoid duplicating the literal). Do NOT bother adding vitruvianControllers/dynamicChains here since clearHistory() already resets them. Separately, in projectSerializer.ts deserializeProject, add ikChains: [] and smartBoneActions: [] to the applyEditorState({...}) call (lines 422-436) so openProject/import also clear the previous project's runtime rigging. Leave the reviewer's 'isDirty confirmation before wiping the scene' suggestion out of scope — that is an unsaved-changes UX prompt, not part of the state-leak fix.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/hooks/useProjectActions.ts`, `apps/web/src/services/projectSerializer.ts`, `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts`
- **Test:** In useProjectActions.test.ts newProject block: preset mockEditorState.guides=[{id:'g1',axis:'x',position:10}], mockEditorState.ikChains=[{id:'ik1'}], mockEditorState.smartBoneActions=[{id:'sb1'}], mockEditorState.globalWind={strength:5,enabled:true,...}; call newProject and assert useEditorStore.setState was called with an object containing guides:[], ikChains:[], smartBoneActions:[], and globalWind with enabled:false/strength:0. Add a projectSerializer.test deserializeProject test asserting applyEditorState received ikChains:[] and smartBoneActions:[].
- **Notes:** Independent of the save-path findings. Severity kept medium because guides/globalWind are actually written to the saved new project (real persisted-state bug), even though ikChains/smartBoneActions are runtime-only and no-op safely. Claim was inaccurate that vitruvian/dynamic leak — they do not.

#### `F093` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/hooks/useToolShortcuts.ts:57`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Tool shortcuts do not ignore focused <select> elements, so type-ahead in any native dropdown switches tools and preventDefault blocks the dropdown's own keyboard navigation.

- **Root cause:** useToolShortcuts' focus guard (apps/web/src/hooks/useToolShortcuts.ts:53-59) returns early only for tagName 'input'/'textarea' or contentEditable — it does NOT check 'select'. So when a native <select> is focused and the user presses a tool-shortcut letter (v/r/o/p/t/j/f per TOOL_SHORTCUTS, lines 14-22), the handler falls through to lines 66-69, calling event.preventDefault() and setActiveTool(tool). This both switches the active tool unexpectedly and swallows the key so the native select's type-ahead letter search is blocked. This is inconsistent with the codebase's other global key hooks, which both exclude select: useProjectShortcuts.ts:26 and useTimelineShortcuts.ts:48. Reproducible for any native <select> (PropertiesPanel blend-mode and other native selects, plus any @quar/ui Select rendering a native element).
- **Fix:** In useToolShortcuts.ts, extend the ignore condition at line 57 from `if (tagName === 'input' || tagName === 'textarea' || isEditable)` to also include select: `if (tagName === 'input' || tagName === 'textarea' || tagName === 'select' || isEditable)`. One-line change matching useProjectShortcuts/useTimelineShortcuts.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/hooks/useToolShortcuts.ts`
- **Test:** In useToolShortcuts.test.ts add a case under 'input focus': create a <select>, append+focus it, dispatch a keydown for 'r' with target set to the select element, and assert useEditorStore.getState().activeTool is unchanged ('selection'). Optionally assert event.defaultPrevented is false to confirm type-ahead is no longer blocked.
- **Notes:** Real and accurately described; arrow-key navigation was never affected (arrows aren't tool shortcuts) — the specific regression is the select's type-ahead plus the spurious tool switch. Trivial, low-risk, consistent with sibling hooks.

#### `F094` · medium · data-loss

**Location:** `apps/web/src/pages/Editor.tsx:31`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Dirty-tracking subscribes to nodeAdded/nodeChanged/nodeRemoved but not nodeMoved, so layer drag-reorder never marks the project dirty and is silently lost.

- **Root cause:** The dirty-tracking effect in apps/web/src/pages/Editor.tsx:30-34 subscribes markDirty to nodeAdded, nodeChanged, nodeRemoved but omits nodeMoved. SceneGraph.moveNode emits { type:'nodeMoved' } (packages/core/src/SceneGraph.ts:178-183), and LayerPanel drag-reorder is the only writer that uses moveNode for reparent/reorder (LayerPanel.tsx:813). The reorder path calls pushUndo first (LayerPanel.tsx:807), but pushUndo (editorStore.ts:2807-2823) only mutates undoStack/redoStack/canUndo/canRedo and never sets isDirty. Autosave only fires when isDirty (useProjectActions.ts:444) and there is no beforeunload guard, so a layer drag-reorder that is the sole change since the last save is silently lost. moveNode always emits nodeMoved even for same-parent reordering (no early-out for same parent), so the event does fire.
- **Fix:** Add sceneGraph.on('nodeMoved', markDirty) to the unsubs array in Editor.tsx (lines 30-34), alongside the existing nodeAdded/nodeChanged/nodeRemoved subscriptions. One-line change; the returned unsubscribe is already handled by unsubs.forEach in the cleanup.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/pages/Editor.tsx`
- **Test:** In Editor.test.tsx: render the Editor, obtain the SceneGraph via the provided context (or add two nodes and call sceneGraph.moveNode to reorder). Set useEditorStore.setState({ isDirty:false }), then trigger sceneGraph.moveNode(childId, null, 0) (a root reorder), and assert useEditorStore.getState().isDirty === true. The test fails before the fix because nodeMoved has no subscriber.

#### `F095` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/pages/Projects.tsx:127`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Project rename on the landing page silently fails for every project saved by the editor, because it JSON.parses binary ArrayBuffer data.

- **Root cause:** handleRenameCommit (apps/web/src/pages/Projects.tsx:124-134) does const data = JSON.parse(stored.data) at line 127. stored.data is typed string | ArrayBuffer (projectStorage.ts StoredProject, line 19). Projects saved by the editor are binary: useProjectActions.saveProject/saveProjectAs call serializeProjectToBinary (returns ArrayBuffer, projectSerializer.ts:189-197) and pass it to dbSave (useProjectActions.ts:170,197). JSON.parse on an ArrayBuffer coerces it to the string '[object ArrayBuffer]', which is invalid JSON and throws SyntaxError, caught by the empty catch at lines 132-134 ('Silently fail rename'). So double-click rename closes the input but never persists for any binary (editor-saved) project. Imported-from-landing projects happen to be JSON strings (handleImport JSON.stringify at line 164), so rename appears to work only for those, masking the bug.
- **Fix:** Replace the JSON round-trip with the format-agnostic helpers already used by the serializer. Import { parseQuarFile, writeQuarFile } from '@quar/core' (root index re-exports them via export \* from './format'). In handleRenameCommit: const stored = await dbLoad(renamingId); if (stored) { const parsed = parseQuarFile(stored.data); parsed.name = newName; const binary = writeQuarFile(parsed); await dbSave(renamingId, newName, binary); setProjects(prev => prev.map(...)); }. parseQuarFile handles both ArrayBuffer (binary v3) and legacy JSON string; updating parsed.name keeps the payload name in sync so a later openProject (which reads data.name) shows the new name, and dbSave's separate name field is what listProjects renders. Consider surfacing failures (toast.error) instead of a fully silent catch, but that is optional polish. Note: do NOT take the shortcut of re-saving stored.data unchanged with just a new record name — that leaves the payload's internal name stale and openProject would revert the rename on next save.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/pages/Projects.tsx`
- **Test:** In Projects.test.tsx: extend the projectStorage mock to include loadProject (currently absent). Mock loadProject to resolve { id:'proj_1', name:'Old', updatedAt, data: writeQuarFile({ version:'3.0', name:'Old', pages:[...], activePageId, settings:{...}, ... }) } (a real binary ArrayBuffer). Spy on saveProject. Render, double-click cardName to enter rename, change input to 'New', blur/Enter to commit, then await and assert saveProject was called with ('proj_1','New', <ArrayBuffer>) AND parseQuarFile(that buffer).name === 'New'. A regression test that fails today because JSON.parse throws on the ArrayBuffer.

### Web — canvas & render loop

#### `F005` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/canvas/BoneOverlay.tsx:74`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Bone, IK-target, and chain-line markers freeze at stale screen positions during camera pan/zoom because none of the three useMemos are invalidated on camera change.

- **Root cause:** In apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx the Camera is created once and stored via `cameraRef.current = camera` (line 484); it is mutated in place on pan/zoom and fires a 'change' event that only bumps a `cameraVersion` state (line 505). BoneOverlay.tsx computes `markers` (line 40), `ikMarkers` (line 77), and `chainLines` (line 94) inside three useMemos whose dependency arrays contain `camera` (lines 74, 91, 121) — but `camera` is the SAME object reference across every pan/zoom, so the memos never re-run on camera change. Canvas re-renders on cameraVersion, BoneOverlay re-renders, but returns the stale memoized screen positions. Unlike ArtboardOverlay (which takes `cameraVersion` and lists it in its useMemo deps, ArtboardOverlay.tsx:60) and GuideOverlay/CanvasRuler, BoneOverlay is not passed cameraVersion at all (Canvas.tsx:2331-2340). Impact is purely visual — the overlay is pointerEvents:'none' so hit-testing is unaffected; markers freeze at stale pixels during pan/zoom and self-correct on the next sceneGraphVersion/selection/ikChains identity change.
- **Fix:** Add `cameraVersion: number` to BoneOverlayProps in BoneOverlay.tsx, destructure it in the component signature, and append `cameraVersion` to all three useMemo dependency arrays (the `markers` memo at line 74, the `ikMarkers` memo at line 91, and the `chainLines` memo at line 121). In Canvas.tsx pass `cameraVersion={cameraVersion}` to the <BoneOverlay> element (around line 2331-2340), mirroring how ArtboardOverlay/GuideOverlay/CanvasRuler already receive it a few lines above/below.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/canvas/BoneOverlay.tsx`, `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx`
- **Test:** In apps/web/src/components/canvas/BoneOverlay.test.tsx add a test that uses a mutable mock camera whose worldToScreen adds a mutable pan offset (e.g. `worldToScreen = (p)=>({x:p.x+panRef.x, y:-p.y})`). Render BoneOverlay with cameraVersion=0 and read the joint circle's cx. Mutate panRef.x, then rerender with the SAME camera object but cameraVersion=1. Assert the joint circle cx changed by the pan delta — proving the memo re-ran on cameraVersion bump rather than returning stale coordinates.
- **Notes:** Reviewer labeled high; downgraded to medium because impact is strictly visual (overlay is pointerEvents:'none', self-corrects). Fix is mechanical and mirrors three sibling overlays already in the file tree.

#### `F065` · medium · data-loss

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/canvas/GradientHandleOverlay.tsx:153`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Dragging gradient handles mutates the node via sceneGraph.updateNode without ever calling pushUndo, so a gradient drag creates no undo entry and Ctrl+Z afterwards jumps back past the previous operation as well.

- **Root cause:** In GradientHandleOverlay.tsx handlePointerDown (line 79) begins a handle drag and its onPointerMove closure repeatedly calls `sceneGraph.updateNode(...)` (lines 153/157) followed by `useEditorStore.getState().markDirty()` (line 159). It never calls `pushUndo`. markDirty (editorStore.ts:558) only does `set({ isDirty: true })` — it does NOT snapshot state and, critically, does NOT clear redoStack. pushUndo (editorStore.ts:2807) is what both snapshots the pre-edit scene AND resets `redoStack: []` (line 2819). Consequences: (1) a gradient drag produces no undo entry, so Ctrl+Z after a gradient edit reverts the PRIOR operation and collapses two logical edits into one undo step; (2) genuine data loss via the redo path — because redoStack is never cleared: [move shape -> Ctrl+Z (redo now holds post-move snapshot) -> drag gradient handle -> Ctrl+Y] hits redo() (editorStore.ts:2852) which sees redoStack.length>0, pops the stale post-move snapshot and calls sceneGraph.fromJSON overwriting the whole scene, destroying the gradient edit with no recovery path.
- **Fix:** In handlePointerDown (GradientHandleOverlay.tsx line 79), immediately after the `if (!camera) return;` guard and before `draggingRef.current = handle;`, call `useEditorStore.getState().pushUndo(sceneGraph);` exactly once per drag. Because handlePointerDown fires once at drag start, this creates a single undo entry for the whole drag and clears redoStack (closing the data-loss path). Do NOT put pushUndo inside onPointerMove (that would push a snapshot per mouse move). Keep the existing markDirty() calls in onPointerMove.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/canvas/GradientHandleOverlay.tsx`
- **Test:** Add apps/web/src/components/canvas/GradientHandleOverlay.test.tsx: build a real SceneGraph with a rect node carrying a linear-gradient fill, seed the editor store's undoStack length and put a snapshot in redoStack, render the overlay, fire pointerDown on the [data-testid="gradient-handle-start"] circle, then assert (a) useEditorStore.getState().undoStack length increased by exactly 1, and (b) useEditorStore.getState().redoStack is now empty — proving redo can no longer clobber the gradient edit.
- **Notes:** Core finding and the data-loss redo path both confirmed against editorStore.ts pushUndo/redo/markDirty.

#### `F066` · medium · memory-leak

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/canvas/GradientHandleOverlay.tsx:168`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** F065  
**Finding:** Document pointermove/pointerup listeners registered on handle drag are not cleaned up on unmount, so pressing Escape mid-drag dismisses the overlay while the invisible drag keeps mutating the gradient until the next pointerup.

- **Root cause:** handlePointerDown in GradientHandleOverlay.tsx registers document 'pointermove'/'pointerup' listeners (lines 168-169) that are removed ONLY by the onPointerUp closure (lines 162-166). The component's Escape handler (useEffect lines 176-184) calls `useEditorStore.getState().clearEditingGradient()`, which sets editingGradient=null; Canvas.tsx renders the overlay conditionally on editingGradient (line 2296), so Escape unmounts the overlay. There is no unmount cleanup for the document listeners, and the Escape handler never resets draggingRef. So pressing Escape mid-drag (button still down) unmounts the SVG but leaves the onPointerMove closure alive and driven by the still-attached listener; draggingRef.current is still set, so every subsequent mouse move keeps calling sceneGraph.updateNode/markDirty on the now-uneditable node until the next document pointerup fires onPointerUp. GuideOverlay (guideCleanupRef, lines 68-73 + assignment at 173) and CanvasRuler (cleanupRef, assignment at 189) implement exactly the unmount-cleanup pattern this file omits.
- **Fix:** Add `const dragCleanupRef = useRef<(()=>void)|null>(null);` to the component. Inside handlePointerDown, after defining onPointerMove/onPointerUp and calling document.addEventListener for both, assign `dragCleanupRef.current = () => { document.removeEventListener('pointermove', onPointerMove); document.removeEventListener('pointerup', onPointerUp); draggingRef.current = null; dragCleanupRef.current = null; };`. In onPointerUp, replace the manual removeEventListener pair with a call to `dragCleanupRef.current?.()`. Add an unmount effect `useEffect(() => () => dragCleanupRef.current?.(), []);` and also invoke `dragCleanupRef.current?.()` inside the Escape keydown handler before clearEditingGradient(). This mirrors GuideOverlay's guideCleanupRef and guarantees listeners + draggingRef are torn down on unmount/Escape.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/canvas/GradientHandleOverlay.tsx`
- **Test:** In apps/web/src/components/canvas/GradientHandleOverlay.test.tsx: render the overlay with a spy on sceneGraph.updateNode, fire pointerDown on a handle, unmount the component (via rtl unmount), record updateNode call count, then dispatch a document `new PointerEvent('pointermove', {clientX, clientY})`. Assert updateNode call count did NOT increase after unmount (orphaned listener removed).
- **Notes:** Independent bug but edits the same handlePointerDown as F065; sequence after F065 to avoid conflicting edits to that function. Category 'memory-leak' is loose (it is an orphaned-listener/continued-mutation bug) but the finding is real.

#### `F067` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/canvas/GuideOverlay.tsx:195`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Guide deselection via `handleSvgPointerDown` is unreachable: the SVG root has `pointerEvents: 'none'` so empty-area clicks pass through, and guide-line clicks call stopPropagation, so a selected guide can never be deselected by clicking.

- **Root cause:** GuideOverlay.tsx: the root `<svg>` sets `pointerEvents: 'none'` (line 191), so it is never itself a pointer hit-target and empty-area clicks pass through to the `<canvas>` beneath. The only descendants that receive events are the transparent hit `<line>`s with `pointerEvents: 'stroke'` (lines 215, 242), and their handler `handleGuidePointerDown` calls `e.stopPropagation()` as its first statement (line 135), stopping synthetic bubbling to the svg. Therefore `onPointerDown={handleSvgPointerDown}` (line 195) can fire from neither a direct hit nor a bubbled child event, making `setSelectedGuideId(null)` at line 180 dead code. Confirmed consequence: after clicking a guide once, `selectedGuideId` stays set (visible 2px stroke) with no way to clear it, which keeps the F006 window Delete listener armed forever.
- **Fix:** Replace the unreachable svg-level deselect with a window-level pointerdown listener that fires for any click that is NOT on a guide. Add a `useRef<SVGSVGElement>(null)` (e.g. `svgRef`) and attach it to the root `<svg>`. In an effect gated on `selectedGuideId` (similar structure to the existing keydown effect at 119-130), add `window.addEventListener('pointerdown', onDown)` where `onDown = (e) => { const t = e.target as Node | null; if (svgRef.current && t && svgRef.current.contains(t)) return; setSelectedGuideId(null); }`, with matching removeEventListener cleanup. Because the guide hit-lines live inside the svg, clicking a guide keeps `contains(target)===true` and does not deselect; clicking the canvas, a panel, or anywhere else clears the selection. Do NOT rely on synthetic stopPropagation to reach window (React 17+ delegation semantics make that unreliable) — the `contains` check is the robust discriminator. Remove the now-unused `handleSvgPointerDown` and its `onPointerDown` wiring, or leave the handler but note it is redundant. This also disarms F006's Delete listener in normal flows.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/canvas/GuideOverlay.tsx`, `apps/web/src/components/canvas/GuideOverlay.test.tsx`
- **Test:** In GuideOverlay.test.tsx: render with one x-guide; select it via `fireEvent.pointerDown` on its hit `<line>` and assert the visible line renders with strokeWidth 2 (selected). Then dispatch `fireEvent.pointerDown(document.body)` (a non-guide target) and assert the visible line reverts to strokeWidth 1 (deselected). Optionally follow with a `keyDown(window,{key:'Delete'})` and assert `onRemoveGuide` is NOT called, proving the selection (and the armed Delete listener) was cleared.
- **Notes:** Medium risk because a mis-scoped target check could deselect on legitimate guide clicks; the svgRef.contains(target) guard prevents that. This is the fundamental fix that also unblocks F006 Scenario A.

#### `F068` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/canvas/TextEditOverlay.tsx:37`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** The text-edit textarea is positioned from the node's local transform.position instead of its world transform, so editing a text node inside a moved group or artboard places the textarea at the wrong screen location.

- **Root cause:** TextEditOverlay.tsx computes worldTopLeft at lines 36-39 using only `node.transform.position` and `node.transform.scale` — the node's LOCAL transform. It never calls sceneGraph.getWorldTransform(node.id), so a text node nested under a translated/rotated/scaled parent (group or artboard) is anchored at the wrong screen point; rotation is ignored entirely (only axis-aligned scale is applied). SelectionTool lets you double-click into a group and then into a child text node (SelectionTool.ts entering-group flow), and groups start identity but acquire a translation once dragged. Repro: group a text node + shape, drag the group 300px right, double-click into the group, double-click the text -> the textarea appears 300px left of the rendered glyphs. The overlay is not even passed sceneGraph (Canvas.tsx:2400-2402 passes only node+camera+callbacks), unlike DirectSelectionOverlay/BoneOverlay which use getWorldTransform.
- **Fix:** Add `sceneGraph: SceneGraph` to TextEditOverlayProps and import type { SceneGraph } from '@quar/core'. Replace the worldTopLeft computation (lines 36-39) with a world-matrix transform of the local top-left corner: `const wt = sceneGraph.getWorldTransform(node.id); const worldTopLeft = mat3.transformPoint(wt, { x: bounds.x, y: bounds.y + bounds.height });` (mat3.transformPoint exists at packages/core/src/math.ts:192 and correctly applies a,b,c,d,tx,ty). Keep `const screenPos = camera.worldToScreen(worldTopLeft);`. In Canvas.tsx pass `sceneGraph={sceneGraph}` to <TextEditOverlay> (around line 2400; sceneGraph is already in scope there).
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/canvas/TextEditOverlay.tsx`, `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx`
- **Test:** Add apps/web/src/components/canvas/TextEditOverlay.test.tsx: build a SceneGraph with a group at translation (300,0) containing a text child at local position (0,0); render TextEditOverlay with an identity-ish mock camera (worldToScreen = p=>({x:p.x,y:-p.y})). Assert the rendered wrapper div's computed `left` reflects the child's WORLD x (~300 plus bounds.x offset), not its local x (~0). A companion assertion with an identity/no-parent transform confirms no regression for un-nested text.
- **Notes:** Position fix is the primary bug. Caveat to flag during implementation: the div still applies `transform: scale(node.transform.scale...)` (line 111) and the textarea font sizing uses camera.zoom only, so a scaled parent group won't scale the textarea size — position is fixed but size fidelity under scaled parents remains approximate. Out of scope for this finding unless expanded.

#### `F069` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/canvas/WeightPaintOverlay.tsx:22`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** The weight-paint brush circle reads `weightPaintBrushSize` from the editor store, which is never synced with the WeightPaintTool's actual brush radius, so after pressing [ or ] the displayed circle no longer matches the painted area.

- **Root cause:** WeightPaintOverlay.tsx reads the brush radius from the editor store: `const brushSize = useEditorStore((s) => s.weightPaintBrushSize)` (line 22) and draws the cursor circle at `brushSize * camera.zoom` (line 47). But the actual paint radius lives on the tool: WeightPaintTool.brushRadius (packages/core/src/tools/WeightPaintTool.ts:36, default 30), adjusted by '['/']' via setBrushRadius clamped 5-200 (lines 197-200) and used for painting in world units (line 264). The store's weightPaintBrushSize (editorStore.ts:929, default 30) has a setter setWeightPaintBrushSize (line 930) with ZERO call sites in the app (grep confirms only the interface decl at 248 and the impl at 930). So the store value is permanently 30 while the tool paints at up to 200 — the visual circle no longer matches the painted area after pressing '['/']'. PointMagnetOverlay demonstrates the correct pattern: it takes a toolManager prop and reads `pmTool.getBrushRadius()` on mousemove (PointMagnetOverlay.tsx:44-49). WeightPaintOverlay is not even passed toolManager (Canvas.tsx:2343-2347).
- **Fix:** Mirror PointMagnetOverlay: add `toolManager: ToolManager | null` to WeightPaintOverlayProps (import type { ToolManager, WeightPaintTool } from '@quar/core'); add local state `const [brushRadius, setBrushRadius] = useState(30);` and inside the existing mousemove effect, after updating mousePos, do `if (toolManager) { const wp = toolManager.getTool<WeightPaintTool>('weight-paint'); if (wp) setBrushRadius(wp.getBrushRadius()); }`; add `toolManager` to that effect's dep array. Compute `const screenRadius = brushRadius * camera.zoom;` from the tool-sourced radius and drop the store `weightPaintBrushSize` read (line 22). In Canvas.tsx pass `toolManager={_toolManagerRef.current}` to <WeightPaintOverlay> (around line 2343), exactly as it already does for <PointMagnetOverlay> two blocks below (line 2354). WeightPaintTool is registered under 'weight-paint' (ToolManager.ts:88) and getBrushRadius exists (WeightPaintTool.ts:65).
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/canvas/WeightPaintOverlay.tsx`, `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx`
- **Test:** Add apps/web/src/components/canvas/WeightPaintOverlay.test.tsx: set activeTool='weight-paint' in the store, pass a mock toolManager whose getTool('weight-paint') returns an object with getBrushRadius()=>100 and camera zoom=1, dispatch a window 'mousemove', and assert the rendered <circle r> equals 100 (not the store default 30) — proving the overlay tracks the tool's actual radius.
- **Notes:** Alternative fix (have WeightPaintTool push radius changes into the store on '['/']') was considered but rejected: the tool lives in @quar/core and must not depend on the web store; the read-from-tool pattern is already established by PointMagnetOverlay. Consider deleting the now-dead weightPaintBrushSize/setWeightPaintBrushSize store fields as cleanup, but that is optional and can stay to avoid churn.

#### `F075` · medium · stale-state

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx:354`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** boneNodes/ikTargetNodes/artboardNodes memos keyed only on sceneGraphVersion go stale after undo/redo, page switches, and symbol-edit transitions because SceneGraph.fromJSON emits no events.

- **Root cause:** boneNodes (Canvas.tsx:335-354), ikTargetNodes (356-366) and artboardNodes (369-379) are useMemo'd with dependency `[sceneGraphVersion]` only. sceneGraphVersion is bumped exclusively by incrementVersion, wired to nodeChanged/nodeAdded/nodeRemoved (Canvas.tsx:189, 200-202). SceneGraph.fromJSON (SceneGraph.ts:419-459) atomically swaps this.nodes/rootNodeIds with NO emit call. Every scene-replacing store transition uses fromJSON without a compensating version bump: undo (editorStore.ts:2839), redo (2866), switchPage (3088), addPage-path (2952), page delete (2986), enterSymbolEdit (3446), exitSymbolEdit (3468). Canvas is rendered with no key (Editor.tsx:96) so it is not remounted. Result: after any of these transitions the three memos keep node references from the previous scene and are handed to BoneOverlay/ArtboardOverlay. Reviewer's non-crash note is correct: getWorldTransform returns identity for missing ids, so stale overlays render at wrong/zero transforms rather than throwing.
- **Fix:** Add a scene-reset event so all fromJSON callers are covered centrally. In SceneGraph.ts: add a new SceneGraphEventType (e.g. 'sceneReset' or 'loaded') to the union (line 13-18) and emit it at the end of fromJSON (after the atomic swap, line 458) via this.emit({ type:'sceneReset' }). In Canvas.tsx effect (185-209), add `const unsubReset = sceneGraph.on('sceneReset', incrementVersion);` and return its unsubscribe in cleanup. This bumps sceneGraphVersion on every fromJSON, invalidating the three memos plus selectionDisplay. Because all cited transitions route through fromJSON, this single hook covers undo/redo/page-switch/symbol-edit without touching each store action.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/SceneGraph.ts`, `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx`
- **Test:** SceneGraph.test.ts: register a listener on 'sceneReset' (or the chosen name), call fromJSON({nodes,rootNodeIds}) -> assert the listener fired once. Canvas-level: mount Canvas, load a scene with a bone, replace via fromJSON with a scene containing a different bone id, and assert the BoneOverlay-fed boneNodes memo reflects the new bone (recomputed) rather than the stale one.

#### `F076` · medium · performance

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx:553`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Onion skinning re-evaluates the entire timeline and allocates fresh Sets/Maps/arrays for every ghost frame on every RAF frame, even when the playhead and scene are unchanged.

- **Root cause:** In the RAF loop's onion-skin block (Canvas.tsx:538-572), getNodesAtFrame (549-563) calls getAnimatedNodes(tl) — which allocates a fresh Set every call (Timeline.ts:331-339) — plus builds a new overrides Map and runs evaluateNodeAtFrame + applyAnimatedValues per animated node. OnionSkinRenderer.render invokes this callback once per ghost frame, and ShapeRenderer re-earcuts each ghost shape, all on every RAF tick whenever onionSkin.enabled, keyed only on the enabled flag with no cache against currentFrame/timeline. Correctly scoped as opt-in (onionSkin.enabled default false) and performance-only; the base per-tick grid+scene render is separate architectural behavior, not this bug.
- **Fix:** Hoist and memoize the ghost evaluation. Hoist `getAnimatedNodes(tl)` out of the per-ghost-frame callback so it runs at most once per render. Add a ref-based cache (e.g. ghostCacheRef holding { key, framesToNodes }) keyed on a signature of (currentFrame, a timeline revision/serialization stamp, and the onionSkin settings that affect which frames render — before/after counts). Compute the per-ghost-frame node arrays once and reuse across RAF ticks while the signature is unchanged; only recompute when currentFrame/timeline/settings change. Since timeline has no revision counter, either add one bumped by keyframe mutations in editorStore or derive a cheap stamp; simplest is to invalidate whenever currentFrame or the onion settings change (playhead-idle is the common idle case).
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx`
- **Test:** Unit-test the extracted ghost-evaluation cache helper: calling it twice with identical (currentFrame, timeline, settings) returns the same cached result and does not re-invoke evaluateNodeAtFrame (spy) the second time; changing currentFrame invalidates and recomputes.

#### `F077` · medium · performance

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx:1007`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** setMouseWorldPos stores a fresh object on every mousemove with no equality bail-out, re-rendering the entire Canvas subtree at pointer-event rate while merely hovering.

- **Root cause:** handleMouseMove (Canvas.tsx:997-1032) calls setMouseWorldPos({ x: round(worldPos.x\*10)/10, y: round(...)/10 }) on every mousemove (1007-1010) with a freshly allocated object and no equality bail-out. mouseWorldPos is consumed only by the status-bar readout at line 2432 (`X: {mouseWorldPos.x.toFixed(1)} Y: {mouseWorldPos.y.toFixed(1)}`). Each setState triggers a full re-evaluation of the Canvas JSX and re-render/reconciliation of every mounted unmounted-memo overlay child at pointer-event rate, even while merely hovering. Reviewer's refinement is correct: the ~15 useMemo values (301-458) do NOT recompute because mouseWorldPos is in none of their dep arrays — only their reference-equality dep checks run — so the wasted cost is the JSX re-eval plus unmemoized child re-renders, purely for a coordinate label.
- **Fix:** Bail out when the rounded coordinate is unchanged. Extract a pure helper `nextMousePos(prev, worldPos)` that computes rounded rx/ry and returns `prev` unchanged (same reference) when rx===prev.x && ry===prev.y, else a new {x:rx,y:ry}. Call `setMouseWorldPos(prev => nextMousePos(prev, positions.worldPos))` — returning the same reference makes React bail out of the re-render. (Alternative, if further isolation is wanted: move the readout into a tiny sibling component with its own useState subscribed from a shared ref, so the rest of the tree never re-renders; not required for the fix.)
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx`
- **Test:** Unit test the extracted nextMousePos helper: given prev={x:1.2,y:3.4}, a worldPos rounding to the same 1.2/3.4 returns the SAME object reference (===prev); a worldPos rounding to different values returns a new object with the new rounded coords.

#### `F078` · medium · data-loss

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx:1114`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Date.now()-seeded node ID counters collide across rapid SVG pastes/drops, making the second import throw and be silently swallowed after already pushing an undo snapshot.

- **Root cause:** importSvgString (Canvas.tsx:1109-1139) seeds its node-id counter with `let idCounter = Date.now()` (1114) and generates `node_${idCounter++}` (1115). Two SVG pastes within the same (or nearly the same) millisecond produce overlapping id ranges: e.g. paste 1 at T consumes node*T..node*{T+k}; paste 2 seeded at T (or T+1) regenerates ids already present, so the first sg.addNode inside importSvg throws 'Node with id already exists' (SceneGraph.addNode:73-75). The throw is swallowed by the empty `catch {}` (1134-1136), but pushUndo(sg) was already called at 1117 — committing an extra undo snapshot for a paste that silently failed. Reviewer's clarification is correct: this is silent-failure of the user's second paste plus undo-stack pollution, not destruction of the first import's data (the first import is preserved). Contrast the image-paste path (1152) which already uses Date.now()+random suffix and does not collide.
- **Fix:** Make id generation collision-proof and surface errors. In importSvgString, replace `let idCounter = Date.now(); const generateId = () => `node*${idCounter++}``with a per-node unique generator, e.g.`const generateId = () => `node*${Date.now()}_${Math.random().toString(36).slice(2,8)}\_${idCounter++}``or`crypto.randomUUID()`-based, matching the image path pattern at line 1152. Additionally, replace the empty catch with one that surfaces failure to the user (toast.error) so a failed import is not silent; consider moving pushUndo to only commit after at least one node is successfully added, or wrapping so a fully-failed import does not leave an extra undo snapshot.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx`
- **Test:** Canvas/import test: mock Date.now to return a constant value, call importSvgString twice in a row with valid multi-node SVG -> assert both imports add distinct, non-colliding node ids and both selections succeed (no swallowed throw), and that no extra/duplicate undo snapshot is pushed for a paste that would previously have failed.
- **Notes:** Category is more precisely silent-failure + undo-stack pollution than pre-existing data-loss; the first import survives, only the second paste is lost.

#### `F090` · medium · type-safety

**Location:** `apps/web/src/hooks/useCanvasTools.ts:733`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** deleteDirectSelectionPoints is returned from useCanvasTools and destructured in Canvas.tsx but is missing from the UseCanvasToolsReturn interface, producing TypeScript strict-mode errors that break `pnpm typecheck`.

- **Root cause:** useCanvasTools is annotated with explicit return type `: UseCanvasToolsReturn` (useCanvasTools.ts:126) and returns a fresh object literal (lines 715-735) that includes `deleteDirectSelectionPoints` (defined at line 705), but the UseCanvasToolsReturn interface (lines 44-86) ends at `marqueeRect` and never declares `deleteDirectSelectionPoints`. TypeScript applies excess-property checking to fresh object literals in return position against the declared return type, so line 733 yields TS2353 ('Object literal may only specify known properties'). Canvas.tsx destructures `deleteDirectSelectionPoints` from the hook result (apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx:175) and uses it at lines 1574 and 1985, yielding TS2339 ('does not exist on type UseCanvasToolsReturn'). Runtime JS is unaffected, but the `pnpm typecheck` gate fails at these two sites.
- **Fix:** Add `/** Delete selected points in DirectSelectionTool (for context menu) */ deleteDirectSelectionPoints: () => void;` to the UseCanvasToolsReturn interface, immediately after the `marqueeRect` member (useCanvasTools.ts:85). No other change needed — the return literal and Canvas destructure already match this signature.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/hooks/useCanvasTools.ts`
- **Test:** In useCanvasTools.test.ts add an assertion that the hook exposes the handler: `expect(typeof result.current.deleteDirectSelectionPoints).toBe('function')`. The primary guarantee is that `pnpm typecheck` passes (TS2353/TS2339 cleared); the runtime assertion guards against accidental removal of the member.
- **Notes:** Real, trivial, purely additive to a type. Verified the interface omits the member and both the return literal and Canvas.tsx:175/1574/1985 reference it.

### Web — editor store

#### `F100` · medium · data-loss

**Location:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts:1641`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** pasteClipboard never sets isDirty, so paste/duplicate as the last edit is skipped by auto-save.

- **Root cause:** pasteClipboard's final `set({ selectedNodeIds: new Set(rootIds) })` (editorStore.ts:1641) omits isDirty. pushUndo (2807-2823) also does not set isDirty. duplicateSelection (1643-1648) delegates to pasteClipboard so it inherits the bug. Auto-save is gated on isDirty (useProjectActions.ts:443-444), so a paste/duplicate as the last action never triggers auto-save and the unsaved-changes indicator stays off.
- **Fix:** Change the final set in pasteClipboard to `set({ selectedNodeIds: new Set(rootIds), isDirty: true })`.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts`
- **Test:** In 'clipboard & node operations': copySelection a node, setState({ isDirty:false }), call pasteClipboard(sg); assert useEditorStore.getState().isDirty === true. (Duplicate covered transitively.)

#### `F101` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts:1660`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** deleteSelection only cleans up IK chains when the ik-target node itself is deleted; deleting a bone that belongs to a chain leaves the stale chain and its orphaned target node in the scene.

- **Root cause:** deleteSelection (editorStore.ts:1656-1672) removes an IKChain only when a deleted node has `type==='ik-target'`. IK target nodes are created as ROOT nodes with parent:null (line 1080/1097), so SceneGraph.removeNode (cascades only children, SceneGraph.ts:99-103) never removes the target when a chain's bone is deleted. Deleting a bone that is a chain's rootBoneId/endEffectorBoneId/intermediate leaves the IKChain in store state and its orphaned ik-target node in the scene (selectable, serialized). dynamicChains are filtered only by rootBoneId (1672), so deleting a non-root member bone leaves a stale chain.
- **Fix:** In deleteSelection, first compute the set of deleted ids (selectedNodeIds plus, ideally, their descendants). For ikChains: for each chain, before removing bones, walk its bone path (parent chain from endEffectorBoneId up to rootBoneId via sceneGraph.getNode) and collect member bone ids; if any member bone id OR the chain's targetNodeId/poleTargetNodeId is in the deleted set, drop the chain AND remove its targetNodeId and poleTargetNodeId from the scene graph (and their keyframe tracks). Gather these membership sets BEFORE the removeNode loop so bone lookups still resolve. For dynamicChains: compute each chain's member bone ids (walk the chain) and filter out any chain with a deleted member, not just rootBoneId.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts`
- **Test:** createIKChain on a single bone; select and deleteSelection the BONE (not the target). Assert ikChains length is 0 AND the IK target node (chain.targetNodeId) no longer resolves via sg.getNode. Add an analogous dynamicChains test: create a dynamic chain and delete a non-root member bone -> chain removed.
- **Notes:** Bone membership must be captured before the removal loop. F026, once landed, will restore these chains/targets on undo.

#### `F102` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts:1934`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** updateKeyframeTimeAndValue can produce two keyframes at the same time on one track, violating the one-keyframe-per-frame invariant maintained everywhere else.

- **Root cause:** updateKeyframeTimeAndValue (editorStore.ts:1920-1941) rewrites the moved keyframe's time to roundedTime and re-sorts, with no collision check. Timeline.addKeyframe/moveKeyframe replace an existing keyframe on time collision (Timeline.ts), but this graph-editor path does not, so two keyframes can end up sharing a time. All other track lookups use `findIndex(kf => kf.time === time)` (e.g. updateKeyframeValue:1911, setKeyframeTangents:1953) and only ever hit the first, making the second an un-editable ghost that corrupts interpolation.
- **Fix:** After computing roundedTime, detect collision: `const collidingIdx = newKeyframes.findIndex((kf, i) => i !== kfIndex && kf.time === roundedTime)`. Apply replace semantics: set newKeyframes[kfIndex] to the new {time,value}, and if collidingIdx >= 0 remove that entry from newKeyframes before sorting. (Alternative: clamp roundedTime to the nearest free integer frame.) Keep the existing sort.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts`
- **Test:** Seed a track with keyframes at times 10 and 20. Call updateKeyframeTimeAndValue(nodeId, prop, 20, 10, newVal). Assert the track has exactly one keyframe at time 10 and its value === newVal (the frame-10 keyframe was replaced).

#### `F103` · medium · state-coherence

**Location:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts:2879`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** clearHistory resets vitruvianControllers and dynamicChains but not ikChains and smartBoneActions, so rigging state leaks across projects.

- **Root cause:** clearHistory (editorStore.ts:2879-2892) resets vitruvianControllers and dynamicChains but not ikChains or smartBoneActions, so those rigging arrays persist across a project switch within the same live session (a full reload re-runs the store literal and clears them).
- **Fix:** Add `ikChains: []` and `smartBoneActions: []` to the set() in clearHistory, matching the existing vitruvianControllers/dynamicChains reset.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts`
- **Test:** Extend the clearHistory tests: setState({ ikChains:[<one>], smartBoneActions:[<one>] }), call clearHistory(), assert both arrays are empty.
- **Notes:** Separate latent issue (not in scope here): ikChains and smartBoneActions are never serialized to .quar, so they are also not persisted across save/load.

#### `F104` · medium · state-coherence

**Location:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts:3093`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** switchPage/addPage/deletePage swap the timeline object but never sync the separate timelineDuration/frameRate store scalars, desynchronizing ruler, playback, and export from the page's actual timeline.

- **Root cause:** setTimelineDuration (editorStore.ts:1800-1821) and setFrameRate (1822-1828) keep the timelineDuration/frameRate scalars in sync with timeline.duration/frameRate, so per-page timelines can hold different values. switchPage (3093), addPage (2957) and deletePage (2991) load the page's timeline object but never update the timelineDuration/frameRate scalars (nor workAreaEnd, which is derived from duration). After changing a per-page duration and switching pages, the ruler (Timeline.tsx), PlaybackController and setCurrentFrame clamping (which all read the scalar) desync from the actual loaded timeline; ExportDialog is partially desynced (endFrame from stale timelineDuration, frameRate from the fresh timeline object).
- **Fix:** In addPage, switchPage and deletePage, in the set() that loads the target/new page timeline, also set `timelineDuration: <loadedTimeline>.duration`, `frameRate: <loadedTimeline>.frameRate`, and `workAreaEnd: <loadedTimeline>.duration - 1` (clamp workAreaStart to < workAreaEnd). Use the same cloned timeline object being assigned (newPage.timeline / targetPage.timeline / switchTo.timeline).
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts`
- **Test:** Default page duration 300; call setTimelineDuration(120) on page 1; addPage (page 2 default 300) and assert timelineDuration===300; switchPage back to page 1 and assert timelineDuration===120 and frameRate matches page1 timeline.frameRate.
- **Notes:** Coordinate with F026: when undo/redo restores a timeline it should also refresh these scalars, so factor the timeline->scalar sync into a small helper reused by both.

### Web — services & persistence

#### `F096` · medium · resource-leak

**Location:** `apps/web/src/services/exportService.ts:138`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** F097  
**Finding:** Every PNG export creates a new WebGL2 context that is never explicitly released, so repeated exports exhaust the browser's WebGL context limit and force-evict the main editor canvas context.

- **Root cause:** exportService.exportSelectionAsPng constructs a fresh WebGLRenderer per export (lines 138-142), and WebGLRenderer.dispose() (packages/core/src/rendering/WebGLRenderer.ts:410-428) only deletes cached programs/buffers and removes event listeners — it never releases the underlying WebGL2 context (no WEBGL_lose_context.loseContext()). Browsers cap simultaneously-live WebGL contexts (~16); because dispose leaves the context alive until GC, repeated PNG exports accumulate contexts and, on hitting the cap, the browser force-evicts the oldest live context — which can be the main editor canvas created in Canvas.tsx. Second leak: dispose is only reached on the success path (lines 195-196); a throw from preloadTextures (176), render (181), or canvasToBlob (189) skips dispose entirely, immediately leaking that export's context/programs/buffers. The reviewer's coupling correction is accurate — canvasToBlob runs after fills are restored (189 vs 184-186) and preloadTextures swallows img.onerror by resolving (ShapeRenderer.ts:1072), so blob/preload failures don't corrupt fills; that corruption window belongs to F097's render() throw only.
- **Fix:** Two parts. (1) In WebGLRenderer.dispose() add a guarded context release as the last step: `this.gl.getExtension?.('WEBGL_lose_context')?.loseContext();`. The optional chaining is required and safe: the test mock in packages/core/src/test/setup.ts (createMockWebGL2Context) has no getExtension property, so `getExtension?.(...)` short-circuits to undefined and existing dispose tests keep passing; real browser contexts return the extension. This also fixes the identical leak in the two ExportDialog.tsx dispose sites. (2) In exportService move `shapeRenderer.dispose(); renderer.dispose();` (currently lines 195-196) into a finally block wrapping the render/mutation section introduced by F097's restructure, so disposal (and now context loss) always runs even when render/preload/canvasToBlob throws. Alternatively the loseContext call can be made directly in exportService's finally (`renderer.context.getExtension('WEBGL_lose_context')?.loseContext()`), but doing it in dispose() is cleaner and covers all three renderer.dispose callers.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/rendering/WebGLRenderer.ts`, `apps/web/src/services/exportService.ts`
- **Test:** WebGLRenderer.test.ts: extend the shared mock gl (createMockWebGL2Context in test/setup.ts) with getExtension: (name) => name === 'WEBGL_lose_context' ? { loseContext: vi.fn() } : null, then assert renderer.dispose() invokes loseContext exactly once. exportService test (WebGLRenderer/ShapeRenderer mocked): assert that when the mocked render() throws, renderer.dispose() and shapeRenderer.dispose() are still called (proving the finally), and on the success path dispose is called once.
- **Notes:** Shares the exportService try/finally restructure with F097, so land F097 first. Touching WebGLRenderer.dispose affects the main canvas and ExportDialog, but the guarded optional-chaining call is a no-op under the test mock and loseContext on the main canvas only occurs at unmount, so regression risk is contained.

#### `F097` · medium · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/services/exportService.ts:170`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** PNG export mutates the live artboard (fills cleared) across await points with no try/finally, so an exception mid-export permanently strips the artboard background, and the mutation spuriously marks a clean project dirty.

- **Root cause:** In apps/web/src/services/exportService.ts, for an artboard export with includeBackground=false, line 170 mutates the live document via `sceneGraph.updateNode(artboard.id, { fills: [] })`, then awaits preloadTextures (line 176) and calls shapeRenderer.render (line 181) before restoring fills at lines 184-186 — all with no try/finally. If render() throws (context loss, or a tessellation error on malformed path data — the artboard background goes through getCachedTessellation via renderArtboardBackground, ShapeRenderer.ts:1784-1806), savedFills is never restored and the user's artboard background is permanently deleted from the document (a subsequent save persists the loss). Confirmed secondary defect: both updateNode calls emit 'nodeChanged', and Editor.tsx (pages/Editor.tsx lines 28-36) subscribes nodeChanged -> markDirty, so merely exporting a PNG flips a clean project to dirty and can trigger a spurious autosave; the editor canvas can also briefly show the artboard without its background during the awaits. Verified the artboard background render keys off node.fills and early-returns when empty (renderArtboardBackground lines 1787-1788), which is exactly why the current code clears fills.
- **Fix:** Stop mutating the scene graph. Add a suppression parameter to ShapeRenderer.render, e.g. `suppressArtboardBackgroundIds?: Set<string>` (append to the existing signature at packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts:1203-1210), and in each place that calls renderArtboardBackground (lines 1363-1364, 1608-1609, 1662-1663) skip the call when the artboard's id is in that set. In exportService, delete the savedFills mutate/restore blocks (lines 167-171 and 184-186) and instead pass `new Set([artboard.id])` for the new parameter on the render() call at line 181. This removes the corruption window, the spurious markDirty (no nodeChanged fired), and the flicker in one change. Minimum fallback if the cross-package signature change must be deferred: wrap the mutate->preload->render->restore sequence in try/finally so fills are always restored on throw — but note this fallback still fires nodeChanged twice and leaves the spurious-dirty and flicker bugs, so the render-flag approach is preferred.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/services/exportService.ts`, `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts`
- **Test:** ShapeRenderer.test.ts: spy on renderArtboardBackground and assert render() skips it for an artboard whose id is in suppressArtboardBackgroundIds, but still renders it otherwise. exportService test (with WebGLRenderer/ShapeRenderer mocked): assert exportSelectionAsPng for an artboard with includeBackground=false does NOT call sceneGraph.updateNode (no mutation) and passes a Set containing the artboard id to render(); add a regression case where the mocked render() throws and assert artboard.fills is unchanged afterward.
- **Notes:** This is the base change for F096 — both restructure the exportService render/dispose region, so implement F097 first.

#### `F098` · medium · data-corruption

**Location:** `apps/web/src/services/projectSerializer.ts:403`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** F001  
**Finding:** deserializeProject replaces the live scene graph before timeline migration, which can throw on data that passes validateProjectData, leaving a half-imported state that autosave then persists over the old project.

- **Root cause:** deserializeProject (projectSerializer.ts:388-437) mutates the live scene graph at line 403 (sceneGraph.fromJSON) BEFORE running the timeline migration loop (lines 406-408) and BEFORE applyEditorState (line 422). SceneGraph.fromJSON does an atomic swap (SceneGraph.ts:456-457) and emits no events, so it does not itself flag isDirty. validateProjectData/validateSettings (lines 312-325) validate version, pages, activePageId, node shape, and numeric timelineDuration/frameRate but NEVER validate page.timeline. migrateTimeline (lines 352-377) then does `for (const track of result.tracks)` and `track.property.startsWith(...)`; it throws if result.tracks is a truthy non-array (not iterable) or if any track lacks a string `property`. Such a file passes validateProjectData yet throws at line 407 after the scene graph was already replaced, leaving a half-imported state: canvas shows imported nodes while the store still holds the old projectId/pages/timeline/activePageId (applyEditorState never ran). importProject (useProjectActions.ts:245) catches the throw with a generic toast. The reviewer's autosave-overwrite claim is conditional: since fromJSON emits no events, autosave only fires if isDirty was already true from prior edits; the guaranteed symptom is the state inconsistency.
- **Fix:** Make deserializeProject all-or-nothing. (a) Harden migrateTimeline: guard `Array.isArray(result.tracks)` before the loop and `typeof track.property === 'string'` before calling startsWith. (b) Reorder deserializeProject so no live state is touched until all fallible work succeeds: first run the migrateTimeline loop over v2.pages, build the PageData array, and clone activePage.timeline into locals; only after those complete call sceneGraph.fromJSON(activePage.sceneGraph) followed by applyEditorState(...). (c) Defense in depth: extend validateProjectData to reject pages whose timeline is not a non-null object, and if timeline.tracks is present require it to be an array whose entries each have a string `property`. Ship (a)+(b) as primary; (c) optional. SceneGraph.ts needs no change.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/services/projectSerializer.ts`, `apps/web/src/services/projectSerializer.test.ts`
- **Test:** Add a test that builds a v2 ProjectDataV2 whose active page timeline has a malformed track (e.g. { id:'t1', nodeId:'x', keyframes:[] } with no `property`) so it passes validateProjectData. Pre-populate the target SceneGraph with an 'old' node. Before the fix this throws AND the old node is gone / imported node present. After the fix assert that deserializeProject either succeeds or, if it rejects malformed data, leaves the SceneGraph untouched (old node still present, imported node absent) and does not call applyEditorState — proving atomicity.
- **Notes:** Reordering touches the shared load path used by importProject, openProject, and loadOnMount, so exercise all three in review. Autosave-corruption is a plausible follow-on requiring pre-existing isDirty, not a guaranteed symptom — the confirmed defect is the half-imported inconsistency.

#### `F099` · medium · performance

**Location:** `apps/web/src/services/projectStorage.ts:123`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** F025  
**Finding:** listProjects uses getAll() on the projects store, deserializing every project's full binary payload just to build an id/name/updatedAt list.

- **Root cause:** listProjects (apps/web/src/services/projectStorage.ts lines 118-136) calls `tx.objectStore(PROJECTS_STORE).getAll()` which materializes every StoredProject record — including each record's full `data` payload (string | ArrayBuffer, up to ~50MB per project per the upload cap) — into memory, then maps to just {id,name,updatedAt} (lines 125-129) and drops the rest. The projects store is created with keyPath 'id' and no secondary index (lines 47-49), so there is no lighter query. Note the reviewer's suggested openCursor does NOT actually fix it: a value cursor's cursor.value still contains the full record; only openKeyCursor avoids values but then yields no name/updatedAt. Callers: MenuBar File>Open and the Ctrl+O prompt path via useProjectActions.listProjectsAction (line 390-392) -> dbList. So opening the project list with several large projects allocates hundreds of MB transiently.
- **Fix:** Store listing metadata separately from the blob. Add a second object store `project-meta` (keyPath 'id') holding only {id,name,updatedAt}. Bump DB_VERSION 1->2 and in onupgradeneeded (lines 45-53) create the meta store and backfill it by opening a cursor over the existing projects store, writing minimal metadata for each existing record. In saveProject open a multi-store readwrite tx: `db.transaction([PROJECTS_STORE, META_STORE], 'readwrite')`, put the full record into PROJECTS_STORE and {id,name,updatedAt} into META_STORE within the same transaction (so onabort/oncomplete still cover both). In deleteProject delete from both stores in one tx. Change listProjects to getAll() on META_STORE (records are already tiny, keep the existing sort). Keep StoredProject/data untouched for loadProject. Coordinate with F025: saveProject/deleteProject get their onabort handlers there, so land F025 first and reuse the same transaction/handler structure.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/services/projectStorage.ts`
- **Test:** In apps/web/src/services/projectStorage.test.ts: (1) save a project whose data is a large ArrayBuffer and assert listProjects returns its {id,name,updatedAt} without the data field (extends existing test at lines 85-92); (2) spy on the projects objectStore's getAll and assert it is NOT called during listProjects (only the meta store's getAll is); (3) a migration test: pre-populate a v1-shaped DB with projects-only records, then trigger the v2 upgrade (resetDB + reopen) and assert listProjects returns the backfilled metadata for the pre-existing records.
- **Notes:** Real and worth doing, but the reviewer's openCursor suggestion is technically insufficient (value cursors still deserialize data); the separate-metadata-store approach is the correct fix and is why this is M not S — it requires a DB version bump, onupgradeneeded backfill, and dual-store writes.
