### Animation engine

#### `F173` · low · data-loss

**Location:** `packages/animation/src/KeyframeManager.ts:200`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** copyKeyframes discards the source nodeId, so copying keyframes selected across multiple nodes and pasting merges them all onto one node, with same-property collisions silently overwriting each other.

- **Root cause:** packages/animation/src/KeyframeManager.ts copyKeyframes (lines 188-217) pushes entries containing only {property,time,value,easing} — the source nodeId is dropped even though the input {nodeId,property,keyframeId} carries it. pasteKeyframes (lines 222-233) writes every entry into getOrCreateTrack(timeline, nodeId, entry.property) for the single target nodeId. When a multi-node selection is copied (reachable via apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts copySelectedKeyframes line 2049, which builds entries across nodes from the flat selectedKeyframeIds set) and pasted, all entries collapse onto one node; two same-property entries at the same relative time then collide and Timeline.addKeyframe's same-time replace (Timeline.ts:132-134) keeps only the last, silently losing the other node's keyframe.
- **Fix:** Carry nodeId through the clipboard and paste per source node. In KeyframeManager.ts: extend the KeyframeClipboard entries type (lines 20-28) to include `nodeId: string`; in copyKeyframes push `nodeId: track.nodeId` (or kf.nodeId) alongside the existing fields. In pasteKeyframes compute `const sourceNodeIds = new Set(clipboard.entries.map(e => e.nodeId)); const singleSource = sourceNodeIds.size === 1;` and for each entry use `const destNode = singleSource ? nodeId : entry.nodeId;` when calling getOrCreateTrack. This preserves the existing single-node cross-node paste (copy from node1, paste to node2) while multi-node copies restore each keyframe to its own source node so nothing is overwritten. editorStore paste/copy call sites need no change (KeyframeClipboard is defined and consumed within these functions; the added field is additive).
- **Files:** `packages/animation/src/KeyframeManager.ts`
- **Test:** In KeyframeManager.test.ts copyKeyframes/pasteKeyframes describe: add keyframes 'transform.position.x' on node1 at frame 0 (value 100) and node2 at frame 0 (value 800); copyKeyframes([both]); pasteKeyframes(clipboard,'nodeIgnored',20); assert node1's track has a keyframe at 20 with value 100 AND node2's track has a keyframe at 20 with value 800 (both preserved). Keep the existing single-node 'copies and pastes keyframes' test (copy node1 -> paste node2) passing.
- **Notes:** Changes the KeyframeClipboard shape (additive) and paste semantics. Verify no serializer persists KeyframeClipboard (it is an in-memory editor clipboard only; editorStore.ts keyframeClipboard state just passes it through). Independent of F030 (different function/collision path).

#### `F174` · low · race-condition

**Location:** `packages/animation/src/PlaybackController.ts:229`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** If pause() (or dispose()) is called from within the onFrameChange callback, the tick's catch-up loop keeps advancing frames after the pause and \_scheduleFrame() still queues another rAF.

- **Root cause:** packages/animation/src/PlaybackController.ts \_tick (lines 207-253). The catch-up while-loop (lines 229-245) calls \_setFrame (lines 266-270) which invokes \_onFrameChange; if that callback calls pause() (sets \_playing=false, cancels pending rAF) or dispose() (sets \_disposed=true), the loop does NOT re-check \_playing/\_disposed and keeps advancing frames — emitting extra onFrameChange calls past the intended stop (overshoot). After the loop, \_scheduleFrame() (line 252) is called unconditionally, queuing a fresh rAF AFTER pause()/\_cancelPendingFrame already ran, so that stray rAF is not cancelled (it fires once and self-clears via the guard at line 208, but it is still an unwanted scheduled frame).
- **Fix:** Add guards in \_tick. (1) Inside the while loop, immediately after the if/else that calls \_setFrame (line 244), add `if (!this._playing || this._disposed) return;` so a pause/dispose triggered by the callback stops further catch-up iterations. (2) Guard the trailing schedule: change line 252 to `if (this._playing && !this._disposed) { this._scheduleFrame(); }`. The existing non-looping end branch (lines 237-241) already does `this._setFrame(effectiveEnd); this.pause(); return;` and is unaffected.
- **Files:** `packages/animation/src/PlaybackController.ts`
- **Test:** In PlaybackController.test.ts add a describe 'callback pause/dispose safety': create a controller whose onFrameChange calls controller.pause() on its first invocation; controller.play(); prime with timer.tick(0) then timer.tick(10\*1000/30) (a delta large enough to trigger many catch-up frames). Assert onFrameChange was called exactly once, controller.isPlaying === false, and timer.pending === false (no stray rAF). Add a parallel variant where the callback calls dispose() and assert no further frames and no pending rAF.
- **Notes:** Currently latent/defensive: the only production caller (apps/web/src/hooks/usePlayback.ts) never pauses/disposes from within onFrameChange (its store-subscriber pause condition at line 91 can't fire mid-playback). The missing guard is nonetheless a genuine defect for this documented reusable engine (a stop-at-marker caller would hit it); fix is pure hardening with no normal-path behavior change, so 'low' severity is appropriate.

#### `F175` · low · boundary-violation

**Location:** `packages/animation/src/PropertyBinding.ts:17`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** @quar/animation deep-imports core source via a relative path ('../../core/src/tweening/shapeTween') instead of the @quar/core package entry, duplicating the module into animation's build output.

- **Root cause:** PropertyBinding.ts:13-17 imports `prepareShapeTween`, `interpolateShapeTween`, and type `ShapeTweenData` via the relative path `'../../core/src/tweening/shapeTween'`, reaching into @quar/core's source tree instead of the declared workspace package entry (@quar/core is in packages/animation/package.json dependencies). Because animation is built with tsup from src, shapeTween.ts gets compiled/bundled INTO @quar/animation's dist while @quar/core ships its own copy — consumers of the built packages load two copies, and animation's bundled copy can go stale against core until rebuilt. It also pulls core source files into animation's rootDir, breaking dts-rollup boundaries and dependency-graph tooling. This is the ONLY such relative cross-package import in animation/src (verified by grep).
- **Fix:** Replace lines 13-17 with `import { prepareShapeTween, interpolateShapeTween, type ShapeTweenData } from '@quar/core';`. These symbols are already public: core/src/index.ts has `export * from './tweening'` and tweening/index.ts has `export * from './shapeTween'` (shapeTween.ts exports both functions and the ShapeTweenData interface). No circular dependency: @quar/core's package.json depends on rigging/types/earcut/opentype/polygon-clipping, NOT @quar/animation. tsup treats @quar/core as an external dependency, so shapeTween will no longer be duplicated into animation's dist. If importing the @quar/core barrel proves too heavy for animation's vitest/build (it re-exports the whole rendering surface), the fallback is to add a `"./tweening": "./src/tweening/index.ts"` subpath to core's package.json `exports` and import from `@quar/core/tweening`; prefer the plain barrel import first since it requires no core changes.
- **Files:** `packages/animation/src/PropertyBinding.ts`
- **Test:** No new behavior test required — the change is behavior-preserving and existing packages/animation/src/PropertyBinding.shapeTween.test.ts already exercises pathInterpolator (prepareShapeTween/interpolateShapeTween). Gate on: that suite still passes and `pnpm typecheck`/`pnpm build` succeed after the import swap. Optionally add a build-boundary guard test asserting shapeTween is imported from the package specifier (e.g. a lint rule / grep test that `packages/animation/src` contains no `'../../core/` imports).
- **Notes:** Trivial one-line import change; the only nuance is barrel-vs-subpath, covered in fixApproach.

### Export (Lottie/PNG/sprite)

#### `F193` · low · correctness

**Location:** `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieExporter.ts:102`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** buildNodeResolver claims to walk children recursively but only maps the passed array, so exportToLottieJson without an explicit resolver silently drops every group.

- **Root cause:** buildNodeResolver (packages/export/src/lottie/lottieExporter.ts:102-111) builds a flat Map from ONLY the passed array (`for (const node of nodes) addNode(node)`) and returns `id => map.get(id)`; the JSDoc at line 100 falsely claims it 'walks children recursively'. Node.children is `string[]` (packages/types/src/index.ts:190), so from a root-only array the map can never contain descendants. In exportToLottieJson line 53, when no nodeResolver is passed, this fallback is used. groupToLottieShapes (lottieConverter.ts:257-290) then calls `nodeResolver(childId)` for each child id; every lookup returns undefined because children live outside the root array, so childItems stays empty and the function returns `[]` (line 289). nodeToLottieShapes returns `[]`, and nodeToLottieLayer returns null at line 66 (`if (!shapes || shapes.length === 0) return null`), so every group layer silently disappears. The in-app caller avoids this by passing `(id) => sceneGraph.getNode(id)` plus `sceneGraph.getRootNodes()` (ExportDialog.tsx:130,140), so only programmatic/library users who omit the resolver are bitten — the documented default behavior contradicts its contract.
- **Fix:** Three parts. (1) Rewrite the buildNodeResolver JSDoc (line 100) to state it builds a flat id->Node map from the given array and does NOT recurse, because children are stored as string IDs. (2) Make the default path able to resolve descendants without forcing a SceneGraph: add an optional `allNodes?: Node[]` parameter to both exportToLottieJson and exportLottieBlob, and when nodeResolver is not supplied use `buildNodeResolver(allNodes ?? nodes)`. Critically, keep the top-level layer loop (lottieExporter.ts:60-69) iterating only `nodes` (the roots) so passing a flat allNodes list does NOT emit descendants as duplicate top-level layers (the concern raised in F194). (3) Add a safety net in groupToLottieShapes (lottieConverter.ts:257): when `node.children` is non-empty but nodeResolver is missing or a childId fails to resolve, emit a single `console.warn` naming the group so the data loss is no longer silent. Keep nodeResolver optional to preserve backward compatibility.
- **Files:** `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieExporter.ts`, `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieConverter.ts`, `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieExporter.test.ts`
- **Test:** In lottieExporter.test.ts add a group scenario. Build a group node with `children: ['c1']` and a child rectangle 'c1'. (a) With an explicit resolver: `exportToLottieJson([group], timeline, opts, (id) => ({g1: group, c1: childRect}[id]))` -> expect result.layers length 1, and layers[0].shapes to contain a nested 'gr' item (group child not dropped). (b) With no resolver but the new allNodes param carrying descendants: `exportToLottieJson([group], timeline, opts, undefined, [group, childRect])` -> expect exactly 1 top-level layer (the group), with the child NOT appearing as a second top-level layer (guards the duplicate-layer regression). (c) With neither resolver nor allNodes and a group that has children -> assert a console.warn spy is called (documents the previously-silent drop).
- **Notes:** Confirmed real. Non-breaking because nodeResolver and the new allNodes param are both optional; existing callers (ExportDialog and current tests, none of which exercise groups through the public API) are unaffected.

#### `F194` · low · correctness

**Location:** `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieExporter.ts:104`  
**Verdict:** partly · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** F193  
**Finding:** buildNodeResolver claims to walk children recursively but only maps the top-level array, so groups silently export empty whenever no explicit nodeResolver is passed.

- **Root cause:** Same underlying defect as F193 (buildNodeResolver at lottieExporter.ts:102-111 maps only the passed array; groups silently export empty via the null-drop at lottieConverter.ts:289 -> nodeToLottieLayer line 66). F194 adds two accurate clarifications rather than a distinct bug: (1) buildNodeResolver literally cannot 'walk children recursively' as its docstring claims, because Node.children holds string IDs (types/src/index.ts:190), not Node objects, so from a root array there is nothing to recurse into; (2) the naive fix of feeding buildNodeResolver a pre-flattened array is wrong, because exportToLottieJson's top-level loop (lines 60-69) turns every element of its input array into a top-level Lottie layer, so a flat array would render each group child twice (once nested in its group's 'gr' item, once as its own top-level layer).
- **Fix:** No separate code change beyond F193. F194's constraints directly shape the F193 fix: keep the top-level layer loop bound to the roots array while sourcing the resolver from a separate allNodes list (so descendants resolve without being double-emitted), correct the misleading docstring, and warn on unresolved children instead of pretending recursion happens. Verify the F193 implementation honors the duplicate-layer constraint before closing this item.
- **Files:** `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieExporter.ts`, `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieConverter.ts`, `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieExporter.test.ts`
- **Test:** The duplicate-layer assertion in F193's test (b): with descendants provided via the new allNodes param and no explicit resolver, assert result.layers has exactly one top-level layer (the group) and the child does not appear as a separate top-level layer. This is the specific regression F194 warns about.
- **Notes:** Duplicate of F193 describing the same defect from a fix-correctness angle. Marked 'partly' only because it is not an independent defect — it is folded into F193's plan; its value is constraining the fix so it does not introduce duplicate top-level layers. Should be closed together with F193.

#### `F195` · low · correctness

**Location:** `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieKeyframes.ts:302`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** bakeTrackToLinearKeyframes samples with plain linear interpolation, ignoring keyframe easing, so 'baking' produces output identical to linear and cannot preserve bounce/elastic as documented.

- **Root cause:** bakeTrackToLinearKeyframes:301-305 samples each frame with sampleTrackAt (lottieKeyframes.ts:344-369), which performs raw linear interpolation between surrounding keyframes and ignores each keyframe's easing entirely. Consequently the baked output is always piecewise-linear regardless of easing, directly contradicting the docstring at lines 282-284 ('preserves visual fidelity for bounce, elastic, back, etc.'). Secondary defects: the fps parameter (line 289) is never referenced in the body (dead param), and the function has no non-test callers (confirmed by grep) so it produces no live .lottie corruption today — it is a broken/misleading exported API rather than an active bug.
- **Fix:** Replace the two sampleTrackAt(track, frame/nextFrame, ...) calls inside bakeTrackToLinearKeyframes with easing-aware sampling from @quar/animation: import { interpolateValue, interpolators } and compute value = interpolateValue(track, frame, interpolators.number) ?? track.keyframes[0].value (interpolateValue applies the 'after' keyframe's easing exactly as Timeline.ts:228-234 documents). Do NOT modify the shared sampleTrackAt helper — it is also used by positionTracksToLottie (:164,:173) and colorTracksToLottie (:254-257) for exact-keyframe-time and misaligned linear sampling, and making it easing-aware would regress those paths and existing sampleTrackAt unit tests. Optionally drop the unused fps parameter (or keep for signature stability); if F061 wires baking in, keep the signature so its call sites don't need editing.
- **Files:** `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieKeyframes.ts`, `packages/export/src/lottie/lottieKeyframes.test.ts`
- **Test:** Bake a track [{time:0,value:0},{time:10,value:100, easing:'easeOutBounce'}] and assert an intermediate baked frame (e.g. frame 5) is NOT the linear midpoint 50 but instead equals 100\*applyEasing(0.5,'easeOutBounce'), proving easing is now preserved. Keep the existing linear-easing bake tests green (they default easing:'linear', which interpolateValue reproduces exactly).
- **Notes:** Real and accurately described including the clarification that it is currently a dormant/misleading API with no live export impact. This should land before F061's bake-wiring, since F061 relies on bakeTrackToLinearKeyframes actually preserving bounce/elastic to be worth wiring in.

### Fonts & text

#### `F178` · low · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/font/FontManager.ts:57`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** loadFontFromBuffer inserts into loadingPromises after the delete has already run, so the entry is never removed and isLoading() reports true forever for buffer-loaded fonts.

- **Root cause:** loadFontFromBuffer (packages/core/src/font/FontManager.ts:49-58) uses a SYNCHRONOUS IIFE: `const promise = (() => { const font = opentype.parse(buffer); this.fontCache.set(key, font); this.availableFonts.set(...); this.loadingPromises.delete(key); return font; })();`. That inner `this.loadingPromises.delete(key)` (line 53) is a no-op because nothing has been registered for `key` yet. Then line 57 runs `this.loadingPromises.set(key, Promise.resolve(promise))` (promise is the raw Font, wrapped in Promise.resolve) AFTER the delete, and that entry is never removed. Consequently isLoading(family) (line 182-190) returns true forever for buffer-loaded fonts, plus a small per-font retained resolved promise. Currently low impact only because isLoading has no callers anywhere in packages/src or apps.
- **Fix:** For the synchronous buffer path, stop registering a loading promise entirely. Delete the no-op `this.loadingPromises.delete(key)` (line 53) and the erroneous `this.loadingPromises.set(key, Promise.resolve(promise))` (line 57). The async method body becomes: parse, fontCache.set, availableFonts.set, `return font;` (the async wrapper produces the Promise<Font>). This is safe: opentype.parse is synchronous with no await before fontCache.set, so a concurrent same-key call always sees the populated fontCache via the `existing` guard at lines 43-44 and returns early — no double parse, so no in-flight guard is needed. (If symmetry with the async loaders is preferred, alternatively move the loadingPromises.set BEFORE the parse and keep the delete after — but removal is simpler and preferred.)
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/font/FontManager.ts`
- **Test:** In packages/core/src/font/FontManager.test.ts (same file/mock as F032): `await fm.loadFontFromBuffer(new ArrayBuffer(4), 'MyFont')` then assert `fm.isLoading('MyFont') === false` and `fm.isLoading('MyFont', 400) === false`, and `fm.hasFont('MyFont') === true`. This currently fails (isLoading returns true) and passes after the fix.
- **Notes:** Independent of F032 (different method), but naturally batched into the same file edit and shared test file.

#### `F179` · low · race-condition

**Location:** `packages/core/src/font/FontManager.ts:227`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** F032  
**Finding:** removeFont does not cancel in-flight loads: a pending loadFontFromUrl/loadGoogleFont for the removed family re-populates fontCache and availableFonts after removal.

- **Root cause:** removeFont (packages/core/src/font/FontManager.ts:227-236) does not cancel or guard against in-flight loads. It iterates `[...this.fontCache.keys()]`, so (a) an in-flight load's key is not yet in fontCache and its loadingPromises entry is therefore never deleted, and (b) when the pending loadFontFromUrl (lines 83-84) or loadGoogleFont (lines 119-120) async body later resolves it unconditionally runs fontCache.set + availableFonts.set, re-adding the removed font. The mechanism is real. Severity is correctly low: removeFont and FontManager.dispose have zero callers in packages/src or apps (verified via grep), so the 'user removes a font mid-load' scenario is currently unreachable — this is a latent correctness bug in a public API.
- **Fix:** Two coordinated edits. (1) In removeFont, also clear in-flight entries: after the fontCache loop, add `for (const key of [...this.loadingPromises.keys()]) { if (key.startsWith(family + ':')) this.loadingPromises.delete(key); }`. (2) In each async loader body (loadFontFromUrl and loadGoogleFont), before committing, verify the load is still current: wrap the `this.fontCache.set(key, font); this.availableFonts.set(family, {...});` in `if (this.loadingPromises.get(key) === promise) { ... }`. The `promise` const is fully initialized by the time this post-await code runs, so the self-reference is safe. After removeFont deletes the loadingPromises entry, the identity check fails and the resolved load will not repopulate fontCache/availableFonts. dispose() already clears loadingPromises so the same guard covers it. (Alternative: a private generation counter incremented in removeFont/dispose, captured at load start and re-checked before commit — simpler but invalidates ALL concurrent loads globally; the identity/presence check is more precise and preferred.) This composes with F032's finally-based cleanup: during the body the entry is present (=== promise) unless removeFont deleted it, and F032's finally delete runs only after the body settles.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/font/FontManager.ts`
- **Test:** In packages/core/src/font/FontManager.test.ts: make fetch return a deferred promise you control (e.g. resolve manually). Start `const p = fm.loadFontFromUrl('u','X','google',400)` (in-flight), call `fm.removeFont('X')`, then resolve the deferred fetch with {ok:true, arrayBuffer: async()=>new ArrayBuffer(4)}, `await p`. Assert `fm.hasFont('X') === false`, `fm.getAvailableFonts().every(f => f.family !== 'X')`, and `fm.isLoading('X') === false`. Currently the font reappears after resolution; passes after the fix.
- **Notes:** dependsOn F032 because both edits touch the same two async IIFE bodies and the loadingPromises lifecycle; implement F032 first (cleanup on failure), then layer the identity guard + removeFont loop so the edits don't conflict. Real but effectively zero current runtime impact until removeFont/dispose gain callers.

#### `F180` · low · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/font/glyphConverter.ts:246`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** textToSubpaths pairs glyphs with characters by index, but opentype.js stringToGlyphs applies GSUB ligature substitution by default, so glyph/char indices desynchronize.

- **Root cause:** textToSubpaths builds chars = [...line] (glyphConverter.ts:238) and labels each glyph char: chars[i] (line 246), assuming 1:1 char↔glyph indexing. But font.stringToGlyphs(line) (line 237) applies GSUB liga/rlig by default: opentype.js 1.3.4 Font.prototype.defaultRenderOptions.features includes {script:'latn', tags:['liga','rlig']} (confirmed in node_modules/.pnpm/opentype.js@1.3.4/.../src/font.js:274-283, applied via bidi.applyFeatures in stringToGlyphs:178-204). So for fonts with ligatures (e.g. Inter, the default family) glyphs.length < chars.length and indices desync, mislabeling glyphGroup.char for all glyphs after the ligature. Impact is purely cosmetic: advanceWidth/kerning (measurement 201-214, layout 271-278) read from the glyph objects, not chars, so spacing/positioning is correct; glyphGroup.char is consumed only as the per-letter PathNode/layer name (textToShape.ts:184).
- **Fix:** Least-invasive, preserves ligature rendering: derive the label from the glyph itself instead of chars[i]. Replace line 246 with a label computed from the glyph — e.g. const cp = (glyph.unicodes && glyph.unicodes.length) ? String.fromCodePoint(...glyph.unicodes) : (glyph.name ?? ''); const glyphGroup: GlyphSubpathGroup = { char: cp, subpaths: [] }; — and delete the now-unused chars array (line 238). A normal 'H' glyph -> unicodes [72] -> 'H'; a ligature glyph -> name like 'f_f_i'. Do NOT disable liga via stringToGlyphs options: renderText shares textToSubpaths, so disabling ligatures would stop them from rendering as well.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/font/glyphConverter.ts`, `packages/core/src/font/glyphConverter.test.ts`
- **Test:** glyphConverter.test.ts currently has no textToSubpaths coverage; add a describe block with a mock opentype font: stringToGlyphs('ffi') returns ONE ligature glyph {name:'f_f_i', unicodes:[], advanceWidth:600, getPath:()=>square}; assert result.glyphs.length===1 and result.glyphs[0].char==='f_f_i' (no index desync / sensible label). Add a second glyph with unicodes:[72] and assert char==='H'.
- **Notes:** Independent of F111 despite editing the same file; sequence the two edits to avoid conflicts but no logical dependency.

#### `F181` · low · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/font/textMetrics.ts:25`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** getTextBounds ignores font weight, measuring bold text with the regular-weight font, so bounds and the renderer's anchor centering are computed from the wrong glyph widths.

- **Root cause:** getTextBounds (textMetrics.ts:16-33) has no fontWeight parameter and resolves the font via fm.getFont(fontFamily) at line 25 — defaulting to weight 400 — whereas both render paths resolve glyphs via getFontOrFallback(node.fontFamily, node.fontWeight) (ShapeRenderer.ts:2114 and 4129) and then compute the anchor-centering offset from getTextBounds (2124 and 4137) passing no weight. When Inter 400 and 700 are both loaded (App loads both), FontManager.getFont('Inter', 400) exact-matches the 400 font (FontManager.ts:135) while the drawn glyphs use the wider 700 font, so bold text's anchor-centering offset is computed from narrower 400 advance widths -> bold renders slightly off-center relative to transform.position; likewise selection/hit-test bounds (SelectionTool.ts:685, SelectionManager.ts:306, DirectSelectionTool.ts:977, PropertiesPanel.tsx:166, TextEditOverlay.tsx:28) under-measure bold text, error growing with length. When only one weight is loaded, getFont's any-weight fallback (FontManager.ts:143-144) masks the divergence.
- **Fix:** Add fontWeight: number = 400 as a trailing parameter to getTextBounds and getTextBoundsFromFont in textMetrics.ts, and resolve the font via fm.getFontOrFallback(fontFamily, fontWeight) to exactly match the renderer's glyph-font resolution (line 25). Thread node.fontWeight at all 7 call sites: ShapeRenderer.ts:2124 and 4137, SelectionTool.ts:685, DirectSelectionTool.ts:977, SelectionManager.ts:306, PropertiesPanel.tsx:166, TextEditOverlay.tsx:28. The new param defaults to 400 so any missed caller still compiles with prior behavior. Trade-off to record: switching from getFont to getFontOrFallback also changes the truly-missing-family path (from Canvas-2D fallback to an arbitrary loaded opentype font) and requires updating textMetrics.test.ts's FontManager mock (currently stubs only getFont, lines 8-13) to also stub getFontOrFallback. If minimizing blast radius is preferred, use fm.getFont(fontFamily, fontWeight) instead (keeps the existing mock and canvas fallback and still fixes the reported 400-vs-700 case, since getFont exact-matches the weighted font); getFontOrFallback is the more exact match to the renderer.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/font/textMetrics.ts`, `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts`, `packages/core/src/tools/SelectionTool.ts`, `packages/core/src/tools/DirectSelectionTool.ts`, `packages/core/src/selection/SelectionManager.ts`, `apps/web/src/components/layout/PropertiesPanel.tsx`, `apps/web/src/components/canvas/TextEditOverlay.tsx`, `packages/core/src/font/textMetrics.test.ts`
- **Test:** In textMetrics.test.ts, make the FontManager mock resolve two fonts by weight (400 -> advanceWidth 500, 700 -> advanceWidth 700). Assert getTextBounds('Hello','Inter',24,1.2,0,'left',700).width is computed from the 700 metrics and is strictly greater than the same call with weight 400 — proving the weight parameter is honored end to end.
- **Notes:** Signature change ripples to 7 call sites plus a test-mock update, but each call-site edit is a single added argument and the param is optional. Blocks F033 (F033's getTextBounds call must pass the same fontWeight to stay consistent with the renderer), so implement F181 first.

### Rendering & GL

#### `F182` · low · memory-leak

**Location:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts:981`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** An image load that resolves after dispose() re-creates and caches a WebGL texture that is never deleted.

- **Root cause:** getTexture starts an async Image load and, in the promise .then (ShapeRenderer.ts:965-982), calls gl.createTexture(), uploads, and this.textureCache.set(src, texture). dispose() (4352-4425) deletes all cached textures and clears textureCache/pendingImages (4377-4381) but sets NO disposed flag and cannot cancel the in-flight promise. If an image resolves after dispose(), the .then re-creates and caches a texture on the already-disposed renderer; nothing will ever delete it → one leaked GPU texture per image still loading at unmount/project switch. The same race applies to disposeTexture(src) called while src is pending.
- **Fix:** Add a private `disposed = false` field set to true at the top of dispose(). In the getTexture promise .then, after `this.pendingImages.delete(src)`, bail early if `this.disposed || !wasPending` before creating/caching the texture (capture whether this src was still expected, e.g. check membership just before deleting). Concretely: `const stillPending = this.pendingImages.delete(src); if (this.disposed || !stillPending) return;` then proceed to createTexture. This also covers the disposeTexture-during-pending race because disposeTexture should also delete the pendingImages entry (so stillPending is false).
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts`
- **Test:** Call getTexture(src) to start a load, call dispose(), then resolve the pending image; assert gl.createTexture is NOT called after dispose and textureCache remains empty. Second test: disposeTexture(src) while src is pending, then resolve; assert the texture is not re-added.
- **Notes:** Low impact (one texture per in-flight image at teardown) but a genuine GPU leak. Combine cleanly with F183 since both patch getTexture's promise callbacks.

#### `F185` · low · resource-leak

**Location:** `packages/core/src/rendering/WebGLRenderer.ts:200`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** createShaderProgram leaks GL objects on its error paths: the vertex shader is never deleted if the fragment shader fails to compile, and the program plus both shaders leak on link failure.

- **Root cause:** createShaderProgram (WebGLRenderer.ts:189-240) leaks GL objects on error paths. compileShader (lines 242-260) deletes only the shader it is compiling before throwing (lines 253-257). So: if the FRAGMENT shader compile fails at line 200, the already-created/compiled vertexShader from line 199 is never deleted. If gl.linkProgram fails (LINK_STATUS false, lines 212-215), the code throws without gl.deleteProgram(program) and without deleting either shader — note the deleteShader cleanup at lines 218-219 runs only after a successful link, so on link failure the program and both shaders all leak. Under a driver/ANGLE-specific compile or link failure (e.g. the 16-branch blend fragment shader in PostProcessShaders on a constrained GPU) each retry accumulates orphaned GL objects until page reload.
- **Fix:** Guard the fragment-compile and the link with cleanup. (1) After `const vertexShader = this.compileShader(gl.VERTEX_SHADER, vertexSource);` wrap the fragment compile: `let fragmentShader; try { fragmentShader = this.compileShader(gl.FRAGMENT_SHADER, fragmentSource); } catch (e) { gl.deleteShader(vertexShader); throw e; }`. (2) In the link-failure branch (lines 212-215), before throwing, call gl.deleteProgram(program); gl.deleteShader(vertexShader); gl.deleteShader(fragmentShader). Keep the existing successful-path deleteShader calls (lines 218-219). Optionally also delete both shaders in the `if (!program)` guard (line 204-206) path for completeness. A try/finally structure is an acceptable equivalent as long as the shaders/program are deleted on every throw.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/rendering/WebGLRenderer.ts`
- **Test:** WebGLRenderer.test.ts: (a) fragment-compile failure — configure mockGL.getShaderParameter to return true for the first (vertex) COMPILE_STATUS query and false for the second (fragment) via mockReturnValueOnce sequence; call createShaderProgram and expect it to throw, then assert gl.deleteShader was called for the vertex shader handle (i.e. deleteShader called for both shaders / at least the vertex one). (b) link failure — getShaderParameter returns true for both, mockGL.getProgramParameter returns false; expect throw and assert gl.deleteProgram was called with the program and gl.deleteShader called for both shader handles.
- **Notes:** Confirmed by reading compileShader vs createShaderProgram. Pure cleanup on cold error paths; no behavior change on the success path, so effectively zero regression risk. Independent of the other findings.

### Rigging

#### `F196` · low · correctness

**Location:** `packages/rigging/src/ik.ts:145`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** solveFABRIK initializes the end-effector tip along the direction from the second-to-last joint to the last joint (the parent bone's segment direction) instead of along the last bone's own world rotation, so the initial tip is wrong whenever the last bone is bent.

- **Root cause:** When building the working positions array, solveFABRIK computes the end-effector tip as lastJoint.worldPos + lastJoint.boneLength in the direction from secondToLast.worldPos to lastJoint.worldPos (ik.ts:144-146) — i.e. along the PARENT bone's segment direction, not the last bone's own world orientation. IKJoint (ik.ts:23-29) carries only worldPos and boneLength, no world rotation/tip, so the solver cannot know the last bone's true orientation. When the last bone is bent relative to its parent, the fabricated tip is wrong: (1) early convergence never triggers even when the true tip already sits on the target, so full iterations run every frame; (2) the artist's bent last-bone orientation is discarded on early-exit; (3) a genuinely wrong final pose occurs only when the last bone has angle constraints excluding the straight orientation (applyIKResult then clamps it off-target).
- **Fix:** Extend IKJoint with optional `worldTip?: Vector2` (or worldRotation). In extractIKJoints (ik.ts:397-406) compute it from the world transform like boneHelpers.getBoneWorldTip / computeFKChain: worldTip = { x: wt.a*bone.length + wt.tx, y: wt.b*bone.length + wt.ty }. In solveFABRIK, when pushing the initial tip, use lastJoint.worldTip if present: `positions.push(lastJoint.worldTip ? {...lastJoint.worldTip} : <existing fabricated fallback>)`. Keep the fabricated fallback so existing direct-solveFABRIK tests (no worldTip) are unchanged.
- **Files:** `packages/rigging/src/ik.ts`
- **Test:** In ik.test.ts, build a 2-bone chain via extractIKJoints where the child bone has a local rotation making it bent relative to the parent (so its true world tip is off the parent's straight-line extension). Set target = the child's true world tip (from getBoneWorldTip). Assert result.converged is true with endEffectorError ~0 immediately, and that the child's applied rotation is essentially unchanged (pose continuity) — before the fix the fabricated straight-extension tip differs from the target and the solver reports a large initial error / discards the bent pose.
- **Notes:** Real but low impact (the reviewer already corrected the original flagship example). Independent of the other findings: the initial tip only affects starting positions and convergence detection, not the final positionsToRotations conversion. Adding an optional IKJoint field does not break existing extractIKJoints assertions.

### SVG import/export

#### `F188` · low · round-trip-fidelity

**Location:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgExporter.ts:210`  
**Verdict:** partly · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** transformToSvgAttr silently drops the skew component of a node transform, so skewed nodes (including ones just imported from SVGs with skewX/matrix shear) export unskewed.

- **Root cause:** transformToSvgAttr (svgExporter.ts:210-226) emits only translate/rotate/scale and never reads transform.skew (Transform.skew exists at packages/types/src/index.ts:116), so any nonzero skew is dropped on export. The literal defect is real. However the finding's framing as an export-only round-trip regression is incomplete: skew is ignored across Quar's ENTIRE runtime transform pipeline — SceneGraph.computeLocalMatrix (SceneGraph.ts:344-346) calls mat3.compose(position, rotation, scale, anchor) which has no skew parameter (math.ts:249-273). So a skewed node is rendered unskewed on Quar's own canvas too; the SVG export is therefore faithful to what the app displays, and only the external SVG->node->SVG round-trip loses shear. The reviewer's note about decomposeMatrix (svgUtils.ts:311-333) folding shear into scaleY=sqrt(c^2+d^2) and storing skewX is accurate — that over-scale already corrupts the node on import, before export.
- **Fix:** Two coherent options; pick based on desired scope. PREFERRED (faithful, larger): add skew support to the whole pipeline so canvas and export agree — extend mat3.compose (math.ts) to accept skew and apply a shear matrix (skewX: [1,0,tan(radX),1], skewY: [1,tan(radY),0,1]) in a fixed order relative to rotate/scale, update SceneGraph.computeLocalMatrix to pass transform.skew, THEN emit 'skewX(<deg>)' / 'skewY(<deg>)' in transformToSvgAttr (skew stored in degrees per decomposeMatrix). Choose and document the same compose order in both places so decomposeMatrix/compose are inverses. MINIMAL (export-only, S): in transformToSvgAttr push `skewX(${fmt(transform.skew.x)})` when skew.x!==0 and `skewY(${fmt(transform.skew.y)})` when skew.y!==0, after rotate and before/after scale consistent with decomposeMatrix's order — but ACCEPT that this makes the SVG show shear the Quar canvas does not, so only do this if export-fidelity-to-source outranks export-matches-canvas. Recommend the preferred option or defer given low severity.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/svg/svgExporter.ts`, `packages/core/src/math.ts`, `packages/core/src/SceneGraph.ts`, `packages/core/src/svg/__tests__/svgExporter.test.ts`
- **Test:** Minimal-fix test: transformToSvgAttr({skew:{x:15,y:0},...identity}) contains 'skewX(15)', and skew {x:0,y:10} contains 'skewY(10)', identity emits neither. Coherent-fix test: a matrix round-trip in svgUtils/math tests — decomposeMatrix(composeSvgTransform([skewX(20)])) then re-emit via transformToSvgAttr and re-parse, asserting the resulting matrix approximately equals the original shear (proving compose and decompose agree and export round-trips).
- **Notes:** Skew is systemically unsupported (mat3.compose and SceneGraph ignore it), so this is not an export-specific bug and export currently matches on-canvas rendering. Lowest priority of the three. If only the export line is patched, exports will diverge from what users see on the Quar canvas — call that out to the implementer. Full coherent support (compose+SceneGraph+export) is the correct fix but is a genuine feature addition, hence effort M and medium regression risk on the transform math.

### Scene graph, symbols & format

#### `F176` · low · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/Camera.ts:163`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** pan() rotates the pan delta even though getViewMatrix composes translation before rotation (T(-pos)·R(-θ)), so panning moves the view in the wrong direction whenever camera rotation is non-zero.

- **Root cause:** getViewMatrix (Camera.ts:259-273) composes the view as T(-pos)·R(-θ): it does m=identity → translate(m,-pos) → rotate(m,-θ). Because mat3.translate/rotate append on the right (translate(m,x,y)=m·T, rotate(m,a)=m·R, and multiply(a,b) applies b-then-a), the result is view(w)=R(-θ)·w − pos, i.e. position is subtracted AFTER rotation. Since projection P is a pure scale, the full screen transform is n=P·R(-θ)·w − P·pos, so dn/dpos=−P is rotation-independent. That means the correct screen-space pan compensation is Δpos=(−dx/zoom, +dy/zoom) with NO rotation term — exactly the base worldDelta on lines 157-160. But pan() (lines 163-171) additionally rotates worldDelta by R(+θ) whenever \_rotation!==0, so at rotation 90° a horizontal drag becomes a vertical content move (verified: pan({100,50}) at 90° yields Δpos=(-50,-100) → content moves (50,-100) on screen instead of the intended (100,50)). fitBounds (lines 231-234) sets \_position to the world-space bounds center, which is likewise wrong under this composition because the screen center (n=0) maps to world R(θ)·pos, not pos. Both pan()'s rotation branch and fitBounds assume the OTHER convention view=R(-θ)·T(-pos) (pos = world point at screen center).
- **Fix:** Adopt the reviewer's option 1 (fixes pan AND fitBounds together, and is the sensible 'orbit about camera position' convention): in getViewMatrix, reorder so rotation is applied BEFORE translation, yielding view=R(-θ)·T(-pos). Concretely change the body to: let m = mat3.identity(); if (this.\_rotation !== 0) { const rad = (-this.\_rotation\*Math.PI)/180; m = mat3.rotate(m, rad); } m = mat3.translate(m, -this.\_position.x, -this.\_position.y); this.\_viewMatrix = m; Also update the comment on line 261 to 'rotate, then translate to camera position (rotate about camera position)'. Do NOT touch pan()'s rotation branch — under the new composition R(+θ)·worldDelta is exactly correct (I verified Δpos=R(θ)·worldDelta solves the pan equation even for non-square viewports). This is a no-op at rotation 0 (R(0)=I commutes with T), so existing rotation-0 tests and all current app behavior are unchanged. Alternative option 2 (delete pan lines 163-171 rotation branch) also fixes pan but leaves fitBounds broken under rotation, so prefer option 1.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/Camera.ts`, `packages/core/src/Camera.test.ts`
- **Test:** In Camera.test.ts add a 'pan under rotation' test: camera.setViewport(800,600); camera.rotation=90; const w={x:30,y:40}; const before=camera.worldToScreen(w); camera.pan({x:100,y:50}); const after=camera.worldToScreen(w); expect(after.x-before.x).toBeCloseTo(100,0); expect(after.y-before.y).toBeCloseTo(50,0). This fails on current code (yields ~(50,-100)) and passes after the fix. Also add a 'fitBounds centers under rotation' test: camera.setViewport(800,600); camera.rotation=45; camera.fitBounds({x:-100,y:-100,width:200,height:200},0); const c=camera.worldToScreen({x:0,y:0}); expect(c.x).toBeCloseTo(400,0); expect(c.y).toBeCloseTo(300,0) — fails currently, passes after fix.
- **Notes:** Latent: camera.rotation is never set outside tests (confirmed via grep — only Camera.test.ts lines 60,203). Reordering is provably identical at rotation 0, so zero runtime/behavior change today and no existing test breaks. Keep pan()'s rotation branch as-is; it becomes correct under the new composition.

#### `F177` · low · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/Camera.ts:314`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** getVisibleBounds computes the world AABB from only two viewport corners, which is wrong when camera rotation is non-zero.

- **Root cause:** getVisibleBounds (Camera.ts:314-333) unprojects only the two diagonal viewport corners — screenToWorld({0,0}) and screenToWorld({W,H}) — then takes min/max of just those two points. At rotation 0 the two opposite corners do define the world AABB, but with \_rotation!==0 the visible world region is a ROTATED rectangle whose axis-aligned bounds require all four corners; the (maxX,minY) and (minX,maxY) corners can extend further than the chosen diagonal. At 45° the two unprojected diagonal corners can have nearly equal x, collapsing width toward zero and drastically underestimating the extent. Consumer impact: Canvas.tsx:533-536 passes this bounds straight into grid.render, so under rotation grid lines would vanish from large parts of the viewport, and any bounds-based culling would wrongly hide shapes.
- **Fix:** Unproject all four viewport corners and take min/max over all of them. Replace the topLeft/bottomRight pair with: const corners = [ this.screenToWorld({x:0,y:0}), this.screenToWorld({x:this._viewportWidth,y:0}), this.screenToWorld({x:0,y:this._viewportHeight}), this.screenToWorld({x:this._viewportWidth,y:this._viewportHeight}) ]; then const xs=corners.map(c=>c.x), ys=corners.map(c=>c.y); const minX=Math.min(...xs), maxX=Math.max(...xs), minY=Math.min(...ys), maxY=Math.max(...ys); return {x:minX,y:minY,width:maxX-minX,height:maxY-minY}. Keep the existing Rect return shape. At rotation 0 the two extra corners are (maxX,minY)/(minX,maxY), so min/max is unchanged — existing tests and current app behavior stay identical.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/Camera.ts`, `packages/core/src/Camera.test.ts`
- **Test:** In Camera.test.ts add a 'getVisibleBounds covers all corners under rotation' test: camera.setViewport(800,600); camera.rotation=45; const b=camera.getVisibleBounds(); const corners=[{x:0,y:0},{x:800,y:0},{x:0,y:600},{x:800,y:600}].map(c=>camera.screenToWorld(c)); for(const p of corners){ expect(p.x).toBeGreaterThanOrEqual(b.x-1e-6); expect(p.x).toBeLessThanOrEqual(b.x+b.width+1e-6); expect(p.y).toBeGreaterThanOrEqual(b.y-1e-6); expect(p.y).toBeLessThanOrEqual(b.y+b.height+1e-6); }. Fails on current 2-corner code (two corners fall outside the collapsed bounds at 45°), passes after the 4-corner fix.
- **Notes:** Latent (rotation never set outside tests). Independent of F176: the 4-corner fix is self-contained and its containment test passes regardless of the view-matrix composition, because it checks corners produced by the same screenToWorld. That said, truly geometrically-correct rotated bounds benefit from F176 too, so ideally land both; there is no hard ordering dependency between them and they touch different methods in the same file.

#### `F186` · low · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/SceneGraph.ts:345`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** computeLocalMatrix passes the normalized anchor (0-1 fraction) to mat3.compose, which subtracts it as absolute local units, offsetting every world transform by a scale-dependent sub-pixel-to-multi-pixel amount.

- **Root cause:** computeLocalMatrix (packages/core/src/SceneGraph.ts:344-346) passes transform.anchor — a normalized 0..1 fraction (createDefaultTransform line 38 = {0.5,0.5}) — as the 4th arg to mat3.compose, which translates by -anchor.x/-anchor.y in raw local units (math.ts:270, `translate(m, -anchor.x, -anchor.y)`). But the shape geometry ALREADY bakes the anchor in pixel units: ShapeRenderer offsets vertices by -node.width*anchor.x / -node.height*anchor.y (e.g. renderRectangle lines 1751-1752, image lines 1935-1936) and getLocalBounds does the same. So the render path double-applies anchor: geometry(-dim*anchor) plus compose(-anchor-normalized). ShapeRenderer's own direct compose calls (lines 1579-1584, 1629-1634, 3743-3747) repeat the same mistake, so the render path is internally consistent but wrong. SelectionManager.getNodeBounds/getNodeBoundsUnrotated (SelectionManager.ts:107,122) deliberately compose WITHOUT the anchor arg, matching the geometry-only convention. Net: a scale-dependent offset of scale*anchor local units between the rendered shape and the selection overlay for root nodes (~0.5px at scale 1; ~5px for a polygon scaled 10x per Sprint 8 where scale encodes size).
- **Fix:** Adopt SelectionManager's convention everywhere (geometry carries the anchor, compose does not). In SceneGraph.computeLocalMatrix change to `mat3.compose(transform.position, transform.rotation, transform.scale)` (drop the anchor arg). For internal consistency the same three ShapeRenderer compose sites must also drop the anchor arg: lines 1579-1584 (renderNode dispatch), 1629-1634 (renderResolvedNode), and 3743-3747 (renderGhostNode) — change each `mat3.compose(pos, rot, scale, node.transform.anchor)` to `mat3.compose(pos, rot, scale)`. Do NOT touch the geometry offsets (they are correct). Leave mat3.compose's optional anchor param in place (other callers / tests may use it). After the change, root and nested nodes render exactly where SelectionManager draws the overlay.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/SceneGraph.ts`, `packages/core/src/rendering/ShapeRenderer.ts`
- **Test:** SceneGraph.test.ts getWorldTransform block: 'anchor does not offset world transform for centered root node' — node width/height 100, transform.position {0,0}, scale {1,1}, anchor {0.5,0.5}; assert getWorldTransform('node-1').tx === 0 and .ty === 0 (currently -0.5). Plus a cross-consistency test (in SelectionManager or an integration test): a rectangle at position {0,0}, anchor {0.5,0.5}, scale {10,10} — assert the AABB from SelectionManager.getNodeBounds equals the AABB obtained by transforming the geometry through sceneGraph.getWorldTransform, proving overlay and render agree.
- **Notes:** getWorldTransform feeds nearly all rendering, IK, bone, and group math, so removing the baked -anchor shifts every anchored node by scale\*anchor. Most existing SceneGraph tests set anchor {0,0} (e.g. lines 316, 509, 555) and are unaffected, but ShapeRenderer/SelectionManager tests should be re-run; expect small pixel deltas that reflect the corrected alignment. If regression scope proves too large, the alternative single-file fix (make SelectionManager compose WITH the same anchor) is NOT recommended because it propagates the geometrically-wrong double offset instead of removing it.

#### `F187` · low · data-loss

**Location:** `packages/core/src/SceneGraph.ts:448`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** F042  
**Finding:** fromJSON's orphan repair nulls the bad parent reference but never adds the node to rootNodeIds, so the node silently disappears yet keeps getting re-saved.

- **Root cause:** In fromJSON's orphan-repair loop (packages/core/src/SceneGraph.ts:446-450), when node.parent references an id not present in newNodes, the code sets node.parent = null but never appends node.id to the root list. validRootIds is built solely by filtering data.rootNodeIds (line 453), so a repaired orphan is unreachable from getRootNodes/traverse (never rendered, never in the layer panel) yet stays in the nodes map — toJSON (line 414) then re-serializes it into every save. The result is silent, unrecoverable content loss plus files that accrete invisible nodes. This is the same fromJSON hardening surface as F042.
- **Fix:** Decide one consistent policy for orphans and apply it in the same fromJSON sanitize pass introduced by F042. Preferred (recoverable): when nulling an orphan's parent at line 448, also push node.id into the root id list so the content becomes visible/selectable (append to validRootIds, or track a `newRoots` array and concat before the swap; guard against duplicates). Alternatively (clean drop): remove the orphan and its entire subtree from newNodes. Implement this as part of F042's DFS: after the DFS from validRootIds marks reachable nodes, any node in newNodes not visited is a true orphan — either promote it to a root (root policy) or delete it and its descendants (drop policy). Do not leave the current half-repair (parent nulled, not rooted, not dropped).
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/SceneGraph.ts`
- **Test:** SceneGraph.test.ts fromJSON block: 'repaired orphan is reachable' — fromJSON with node A(parent:'ghost') where 'ghost' is absent and A not in rootNodeIds; after load assert (root policy) sceneGraph.getRootNodes() includes A and A.parent === null, AND that toJSON().rootNodeIds includes A so a re-save round-trips it. If drop policy is chosen instead, assert getNode(A) is undefined and getNodeCount excludes it. Either way assert no node exists that is in the map but unreachable from any root.
- **Notes:** Overlaps F042: both rewrite fromJSON's hierarchy handling and both need the roots/reachability computation. Implement together as a single sanitize pass; pick the root-promotion policy unless the team prefers strict dropping of unreachable data.

### Tools, selection & coordinate spaces

#### `F189` · low · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/tools/EraserTool.ts:182`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Eraser stroke preview fill uses 0-1 color components against the project's 0-255 Color convention, rendering near-black instead of red.

- **Root cause:** getPreviewNode() at EraserTool.ts:182 sets the preview fill to `{ r: 1, g: 0, b: 0, a: 1 }`. The Color type documents r/g/b as 0-255 (packages/types/src/index.ts:42-45) and ShapeRenderer uploads color.r/255, color.g/255, color.b/255 (ShapeRenderer.ts:2923 and 4341). So 1/255 = 0.004 renders an almost-black blob at 30% opacity instead of the intended red eraser indicator. ArtboardTool.ts:143 correctly uses 255.
- **Fix:** Change the preview fill color at EraserTool.ts:182 from `color: { r: 1, g: 0, b: 0, a: 1 }` to `color: { r: 255, g: 0, b: 0, a: 1 }`. IMPORTANT: the existing preview test locks in the bug — update EraserTool.test.ts:698 from `expect(preview!.fills[0]!.color.r).toBe(1); // Red` to `expect(preview!.fills[0]!.color.r).toBe(255);` (line 699 asserting g === 0 stays). Without this test edit the change will fail CI.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/tools/EraserTool.ts`, `packages/core/src/tools/EraserTool.test.ts`
- **Test:** No new test file needed; amend the existing 'should return a PathNode during drag in stroke mode' assertion (EraserTool.test.ts:698) to expect color.r === 255 (and keep g === 0), which now proves the preview is truly red under the 0-255 convention.
- **Notes:** Cosmetic only (preview overlay); no data impact. The main gotcha is the test lock-in at line 698.

#### `F190` · low · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/tools/EraserTool.ts:527`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** F137  
**Finding:** Sibling indices captured before mutation cause z-order shuffling when one eraser stroke removes some shapes and replaces others under the same parent.

- **Root cause:** In finalizeStrokeErase the sibling `index` is captured during the pre-mutation traversal (EraserTool.ts:381-394) before any node is removed. Replacement then does removeNode(node.id) (line 522), addNode which appends to the end (line 523), then moveNode(resultNode.id, parentId, index) with that STALE index (line 527). When an earlier candidate is fully erased first (removeNode at line 433/442) the survivors' captured indices no longer match the mutated children array, so moveNode places the replacement at the wrong slot. Example: roots [A,B,C]; A fully erased, C untouched, B replaced -> after A removal children=[B,C]; removeNode(B)->[C]; addNode(B') ->[C,B']; moveNode(B', null, stale 1) keeps [C,B'] so B now renders after C instead of before it.
- **Fix:** Recompute the replacement index at replacement time instead of using the captured one. Just before removeNode(node.id) at line 522, compute the node's CURRENT sibling position: `let currentIndex: number; if (parentId) { const p = this.context.sceneGraph.getNode(parentId); currentIndex = p ? p.children.indexOf(node.id) : -1; } else { currentIndex = this.context.sceneGraph.getRootNodes().findIndex(n => n.id === node.id); }`. Then use `currentIndex` in the moveNode guard (`if (currentIndex >= 0) this.context.sceneGraph.moveNode(resultNode.id, parentId, currentIndex);`). The traversal-time `index` field at lines 383-394 becomes unused and can be removed from the candidates entries (or left; harmless). Because addNode appends, moving to the removed node's just-vacated slot restores original stacking.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/tools/EraserTool.ts`, `packages/core/src/tools/EraserTool.test.ts`
- **Test:** In EraserTool.test.ts add a 'z-order' test under stroke mode: add three root rectangles in order A (tiny, e.g. 5x5 at x=-300, fully erasable), B (100x100 at x=0), C (100x100 at x=400, out of eraser range). Run a horizontal performStrokeErase from {x:-350,y:0} to {x:0,y:0} with size ~20 so A is fully removed, B is bitten (replaced), C is untouched. Assert getRootNodes() order: roots[1].id === C.id (C keeps its original id and stays LAST) and roots[0].id !== C.id (the new B' comes first). Under the current bug roots[0].id === C.id, failing the test.
- **Notes:** dependsOn F137 is an edit-ordering convenience, not a logical dependency: both fixes touch the same replacement block (lines ~509-528). Do F137 (contour-to-local restructuring) first, then apply this index recompute right before removeNode, to avoid conflicting edits.

#### `F191` · low · correctness

**Location:** `packages/core/src/tools/PenTool.ts:288`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Degenerate-path check only inspects anchor positions and ignores bezier handles, discarding valid loop-shaped paths whose anchors coincide.

- **Root cause:** PenTool.finalizePath degenerate-path check (PenTool.ts:277-291) computes a bounding box over only p.position for each point and cancels when maxX-minX < 0.1 && maxY-minY < 0.1, ignoring handleIn/handleOut. Handles are stored as offsets relative to position (set in onPointerMove line 121-126 as worldPos - lastPoint.position). A valid loop drawn by clicking a point, dragging out large smooth handles, then clicking near the same position and pressing Enter has anchors within <0.1 units but handles spanning a visible curve — finalizePath cancels and silently discards the drawn path.
- **Fix:** Include handle extents in the degenerate-path bounding box. In the loop over this.currentPath, for each point also consider the absolute handle endpoints position+handleIn and position+handleOut when present, expanding minX/maxX/minY/maxY. Concretely, for each p: consider candidates [p.position, p.handleIn && {x:p.position.x+p.handleIn.x, y:p.position.y+p.handleIn.y}, p.handleOut && {x:p.position.x+p.handleOut.x, y:p.position.y+p.handleOut.y}] (skip nulls) and fold each into the min/max. Then keep the same <0.1 threshold test. (Alternatively use bezier.bounds() over the segments, but folding handle endpoints is simpler and sufficient.) The existing test (PenTool.test.ts:651-674, four clicks at the same point with no handles) still cancels because those points have null handles.
- **Files:** `packages/core/src/tools/PenTool.ts`
- **Test:** In PenTool.test.ts degenerate describe: onPointerDown at (100,100) then onPointerMove to (100,150) to drag out a large handleOut (smooth point 0), onPointerUp; onPointerDown again near (100,100) (second anchor, anchors coincide) then onPointerUp; press Enter. Assert a path node WAS added (sceneGraph node count 1) because the handle-inclusive bbox exceeds 0.1, and tool.isCurrentlyDrawing() is false.

### UI component library

#### `F197` · low · ui-state

**Location:** `packages/ui/src/components/Button.tsx:149`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Loading buttons keep enabled styling and hover state, and `isHovered` sticks true when the button becomes disabled while hovered because disabled elements do not dispatch mouseleave.

- **Root cause:** In Button.tsx the disabled/hover style branches key off `disabled` alone, not the effective disabled state. Line 149 `...(disabled && disabledStyles)` and line 150 `...(isHovered && !disabled && getHoverStyles(variant))` use `disabled`, but the button is actually DOM-disabled when loading too (line 157 `disabled={disabled || loading}`). So a loading-but-not-disabled button keeps `cursor:pointer` and full opacity (disabledStyles not applied) — unconditionally wrong. Hover coloring additionally sticks: if isHovered was true before the button became loading/disabled, it stays applied because `!disabled` is still true; and because a DOM-disabled element does not fire mouseleave, `isHovered` (line 132) never resets. The precision note is accurate: a freshly-mounted `<Button loading>` shows the wrong cursor/opacity but not hover coloring (it can't receive mouseenter while disabled). Confirmed real; the loading test (lines 63-68) only checks disabled+spinner, not styles.
- **Fix:** Introduce `const isDisabled = disabled || loading;`. Use it in both style branches: `...(isDisabled && disabledStyles)` and `...(isHovered && !isDisabled && getHoverStyles(variant))`. Keep the button attribute `disabled={isDisabled}`. Add `React.useEffect(() => { if (isDisabled) setIsHovered(false); }, [isDisabled]);` to clear stuck hover when the effective disabled flag flips true.
- **Files:** `packages/ui/src/components/Button.tsx`
- **Test:** In Button.test.tsx: `render(<Button loading>Save</Button>)` then `expect(screen.getByRole('button')).toHaveStyle({ cursor: 'not-allowed', opacity: '0.5' })`. Optional hover-stick regression: `fireEvent.mouseEnter(button)` then rerender the same button with `loading` and assert the hover background is no longer applied (isHovered reset).
- **Notes:** Button.tsx also edited by F198; batch both in one pass. IconButton has an analogous stuck-hover pattern but is out of scope for the listed files.

#### `F198` · low · accessibility

**Location:** `packages/ui/src/components/Button.tsx:168`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** iconOnly buttons drop `children` from the DOM with no accessible-name fallback, producing nameless buttons for screen readers.

Additionally, when `loading` (line 163) the label vanishes with no `aria-busy` to signal a busy state to AT. Confirmed real; the iconOnly test (lines 82-86) asserts the text is NOT in the DOM but checks no accessible name.
- **Fix:** On the `<button>` (lines 155-161), derive an accessible name for icon-only usage: set `aria-label={iconOnly && typeof children === 'string' ? children : undefined}` placed BEFORE `{...props}` so an explicit caller `aria-label` overrides. Also add `aria-busy={loading || undefined}`. (Optionally document that non-string children in iconOnly mode still require an explicit aria-label.)
- **Files:** `packages/ui/src/components/Button.tsx`

Add `render(<Button loading>Save</Button>)` asserting `screen.getByRole('button')` has `aria-busy="true"`. Add a case where an explicit `aria-label` overrides the children-derived name.
