The sibling IconButton has the same nameless-button trap when its optional `tooltip` (used as title, line 138) is omitted, but IconButton.tsx is outside the listed files, so leave it out of this plan. Placing aria-label before {...props} preserves caller override.

#### `F199` · low · race-condition

**Location:** `packages/ui/src/components/Tooltip.tsx:76`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** showTooltip never clears an already-pending timer, so the mouseenter+focus double-arm leaves an orphaned timeout that makes the tooltip appear and stick after the pointer has left.

- **Root cause:** In packages/ui/src/components/Tooltip.tsx, showTooltip (lines 73-80) assigns `timeoutRef.current = window.setTimeout(...)` without first clearing any timer already stored in timeoutRef.current. The wrapper div binds showTooltip to BOTH onMouseEnter (line 147) and onFocus (line 149). When a user hovers then clicks a focusable child, focusin bubbles to the wrapper and fires showTooltip a second time, overwriting the ref with timer B and orphaning timer A. hideTooltip (lines 82-88) only clears the currently-referenced timer, so on mouseLeave it cancels B but not A; A later fires setIsVisible(true)+updatePosition(), showing the tooltip while the pointer is elsewhere. It then lingers because no further mouseleave will occur (only a later blur hides it).
- **Fix:** At the very top of showTooltip (before the disabled check is fine, but do it before scheduling), add: `if (timeoutRef.current) { clearTimeout(timeoutRef.current); timeoutRef.current = null; }`. This guarantees at most one pending show-timer regardless of how many onMouseEnter/onFocus events arm it. Do not change hideTooltip; it already nulls the ref after clearing. Optionally also set timeoutRef.current = null inside the setTimeout callback after it runs, for tidiness (not required for correctness).
- **Files:** `packages/ui/src/components/Tooltip.tsx`
- **Test:** In Tooltip.test.tsx, add a test that imports fireEvent from '@testing-library/react'. Render <Tooltip content="X" delay={300}><button>B</button></Tooltip>. Grab the wrapper via screen.getByRole('button').parentElement. fireEvent.mouseEnter(wrapper) (arms timer A), fireEvent.focus(wrapper) (arms timer B), fireEvent.mouseLeave(wrapper) (clears the ref timer). Then vi.advanceTimersByTime(300) and assert screen.queryByText('X') is not in the document. Pre-fix this fails because orphaned timer A fires; post-fix it passes because the second showTooltip cleared A and mouseLeave cleared B.
- **Notes:** Matches the reviewer's suggested fix exactly. Independent of F200/F201.

#### `F200` · low · tooltip-positioning

**Location:** `packages/ui/src/components/Tooltip.tsx:99`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Tooltip has no viewport clamping or flipping, so tooltips on elements near screen edges render fully or partially off-screen.

- **Root cause:** updatePosition (Tooltip.tsx lines 90-119) computes top/left purely from the trigger's getBoundingClientRect plus a fixed 8px offset and stores it in state; there is no comparison against window.innerWidth/innerHeight, so a trigger near a viewport edge yields a tooltip position that renders partly or fully off-screen. whiteSpace:'nowrap' (line 37) additionally prevents the tooltip from wrapping to stay on-screen. Positioning is also one-shot: updatePosition is invoked only once inside the delayed setTimeout callback (line 78) with no scroll/resize listener, so a scroll after show leaves the tooltip mispositioned. Confirmed the component has no consumers (grep for `<Tooltip` finds only Tooltip.test.tsx; apps/web uses the native title attribute per Toolbar.module.css:137), so this is a latent library flaw with no current user-facing impact.
- **Fix:** Add a ref for the tooltip div (const tooltipRef = useRef<HTMLDivElement>(null)) and attach it to the rendered tooltip element (line 155). Because the tooltip's own size is unknown until it renders, do the clamp/flip in a useLayoutEffect that runs when isVisible becomes true: read tooltipRef.current.getBoundingClientRect(), and adjust the state position so the box stays within [0, window.innerWidth] x [0, window.innerHeight] with a small margin (e.g. 4px). Implement flipping: if position is 'top' and the box top < 0, recompute as 'bottom' (and vice versa); if 'left' and box left < 0 recompute as 'right' (and vice versa). After flipping, additionally clamp left into [margin, innerWidth - width - margin] and top into [margin, innerHeight - height - margin]. Keep getTransform consistent with the effective (possibly flipped) side by tracking an effective-position state. Also add window 'scroll' (capture:true) and 'resize' listeners while isVisible is true that call updatePosition()+the clamp, removed on cleanup. Consider removing whiteSpace:'nowrap' or adding a maxWidth so long content can wrap.
- **Files:** `packages/ui/src/components/Tooltip.tsx`
- **Test:** In Tooltip.test.tsx add a test that mocks layout: spy triggerRef's element via Element.prototype.getBoundingClientRect (or mock on the specific button/wrapper) to return a rect near the right/bottom edge (e.g. {left: 1000, right: 1010, top: 1000, bottom: 1010, width: 10, height: 10}), set window.innerWidth/innerHeight to 1024/768, and mock the tooltip div's getBoundingClientRect to a 200x40 box. Show the tooltip (hover + advance timers), then read the rendered tooltip element's style.left/style.top (or its measured rect) and assert left + width <= window.innerWidth and top + height <= window.innerHeight (i.e. it was clamped/flipped on-screen). jsdom returns zero-size rects by default, so the getBoundingClientRect mocks are required.
- **Notes:** Touches the same tooltip render block as F201, so coordinate the two edits (add tooltipRef alongside role/id). No current consumers, so real-world regression risk is minimal, but the positioning-logic rewrite warrants medium risk. Existing 'supports different positions' test only asserts text presence, not coordinates, so it should keep passing.

#### `F201` · low · accessibility

**Location:** `packages/ui/src/components/Tooltip.tsx:155`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Tooltip content is not exposed to assistive technology: no role="tooltip", no aria-describedby link, and the shortcut text is invisible to screen readers.

- **Root cause:** The tooltip div (Tooltip.tsx lines 155-165) has no role and no id, and the wrapper div (lines 144-153) has no aria-describedby, so screen readers get no association between trigger and tooltip text. The shortcut hint (line 164) is rendered only inside this visual-only div, so it is unreachable non-visually. There is also no Escape-to-dismiss handler, diverging from the ARIA tooltip pattern.
- **Fix:** Import useId (add to the existing react import: `import React, { type ReactNode, useRef, useState, useEffect, useId } from 'react'`). In the component, const tooltipId = useId(). On the tooltip div add role="tooltip" and id={tooltipId}. On the wrapper div add aria-describedby={isVisible ? tooltipId : undefined} (conditional so it only references an element that exists in the DOM). Add an onKeyDown handler on the wrapper that calls hideTooltip() when e.key === 'Escape', per the ARIA tooltip pattern. Leave the shortcut span in place; it now becomes part of the described-by text so it is announced when the tooltip is shown.
- **Files:** `packages/ui/src/components/Tooltip.tsx`
- **Test:** In Tooltip.test.tsx: (1) show the tooltip (hover + advance timers) and assert screen.getByRole('tooltip') is in the document and its textContent includes the content and shortcut; (2) assert the wrapper (button.parentElement) has an aria-describedby whose value equals the tooltip element's id; (3) with the tooltip visible, fireEvent.keyDown(wrapper, { key: 'Escape' }) and assert queryByRole('tooltip') is null.
- **Notes:** React 18.2 (confirmed in packages/ui/package.json) supports useId. Shares the tooltip render block with F200; do both edits together to avoid conflicting rewrites of that JSX. Independent of F199.

#### `F202` · low · theme-consistency

**Location:** `packages/ui/src/theme.ts:39`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** theme.ts (and the Storybook preview that mirrors it) still carries the pre-Sprint-3.5 token set — blue #3B82F6 accent, Inter/JetBrains fonts, z-tooltip 500 — diverging from every value the app actually uses.

- **Root cause:** packages/ui/src/theme.ts holds the pre-Sprint-3.5 design tokens that were never updated when the app moved to the 'Neo-Industrial Studio' look. Concretely: colors.accent.primary='#3B82F6' (line 39) and colors.border.focus='#3B82F6' (line 34) vs the app's violet #a855f7 (apps/web/src/styles/globals.css:38) and amber #e89b47 (globals.css:35); typography.fontFamily.ui=Inter (line 78) and .mono=JetBrains Mono (line 79) vs DM Sans / IBM Plex Mono (globals.css:72-73); zIndex only reaches modal=300/tooltip=500 (lines 152,154) vs the app's expanded scale base0..overlay1000..context-menu1010..popover1020..modal1030..color-picker1040..tooltip1050 (globals.css:115-123). generateCSSVariables() (line 161) reflects these stale values and has ZERO callers in apps/ or packages/ source — it is dead code. Verified the whole @quar/ui package is imported nowhere in app/package source, so this divergence produces no shipped-product rendering bug; the only live impact is Storybook, whose preview.ts (packages/ui/.storybook/preview.ts) hand-mirrors the same stale tokens (blue #3B82F6 line 28, Inter line 53, z-tooltip 500 line 91) and renders the 4 .stories.tsx against the wrong theme. A third stale mirror not named in the finding also exists: packages/ui/src/styles/globals.css (blue #3B82F6 line 33, Inter line 58, JetBrains line 59, z-tooltip 500 line 102).
- **Fix:** Keep apps/web/src/styles/globals.css as the authoritative source of truth (it is richer and is what the app actually imports) and bring the ui package's copies into alignment: (1) In packages/ui/src/theme.ts update the stale VALUES to match Sprint-3.5: colors.accent.primary '#a855f7', primaryHover '#c084fc', primaryActive '#9333ea', secondary '#9f1239', success '#34d399', warning '#fbbf24', error '#fb7185'; colors.border.focus '#e89b47'; typography.fontFamily.ui to "'DM Sans', -apple-system, BlinkMacSystemFont, system-ui, sans-serif" and .mono to "'IBM Plex Mono', 'SF Mono', 'Consolas', monospace"; expand the zIndex object to the app's scale (base:0, dropdown:100, sticky:200, overlay:1000, contextMenu:1010, popover:1020, modal:1030, colorPicker:1040, tooltip:1050) and mirror those keys plus the added tokens inside generateCSSVariables(). (2) Kill the dead-code / mirror problem in one move: refactor packages/ui/.storybook/preview.ts to import { generateCSSVariables } from '../src/theme' and inject its output instead of the hand-maintained inline globalStyles string — this gives generateCSSVariables a real caller and makes Storybook auto-track theme.ts. (3) Update packages/ui/src/styles/globals.css to the same Sprint-3.5 values, or delete it if it is confirmed unused (grep shows nothing imports it — the apps/web main.tsx import resolves to apps/web's own copy, not this one). Do NOT attempt to make apps/web/src/styles/globals.css generated from theme.ts in this pass — that is a larger refactor with real regression risk to the shipped app and is out of scope for a low-severity token-consistency fix.
- **Files:** `packages/ui/src/theme.ts`, `packages/ui/.storybook/preview.ts`, `packages/ui/src/styles/globals.css`
- **Test:** Add packages/ui/src/theme.test.ts (none exists today) asserting: colors.accent.primary === '#a855f7' and is NOT '#3B82F6'; colors.border.focus === '#e89b47'; typography.fontFamily.ui contains 'DM Sans' and typography.fontFamily.mono contains 'IBM Plex Mono'; a z-index ordering guard that zIndex.tooltip is the maximum of the scale and strictly greater than modal/popover/overlay (prevents future inversion); and a generateCSSVariables() output check that the returned string contains '--color-accent-primary: #a855f7' and '--font-family-ui:' with 'DM Sans' and '--z-tooltip: 1050'. Optionally add a drift-guard that reads apps/web/src/styles/globals.css and asserts the accent-primary / font-family-ui / z-tooltip values match theme.ts (note: cross-package fs read in a unit test is somewhat fragile, mark it as such).
- **Notes:** Verdict real but low: the core staleness/divergence claim is factually confirmed. Two honesty caveats carried from the reviewer's own refinements: (a) there is NO shipped-product rendering bug because nothing imports @quar/ui — the concrete impact is limited to Storybook visual-review fidelity plus generateCSSVariables being dead code; (b) the ORIGINAL 'tooltips underneath modals' example is wrong (within theme.ts's own scale tooltip=500 > modal=300, so tooltip sits above modal) — the real defect is that theme.ts's 0-500 scale is wholly inconsistent with the app's 0-1050 scale. Also note the finding under-counts the mirrors: besides theme.ts and .storybook/preview.ts, packages/ui/src/styles/globals.css is a third stale copy that must be fixed or deleted for the cleanup to be complete.

### Web — UI, panels & timeline

#### `F156` · low · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/common/ColorPicker.tsx:179`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** emitColor (parent onChange + setHexInput) is called inside setHsv updater functions, a side effect in a state updater that double-fires onChange under StrictMode and risks setState-during-render when updaters are replayed.

- **Root cause:** In ColorPicker.tsx, updateSV (lines 179-183) and updateHue (lines 207-211) call `emitColor(...)` — which invokes the parent `onChange` and `setHexInput` — from INSIDE the `setHsv((prev) => {...})` updater function. That is an impure state updater (side effects in a reducer). React StrictMode intentionally double-invokes updater functions in development, so `onChange`/`setHexInput` fire twice per interaction in dev. updateAlpha (lines 229-237) already does it correctly: it computes the value and calls setAlpha + emitColor OUTSIDE any updater. The reviewer's overstatement (a render-phase "Cannot update a component while rendering a different component" error) does not fire for the real PropertiesPanel caller (handleFillPickerChange, line 724) because onChange writes to sceneGraph.updateNode and the Zustand store, not an ancestor React setState; and the double emits are idempotent (same hex, same node fill, same keyframe). So genuine but low/dev-only.
- **Fix:** Mirror updateAlpha. In updateSV replace the updater body with: `const next = { ...hsv, s, v }; setHsv(next); emitColor(next.h, next.s, next.v, alpha);` and add `hsv` to its useCallback deps (matching updateAlpha's [hsv, alpha, emitColor] — during a drag handlePointerMove re-reads the latest hsv, and only s/v change so h is preserved correctly). Do the same in updateHue: `const next = { ...hsv, h }; setHsv(next); emitColor(next.h, next.s, next.v, alpha);` with deps [hsv, alpha, emitColor]. No behavior change outside StrictMode; eliminates the impure updater.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/common/ColorPicker.tsx`, `apps/web/src/components/common/ColorPicker.test.tsx`
- **Test:** Add a ColorPicker.test.tsx case that renders the picker wrapped in <React.StrictMode>, mocks sv-area getBoundingClientRect, fires a single pointerDown on `sv-area`, and asserts `onChange` was called exactly once (toHaveBeenCalledTimes(1)). Before the fix the impure updater is double-invoked in dev and onChange fires twice; after the fix it fires once. (Vitest runs the dev React build so StrictMode double-invocation applies.)

#### `F157` · low · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/common/ExportDialog.tsx:333`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** F072, F073  
**Finding:** The Escape key handler is effectively dead: it is attached to a non-focusable backdrop div and the dialog never takes focus, so Escape neither closes the dialog when freshly opened nor cancels a running export.

- **Root cause:** handleKeyDown (lines 97-110) is wired only via `onKeyDown={handleKeyDown}` on the backdrop div (line 333). That div has no tabIndex and nothing focuses it or the dialog on mount, so React's synthetic onKeyDown never fires on a fresh open (focus remains on document.body / the trigger). Escape therefore neither closes a freshly-opened dialog nor cancels a running export. It only works after the user manually focuses a descendant input/tab (focus inside the subtree). Multiple other dismissal paths work (X, Cancel, backdrop mousedown), so impact is low, but the Escape affordance is genuinely dead in the common states.
- **Fix:** Replace the subtree-scoped onKeyDown with a document-level listener, mirroring ColorPicker.tsx:353-359. Add `useEffect(() => { const handler = (e: KeyboardEvent) => { if (e.key !== 'Escape') return; e.preventDefault(); if (state.exporting) { cancelledRef.current = true; setState((s)=>({...s, cancelled:true})); } else { close(); } }; document.addEventListener('keydown', handler); return () => document.removeEventListener('keydown', handler); }, [state.exporting, close]);`. Then remove the now-redundant `onKeyDown={handleKeyDown}` on the backdrop (line 333) and the handleKeyDown callback (or keep it only if still referenced). Re-registering on [state.exporting] keeps the exporting branch current.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/common/ExportDialog.tsx`
- **Test:** Add a test: open the dialog, `fireEvent.keyDown(document, { key: 'Escape' })` (without first focusing any input), then after the EXIT_MS timer assert the dialog is removed. Add a second test that during export Escape sets cancellation (progress cancel path) rather than closing — using the enriched '@quar/export' mock.
- **Notes:** Should follow F072/F073 so the Escape branch shares the same cancellation semantics being finalized there (cancelledRef + exporting reset), avoiding divergent cancel logic across the X button, Cancel button, and Escape. Independent code-wise but best sequenced after the cancellation model is settled.

#### `F158` · low · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/common/ImageAdjustments.tsx:145`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Negative values cannot be typed into the adjustment value fields even though half of every bipolar range is negative.

- **Root cause:** In ImageAdjustments.tsx the value field is a CONTROLLED `type="text"` input: `value={displayValue}` (line 207) where displayValue (line 180) derives from the numeric `value` prop. handleInputChange (lines 141-151) cleans with `/[^-\d.]/g` then `parseFloat`, and the guard `if (!isNaN(num))` (line 145) skips onChange when the parse fails. Typing a lone leading '-' yields parseFloat('-')===NaN, so onChange is not called, the parent `value` prop does not change, and React reconciles the controlled input back to the previous displayValue — erasing the '-' keystroke. Net: you cannot type a negative number left-to-right, even though every bipolar range (e.g. brightness -100..100, hue -180..180) is half negative. It is a data-entry papercut, not lost functionality: the slider covers negatives, ArrowDown clamps toward def.min, and typing digits then prepending '-' works. Correctly scoped to ImageAdjustments only — DynamicChainPanel.tsx:237 and WindPanel.tsx:129 use type="number" which preserves the intermediate '-' at the browser level.
- **Fix:** Give AdjustmentSlider a local draft-string state for the field while editing: `const [draft, setDraft] = useState<string | null>(null);` and `const displayValue = draft ?? (def.suffix ? ... : String(Math.round(value)))`. In handleInputChange: `setDraft(cleaned)`; only when parseFloat(cleaned) is finite, compute the clamped value and call onChange(def.key, clamped) — intermediate '', '-', '-.' keep the draft and skip the parent callback. On blur and on Enter (handleInputKeyDown), commit: clear draft with `setDraft(null)` so the field snaps back to the canonical formatted value, and on Enter also push the last valid clamped value. This lets a leading '-' persist in the field.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/common/ImageAdjustments.tsx`, `apps/web/src/components/common/ImageAdjustments.test.tsx`
- **Test:** Add ImageAdjustments.test.tsx cases: (1) get the brightness value input, fireEvent.change to '-' and assert the input value is retained as '-' (not reverted to '0') and onChange was NOT called; then fireEvent.change to '-50' and assert onChange('brightness', -50). (2) after typing an intermediate '-', fireEvent.blur and assert the field resets to the canonical formatted value. Confirm the existing 'ignores non-numeric text input' ('abc'→no onChange) and 'strips suffix' ('45°'→45) tests still pass under the draft approach.

#### `F159` · low · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/common/PromptDialog.tsx:174`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** A second promptDialog() call while one is pending orphans the first promise, leaving its awaiting caller hung forever.

- **Root cause:** In PromptDialog.tsx, promptDialog() (lines 166-176) creates a Promise, stores its `resolve` on the request object, and broadcasts the request to all hostListeners. PromptDialogHost's listener is `(req) => setRequest(req)` (line 185) and it holds only a single request in state. If promptDialog() is called again while a dialog is already open, setRequest replaces the first request object without ever invoking its stored `resolve`, so the first `await promptDialog(...)` never settles and its caller's continuation silently never runs. Confirmed the same replace-without-notify shape exists in ExportDialogHost, but that host holds no promise so there is no orphaned await there.
- **Fix:** In PromptDialogHost, track the active request in a ref and resolve the previous one with null before replacing. Add `const currentRef = useRef<PromptRequest | null>(null);` and change the listener to: `const listener: HostListener = (req) => { if (currentRef.current && req) currentRef.current.resolve(null); currentRef.current = req; setRequest(req); };`. In the onConfirm and onCancel handlers (lines 200-207), set `currentRef.current = null` after resolving so a normal close does not double-resolve. (Alternative: queue requests FIFO; the resolve-previous-with-null approach matches the reviewer's suggestion and is simpler.)
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/common/PromptDialog.tsx`, `apps/web/src/components/common/PromptDialog.test.tsx`
- **Test:** New PromptDialog.test.tsx: render <PromptDialogHost/>, then (inside act) call `const p1 = promptDialog({title:'A'})` and `const p2 = promptDialog({title:'B'})`. Assert `await p1` resolves to null (first is superseded, not orphaned) and that the visible dialog now reflects request B; then confirm B via the input/confirm button and assert p2 resolves to the typed value. Before the fix p1 would hang forever.
- **Notes:** Fix is isolated to PromptDialogHost; ExportDialogHost shares the pattern but has no orphaned-promise risk, so it is out of scope for this finding.

#### `F162` · low · performance

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/MenuBar.tsx:209`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** MenuBar subscribes to currentFrame and traverses the entire scene graph on every render, so it re-renders and does an O(n) traversal every frame during playback.

- **Root cause:** MenuBar subscribes to currentFrame via useEditorStore((state)=>state.currentFrame) at MenuBar.tsx:121. During playback PlaybackController updates currentFrame every frame, so this subscription re-renders the whole MenuBar function every frame. currentFrame (and timelineDuration, line 122) are consumed ONLY inside Animation-menu onClick closures (lines 780, 789-790, 799, 808, 825) — never in rendered JSX or disabled props — so the subscription adds nothing to output yet forces a full component re-execution per frame. Each such render also runs the unconditional sceneGraph.traverse for hasBoneNodes (MenuBar.tsx:208-215, deliberately not memoized per the comment at 206-207) plus ~13 useMemo dependency comparisons. hasBoneNodes is used only to disable 'Bind Selection to Bones' (line 877), which lives inside the Rigging dropdown that is conditionally rendered only when openMenu==='rigging' (line 854).
- **Fix:** 1) Drop the currentFrame and timelineDuration store subscriptions (remove lines 121-122) and instead read them lazily inside each Animation-menu onClick handler via `const { currentFrame, timelineDuration } = useEditorStore.getState();` at the top of the handler (handlers at 778-826). This removes the per-frame re-render entirely. 2) Gate the bone traversal so it only runs when the Rigging menu is open: replace the unconditional block at 208-215 with `let hasBoneNodes = false; if (openMenu === 'rigging') { sceneGraph.traverse(...) }`. Since the only consumer (line 877) is inside the rigging dropdown that only renders when openMenu==='rigging', the default false is never observed while closed and behavior is unchanged. Keep the short-circuit `return false` in the traverse callback.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/MenuBar.tsx`
- **Test:** MenuBar.test.tsx: render MenuBar, open Animation menu, click 'Next Frame' and assert setCurrentFrame was called with currentFrame+1 read from the store at click-time (set store currentFrame to a known value first) — proves lazy read still works. Add a render-count assertion test: wrap MenuBar render body counter (or spy on sceneGraph.traverse) and update currentFrame via store while no menu is open, asserting sceneGraph.traverse is not called on that update (proves traversal is gated and no per-frame work happens).
- **Notes:** Behavior-preserving. Verify no other rendered JSX reads currentFrame/timelineDuration before removing the subscriptions (grep confirms they appear only in the onClick handlers). Touches same file as F013 — merge carefully.

#### `F163` · low · performance

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/PropertiesPanel.tsx:361`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** L · **Depends on:** F017, F081, F082, F083  
**Finding:** PropertiesPanel subscribes directly to currentFrame, so the entire 4,200-line panel re-renders on every frame during playback just to refresh keyframe indicator diamonds

- **Root cause:** PropertiesPanel subscribes to currentFrame (line 361) and timeline (line 364) at the top of the 4,200-line component. usePlayback calls setCurrentFrame 30-60x/sec during playback, so the entire panel (all sections, inputs, ScrubLabels, effect editors) re-renders every frame even though only the ~19 small KeyframeIndicators need the frame to recompute active/inactive state. timeline is also replaced wholesale on every keyframe op and graph-editor drag, adding large reconciliations. Most non-indicator uses of currentFrame are inside event handlers (addKeyframeAtFrame(nodeId,prop,currentFrame,val)) that do not need to be render-reactive; shouldKeyframe already reads timeline via useEditorStore.getState().
- **Fix:** Push the frame/timeline reactivity down into KeyframeIndicator. Change its API to accept nodeId+property (+ a value or getValue for onToggle) and compute its own state via a Zustand selector: `const state = useEditorStore(s => getKeyframeState(s.timeline, nodeId, property, s.currentFrame));` — selector returns a primitive string so default equality re-renders only that diamond when its state changes. Update all ~19 call sites (e.g. 1487-1490, 1557-1559, 1736-1739, 1769-1772, 2589-2607, 2673-2688, and fill/stroke/effect indicators) to the new props. Then drop the top-level currentFrame subscription (361) and read the frame lazily in handlers/toggleKeyframe via useEditorStore.getState().currentFrame (toggleKeyframe at 1346-1354 and each handler's addKeyframeAtFrame); remove currentFrame from those useCallback deps. Audit remaining reactive timeline reads outside indicators (e.g. easing editor findTrack, selectedKeyframeIds display) and either keep a narrow timeline subscription or select derived values with an equality fn. Do after the correctness fixes so indicator call sites are only rewritten once.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/PropertiesPanel.tsx`, `apps/web/src/components/common/KeyframeIndicator.tsx`
- **Test:** Add a render-count probe: wrap PropertiesPanel body with a module-level counter incremented on each render (or use React Profiler onRender). Render with a node selected, then act -> useEditorStore.getState().setCurrentFrame across several frames; assert the panel body render count does not increase per frame while a KeyframeIndicator's state still updates when a keyframe exists/does not at the new frame.
- **Notes:** Low severity/perf but touches the same ~19 KeyframeIndicator call sites as the correctness fixes; sequence it after them to avoid rewriting call sites twice. Verify no other render path silently depends on the top-level currentFrame/timeline subscription before removing it.

#### `F164` · low · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/PropertiesPanel.tsx:2294`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Line Height scrub passes sensitivity 0.01 for a fractional property, but ScrubLabel rounds every output to an integer, so scrubbing snaps lineHeight to whole numbers

- **Root cause:** ScrubLabel unconditionally rounds output to an integer: ScrubLabel.tsx:51 `const newValue = Math.round(Math.min(max, Math.max(min, startValueRef.current + delta)))`. The Line Height ScrubLabel (PropertiesPanel.tsx:2284-2297) passes sensitivity=0.01, min=0.5, max=5 for a fractional property, so scrubbing can only ever emit integers 1-5; the onChange handler's `Math.max(0.5, +v.toFixed(2))` (2289) receives an already-integer v. A user dragging from lineHeight 1.2 snaps to 1.0 and no fractional value in the intended 0.01-step range is reachable.
- **Fix:** Add an optional step/precision prop to ScrubLabel (default preserving current integer behavior). E.g. add `step = 1` to props and compute `const newValue = Math.round(clamped / step) * step;` (or add `precision=0` and round to that many decimals). Default step=1 keeps every existing caller unchanged. Then pass step={0.01} to the Line Height ScrubLabel at 2284. Verify other fractional-intent callers are unaffected (only lineHeight needs sub-integer scrubbing; sides/CR remain integer).
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/common/ScrubLabel.tsx`, `apps/web/src/components/layout/PropertiesPanel.tsx`
- **Test:** Two tests: (1) ScrubLabel unit test — render with value=1.2, sensitivity=0.01, min=0.5, max=5, step=0.01; pointerdown then pointermove dx=3 (delta 0.03); assert onChange called with ~1.23 (fractional), not 1. (2) Regression: ScrubLabel with no step prop still rounds to integers as before.

#### `F165` · low · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Timeline.tsx:180`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Releasing a work-area handle/body drag fires a click that bubbles to the ruler, jumping the playhead to the release position and clearing keyframe selection.

- **Root cause:** The work-area bar and both handles (Timeline.tsx:934-964) are DOM children of the ruler div whose onClick is handleRulerClick (901-904). handleWorkAreaPointerDown calls e.stopPropagation() on pointerdown (336) but nothing stops the click event the browser synthesizes after pointerup; that click bubbles to handleRulerClick (180-191) which runs setCurrentFrame(round(x/width\*duration)) + clearKeyframeSelection(). So finishing a work-area handle/bar drag (release lands within the ruler subtree, the normal case for horizontal drags) — or even a no-move click on a handle — jumps the playhead to the release X and wipes the keyframe selection. handleWorkAreaPointerUp (363-365) nulls workAreaDragRef before the click, so the click cannot tell an interaction just ended.
- **Fix:** Track that a work-area interaction just ended and swallow the following ruler click. Add `justFinishedWorkAreaRef = useRef(false)`; set it true in handleWorkAreaPointerDown (covers no-move clicks) and in handleWorkAreaPointerUp, and clear it on the next tick via `setTimeout(() => { justFinishedWorkAreaRef.current = false; }, 0)` in pointerup so a stray interaction without a click doesn't permanently swallow the next genuine ruler click. At the top of handleRulerClick add: `if (justFinishedWorkAreaRef.current) { justFinishedWorkAreaRef.current = false; return; }`. This covers both release-over-ruler-background and release-over-handle cases. Belt-and-suspenders: also add onClick={(e)=>e.stopPropagation()} to the bar/start-handle/end-handle divs for clicks that land directly on the handle.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Timeline.tsx`
- **Test:** Timeline test: enable work area, select a keyframe (selectedKeyframeIds non-empty), record currentFrame, simulate a handle (or bar) pointerdown→pointerup then dispatch the trailing click within the ruler element; assert currentFrame is unchanged AND selectedKeyframeIds is still non-empty. Contrast: a genuine ruler click NOT preceded by a work-area interaction still updates currentFrame and clears keyframe selection.
- **Notes:** Independent of F087 but in the same work-area handler cluster; sensible to implement in the same change. The setTimeout(0) reset avoids the edge case where a work-area pointerdown never produces a click.

#### `F166` · low · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/timeline/GraphEditor.tsx:337`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** F020  
**Finding:** Shift-constrained keyframe drag never locks its axis: the second setDragMode in the same handler overwrites the first, so the constraint axis can flip mid-drag.

- **Root cause:** GraphEditor.tsx handleMouseMove keyframe branch: line 338 setDragMode({...dragMode, axis}) is immediately superseded by line 353 setDragMode({...dragMode, startTime: newTime, startValue: newValue}), which spreads the SAME stale closure dragMode (axis still null) and only overrides startTime/startValue. React state updates within one render's closure are last-write-wins over the same base object, so the axis assignment from 338 is discarded and dragMode.axis is never persisted. Consequently every subsequent mousemove re-derives axis at line 331 from `dx > dy` of the cumulative displacement (dx/dy computed at 329-330 from dragMode.startScreenX/Y, which are never updated). A shift-drag that begins mostly-horizontal (axis 'x', value locked to startValue) flips to axis 'y' the instant cumulative |dy| exceeds |dx|, making the keyframe value jump to the full mouse offset.
- **Fix:** Collapse the two setDragMode calls into one that resolves and persists the axis. Compute nextAxis = dragMode.axis ?? (dx>dy ? 'x' : 'y') only after the 5px threshold, apply the constraint (newValue=startValue for 'x', newTime=startTime for 'y') using nextAxis, then issue a single setDragMode({...dragMode, axis: nextAxis, ...(startTime/startValue if still tracked)}) — removing the separate line-338 call. Once locked, keep using the stored axis so it cannot flip mid-drag. Because this rewrites the same setDragMode at line 353 that F020 changes (F020 stops mutating startTime/startValue), do this edit together with F020 to avoid a merge conflict; after F020 the merged call becomes setDragMode({...dragMode, axis: nextAxis}).
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/timeline/GraphEditor.tsx`
- **Test:** GraphEditor.test.tsx: mousedown on a keyframe to enter keyframe drag, then dispatch two shift-held mousemove events — first mostly horizontal (large clientX delta, small clientY) to lock axis 'x', then a second where cumulative clientY delta exceeds clientX delta; read the track from the store and assert the keyframe's value still equals its startValue (axis stayed 'x', no vertical jump) while its time changed. If direct simulation is brittle, extract the axis-resolution into a pure helper resolveDragAxis(prevAxis, dx, dy, threshold) and unit-test that a non-null prevAxis is always returned unchanged.

#### `F167` · low · performance

**Location:** `apps/web/src/hooks/useProjectActions.ts:164`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** saveProject serializes the entire project twice per save (serializeProject, then serializeProjectToBinary which calls serializeProject again), doubling deep-clone cost on every 30s autosave.

- **Root cause:** saveProject serializes the whole project twice: serializeProject at useProjectActions.ts:152 (structuredClone of every page scene graph, timeline, symbols, rigging), then serializeProjectToBinary at line 164 which internally calls serializeProject AGAIN (projectSerializer.ts:195). The first result `data` is used only for data.createdAt (line 161). For a large multi-page project this doubles a main-thread deep clone on every 30s autosave tick. There is also a real minor correctness bug: `state` (captured line 144) is the pre-setState immutable Zustand object, so after setState at 159 `state.projectCreatedAt` is still null on a first save; serializeProjectToBinary(line 164) therefore receives undefined and generates a fresh `now` for createdAt, so the binary written to disk gets a slightly different createdAt than the store's projectCreatedAt (data.createdAt). saveProjectAs (lines 189-196) has the identical double-serialize.
- **Fix:** Add an exported helper to projectSerializer.ts, e.g. `export function projectDataToBinary(data: ProjectDataV2): ArrayBuffer { return writeQuarFile(data as unknown as Record<string, unknown>); }` (writeQuarFile is already imported there, line 19). In useProjectActions.ts saveProject, replace the serializeProjectToBinary call (lines 164-169) with `const binary = projectDataToBinary(data);` reusing the single `data` from line 152 — this both removes the second serialize and fixes the createdAt inconsistency (binary now uses data.createdAt). Do the same in saveProjectAs (reuse `data` from line 189 via projectDataToBinary instead of serializeProjectToBinary at line 196). serializeProjectToBinary can stay exported for other callers (importProject at line 260 still uses it, which is fine). Coordinate with F022 since both restructure the same 152-172 block.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/hooks/useProjectActions.ts`, `apps/web/src/services/projectSerializer.ts`
- **Test:** In useProjectActions.test.ts, mock the new projectDataToBinary and assert that on saveProject, serializeProject (mockSerialize) is called exactly once and projectDataToBinary is called once with the SAME object returned by mockSerialize (proving no re-serialize). Add an assertion that the binary is derived from the same `data` whose createdAt is written to the store (consistency). Note: the current hook-level test can't catch the double-serialize because serializeProjectToBinary is mocked separately, so the assertion must target the new single-serialize call shape.
- **Notes:** Foundational refactor; implement before F022 so the isDirty reorder lands on top of the single-serialize structure. The createdAt-inconsistency detail is masked in the current test because its setState mock uses Object.assign (mutates in place) rather than immutable replacement like real Zustand.

#### `F168` · low · race-condition

**Location:** `apps/web/src/hooks/useProjectActions.ts:171`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** F022  
**Finding:** An in-flight autosave of the previous project can overwrite lastProjectId after openProject sets it, so the next app launch reopens the wrong project.

- **Root cause:** saveProject in useProjectActions.ts captures projectId synchronously (line 145, or generated at 148), then awaits dbSave (line 170) and calls `await setLastProjectId(projectId)` at line 171 with no check that projectId is still the open project. lastProjectId is a single shared IndexedDB key. If the user opens project B (openProject sets setLastProjectId(B) at line 222) while project A's autosave dbSave is still in flight, A's setLastProjectId(A) can land last, leaving lastProjectId pointing at A while the user works in B. On next launch loadOnMount (line 408 reads getLastProjectId) auto-loads A. autoSavingRef/manualSavingRef only prevent overlapping saves; they do not prevent openProject from racing a save, and there is no generation/epoch guard.
- **Fix:** In useProjectActions.ts saveProject, guard the lastProjectId write against the currently-open project: after `await dbSave(...)`, replace `await setLastProjectId(projectId)` with `if (useEditorStore.getState().projectId === projectId) { await setLastProjectId(projectId); }`. Because getState() is re-read after the await, if openProject changed projectId to B in the meantime the stale autosave of A skips the lastProjectId update (dbSave of A's data under key A is unaffected and still correct). Apply the same guard in saveProjectAs before its setLastProjectId at line 198 for consistency. This general guard covers both autosave and manual saves without needing a separate autosave-only branch.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/hooks/useProjectActions.ts`
- **Test:** In useProjectActions.test.ts, add a race test: set mockEditorState.projectId='A'; make mockSave return a manually-controlled deferred promise; call saveProject (do not await); while dbSave is pending, mutate mockEditorState.projectId='B'; resolve dbSave and await; assert mockSetLastProjectId was NOT called with 'A' (guard skipped it). Add a positive test: when projectId is unchanged, setLastProjectId IS called with that id.
- **Notes:** Real but low-frequency (requires opening another project during an in-flight autosave). Best implemented after F022 restructures saveProject so the guard sits in the finalized post-dbSave block.

### Web — canvas & render loop

#### `F155` · low · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/canvas/GuideOverlay.tsx:161`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Drag-guide-back-onto-ruler removal checks `screen.x <= 0` / `screen.y <= 0`, but the rulers occupy canvas-local 0..RULER_SIZE, so dropping a guide on the visible ruler strip does not remove it.

- **Root cause:** GuideOverlay.tsx lines 161-167: the drag-release removal branch tests `guide.axis === 'x' && screen.x <= 0` and `guide.axis === 'y' && screen.y <= 0`, where `screen` comes from `toCanvasScreen` (lines 159 / 76-86) = clientX/Y minus the `<canvas>` bounding rect. Confirmed via layout: `.canvas` has `flex:1` in a `position:relative` container and fills it from (0,0) (Canvas.module.css), and the rulers are absolute overlays on top of it (`.hRuler` top:0 height RULER_SIZE, `.vRuler` left:0 width RULER_SIZE). So canvas-local coordinates over a ruler strip lie in `[0, RULER_SIZE]` (RULER_SIZE=20), never `<= 0`. The removal therefore only triggers when the pointer leaves the container entirely (over the neighboring panel), not when dropped on the visible ruler as the header comment (line 8, 'Figma behavior') intends. `RULER_SIZE` is imported on line 14 but otherwise unused, confirming the intended threshold.
- **Fix:** Change the two comparisons in the `onUp` handler to use RULER_SIZE: `if (guide.axis === 'x' && screen.x <= RULER_SIZE)` and `else if (guide.axis === 'y' && screen.y <= RULER_SIZE)`. This matches the ruler-strip geometry (vertical ruler occupies canvas-local x in [0,RULER_SIZE], horizontal ruler occupies canvas-local y in [0,RULER_SIZE]) and consumes the already-imported RULER_SIZE constant. Update the inline comment on line 160 from 'negative canvas-local coords' to 'onto the ruler strip (canvas-local coord within RULER_SIZE)'.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/canvas/GuideOverlay.tsx`, `apps/web/src/components/canvas/GuideOverlay.test.tsx`
- **Test:** In GuideOverlay.test.tsx add a drag-remove test: create a real `<canvas>` element, stub `getBoundingClientRect` to return `{left:0, top:0, ...}`, and pass it as `canvasRef={{ current: canvasEl }}` with a viewport-set Camera. Render one x-guide, `fireEvent.pointerDown` on its hit line to start the drag, then `fireEvent.pointerUp(window, { clientX: 10, clientY: 300 })` (canvas-local x=10, inside [0,RULER_SIZE]) and assert `onRemoveGuide` is called with the guide id. Add the symmetric y-guide case releasing at clientY=10. A pre-fix run of these tests should fail (removal not triggered at x/y=10).
- **Notes:** Independent of F006/F067. Purely a threshold correction; no behavior change to the create/drag paths.

#### `F160` · low · performance

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx:634`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** Smart Bones evaluation allocates fresh morph-offset Float32Arrays every RAF frame, permanently defeating the GPU skinning cache — packSkinnedVertices and a full VBO re-upload run per morphed node per frame even when the pose is static

- **Root cause:** evaluateSmartBones (packages/rigging/src/smartBones.ts:208-232) starts with `const accumulated = new Map()` and always stores `new Float32Array(offsets)` per node (line 226), so its returned Map holds brand-new Float32Array references every call. The Canvas render loop calls it every RAF frame (Canvas.tsx:633-639) and passes the result as morphOffsetsMap into ShapeRenderer.render. ensureSkinnedCacheData (ShapeRenderer.ts:3166-3184) detects change via reference identity: `morphChanged = morphOffsets !== cached.lastMorphOffsets` (3172), which is therefore always true, so buildBoneIdToIndex + packSkinnedVertices (a numVertices\*10 Float32Array alloc+fill) rerun every frame per morphed node even when the driver pose is static. Reviewer's correction holds: the bufferSubData VBO upload runs unconditionally regardless (shared skinnedVertexBuffer), so fixing this removes only the per-frame CPU repack and Float32Array allocations, not the GPU upload.
- **Fix:** Make the morph output stable-by-reference when driver values are unchanged so ShapeRenderer's reference check stays valid. Lowest-risk option at the call site (Canvas.tsx:615-666): cache the last morphOffsetsMap and a signature of the driver inputs in refs — signature = concatenation/hash of each SmartBoneAction's driver bone rotation(s) plus smartBoneActions identity and nodeVertexCounts; only call evaluateSmartBones when the signature changes, otherwise reuse the cached map reference. Guard the recording branch (643-665): while smartBoneRecordingActionId is set the working offsets change continuously, so bypass the cache (always recompute) during recording. Also memoize nodeVertexCounts (rebuild only when scene structure changes) rather than re-traversing every frame (624-631). Alternative deeper fix: give evaluateSmartBones a persistent internal cache keyed on driver rotations so it returns the same array references when unchanged.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx`
- **Test:** Test the Canvas-level smart-bone caching: with driver bone rotations unchanged across two render ticks, evaluateSmartBones is invoked only once (spy) and the morphOffsetsMap passed to ShapeRenderer.render keeps the same reference; changing a driver rotation invalidates and produces a new map. (Or, for the deeper fix, a smartBones.test.ts asserting reference-stable arrays across calls with identical driver state.)

#### `F161` · low · performance

**Location:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx:697`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** F010  
**Finding:** getDeformedBounds runs a second full CPU skinning pass (deformVertices over all mesh vertices) for every selected skinned node on every RAF frame, even when idle

- **Root cause:** The render loop's deformed-bounds block (Canvas.tsx:687-753) runs every RAF frame whenever anything is selected. For each selected skinned node (and each skinned child of a selected group) it calls shapeRenderer.getDeformedBounds (ShapeRenderer.ts:3578-3614), which re-collects bone world transforms and runs deformVertices(cached.vertices, skinData, boneWorldTransforms) at line 3597 — a full linear-blend-skinning pass allocating a fresh Float32Array over the entire mesh — purely to compute the selection-overlay AABB. This duplicates skinning work and runs even when no bone moved, so selecting a 5,000-vertex skinned character doubles its per-frame CPU skinning cost while idle.
- **Fix:** Gate the deformed-bounds recomputation on a change detector instead of running it unconditionally. Add a ref (e.g. lastDeformedBoundsStamp) capturing the inputs that affect deformation — the current sceneGraphVersion (read via a ref) plus the selection id set. At the top of the block, if the stamp is unchanged AND deformedBoundsRef already has entries for the current selection, skip the getDeformedBounds calls and reuse the cached bounds; recompute only when sceneGraphVersion or selection changed. This works because bone movement (IK apply, manual drag) emits nodeChanged and bumps sceneGraphVersion, while an idle pose leaves it constant. Depends on F010: until the idle-IK spurious nodeChanged is fixed, sceneGraphVersion bumps every frame under an enabled IK chain and the gate would not help. Alternatively reuse CPU-deformed vertices already computed during the stroke render pass by caching them per node.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/components/layout/Canvas.tsx`
- **Test:** Render-loop test: select a skinned node, run two consecutive RAF ticks with no bone transform change (sceneGraphVersion constant) and assert shapeRenderer.getDeformedBounds is called on the first tick but NOT the second (spy); then mutate a bone transform and assert it is called again.

### Web — editor store

#### `F171` · low · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts:1664`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** deleteSelection removes keyframe tracks only for the selected node ids, leaving orphaned tracks for all descendants of deleted groups.

- **Root cause:** deleteSelection (editorStore.ts:1664) calls mgr.removeAllKeyframesForNode(id) only for each selected id. SceneGraph.removeNode cascade-deletes descendants (SceneGraph.ts:99-103), but their keyframe tracks are never removed, leaving orphaned tracks that bloat in-memory timeline state and are serialized into saved .quar files. Runtime impact is benign: usePlayback.applyAnimations guards each track with `if (!node) continue` (usePlayback.ts:37-38), so orphaned tracks are skipped, not mis-applied — hence low, not medium.
- **Fix:** In deleteSelection, before `sceneGraph.removeNode(id)`, collect `const descendants = sceneGraph.getDescendants(id)` and call `mgr.removeAllKeyframesForNode(d.id)` for each descendant (in addition to the node itself).
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts`
- **Test:** Using the real SceneGraph (mock getDescendants returns []), create a group with a child rect, add a keyframe track for the child id, select+deleteSelection the group, then assert timeline.tracks contains no track with the child's nodeId.
- **Notes:** Test needs the real SceneGraph or a mock whose getDescendants returns the child; existing helpers stub getDescendants as () => [].

#### `F172` · low · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts:3251`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** medium · **Effort:** M · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** createSymbol on a node nested inside a transformed group places the new instance at the node's parent-relative coordinates at scene root, making the artwork jump.

- **Root cause:** createSymbol computes centerX/centerY from `node.transform.position` (parent-relative) at lines 3193-3202, removes the originals, and adds the instance node with parent:null at position (centerX,centerY) (3251, 3265). The parent chain's world transform is never applied, so a node nested inside a transformed group lands at its parent-relative coordinates at scene root and visibly jumps.
- **Fix:** Preferred (simple, exact): add the instance under the original common parent at the same child index rather than at root — capture the root-selected nodes' shared parent and child index, set instanceNode.parent to that parent, and call sceneGraph.addNode(instanceNode, parentId) with a moveNode to the recorded index. If roots span multiple parents, fall back to world-space: convert each root position via sceneGraph.getWorldTransform(parentId) (apply the parent matrix to the local position) before averaging into centerX/centerY, and place the instance at parent:null with that world position. Also make the definition's per-root re-centering consistent with whichever space is chosen.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/stores/editorStore.ts`
- **Test:** Real SceneGraph: create a group at (200,200) with a child rect at local (10,10); select the rect; createSymbol(sg). Assert the created instance's world position equals (210,210) — e.g. instance parented under the group at local (10,10), or at root (210,210) if world-space placement is chosen.
- **Notes:** getWorldTransform is available on SceneGraphLike (used by IK code at 1067), so world-space placement is feasible without new plumbing.

### Web — services & persistence

#### `F169` · low · duplication

**Location:** `apps/web/src/services/projectSerializer.ts:331`  
**Verdict:** partly · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** F098  
**Finding:** The v1->v2 .quar migration is maintained in three places (core TS, web TS, Python MCP) and the copies have already drifted; the web copy is dead code that silently drops symbols.

- **Root cause:** migrateV1ToV2 is triplicated and has drifted. The web copy (projectSerializer.ts:331-350) omits `symbols`, while @quar/core's copy (packages/core/src/format/quarMigration.ts:32-52, symbols at line 50) and the Python copy (tools/quar-mcp/app/quar_format.py:211-230, symbols at line 228) both carry it; the three also use different page ids and default builders. However the 'silently drops symbols' data loss is not reachable in practice: ProjectDataV1 (lines 27-49) has no symbols field, symbols were introduced in the v2 era (Sprint 22) after v1 was superseded, so a genuine v1 .quar cannot contain symbols. The web migrateV1ToV2 branch inside deserializeProject (line 397) only runs when data.version is neither 2.0 nor 3.0, but every production caller (importProject, openProject, loadOnMount) routes through parseQuarFile -> migrateToLatest which already migrates v1->v3, so the branch is effectively dead in production and is only exercised by tests calling deserializeProject with raw v1 (projectSerializer.test.ts:257, :309), none of which include a symbols field. The substantive issue is the cross-language duplication/drift, not runtime data loss.
- **Fix:** Delete the local migrateV1ToV2 (projectSerializer.ts:331-350) and instead import { migrateV1ToV2 } from '@quar/core'; at line 397 call `migrateV1ToV2(data as unknown as Record<string, unknown>) as unknown as ProjectDataV2`. This removes the drift and inherits core's symbols handling. Verify @quar/core re-exports migrateV1ToV2 (packages/core/src/format/index.ts) — it does. Follow-up (separate, low priority): add shared .quar fixture files consumed by both the TS suites (projectSerializer.test.ts / quarMigration.test.ts) and the Python suite (tools/quar-mcp/tests/test_quar_format.py) to lock the formats together.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/services/projectSerializer.ts`, `apps/web/src/services/projectSerializer.test.ts`
- **Test:** Extend the existing v1->v2 migration test (projectSerializer.test.ts:236) to cast a v1 input that carries a `symbols: [{id:'s1',...}]` field and assert appliedState.symbols preserves it after deserialize — this proves the web path no longer drops symbols once it delegates to @quar/core. (Documents the drift regression even though real v1 files can't carry symbols.)
- **Notes:** Skip-if-deferred is acceptable: no production data path currently loses symbols. Fix is worthwhile purely as de-duplication. Genuinely independent of F098's reorder (it edits the normalize expression at line 397, which F098 does not move), but touches the same function so sequence after F001/F098 to minimize churn.

#### `F170` · low · correctness

**Location:** `apps/web/src/services/projectSerializer.ts:463`  
**Verdict:** real · **Risk:** low · **Effort:** S · **Depends on:** —  
**Finding:** uploadProjectFile's promise never settles when the user cancels the file picker, leaving importProject permanently pending.

- **Root cause:** uploadProjectFile (projectSerializer.ts:457-497) creates a Promise that resolves/rejects only inside input.onchange (lines 463-493). When the user dismisses the native OS file picker without selecting a file, no change event fires, so the Promise never settles. importProject (useProjectActions.ts:241-268) awaits it (line 243), so on every cancel a pending promise and a detached <input> element are stranded and the import flow never completes. Currently not user-visible because importProject's only post-await work sits inside the try and there is no spinner/disabled-button tied to completion, but any future UI state keyed on importProject resolving would hang.
- **Fix:** In uploadProjectFile add cancellation handling: define a distinguishable error (e.g. `class ProjectImportCancelledError extends Error` exported, or a sentinel with a `cancelled: true` flag) and a `let settled = false` guard so onchange/onerror/cancel each settle at most once. Attach `input.addEventListener('cancel', () => { if (!settled) { settled = true; reject(new ProjectImportCancelledError()); } })` (supported in modern Chromium/Firefox/Safari 16.4+). Optionally add a window 'focus' fallback for older browsers: after input.click(), on the next window focus start a short timeout that rejects with the cancellation error if still unsettled and no file present. Then in importProject's catch, change `} catch {` (useProjectActions.ts:265) to `} catch (err) {` and return silently (skip toast.error) when err is the cancellation sentinel, so cancelling shows no spurious 'Failed to import' toast.
- **Files:** `apps/web/src/services/projectSerializer.ts`, `apps/web/src/hooks/useProjectActions.ts`, `apps/web/src/services/projectSerializer.test.ts`
- **Test:** In projectSerializer.test.ts (jsdom) stub document.createElement('input') to capture the created input, call uploadProjectFile(), dispatch a 'cancel' event on the captured input, and assert the returned promise rejects with the cancellation error (and does not stay pending). Optionally add a useProjectActions test asserting importProject does not call toast.error when uploadProjectFile rejects with the cancellation sentinel.
- **Notes:** Independent of the other three (different function). Reject with a cancellation-specific error, not a generic one, otherwise importProject's catch would surface a misleading error toast on a normal cancel.
